\begin{document}

\maketitle

\begin{abstract}
For \(X=K3\times E\) the theorem-level physical input used here is the
protected index.  Right-moving localization in the K3 Ramond sector gives
\[
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1},\qquad
\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l.
\]
Replacing the protected K3 index by its Borcherds half produces only a
virtual \(K_0\)-determinant package.  It does not produce a microscopic
Hilbert space.  Unitarity is used to localize the right-moving K3
supertrace before the index is taken; the index itself is a charge-graded
virtual object that no longer requires Hilbert positivity.  For virtual super vector spaces
\(\mathbb U_{n,l}\) with \(\sdim\mathbb U_{n,l}=f(n,l)\), set
\(\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=\mathbb U_{nm,l}\).  In the Borcherds cusp
chamber the determinant is
\[
\mathcal D_X(Z)
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=\Delta_5(Z).
\]
The constant \(64\) is the theta-constant normalization
\([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5=64\); hence the monic Borcherds
product is \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\).

The same coefficients are the signed root supermultiplicities in the
Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds--Kac--Moody denominator algebra.  Under
\[
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}
\]
one has
\[
\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})
=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z),\qquad
\smult\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l)
\]
on the active support.  Thus the denominator algebra supplies the
algebraic square root target and its target-internal Borcherds bracket.
It does not supply a compact BPS Hilbert space, compact Hall
correspondences, an orientation, or a BPS operator product/local
collision map.

The square root in the title is meant in Dirac's sense.  The scalar
OP/DT branch \(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP/DT}}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) is
orientation-forgetful: the sign character is squared away.  The
recognition target is a first-order protected operator/algebra
\(\mathfrak D_X\) whose protected Pfaffian, after a supplied
Pfaffian-to-automorphic line comparison, is \(\Delta_5\), and whose scalar trace
\(\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{prot}}((-1)^F\mathfrak D_X^{-2})
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\); the orientation/Pfaffian datum is the
algebraic input that distinguishes \(\Delta_5\) from \(-\Delta_5\) and
that the squared scalar cannot recover.  Constructing
\(\mathfrak D_X\) is the open recognition problem; this paper formulates
the target and the orientation-character constraint
\(\epsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on
\(W^{(2)}(\Lambda_{II}^{2,1})\).

The scalar Behrend-weighted branch is imported from
Oberdieck--Pixton, Oberdieck--Pandharipande, and Oberdieck.  In OP's
normalization \(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2\), so
\[
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=(64^{-1}\Delta_5)^2
=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2,\qquad
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}
=-\left(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}\right)^{-1}
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}.
\]
The factor \(4096=64^2\) is a normalization conversion; the minus sign is
the OP scalar convention.  Neither fixes the automorphic reflection
character or the compact orientation monodromy.

A compact realization would have to begin with an additive formal dyonic
charge lattice \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\), its algebraic/effective Hall
support, the Gram map
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), and a
holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra on \(K3\times E\).  The formal
lattice is \(\Lambda_S\oplus\Lambda_S\).  The algebraic even Mukai sector
relevant to the OP/DT D6--D2--D0 branch, and its stability-dependent
effective semigroup, are smaller inputs; the present construction does
not assert that every formal full-Mukai class is a compact Hall state.
The triple \((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) records Gram-degree
invariants \((Q^2/2,Q\cdot P,P^2/2)\) of a formal pair \(c=(Q,P)\); it is
not the additive Hall grading itself.  The Gram map is quadratic:
\[
\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c').
\]
Thus strict fixed-lift raw Gram descent cannot carry the type-II
real-root brackets.  The first
structural correction is the normal-ordered extension
\[
\widehat\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T,
\]
for which \(\overline\Pi_X\) is additive.  A compact realization would
then require a specified formality point, model-dependent
homotopy/framing datum, quantum master equation, anomaly control,
descent, and finite-first HN completion.  It would then
specialize along the K3 direction to a chiral object on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\), solve the
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)-support-locality obstruction in the
K3-integrated chiral shadow by mixed local/wrapped correspondences, and
identify the Gram-descended protected primitive bracket with
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\).  This paper proves the virtual
determinant, the lattice normal-ordering theorem, and the fixed-lift
raw-descent obstruction; records the imported scalar and denominator
theorems; and
formulates that compact Hall/factorization realization as an open
recognition problem.  The final part records the eight Clery--Gritsenko
diagonal-divisor rows and the certificate required before any boundary
row becomes a physical host.
\end{abstract}

\bigskip
\tableofcontents

\section{Introduction and claim strength}
\label{sec:introduction-claim-strength}

The local object comes first.  A compact BPS theory on
\(X=K3\times E\), if it exists in the form needed here, should produce
protected local observables before any trace is taken.  After twisting
and passing to the protected index, the positive Hilbert space has
collapsed to a charge-graded virtual object, but locality has not
disappeared: disjoint insertions must still factorize and collisions
must remember extensions.
Throughout the compact-realization problem, \(S\) is a smooth complex
K3 surface and \(E\) is a smooth elliptic curve; singular K3 limits,
nodal elliptic limits, imprimitive curve-class contributions, the
\(s=0\) compact Hall cusp, and multi-component charge closures are
deferred boundary problems, not standing hypotheses.

Thus the exposition follows the dependency chain
\[
\begin{array}{rcl}
\hbox{protected K3 index} & \rightsquigarrow_{\mathrm{computes}} &
\hbox{virtual }K_0\hbox{-determinant},\\
\hbox{Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin} & \rightsquigarrow_{\mathrm{imports}} &
\hbox{denominator target},\\
\hbox{formal Mukai charge and }B & \rightsquigarrow_{\mathrm{proves}} &
\hbox{normal-ordered Gram map},\\
\hbox{supplied finite Hall--Dirac source} & \rightsquigarrow_{\mathrm{conditional}} &
\hbox{primitive recognition},\\
\hbox{Oberdieck--Pixton/Oberdieck} & \rightsquigarrow_{\mathrm{checks}} &
\hbox{orientation-forgetful scalar square},\\
\hbox{Clery--Gritsenko rows} & \rightsquigarrow_{\mathrm{certificate}} &
\hbox{boundary host tests}.
\end{array}
\]
The scalar OP/DT equality is a check on the square of a supplied
first-order Pfaffian object.  It is not an input to the compact Hall
source, the Pfaffian line, or primitive recognition.
\paragraph{Protected locality.}
The protected index is theorem-level.  Right-moving localization of the
unitary K3 sigma model gives
\[
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1},\qquad
\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l.
\]
The half-index used by the Borcherds lift is represented only in
\(K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}})\).  Its coefficients are signed
superdimensions, not dimensions of a constructed compact D-brane Hilbert
space.

\paragraph{Compact and hybrid factorization.}
A compact realization would first supply the formal dyonic lattice, the
algebraic/effective Hall support inside it, the non-additive Gram map
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), and a
charge-completed holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra
\[
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X,\qquad X=K3\times E,
\]
then a chain-level K3-to-\(E\) specialization
\[
\mathcal F_X^{(0)}\simeq
\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X)
\in\mathrm{Fact}(\operatorname{Ran}(E)).
\]
This projection-finite chiral shadow is not reconstructed from the
scalar partition function or from the Borcherds product.  The full
object is the hybrid \(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) only after the
finite hybrid certificate is supplied.  There is also a geometric
obstruction: a
one-dimensional subscheme with positive elliptic degree projects onto
all of \(E\).  Hence a naive support-local object on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) sees only projection-finite sectors.  The full
Igusa \(s\)-direction requires finite-stage local/wrapped correspondence
data for positive elliptic degree: the elliptic-degree map \(b_R\),
rigidified wrapped prequotients with anchors, local-local, ordered
local/wrapped, and wrapped-wrapped extension stacks, the eight-word
two-step binary flag atlas,
quotient-after-correspondence descent, and protected integration with
trace degree \(s^{b_R}\).  A detached global Hecke/Fock factor is only a
determinant-level repair.  It becomes relevant to the compact
realization only after it is represented by those wrapped prequotients
and acts through mixed Hall correspondences before the reduced
\(E\)-quotient.  This is open.

\paragraph{Primitive recognition.}
Until Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}, the notation
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) denotes the same formal full-Mukai
bookkeeping lattice later written
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\); the superscript is mnemonic and not the
four-dimensional \(\mathcal N=4\) electric--magnetic charge lattice.
The microscopic algebra sought from such a compact realization is first
the upstairs protected primitive bracket
\[
[\ ,\ ]:\Prim_{c}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)
\otimes
\Prim_{c'}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)
\longrightarrow
\Prim_{c+c'}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X),
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}.
\]
The recognition criterion proved later is conditional: it specifies the
certificate and its consequences.  If the
Dirac--Igusa certificate \(\mathfrak K_X\) exists, including the oriented Hall object,
protected integration, cocycle-corrected Gram descent
\(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\), a conilpotent source coalgebra \(C_X\)
with finite source filtration and collision coproduct, the bar comparison
\(b_X\), the cobar map
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}\), Koszul Mittag--Leffler exactness for the
completed bar/cobar inverse system, presentation-level primitive Lie
comparison, no-extra-relations theorem, completed PBW compatibility,
exact triangular completion/\(\lim^1\)-vanishing, and radical quotient,
then
\[
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X)
\cong
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}
\]
and the supplied chiral cobar comparison identifies
\(\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X\) with the formal current envelope
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\).  This is a recognition criterion, not an
existence theorem and not a reconstruction from the determinant.

\paragraph{Borcherds denominator.}
The target algebra is imported from the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin
construction.  With
\[
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2},
\]
the visible active coefficients satisfy
\[
\smult\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l),\qquad
\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z).
\]
This determines signed root supermultiplicities and the denominator
identity.  It does not determine compact Hall constants.

\paragraph{OP scalar square.}
The reduced scalar branch is imported from
Oberdieck--Pixton, Oberdieck--Pandharipande, and Oberdieck:
\[
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(T,Q,P)=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T)
=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.
\]
The constants are fixed once.  The theta-constant form satisfies
\[
[q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5=64,\qquad
D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5.
\]
OP's monic product is \(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2\), hence
\[
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2,\qquad
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}
=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}.
\]
The number \(64\) is a theta-leading coefficient.  The number
\(-4096\) is the OP scalar normalization.  Neither proves the compact
orientation character.  The comparison
\[
\epsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}
\]
between geometric orientation monodromy and the automorphic reflection
character remains part of the open Dirac--Igusa realization certificate.

\paragraph{Eight-row host certificates.}
The diagonal-divisor boundary problem concerns the eight
Clery--Gritsenko forms
\[
\Delta_5,\Delta_2,\Delta_1,\Delta_{1/2},
\nabla_3,\nabla_2,\nabla_{3/2},Q_1 .
\]
Rows \(1\)--\(4\) have Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator theorems.  Rows
\(5\)--\(8\) have Clery--Gritsenko products and Govindarajan CHL/WKB
denominator theorems; \(F_7=\nabla_{3/2}\) is on the required
\(\mu_4\)-multiplier cover.  A physical host for any boundary row
requires a certificate fixing the modular group or cover, character,
divisor, cusp Jacobi inputs, product lattice, Weyl vector, real roots,
reflection character, physical charge lattice, protected Gram-index,
orientation, reduced scalar theorem if one is claimed, and
primitive algebra comparison.  Without that certificate the row is only
an automorphic product plus any separately proved denominator theorem.

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.23\textwidth}p{0.25\textwidth}p{0.41\textwidth}}
\hline
Structural level & Claim strength & Content \\
\hline
Virtual determinant &
proved here from \(K_0\) data plus imported Borcherds product &
\(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\).  No canonical half-Hilbert space or operator
product is constructed. \\
Scalar Behrend square &
imported theorem &
Oberdieck--Pixton, Oberdieck--Pandharipande, and Oberdieck give
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}\) in the
reduced quotient-by-\(E\), Behrend-weighted setting. \\
BKM denominator &
imported theorem &
Gritsenko--Nikulin give \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\) and
\(\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\). \\
Compact Hall/factorization realization &
conditional/open &
If \(\mathfrak K_X\) exists, the primitive and chiral comparisons follow
by the recognition criterion.  Existence, \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)
hybrid locality,
protected integration, and orientation monodromy are open. \\
Eight-row host certificates &
framework; mostly open &
The catalogue and denominator rows are imported where cited.  Physical
row maps and scalar squares require row-by-row certificates. \\

\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\paragraph{Status and dependencies of results.}
The manuscript uses the words proved, computed, imported, certificate,
conditional, conjectural, open, and obstructed in the following strict
sense.  A proved statement is established in the paper; a computed
statement is verified by the displayed calculation or script; an imported
statement is a cited theorem; a certificate is a finite list of data and
tests; a conditional statement follows after the certificate is supplied;
an open statement names missing construction data.

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.20\textwidth}p{0.18\textwidth}p{0.52\textwidth}}
\hline
Result & Status & Dependencies and exclusions \\
\hline
Protected K3 index and \(K_0\) half-index &
proved/imported/defined &
Right-moving localization gives
\(Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1}\).  The half-index
\(\mathbb U_{n,l}\) is an arbitrary \(K_0\)-representative with
\(\sdim\mathbb U_{n,l}=f(n,l)\), not a canonical half-Hilbert space,
operator product, or compact D-brane state space. \\
Virtual determinant \(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\) &
computed/imported &
Computed from the \(K_0\)-half-index and identified with the
theta-normalized Borcherds product by the imported
Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin theorem.  No compact Hilbert space,
operator product, or Pfaffian line is supplied. \\
Lattice normal ordering &
proved &
The formal Mukai lattice, cocycle \(B\), central extension
\(\widehat\Gamma_X\), and homomorphism \(\overline\Pi_X\) are proved
lattice algebra.  Algebraic/effective Hall support is open. \\
Raw Gram descent &
proved obstruction &
Strict homogeneous fixed-lift raw \(\Pi_X\)-pushforward cannot realize
the type-II real-root strings.  Fibre-summed raw descent over different
lifts is open. \\
Denominator algebra &
imported &
Gritsenko--Nikulin give \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\) and
\(\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\). \\
Compact Dirac--Igusa source &
certificate/conditional/open &
The \(D_0\)-stage, strong orientation, Weyl cocycle, type-II Pfaffian
wall model, hybrid wrapped factorization, source Koszul comparison, and
primitive recognition are certificate data.  The consequences are
conditional on these data, Koszul Mittag--Leffler exactness, exact
triangular completion, and compatible transitions; the compact state-side
construction is open. \\
Scalar OP/DT square &
imported/check &
Oberdieck--Pixton, Oberdieck--Pandharipande, and Oberdieck identify the
Behrend-weighted reduced scalar branch with
\(-4096\Delta_5^{-2}\).  This checks the orientation-forgetful square and
does not construct \(\mathfrak D_X\) or \(\epsilon_o\). \\
Eight-row host certificates &
certificate/open &
The automorphic products and denominator rows are imported where cited.
Physical row maps and scalar squares require row-by-row host
certificates. \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

All super vector spaces in the representation-theoretic constructions
are over \(\C\).  Real vector spaces occur only after tensoring
lattices with \(\R\) to discuss cones, chambers, and period domains.
Products may be written over \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\); the active
factors are exactly the triples in \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\), where
the exponent \(f(nm,l)\) is non-zero.

\part{The automorphic square root}

\section{The physical question}
\label{sec:physical-question}

A charged BPS state is not, in the first instance, a local field.  It
lies in a superselection sector.  Its charge is measured at infinity,
and its existence depends on a stability chamber.  Thus the ordinary
local operator algebra of an untwisted four-dimensional theory is not
the primary object of this paper.

At the level of the protected index the situation is different.  After
taking the cohomology of the chosen supercharge, long multiplets cancel.
The object which remains is a charge-graded virtual object,
not a positive Hilbert space, whose Euler characteristic is stable under
deformation.  The index remembers the cancellation law of a unitary
theory, not its positive inner product.

For \(X=K3\times E\) the expected local object in a compact realization
is a supplied holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra
$$
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X,\qquad X=K3\times E.
$$
The auxiliary notation \(\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_3(X)\), when used, is only a
placeholder for this source datum; no such functor is constructed in
this paper.  No external \(\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_3\) formalism is used here
as an existence theorem unless it supplies the chain-level local
observables, factorization maps, descent, anomaly/QME control, and
compact charge completion required below.  In a compact realization
\(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) is the object whose disjoint holomorphic
insertions factorize.  The elliptic curve \(E\) enters only after a
supplied chain-level \(K3\)-specialization whose output is denoted
$$
\mathcal F_X\in\mathrm{Fact}(\operatorname{Ran}(E)).
$$
This is the first compact-realization obstruction.  The
projection-finite sector, where \(p_E(\operatorname{Supp}A)\) is a finite
subset of \(E\), is naturally local on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\).  A
one-dimensional sector of positive elliptic degree is not.  If
\(C\subset K3\times E\) has positive elliptic degree, then
\((p_E)_*[C]\) is a positive multiple of \([E]\); hence \(p_E(C)\) is a
one-dimensional closed subset of the irreducible curve \(E\), and so
\(p_E(C)=E\).  Such a class is wrapped or global over \(E\), not
localized at finitely many points of \(E\).

This is the \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)-support-locality obstruction in
the K3-integrated chiral shadow.  Naive support-local factorization on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) sees projection-finite sectors, but by itself
it misses the positive \(s\)-direction of the Igusa product, the
direction which records elliptic degree after the OP/Borcherds variable
conversion.  A compact realization must therefore choose at least one
finite categorical repair: projection-finite local factorization,
rigidified wrapped prequotients, local-local, ordered local/wrapped, and
wrapped-wrapped extension correspondences, the eight-word two-step binary
flag atlas with higher factorization separate,
quotient-after-correspondence descent, and protected integration whose
\(s\)-degree is the elliptic degree.  A separate
global Fock/Hecke mode is insufficient unless it is realized by these
wrapped prequotients and coupled to the local sector by mixed Hall
actions before the reduced \(E\)-quotient.  This is a realization
obstruction.  It is not a defect in the
Borcherds determinant or in the Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator identity.

Thus, in a realization, the curve-level rule is not imposed externally.
It is the one-dimensional chiral shadow of the holomorphic
\(E_3\)-observable: well-separated protected insertions on \(E\)
multiply, while collisions remember extension and bound-state data.  In
primitive form this is the expected bracket
$$
[\ ,\ ]:
\Prim_{c}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)
\otimes
\Prim_{c'}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)
\longrightarrow
\Prim_{c+c'}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X),
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}.
$$

The Igusa square-root problem is to construct or recognize this
primitive protected algebra and its Gram descent.  The determinant below
gives the decategorified signed Gram-index shadow that such a realization
would have as a recognition target, not as a source-derived
multiplicity:
$$
\sdim\Prim_{\gamma}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X)
=f(nm,l),
\qquad \gamma=(n,l,m).
$$
The Borcherds--Kac--Moody denominator algebra gives the algebraic
candidate:
$$
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X)
\stackrel{?}{\cong}
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}.
$$
The theorem-level content of the paper is the determinant and
denominator comparison.  The displayed isomorphism is the compact
\(E_3\)/Hall/chiral realization problem.

The square root is therefore not an analytic ambiguity in
\(\Delta_5^2\).  It is the normalized automorphic determinant of the
virtual protected one-particle index.  The scalar square forgets the
automorphic reflection character; a compact Hall orientation realizing
that character is part of the open Dirac--Igusa certificate.

\subsection*{Schema of the local protected observable algebra}
\label{sec:local-protected-observable-algebra}

\begin{definition}[Conditional local protected observable algebra schema]
\label{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}
For an open \(U\subset X=K3\times E\), let
\(\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}(U)\subset
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{alg}}\subset\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\) be the supplied
algebraic/effective charge support.  For
\(c\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}(U)\), let
\(\mathfrak M_c(U)\) denote the derived moduli stack of compactly
supported B-branes on \(U\) of Mukai charge \(c\), in the sense of
Pantev--Toen--Vaquie--Vezzosi \cite{PTVV2013}, so that
\(\mathfrak M_c(U)\) carries a \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structure;
let \(\Phi_c\) denote the perverse sheaf of vanishing cycles of any
local d-critical chart, in the sense of
Brav--Bussi--Dupont--Joyce--Szendroi \cite{BBDJS2015} (BPS sheaf, alias
DT sheaf), well defined globally as a pre-D-critical structure on
\(\mathfrak M_c(U)\); let \(o_c\) denote the orientation line, a
square root of the determinant line of the cotangent complex of
\(\mathfrak M_c(U)\), supplied as part of the Hall datum.  The
\emph{local protected observable algebra of \(X\) on \(U\)} is the
conditional source object
\[
\mathcal A_X(U)
:=\bigoplus_{c\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}(U)}
H_*^{\mathrm{BM}}\!\bigl(\mathfrak M_c(U),\,
\Phi_c\otimes o_c\bigr),
\]
graded by that supplied support, not by the full formal lattice.  For disjoint
\(U_1,\ldots,U_k\subset X\), the proposed factorization map is
\[
\mathcal A_X(U_1)\otimes\cdots\otimes\mathcal A_X(U_k)
\longrightarrow
\mathcal A_X(U_1\sqcup\cdots\sqcup U_k),
\]
defined chain-level by Massey--Saito Thom--Sebastiani for vanishing
cycles
\[
\Phi_{F_1\oplus\cdots\oplus F_k}\simeq
\Phi_{F_1}\boxtimes\cdots\boxtimes\Phi_{F_k}
\]
on disjoint d-critical charts \cite{MasseyST,SaitoMHM}, together with the Ext-vanishing
\(\operatorname{Ext}^*(\mathcal F,\mathcal G)=0\) for branes
\(\mathcal F,\mathcal G\) with disjoint supports.  This is the
local protected-observable pre-interface schema for the present paper.
It becomes a compact \(E_3\) source \(\mathcal A_X^{E_3}\) only after
the finite witnesses of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-e3-source-interface} are supplied; the
disjoint-supports factorization on opens of \(X=K3\times E\) is only the
first holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization test.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}
The components are external assumptions:
PTVV \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structure on derived moduli of
B-branes \cite{PTVV2013}; BBDJS vanishing-cycle perverse sheaf and its
Thom--Sebastiani isomorphism (extending Massey 2001 and Saito 1990 to
the d-critical setting \cite{MasseyST,SaitoMHM}) \cite{BBDJS2015}; orientation lines from the
Joyce--Upmeier orientation theory \cite{JoyceUpmeier} or
Kontsevich--Soibelman \cite{KSCoHA}.  The factorization map relies on
disjoint-supports Ext-vanishing for compactly supported branes
(absent for non-compact supports, where one recovers chiral algebra
structure, not commutative factorization).  Compactness on
\(K3\times E\) is open because the relevant moduli of branes are
typically non-quasicompact in \(\La_S\)-charge; the sectorial
truncation of
Proposition~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation} is the candidate
truncation.
\end{remark}

\section{The one-particle index and its determinant}

For the determinant calculation set
$$
Z=\begin{pmatrix}z_1&z_2\\z_2&z_3\end{pmatrix},\qquad
q=e^{2\pi iz_1},\qquad r=e^{2\pi iz_2},\qquad s=e^{2\pi iz_3}.
$$
The Gram-index lattice is
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}=\Z^3,\qquad
\gamma=(n,l,m),\qquad x^\gamma=q^nr^ls^m.
$$
The standard cusp polarization is the ordered limit
$$0<|s|\ll |q|\ll |r|^{-1}\ll1.$$
It determines the semigroup
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}
=\{(n,l,m)\mid m>0,\ n\geq0,\ l\in\Z\}
\cup\{(n,l,0)\mid n>0,\ l\in\Z\}
\cup\{(0,l,0)\mid l<0\}.
$$
\(m>0\) is positive because \(s\) is the smallest parameter; if
\(m=0\), then \(n>0\) is positive because \(q\) is next; if \(m=n=0\),
positivity is \(l<0\) because \(|r|^{-1}\ll1\).  This is a chamber
convention for the completed product, not a microscopic charge
positivity statement.

\begin{definition}[Ramond-sector K3 index and its half]
Let $\mathcal H_{\mathrm{RR}}(S)$ be the Ramond--Ramond Hilbert space of
a unitary $\mathcal N=(4,4)$ sigma model on a K3 surface $S$.  Its
central charges are
$$c=\overline c=6.$$
This Hilbert space is a supplied worldsheet input for the protected K3
index.  It is not a construction of the compact \(K3\times E\)
D-brane Hilbert space.
Choose a right-moving Ramond supercharge $Q_R$ with
$$Q_R^2=0,\qquad
\{Q_R,Q_R^\dagger\}=
2\left(\overline L_0-\frac{\overline c}{24}\right).$$
The K3 elliptic genus is the protected supertrace
$$
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}(\tau,z)=
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{RR}}(S)}
(-1)^{F_L+F_R}q^{L_0-c/24}
\overline q^{\,\overline L_0-\overline c/24}r^{J_0}.
$$
The BPS space in degree $(n,l)$ is
$$
\mathcal H^{\mathrm{BPS}}_{n,l}(S):=
H^\bullet\!\left(
\{\psi\mid (L_0-c/24)\psi=n\psi,\ J_0\psi=l\psi\},Q_R
\right).
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Right-moving localization]
Then
$$
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}(\tau,z)=
\sum_{n\geq0,\;l\in\Z}
\sdim\mathcal H^{\mathrm{BPS}}_{n,l}(S)q^nr^l.
$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If $\overline L_0-\overline c/24>0$, the displayed anticommutator pairs
states with opposite $(-1)^{F_R}$ parity.  Their supertrace cancels.
The unpaired states are the $Q_R$-harmonic representatives, hence the
graded superdimension of $Q_R$-cohomology gives the elliptic genus.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Where unitarity enters]
Unitarity is used here before the index is taken: it gives the adjoint
relation which pairs positive right-moving energy states and makes the
supertrace localize.  After passing to the protected index, the object is
virtual.  A coefficient \(f(n,l)\) is a superdimension, not a positive
dimension.  Negative coefficients record an odd excess in the protected
supertrace, or in the chosen \(K_0\)-representative.  They do not
determine the two parity dimensions without an additional Hilbert-space
or denominator-algebra parity datum.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Grothendieck half-index representative]
Eichler--Zagier normalization \cite{EZ:1}:
$$Z_{\mathrm{K3}}(\tau,z)=2\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z),$$
$$\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)
=\sum_{n\geq 0,\;l\in\Z}f(n,l)q^nr^l.$$
Thus
$$\sdim\mathcal H^{\mathrm{BPS}}_{n,l}(S)=2f(n,l).$$
The arbitrary Grothendieck representative
$$\mathbb U_{n,l}\in K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}}),
\qquad \sdim\mathbb U_{n,l}=f(n,l),$$
is the normalized half-index class used by the Borcherds lift.  It is
not asserted to be a canonical half of
$\mathcal H^{\mathrm{BPS}}_{n,l}(S)$ as a Hilbert space.
As a \(K_0\)-model one may take \(\mathbb U_{n,l}\) to be
\(\C_{\overline0}^{f(n,l)}\) when \(f(n,l)\ge0\), and
\(\C_{\overline1}^{-f(n,l)}\) when \(f(n,l)<0\).  No canonical choice of
basis, parity lift, or operator product is implied.
$$\phi_{0,1}=r^{-1}+10+r+O(q),\qquad
\frac{f(0,0)}{2}=5.$$
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Fock trace and superdeterminant]
Let
$$V=\bigoplus_{\lambda\in P}V_\lambda$$
be a $P$-graded super vector space with finite-dimensional homogeneous
pieces and let $a_\lambda=\sdim V_\lambda$.  Put
$$\mathcal F(V)=\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\overline 0})
\otimes \bigwedge(V_{\overline 1}).$$
As a formal character,
$$\sch\mathcal F(V):=
\sum_{\mu\in P}\sdim\mathcal F(V)_\mu\,x^\mu
=\prod_{\lambda\in P}(1-x^\lambda)^{-a_\lambda}.$$
The inverse character is the superdeterminant
$$\sdet_V(1-x)=\prod_{\lambda\in P}(1-x^\lambda)^{a_\lambda}.$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
$$V_\lambda=\C_{\overline0}:\qquad
\sch\operatorname{Sym}(V_\lambda)=(1-x^\lambda)^{-1}.$$
$$V_\lambda=\C_{\overline1}:\qquad
\sch\bigwedge(V_\lambda)=1-x^\lambda.$$
Tensor product over a homogeneous basis proves the product.
\end{proof}

When \(P=\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\), all products below are taken in the
cusp-completed semigroup algebra determined by
\(0<|s|\ll |q|\ll |r|^{-1}\ll1\).  Every coefficient receives only
finitely many contributions in this completion.

$$x^{(n,l,m)}=q^nr^ls^m.$$
Form now the virtual Borcherds determinant package.  The third index
\(m\) is the second-quantized/Borcherds degree.  The positive \(m\)
sector carries the Hecke--DMVV exponents \(f(nm,l)\).  The \(m=0\)
sector is a cusp/Weyl boundary package carrying the repeated boundary
indices \(f(0,l)\).  Neither sector is a microscopic one-particle Hilbert
space.
The compact Hall \(s=0\) cusp is therefore a separate boundary
certificate: it is controlled by the Borcherds chamber data only after
the corresponding source-side boundary operations are supplied.
\[
\mathcal V^{\mathrm{bulk}}
:=\bigoplus_{\substack{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\\m>0}}
\mathbb U_{nm,l},
\qquad
\mathcal V^{\mathrm{cusp}}
:=\bigoplus_{\substack{(n,l,0)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}}
\mathbb U_{0,l}.
\]
\[
\mathcal V=\mathcal V^{\mathrm{bulk}}\oplus\mathcal V^{\mathrm{cusp}},
\qquad
\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=\mathcal V_{n,l,m}:=\mathbb U_{nm,l},\qquad
\sdim\mathcal V_{n,l,m}=f(nm,l).
\]
This is a definition in \(K_0\), not a microscopic state space.  The
\(m>0\) sector is the \(K_0\)-level virtual half of the DMVV product
\cite{DMVV}, obtained by replacing
\(Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1}\) by \(\phi_{0,1}\).  The normalized Fock
character in the Borcherds chamber is
$$\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)
=\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-x^\gamma)^{-\sdim\mathcal V_\gamma}
=\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{-f(nm,l)}.$$
$$\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)
=\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-x^\gamma)^{\sdim\mathcal V_\gamma}
=\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
The sector $m>0$ is the normalized half of the second-quantized DMVV
index.  The terms with $m=0$ are cusp and Weyl-chamber boundary factors
of the Borcherds product; the determinant reads only their signed
indices $f(0,l)$.
The normalized cusp-form section below proves the leading coefficient
which fixes the Weyl monomial
$$v_0(Z)=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}.$$
$$v_0\notin\bigoplus_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}\mathcal V_\gamma.$$

\begin{definition}[Normalized \(K_0\)-determinant]
$$\mathcal{D}_X(Z)
=v_0(Z)\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
$$\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}(Z)
=\mathcal D_X(Z)^{-1}
=\frac{1}{64}q^{-1/2}r^{-1/2}s^{-1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{-f(nm,l)}.$$
The object constructed here is the virtual \(K_0\)-determinant; compact
BPS meaning is part of the separate realization problem.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Determinant normalization]
$$[q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\,\mathcal D_X=64,$$
$$\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}
=\frac{1}{64}q^{-1/2}r^{-1/2}s^{-1/2}\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V),$$
$$\mathcal D_X
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x).$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$$\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)
=\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{-f(nm,l)},\qquad
\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)
=\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
$$v_0(Z)\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)=\mathcal D_X,\qquad
v_0(Z)^{-1}\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)
=\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}.$$
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Virtuality of the square root]
\label{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root}
The displayed construction produces a class
$$
[\mathcal V]\in
K_0(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\hbox{-graded finite-dimensional super vector spaces})
$$
together with its Fock determinant.  By itself this determinant does not
construct a Hilbert space, a vertex algebra, a holomorphic
\(E_3\)-factorization algebra, or a chiral factorization algebra whose
character is $\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}$.

All denominator statements use only the equalities
$$\sdim\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l),\qquad
\mathcal D_X=v_0\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x).$$
The denominator algebra and formal current envelope are constructed
later from the Borcherds root datum, not from a canonical half of the K3
Hilbert space.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By definition, $\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=\mathbb U_{nm,l}$ is specified only
through its class in $K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}})$ and through the
integer $\sdim\mathbb U_{nm,l}=f(nm,l)$.  The Fock trace and
superdeterminant lemma depends only on these signed dimensions.  No
operation in the construction supplies composition maps, operator
products, locality, or a Hilbert completion.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Dirac/Pfaffian recognition target]
\label{prop:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-target}
The class \([\mathcal V]\in K_0\) and its Fock determinant
\(\mathcal D_X=v_0\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)=\Delta_5\) record signed
Gram-degree multiplicities and a formal infinite-product; they do not
produce an operator with a spectrum.  The structural upgrade demanded
by the protected-locality side of the constellation is an
\emph{open recognition target}:
\begin{quote}
construct from the compact \(K3\times E\) Dirac--Igusa certificate of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum} a first-order
protected operator/algebra
\(\mathfrak D_X\) acting on a chiral protected module, whose
charge-graded Pfaffian, after the supplied Pfaffian-to-automorphic line
comparison, satisfies
$$
\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X))
=\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5.
$$
Its scalar trace, in the OP normalization of
Definition~\ref{def:op-normalization-branch} below, satisfies
$$
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{prot}}
\bigl((-1)^F(\mathfrak D_X)^{-2}\bigr)
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}.
$$
\end{quote}
Existence of \(\mathfrak D_X\) is open; it would convert the \(K_0\)
identity of Proposition~\ref{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root}
into a first-order protected statement.  The target carries the
sign-square ambiguity of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:protected-d-brane-index} and the orientation
monodromy of Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character};
choosing a square root of \((\mathfrak D_X)^{-2}\) requires the
orientation datum of that open problem and is not fixed by the OP
scalar.
\end{proposition}

\begin{definition}[Finite generic type-II local-sign subcertificate]
\label{def:type-ii-pfaffian-wall-certificate}
A finite generic local-sign subcertificate for the type-II Pfaffian model consists, for
each of the three simple type-II walls
\(\Hpl_{\delta_i}\), \(i=1,2,3\), of the following data.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(Pf1)}] A generic wall point \(x_i\) in the reduced compact
Hall sector and an \(s_{\delta_i}\)-equivariant real analytic slice
\((U_i,u_i)\) through \(x_i\), with
\[
\Hpl_{\delta_i}\cap U_i=\{u_i=0\},
\qquad
s_{\delta_i}(u_i)=-u_i .
\]
\item[\textup{(Pf2)}] A splitting of the reduced determinant complex on
the slice into its tangent determinant factor and a normal factor
\[
K^{\mathrm{red}}|_{U_i}\simeq
K^{\mathrm{tan}}_i\oplus K^{\mathrm{nor}}_i,
\]
with \(s_{\delta_i}\) preserving the tangent determinant factor.
\item[\textup{(Pf3)}] An oriented quasi-isomorphism of the normal factor
to a finite sum of odd rank-one Pfaffian crossings
\[
K^{\mathrm{nor}}_i\simeq
\bigoplus_{j=1}^{N_i^{\mathrm{Pf}}}
\bigl[\mathbb R\xrightarrow{\,u_i\,}\mathbb R\bigr].
\]
In the induced trivialization the normal Pfaffian section is
\(u_i^{N_i^{\mathrm{Pf}}}\) times a unit.
\item[\textup{(Pf4)}] The three normal-mode ranks
\(N_i^{\mathrm{Pf}}=N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}\) are
\[
N_1^{\mathrm{Pf}}=N_2^{\mathrm{Pf}}=N_3^{\mathrm{Pf}}=1 .
\]
\end{enumerate}
This is a finite generic local-sign subcertificate: three wall charts, three
anti-invariance checks \(s_{\delta_i}(u_i)=-u_i\), three tangent-factor
compatibility checks, and three odd Pfaffian normal-mode ranks.  These
ranks are local Dirac/Pfaffian data; they are not read from the
automorphic divisor.  The subcertificate constructs neither the global
reduced orientation line nor the Weyl lift, and it is not the full O2 wall
atlas with component, boundary, and overlap compatibility.  It uses no scalar
normalization of \(\Delta_5\), no factor \(64\), and no OP/DT scalar sign.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Local obstruction certificate for \textup{(O2)}]
\label{prop:o2-local-obstruction-certificate}
Fix one of the three simple type-II roots
\(\delta\in\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}\).  A geometric proof of the
rank-one Pfaffian model at \(\Hpl_\delta\) is not a consequence of
\((\delta,\delta)=2\), of the automorphic divisor order, or of the Maass
character.  In the reduced compact Hall framework it must supply the
following local deformation-obstruction calculation.

\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(L1)}] Let \(x_\delta=[\mathcal C_\delta]\) be a generic
wall object.  An \(s_\delta\)-equivariant real analytic
d-critical/Kuranishi chart
\[
(U_\delta,x_\delta,u_\delta,K^{\mathrm{red}}_\delta)
\longrightarrow \mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C_\delta}
\]
is supplied, where
\(K^{\mathrm{red}}_\delta\) is the real form of the cosection-reduced
self-Ext complex
\[
\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C_\delta,\mathcal C_\delta)
\]
in that chart, the wall is exactly \(U_\delta\cap\{u_\delta=0\}\), and
\[
s_\delta(u_\delta)=-u_\delta,\qquad
T_{x_\delta}(U_\delta\cap\Hpl_\delta)=T_{x_\delta}U_\delta^{s_\delta}.
\]
\item[\textup{(L2)}] A splitting in the \(s_\delta\)-equivariant derived
category
\[
K^{\mathrm{red}}_\delta
\simeq K^{\mathrm{tan}}_\delta\oplus K^{\mathrm{nor}}_\delta
\]
whose tangent factor carries the wall tangent determinant and whose normal
factor is the anti-invariant normal determinant factor.  Equivalently, the
extension class
\[
\eta_\delta\in
\operatorname{Ext}^1_{D^{s_\delta}(U_\delta)}
(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_\delta,K^{\mathrm{tan}}_\delta)
\]
vanishes after the reduced \(E\)-quotient and the chosen quotient
orientation trivializations are imposed.
\item[\textup{(L3)}] In an oriented trivialization of the normal Pfaffian
line,
\[
\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_\delta)
=\upsilon_\delta\,u_\delta^{N_\delta^{\mathrm{Pf}}},
\qquad
\upsilon_\delta(x_\delta)\ne0,\qquad
s_\delta(\upsilon_\delta)=\upsilon_\delta,
\]
and \(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_\delta\) is oriented quasi-isomorphic to
\[
\bigoplus_{j=1}^{N_\delta^{\mathrm{Pf}}}
\bigl[\mathbb R\xrightarrow{\,u_\delta\,}\mathbb R\bigr].
\]
The rank-one assertion used in \textup{(O2)} is the further equality
\[
N_\delta^{\mathrm{Pf}}=1.
\]
\end{enumerate}

If \textup{(L1)}--\textup{(L3)} hold, then the local Hall/Pfaffian sign is
\[
s_\delta^*\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_\delta)
=(-1)^{N_\delta^{\mathrm{Pf}}}
\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_\delta),
\]
while the squared determinant section is fixed.  If the unit
\(\upsilon_\delta\) has a nontrivial reflection character, that character
multiplies the displayed sign and belongs to the orientation-transport
datum \(\textup{(O1)}^+\).  If the splitting obstruction
\(\eta_\delta\) does not vanish, the tangent and normal determinants cannot
be separated and no rank-one normal sign has been computed.  If
\(N_\delta^{\mathrm{Pf}}\ne1\), the order-one automorphic divisor is at
best a target check and the local Hall model required by \textup{(O2)} is
false or incomplete.  Thus the exact missing inputs are the three charts,
the three reduced self-Ext complexes, the three equivariant splittings, the
three invariant Pfaffian units, and the three rank computations
\(N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}=1\).  In any compact source claim these
local data must also come from the same finite hybrid correspondence
system that supplies the positive elliptic-degree sector; this is the
compatibility obstruction of
Proposition~\ref{prop:o2-hybrid-compatibility-obstruction}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional finite type-II local-sign computation]
\label{thm:stable-finite-type-ii-local-theorem}
Fix a finite HN height \(R\) and a simple type-II wall
\(\Hpl_{\delta_i}\), \(i\in\{1,2,3\}\).  The following is a conditional
local-sign computation: it applies only after the residual tuple below
has been trivialized.  A finite geometric computation of the generic
local sign required by \textup{(O2)} at this wall is the vanishing of the
residual
\[
\mathfrak O^{\mathrm{O2}}_{\delta_i,R}
=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{chart}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{wall}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{split}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{unit}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rank}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{\delta_i,R'R}
\right)
\]
for every \(R'\ge R\).  These entries mean, respectively:
existence of a wall object and \(s_{\delta_i}\)-equivariant real
d-critical chart; equality of the fixed tangent with the wall tangent and
anti-invariance \(s_{\delta_i}(u_{\delta_i,R})=-u_{\delta_i,R}\);
vanishing of the tangent/normal extension class; invariance of the normal
Pfaffian unit after quotient orientation trivialization; the rank-one
normal quasi-isomorphism
\[
K^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R}
\simeq
\bigl[\mathbb R\xrightarrow{\,u_{\delta_i,R}\,}\mathbb R\bigr];
\]
and compatibility of these choices under the HN transition
\(R'\to R\).

If \(\mathfrak O^{\mathrm{O2}}_{\delta_i,R}=0\), then in the reduced chart
\[
\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R})
=\upsilon_{\delta_i,R}u_{\delta_i,R},
\qquad
s_{\delta_i}(\upsilon_{\delta_i,R})=\upsilon_{\delta_i,R},
\]
and therefore
\[
s_{\delta_i}^*\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R})
=-\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R}),\qquad
s_{\delta_i}^*\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R})^{2}
=\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R})^{2}.
\]
Vanishing of these residuals for \(i=1,2,3\) gives the three finite
generic type-II local-sign subcertificates at height \(R\), and the computed local
wall-chart signs are
\[
\varepsilon^{\mathrm{loc}}_{\delta_i,R}=-1,\qquad i=1,2,3.
\]
The theorem computes only the sign from the local chart after the residuals
vanish.  It does not construct the wall charts, the reduced self-Ext
complexes, the splittings, the quotient orientation trivializations, or
the transition null-homotopies, and no global character is defined by
this theorem.  The full O2 wall-atlas certificate also requires the
component, boundary, and overlap data of
Proposition~\ref{prop:o2-hybrid-compatibility-obstruction}.  If, in
addition, (O1) descends the reduced orientation and
(O1)\(^+\) supplies an honest HN-compatible Weyl action on the quotient
orientation, these local signs induce the global values
\(\epsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})=-1\).  The automorphic divisor order
\(d_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{aut}}=1\) is only the target check recorded in
Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The vanishing of
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{chart}}_{\delta_i,R}\) and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{wall}}_{\delta_i,R}\) gives the local coordinate
\(u_{\delta_i,R}\) and the reflection rule
\(s_{\delta_i}(u_{\delta_i,R})=-u_{\delta_i,R}\).  The splitting residual
separates the tangent determinant from the anti-invariant normal
determinant.  The unit residual removes an extra reflection character from
the normal Pfaffian unit.  The rank residual identifies the normal factor
with one odd rank-one crossing.  Hence the normal Pfaffian is
\(\upsilon_{\delta_i,R}u_{\delta_i,R}\), and reflection multiplies it by
\(-1\).  Squaring removes this sign.  The transition residual says that
the same computation survives restriction from \(R'\) to \(R\).
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional Dirac--Pfaffian normalization and
orientation character]
\label{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}
Suppose the following data items are granted on the reduced compact
critical Hall/CoHA sector of \(X=K3\times E\) of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.

\smallskip
\textup{(D0)} \emph{Compact first-order certificate.}  A finite-stage
first-order \(D_0\)-certificate in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate} is supplied.  Thus, for
every \(R\) in the chosen cofinal HN subsystem, the datum contains a
finite Hall/factorization stage \(D_{0,R}\) on the finite support
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\), a finite target test window
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\), successor transition maps whose composites
give the smaller-stage maps, source/observable comparison maps, and a
vanishing stage residual tuple \(\mathfrak O_{D_0,R}\).  Only after these
finite data, transition cocycles, and support/parity residuals vanish may
one form the
HN-completed state object.  The completed object is part of the supplied
certificate: it carries its charge completion by \(\widehat\Gamma_X\), a
source observable shadow on \(\operatorname{Ran}^{\mathrm{hyb}}(E)\), a
protected first-order operator/algebra \(\mathfrak D_X\), a Pfaffian line
with normalized section, and a \(\Theta_\Pi\)-corrected descent whose
primitive algebra is \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded with signed
superdimensions
\[
\sdim P^\Pi_{X,(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l)
\qquad ((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}).
\]
This is an assumption of the theorem.  The proved lattice part is the
normal-ordered homomorphism \(\overline\Pi_X\); the imported target part is
the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator algebra; the compact
state-side construction remains open unless the finite stages, transition
maps, source/observable comparison, and residual trivializations of
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate} are supplied.

\smallskip
\textup{(O1)} \emph{Strong multiplicative reduced orientation datum.}
There exists a Joyce--Upmeier-type orientation line \cite{JoyceUpmeier}
$$
o_{\mathcal C}\in\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak M^{or}_X),\qquad
o_{\mathcal C}^{\otimes 2}\;\simeq\;
\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C),
$$
in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}, satisfying
$$
o_{\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'}
\;\simeq\;
o_{\mathcal C}\otimes o_{\mathcal C'}
\quad\text{compatibly with the reduced extension correspondences},
$$
and equipped with the quotient-descent package for the reduced
\(E\)-quotient.  The Weyl-equivariant lift is a separate additional
datum, isolated in (O1)\(^+\), and is transported by Gram-projection
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\).
Here descent under the reduced \(E\)-quotient is part of the datum and
means the simultaneous vanishing, on every stratum used by the Hall
correspondences, of
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
\in H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2),
\qquad
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C}
=a_1(\mathcal C)u_1+a_2(\mathcal C)u_2
\in H^2(BE;\mathbb F_2),
\]
and of the finite-stabilizer classes
\[
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}\in H^2(BE[N];\mathbb F_2).
\]
The displayed finite-stabilizer groups are the point-stabilizer
restrictions of the actual Borel equivariant obstruction classes.  For a
finite-stabilizer stratum \(S\) with stabilizer \(E[N]\), the primary
class is
\[
\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{R,S}
\in H^2_{E[N]}(S;\mathbb F_2).
\]
A point-stabilizer calculation closes (O1) only after the mixed Borel
terms, the stabilizer action on \(H^\bullet(S;\mathbb F_2)\), and the
spectral-sequence differentials on the corresponding stratum are shown to
vanish.  These are degree-two gerbe obstruction classes.  Their vanishing
is not the same datum as a trivial finite-stabilizer action on an already
linearized line.  After the degree-two class has been null-trivialized,
the residual choices of finite-stabilizer linearization form an
\(H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)\)-torsor; the trivial quotient orientation
requires the zero point of this torsor.  This \(H^1\)-choice is part of
the quotient-orientation package transported in (O1)\(^+\).  Thus (O1)
is not merely an ordinary Picard-line assertion: it consists of an
ordinary square root in \(\operatorname{Pic}\), null-trivializations of
the reduced and equivariant degree-two gerbes, and an equivariant line
whose finite-stabilizer degree-one characters
\[
\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E,N}\in H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)
\]
are all chosen to be zero after the corresponding gerbes have vanished.
On finite compact/wrapped HN stages this is precisely the
quotient-orientation character system of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-stage-quotient-orientation-character-system}.
For \(N=2\), with \(E[2]=\langle e_1,e_2\rangle\) and
\(e_3=e_1+e_2\), this is the Klein-four condition
\[
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}
=b_{20}x_1^2+b_{11}x_1x_2+b_{02}x_2^2,\qquad
(b_{20},b_{11},b_{02})
=(r_1,r_1+r_2+r_3,r_2),
\]
where
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\langle e_i\rangle}
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=r_i\tau_i^2 .
\]
If this class vanishes, an \(E[2]\)-linearization still has character
\[
\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}
=\lambda_1x_1+\lambda_2x_2\in H^1(BE[2];\mathbb F_2),
\]
with cyclic restrictions
\[
\rho_1=\lambda_1,\qquad
\rho_2=\lambda_2,\qquad
\rho_3=\lambda_1+\lambda_2.
\]
Trivial \(E[2]\)-linearization means \(\rho_1=\rho_2=\rho_3=0\).
The bits \(r_i\) live in degree two; the bits \(\rho_i\) live in degree
one.
For even \(N\) with \(2^a\parallel N\), the mod-\(2\) residual is a
class on the two-primary stabilizer
\[
E[N]_{(2)}\simeq(\Z/2^a)^2.
\]
The case \(a=1\) is the displayed Klein-four calculation.  For
\(a\ge2\),
\[
H^*\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
=\Lambda(x_1,x_2)\otimes\mathbb F_2[y_1,y_2],
\qquad |x_i|=1,\quad |y_i|=2,\quad x_i^2=0,
\]
and hence
\[
H^2\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
=\mathbb F_2\langle y_1,x_1x_2,y_2\rangle.
\]
Writing
\[
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_1^{(N)}y_1+A_{12}^{(N)}x_1x_2+A_2^{(N)}y_2,
\]
the order-two cyclic restrictions see
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\langle h_1\rangle}\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_1^{(N)}\tau_1^2,\quad
\operatorname{res}_{\langle h_2\rangle}\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_2^{(N)}\tau_2^2,\quad
\operatorname{res}_{\langle h_3\rangle}\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=(A_1^{(N)}+A_2^{(N)})\tau_3^2,
\]
where \(h_i=2^{a-1}g_i\) for a basis \(g_1,g_2\) of
\((\Z/2^a)^2\) and \(h_3=h_1+h_2\).  The coefficient
\(A_{12}^{(N)}\) is invisible to these cyclic order-two restrictions.
Thus the \(E[2]\) vector \((r_1,r_2,r_3)\) detects only the
two-torsion residual; it is not a computation of
\(\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}\) for even \(N\ge4\).
For \(a\ge2\), even after
\(\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}=0\), the remaining two-primary
linearization choices form
\[
H^1\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
=\mathbb F_2\langle x_1,x_2\rangle,
\]
and the trivial linearization requires that character to vanish on the
chosen two-primary generators.
Invariance of the underlying line under translations of \(E\) is not a
substitute for these quotient-linearization data.

\smallskip
\textup{(O1)\(^+\)} \emph{Weyl-equivariant determinant-line transport.}
The orientation line of (O1) is equipped with coherent lifts of the three
type-II wall transports
\[
\tau_i:o_{\mathcal C}\longrightarrow s_{\delta_i}^{*}o_{\mathcal C},
\qquad i=1,2,3,
\]
but the word ``coherent'' is load-bearing.  At finite height \(R\), the
first object is the finite partial action groupoid
\(\mathcal G_R\) whose objects are retained oriented quotient strata and
whose arrows are the retained type-II wall transports.  A choice of
determinant-line lifts gives
\[
c_{o,R}\in Z^2(\mathcal G_R;\underline{\mathbb F}_2).
\]
The finite obstruction is
\([c_{o,R}]\in H^2(\mathcal G_R;\underline{\mathbb F}_2)\), together
with the quotient-torsor defects.  Only on a complete
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\)-orbit with constant coefficients does this
reduce to the group cohomology class below.  A choice of lifts over words
in the simple reflections is then first only a projective
determinant-line action: for \(w,w'\in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) one has
a composition defect
\[
w'^*\tau_w\circ \tau_{w'}=(-1)^{c_o(w,w')}\tau_{ww'},
\qquad
c_o\in Z^2\!\left(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II});\mathbb F_2\right).
\]
Its class
\[
[c_o]\in H^2\!\left(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II});\mathbb F_2\right)
\]
is the Weyl determinant-line cocycle obstruction.  The datum (O1)\(^+\)
requires \([c_o]=0\), a choice of \(1\)-cochain killing \(c_o\), and
normalization \(\tau_i^2=1\) for \(i=1,2,3\).  Only then do the lifts
satisfy the Coxeter presentation of \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\), or
equivalently give an honest action on the oriented Pfaffian line over
the wall-complement of the reduced compact Hall sector.  This is a
geometric determinant-line monodromy datum.  It does not include a scalar
formula;
\(\tau_i\) must also transport the quotient-orientation package
\[
\mathfrak q_{\mathcal C}:=
\left(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C},
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C},
\{(\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C},
\lambda^{E,N}_{\mathcal C})\}_{N\ge2}\right)
\]
and the chosen trivializations of these classes between the charge strata
lying over Weyl-related Gram degrees.  Equivalently, after the
degree-two classes in \(\mathfrak q_{\mathcal C}\) vanish and the zero
finite characters \(\lambda^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}=0\) are selected, choose
null-trivializations
\[
\theta_{\mathcal C}=
\left(\theta^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C},
\theta^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C},
\{\theta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}\}_{N\ge2}\right).
\]
For finite stabilizers \(\theta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}\) includes the
null-trivialization of the finite Borel class and, after the mixed Borel
terms and differentials vanish, its point-stabilizer restriction
\(\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}\in H^2(BE[N])\), together with the choice of
the zero \(H^1(BE[N])\)-linearization character.
For a simple type-II reflection \(s_{\delta_i}\), the failure of
\(\tau_i\) to preserve the quotient trivialization is the torsor
difference
\[
\omega_{i,\mathcal C}
\in
H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{s_{\delta_i}\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\oplus
\bigoplus_{N\ge2}H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2).
\]
Here \(s_{\delta_i}\mathcal C\) denotes the chosen target stratum over
the Weyl-reflected Gram degree.  The connected \(BE\)-linearization
contributes no \(H^1\)-term because \(H^1(BE;\mathbb F_2)=0\).  The datum
(O1)\(^+\) includes the vanishing of all \(\omega_{i,\mathcal C}\) and
the Coxeter coherence of the resulting transports.  Without this
compatibility the reflection sign is a sign of an ordinary square-root
line, not a sign on the reduced \(E\)-quotient Hall sector.  The passage
from three generator
signs to a character is then the pure
group-theoretic Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle},
after the projective and quotient-torsor obstruction package of
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-quotient-orientation-obstruction} has vanished.
At finite HN height this is the cocycle system of
Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-stage-weyl-cocycle-character-system}; the
global datum is the compatible cofinal inverse system of those splittings.

\smallskip
\textup{(O2)} \emph{Pfaffian local model and wall atlas on type-II
walls.}  The finite generic local-sign subcertificate of
Definition~\ref{def:type-ii-pfaffian-wall-certificate} is supplied.
Proposition~\ref{prop:o2-local-obstruction-certificate} records the
geometric computation required to remove this hypothesis.  The
local wall-chart signs which feed the geometric reflection character
$$
\epsilon_o:W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\longrightarrow\{\pm1\}
$$
of Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character} are computed
from local Pfaffian normal forms at generic points of the type-II walls
\(\Hpl_\delta\).  Namely, the reduced determinant complex is assumed to
split, after removing the tangent determinant factor, as
\[
K_{\delta}^{\mathrm{nor}}
\simeq
\bigoplus_{j=1}^{N_\delta^{\mathrm{Pf}}}\bigl[\mathbb R\xrightarrow{\,u_\delta\,}
\mathbb R\bigr],
\]
where \(u_\delta\) is a real local equation of the wall,
\(s_\delta(u_\delta)=-u_\delta\), and the Pfaffian section is
\(u_\delta^{N_\delta^{\mathrm{Pf}}}\) times a unit.  For the three simple type-II walls
the supplied normal-mode model has
\[
N_{\delta_1}^{\mathrm{Pf}}=N_{\delta_2}^{\mathrm{Pf}}
=N_{\delta_3}^{\mathrm{Pf}}=1 .
\]
This local normal form is part of the hypothesis.  The Borcherds divisor
order and the Maass character give an independent automorphic target
check after the local model is supplied; they do not construct the Hall
orientation line and do not use scalar normalization.
For the global orientation-character conclusion below, \textup{(O2)} also
includes the component, boundary, overlap, quotient, and protected
integration compatibility package of
Proposition~\ref{prop:o2-hybrid-compatibility-obstruction}; the generic
wall sign by itself is not a global Weyl-transport datum.

\smallskip
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] (\emph{Pfaffian normalization.})  After the supplied
Pfaffian-to-automorphic comparison
$$
\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}:\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},X}\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5},
$$
compatible with cusp trivialization and squaring, the supplied first-order
object has protected Pfaffian equal to the theta-normalized Borcherds
determinant:
$$
\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X))
\;=\;\mathcal D_X\;=\;\Delta_5.
$$
Without \(\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}\), this is only equality of normalized
formal Borcherds products at \(\mathfrak c_\infty\).
Its scalar trace, in the OP normalization of
Definition~\ref{def:op-normalization-branch}, satisfies
$$
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{prot}}\bigl((-1)^F\,\mathfrak D_X^{-2}\bigr)
\;=\;-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}.
$$
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (\emph{Three-sign identification and Weyl character.})  For the three
type-II simple reflections \(\delta_i\) of the Weyl chamber
\(\Poly_{II}\) of Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}
(notation \(\delta_1=2f_2-f_3\), \(\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3\),
\(\delta_3=f_3\)),
$$
\epsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})\;=\;-1\;=\;\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i}),
\qquad i=1,2,3,
$$
and therefore
$$
\epsilon_o\big|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}
\;=\;\nu_{\Delta_5}\big|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}.
$$
The three \(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3\) chamber-permuting reflections
\(s_{f_{-2}-f_2},s_{f_2-f_3},s_{f_2+f_3}\) have automorphic Maass value
\(+1\), but no Hall orientation sign on them is asserted unless the
oriented Hall action is separately extended from
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) to the semidirect product
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II})\).
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (\emph{Categorical refinement.})  Under
\textup{(D0)}, \textup{(O1)}, \textup{(O1)}\(^+\), and \textup{(O2)},
the supplied chiral protected first-order theory refines the virtual
\(K_0\)-determinant package \([\mathcal V]\), \(\mathcal D_X\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root}.  Its
decategorification is the Borcherds product
$$
\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}\bigl(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\bigr)
\big|_{\mathfrak c_\infty}
=64\,q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\!\!\!\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}\!\!
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}=\Delta_5,
$$
and its orientation monodromy character is the Maass character
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) restricted to \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\(D_0\) has the status split of
Theorem~\ref{thm:first-order-d0-certificate}: the normal-ordered lattice
part is proved and the denominator target is imported, but the compact
finite stages, transition maps, and obstruction trivializations of \(D_0\)
are open on the reduced \(K3\times E\) sector.  The orientation clauses
(O1), (O1)\(^+\), and (O2) are likewise
open on that sector;
on Calabi--Yau threefolds (O1) is Joyce--Song \cite{JoyceSong},
the multiplicative orientation cocycle on
\(\mathrm{Perf}(X)\) is Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} and
Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, on Calabi--Yau
\(4\)-fold analogues the unreduced orientation exists by Borisov--Joyce
\cite{BorisovJoyce}, Cao--Gross--Joyce \cite{CaoGrossJoyce}, and
Bojko's quasi-projective Borisov--Joyce extension \cite{Bojko};
the virtual-cycle constructions of Oh--Thomas \cite{OhThomasI},
\cite{OhThomasII} and rank-one
Pin\(^c\)-orientation sign conventions in DT/PT Hilbert-scheme models
are compatible with the BBDJS/Joyce--Upmeier framework and with the
Cao--Kool--Monavari Calabi--Yau \(4\)-fold orientation package
\cite{CaoKoolMonavari}; non-compact and Joyce--Song extensions are
Bojko \cite{Bojko}.  These sources supply the orientation technology and
partial local inputs.  They do not by themselves prove the
cosection-reduced \(K3\times E\) quotient orientation, its
\(E[2]\)-linearization, or its type-II Weyl-equivariant lift.  The
cosection-induced
parity flip
\(\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{red}}=\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{std}}+1\) of the
Maulik--Toda / Oberdieck reduced obstruction theory
\cite{MaulikTodaGV,OberdieckReducedPT} is absorbed into
(O1) as a \(\mathbb Z/2\)-grading shift
\(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=o^{\mathrm{std}}_{\mathcal C}\otimes\Pi\)
of the BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} line under cosection contraction of
the PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form by
\(\sigma_{K3}\) (clause (P4) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}).  This parity
shift is part of the reduced orientation datum and may be compatible
with the fermionic grading used in the protected supertrace.  It is not
the source of the OP scalar minus sign and it does not determine the
Hall reflection character.  The latter must be computed from monodromy
of the orientation line around the type-II walls.  The theorem therefore
has certificate form: granted \textup{(D0)}, \textup{(O1)},
\textup{(O1)}\(^+\), and \textup{(O2)}, the normalization and character
follow.

\begin{proof}[Proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}]

\emph{Step 1 (Pfaffian product from the supplied first-order datum).}
By \textup{(D0)}, the compact first-order object \(\mathfrak D_X\) and
its normal-ordered primitive multiplicities are supplied.  By
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}, the orientation line of a stable
charge-\(c\) object satisfies
\(o_{\mathcal C}^{\otimes 2}\simeq
\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\).  The hypothesis (O1)
promotes this to an extension-multiplicative system: on every direct sum
\(\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'\),
\(o_{\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'}\simeq
o_{\mathcal C}\otimes o_{\mathcal C'}\), compatibly with the Hall
extension stack and descended under the reduced \(E\)-quotient.  Thus
the supplied \(\mathfrak D_X\) has a protected Pfaffian product whose
exponent in normal-ordered Gram degree \((n,l,m)\), by the supplied
\(D_0\) signed-superdimension residual, is
\[
\sdim P^\Pi_{X,(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l).
\]
With the leading cusp normalization fixed by the theta coefficient,
the graded product is
$$
\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)
=v_0\,\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)
\quad\text{with}\quad v_0=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2},
$$
where \(\sdet\) is the superdeterminant of
Proposition~\ref{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root}.  The theorem
does not construct \(\mathfrak D_X\); it identifies the Pfaffian of a
supplied object satisfying \textup{(D0)} and \textup{(O1)}.

\emph{Step 2 (Comparison with the automorphic section).}
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification} identifies
\(v_0\,\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)\) with the Igusa cusp form \(\Delta_5\) at
the level of Fourier coefficients.  To state an equality of sections,
the supplied \(D_0\)-Pfaffian datum must also contain an isomorphism
\[
\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}:
\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},X}\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5}
\]
compatible with the cusp trivialization and with squaring to
  \(\mathcal L^{10}\).  Under this supplied comparison,
\(\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}(\operatorname{pf}_X)\) and \(\Delta_5\) have the
same Borcherds expansion at \(\mathfrak c_\infty\), hence are equal.
By the \(q\)-expansion principle for holomorphic genus-two Siegel modular
forms with Maass character, after the supplied line comparison and cusp
trivialization, equality of this cusp expansion gives equality of
sections.
Without \(\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}\), the conclusion is only equality of
normalized formal products.

\emph{Step 3 (Scalar square in OP normalization).}
Squaring forgets the orientation.  Under
\(\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}^{\otimes2}\),
\[
\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}^{\otimes2}
\bigl(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)^2\bigr)
=\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)|_{\mathrm{tot}}
=\Delta_5^2,
\]
as sections of \(\mathcal L^{10}\) (the squared automorphic line is the
trivially-charactered determinant, since
\(\Delta_5^2=\Delta_{10}\) is scalar by
Section~\textup{The normalized cusp form}).
The protected scalar trace is then
\(\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{prot}}((-1)^F\mathfrak D_X^{-2})
=C_{\square,X}\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) for
some normalization scalar \(C_{\square,X}\); the explicit
\(C_{\square,X}=-4096\) follows
from Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization} of Oberdieck--Pixton, which
gives
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\),
together with the arithmetic \(-4096=-(64)^2\) of the squared
theta-leading coefficient and the OP scalar sign convention recorded in
Definition~\ref{def:op-normalization-branch}.

\emph{Step 4 (Orientation-character identity (ii)).}  By (O2), after the
full wall-atlas compatibility package has been supplied, each
type-II simple reflection \(s_{\delta_i}\) acts on
\(o_{\mathcal C}\) by the parity of its oriented real normal modes.
Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation} is the Hall-side local
calculation: under the supplied Pfaffian normal form
\(N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}=1\), hence
\(\epsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})=(-1)^{N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}}=-1\).
Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction} is the independent
automorphic calculation:
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1\) for the same three simple
reflections, and \(+1\) on the three chamber-permuting
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)-reflections.  The latter \(+1\)-values are
automorphic target data only; they are not Hall orientation signs unless
a semidirect-product Hall lift is supplied.

The passage from the three simple Hall signs to a character on the full
type-II Weyl group is purely group-theoretic only after (O1)\(^+\) has
killed the projective determinant-line cocycle and the quotient
trivialization torsors of
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-quotient-orientation-obstruction}.  Then (O1)\(^+\)
gives an honest lifted Coxeter action on the reduced quotient
orientation.  By
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle},
\[
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})_{\mathrm{ab}}\simeq(\Z/2)^3,
\]
with one generator for each \(s_{\delta_i}\).  Therefore two
\(\{\pm1\}\)-valued characters of \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) that agree
on \(s_{\delta_1},s_{\delta_2},s_{\delta_3}\) agree everywhere.  Hence
\(\epsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).

\emph{Step 5 (Categorical refinement (iii)).}  The chiral protected
theory is supplied by \textup{(D0)}.  Steps 1--4 identify its
decategorification and character: the class
\([\mathcal V]\in K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}})\) is the
decategorified primitive content, the formal product
\(v_0\,\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)\) is the Pfaffian section
\(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\), and the formal
character equality is the orientation-character identity of (ii).  At
the chosen isotropic cusp \(\mathfrak c_\infty\) this decategorification
is the Borcherds product, and the orientation monodromy character is
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on the type-II Weyl group as computed.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Conditional Pfaffian signs on the type-II simple walls]
\label{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation}
Under the compact first-order certificate (D0), the strong orientation
datum (O1), the Weyl-equivariant extension (O1)\(^+\), and the
Pfaffian local model (O2) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}, for each
\(\delta_i\in\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}\) the
orientation-monodromy reflection sign is
$$
\epsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})\;=\;(-1)^{N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}}\;=\;-1,
\qquad N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}=1.
$$
Here \(N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}\) is the number of supplied odd real
normal modes in the local Pfaffian normal form.  It is not the
automorphic divisor order, although the independent target order agrees
in the three simple type-II cases.  The lemma makes no Hall-orientation
claim for the three chamber-permuting reflections in
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Local Pfaffian calculation.}  Hypothesis (O2) supplies, at a
generic point of each \(\Hpl_{\delta_i}\), a real local equation
\(u_i=u_{\delta_i}\) with \(s_{\delta_i}(u_i)=-u_i\) and a normal
determinant-complex splitting
\[
K_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{nor}}
\simeq
\bigl[\mathbb R\xrightarrow{\,u_i\,}\mathbb R\bigr].
\]
The normal Pfaffian section is \(u_i\) times an invariant unit after
quotient-orientation trivialization.  Transport by the reflection sends
\(u_i\) to \(-u_i\), so it multiplies the Pfaffian line by \(-1\); after
squaring, the determinant section \(u_i^2\) is fixed.
Hence one supplied odd real normal mode gives
\[
\epsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})
=(-1)^{N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}}=(-1)^1=-1,
\qquad i=1,2,3.
\]

\emph{Independent automorphic target labels.}  The three roots
\(\delta_1=2f_2-f_3\), \(\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3\), \(\delta_3=f_3\) have
Gram pairing
\((\delta_i,\delta_i)=2\), \((\delta_i,\delta_j)=-2\) for \(i\ne j\),
by the matrix displayed in
Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}.  All three are
real simple roots of the Lorentzian Kac--Moody algebra \(\autcor\).  In
the Gram-index
chart of Definition~\ref{def:gram-index-degrees-weyl-chamber} (using
\(\alpha(\gamma)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}\)), the three simple walls
correspond to the lattice triples
$$
\delta_1\;\leftrightarrow\;(n,l,m)=(1,1,0),\qquad
\delta_2\;\leftrightarrow\;(0,1,1),\qquad
\delta_3\;\leftrightarrow\;(0,-1,0),
$$
matching the K3 elliptic-genus support
\(f(0,\pm1)=1\), \(f(0,0)=10\), \(f(nm,l)=0\) for \(4nm-l^2<-1\).
Thus the automorphic divisor order
\[
d_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{aut}}
:=\ord_{\Hpl_{\delta_i}}(\Delta_5)
\]
is \(1\) for \(i=1,2,3\).  This target order is a check against the
supplied local model; it is not a construction of the compact Hall
orientation line.

The computation is:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.16\textwidth}p{0.31\textwidth}p{0.13\textwidth}p{0.13\textwidth}p{0.12\textwidth}}
\hline
\(\delta_i\) & Gram label & \(N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}\) &
\(d_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{aut}}\) & \(\epsilon_o\) \\
\hline
\(\delta_1=2f_2-f_3\) &
\((n,l,m)=(1,1,0)\), \(f(0,1)=1\) & \(1\) & \(1\) & \(-1\) \\
\(\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3\) &
\((n,l,m)=(0,1,1)\), \(f(0,1)=1\) & \(1\) & \(1\) & \(-1\) \\
\(\delta_3=f_3\) &
\((n,l,m)=(0,-1,0)\), \(f(0,-1)=1\) & \(1\) & \(1\) & \(-1\) \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Automorphic target check via the Maass character]
The argument below verifies the target character
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}\) using only the Maass
multiplier and the Borcherds product.  It does not construct the Hall
orientation character \(\epsilon_o\).  The comparison
\(\epsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) remains a geometric statement supplied
by (O1), (O1)\(^+\), and (O2).  No scalar normalization enters this
sign comparison: replacing \(\Delta_5\) by \(c\Delta_5\),
\(c\in\mathbb C^\times\), changes neither the Maass character nor the
divisor orders.  The factor \(64\) only names the monic Borcherds product
\(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\), and the OP/DT scalar \(-4096\) is unused.

\emph{Step 1 (Maass-side coboundary).}  Define the automorphic parity
cochain
\(\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}\colon
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\to\Z/2\) by
\(\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(g):=\tfrac12(1-\nu_{\Delta_5}(g))\),
so
\((-1)^{\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(g)}=\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\).
Maass's character is a homomorphism \cite{MAASS:1},
\cite[Section 3]{GN}, \cite{Gritsenko99}, hence
$$
c_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(g,h)
:=\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(g)
+\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(h)
-\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(gh)
\equiv0\pmod2.
$$
The displayed value of \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on the six generators is
Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction}: \(-1\) on
\(s_{\delta_1},s_{\delta_2},s_{\delta_3}\), \(+1\) on
\(s_{f_{-2}-f_2},s_{f_2-f_3},s_{f_2+f_3}\); equivalently
\(\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(s_{\delta_i})=1\) and
\(\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(s_{f_{-2}-f_2})
=\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(s_{f_2-f_3})
=\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(s_{f_2+f_3})=0\).

\emph{Step 2 (Verification on the nine pairs of three-wall generators).}
For the three-wall computation the only nontrivial check is on the
\(3\times3\) table of pairs \((g,h)\in\{s_{\delta_1},s_{\delta_2},
s_{\delta_3}\}^{\times2}\).  The relations used here are only
\(s_{\delta_i}^2=1\) and the fact that \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) is a
character.  For \(i\ne j\) the Coxeter exponent is \(m_{ij}=\infty\), so
there is no braid relation to impose:
\begin{itemize}
\item Diagonal \((g,g)=(s_{\delta_i},s_{\delta_i})\) for \(i=1,2,3\)
(three pairs): \(gh=1\), \(\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(gh)=0\),
so \(c_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(g,h)=1+1-0=2\equiv0\pmod2\).
\item Off-diagonal \((g,h)=(s_{\delta_i},s_{\delta_j})\), \(i\ne j\)
(six pairs): since \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) is a character,
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}(gh)=(-1)(-1)=+1\), giving
\(\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(gh)=0\) and
\(c_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}(g,h)=1+1-0=2\equiv0\pmod2\).
\end{itemize}
All nine pairs vanish modulo \(2\); \(c_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}\) is a
coboundary on the three-wall block, with primitive
\(\varepsilon_{\Delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}\).  This is an automorphic
calculation only.

\emph{Step 3 (Divisor-exponent target check).}  The Gritsenko--Nikulin
specialization of Borcherds' product theorem \cite{Borcherds95},
\cite[Theorem~2.1, (2.1)--(2.3), Example~2.4]{GNII}, together with the
theta normalization \cite[Theorem~4.1]{GN}, writes
$$
D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5
=\operatorname{Borch}(\phi_{0,1})
=q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\!\!
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}^+}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
$$
in the type-II cusp polarization
\((q,r,s)=(e^{2\pi iz_1},e^{2\pi iz_2},e^{2\pi iz_3})\).  This fixes the
automorphic divisor orders
\[
d_{\delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}:=\ord_{\Hpl_\delta}(\Delta_5).
\]
For the three type-II roots these orders are
\[
d_{\delta_1}^{\mathrm{aut}}=f(0,1)=1,\qquad
d_{\delta_2}^{\mathrm{aut}}=f(0,1)=1,\qquad
d_{\delta_3}^{\mathrm{aut}}=f(0,-1)=1.
\]
Together with Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction}, this gives
the automorphic target signs
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1=(-1)^{d_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{aut}}}\).
The symbol \(d_{\delta}^{\mathrm{aut}}\) is deliberately distinct from
the Pfaffian normal-mode rank \(N_{\delta}^{\mathrm{Pf}}\) in (O2).

The chamber-permuting roots
\[
\alpha_1=f_{-2}-f_2,\qquad
\alpha_2=f_2-f_3,\qquad
\alpha_3=f_2+f_3
\]
are type-I roots in
\(\La^{2,1}\setminus\La^{2,1}_{II}\).  In the type-II parametrization
\(\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}\), the coefficients of \(f_2\) and
\(f_{-2}\) must be even.  Thus \(k=1\) does not contribute to any
\(\alpha_i\).  For \(2\alpha_1\) one obtains either
\((-1,0,1)\) or \((1,0,-1)\), outside
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\).  For \(2j\alpha_2\) one obtains
\((j,2j,0)\), and for \(2j\alpha_3\) one obtains \((j,-2j,0)\);
the \(q^0\)-row of \(\phi_{0,1}\) has support only at
\(l=0,\pm1\), so \(f(0,\pm2j)=0\) for \(j\ge1\)
\cite[\S2.2]{EZ:1}.  Hence
\[
\ord_{\Hpl_{\alpha_i}}(\Delta_5)=0,\qquad i=1,2,3,
\]
and Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction} gives automorphic
monodromy \(+1\) around these chamber-permuting reflections.

\emph{What this check proves.}  It proves the automorphic target values
\[
\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1,\qquad
\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_{-2}-f_2})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2-f_3})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2+f_3})=+1.
\]
It does not prove that a compact Hall orientation line transports with
these signs.  That bridge is exactly the geometric content of the
Pfaffian local model and Weyl-equivariant orientation cocycle.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Comparison of the two proofs]
\label{rem:thm3-cross-verification}
The proof of Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation} and the
Maass-character check have different logical roles.  The first computes
the Hall orientation signs from the supplied Pfaffian local model (O2).
The second computes the automorphic target signs of
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}\).  The equality
\(\epsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) follows only after the local Dirac model
supplies the Pfaffian normal-mode parity and the Weyl-equivariant
orientation cocycle transports it as a character.  The Borcherds product
and Maass character supply the target character but not the Hall
orientation character.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Imaginary roots are not Weyl reflections]
\label{lem:imaginary-wall-orientation-extension}
The Weyl group of the Borcherds--Kac--Moody datum is generated by real
simple roots only.  Imaginary simple roots contribute to the
Weyl--Kac--Borcherds denominator through the additive correction
coefficients \(m(a)\) and \(\tau(a)\) of Gritsenko--Nikulin
\cite[Theorem~2.1, (2.1)--(2.3)]{GNII}, \cite[Sections~3--4]{GN}; they
do not define reflections \(s_a\) in \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).
Thus the orientation character
\[
\epsilon_o:W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\to\{\pm1\}
\]
is a real-root reflection datum.  A compact Hall theory may also have
local divisor monodromy around imaginary components of the Borcherds
divisor, but that monodromy is not a Weyl character and is not asserted
here.  In particular, no formula \(\epsilon_o(s_a)=(-1)^{m(a)}\) is
available for imaginary \(a\), and the coefficients \(m(a)\) must not be
identified with the visible product exponents \(f(nm,l)\) without the
Gritsenko--Nikulin additive-side computation.
\end{remark}
