\begin{lemma}[Pure group-theoretic Weyl sign extension]
\label{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle}
For any signs \(\epsilon_i\in\{\pm1\}\), \(i=1,2,3\), there is a unique
character
\[
\chi_\epsilon:W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\longrightarrow\{\pm1\}
\]
with \(\chi_\epsilon(s_{\delta_i})=\epsilon_i\).  Hence a supplied
Weyl-equivariant determinant-line transport datum (O1)\(^+\), together
with local Pfaffian signs
\(\epsilon_i=(-1)^{N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}}\) from (O2),
induces a unique orientation character.  For
\(N_{\delta_1}^{\mathrm{Pf}}=N_{\delta_2}^{\mathrm{Pf}}
=N_{\delta_3}^{\mathrm{Pf}}=1\), this character is the determinant
character on \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The Cartan matrix of the type-II simple reflections, by
\((\delta_i,\delta_i)=2\) and \((\delta_i,\delta_j)=-2\) for \(i\ne j\)
(Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}), is
\[
\begin{pmatrix}2&-2&-2\\-2&2&-2\\-2&-2&2\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Thus \(A_{ij}A_{ji}=4\) for \(i\ne j\), so the Coxeter exponents are
\(m_{ij}=\infty\).  The chamber calculation in
Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector} identifies
\(\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}\) as the primitive walls of the
fundamental type-II chamber \(\Poly_{II}\), and the Gritsenko--Nikulin
reflection-group input supplies the Coxeter presentation from these
walls.  Hence the type-II reflection group is the universal rank-three
Coxeter group
\[
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})
\simeq
\langle s_{\delta_1},s_{\delta_2},s_{\delta_3}\mid
s_{\delta_1}^2=s_{\delta_2}^2=s_{\delta_3}^2=1\rangle .
\]
Its abelianization is
$$
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\big/[W^{(2)},W^{(2)}]
\;\simeq\;(\Z/2)^3,
$$
one \(\Z/2\) per Coxeter generator \(s_{\delta_i}\).

The only defining relations are \(s_{\delta_i}^2=1\).  Any assignment
\(s_{\delta_i}\mapsto\epsilon_i\in\{\pm1\}\) respects these relations,
since \(\epsilon_i^2=1\), and therefore extends uniquely to a
\(\{\pm1\}\)-valued character, equivalently to a homomorphism factoring
through \((\Z/2)^3\).  This is pure group theory.  Applied to a supplied
determinant-line action from (O1)\(^+\), the scalars computed by (O2) on
the three generators give the orientation character.  If all three
\(\epsilon_i=-1\), the character sends every Coxeter generator to
\(-1\), hence is the determinant character.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Weyl quotient-orientation obstruction package]
\label{lem:weyl-quotient-orientation-obstruction}
Let \(W=W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\), and let
\(\mathcal G_W\) be the action groupoid of the retained reduced quotient
strata under the supplied type-II wall transports.  On a complete
\(W\)-orbit with constant coefficients this groupoid cohomology reduces to
ordinary group cohomology of \(W\).  Suppose (O1) supplies an ordinary
orientation line together with the full reduced quotient package
\[
\theta_{\mathcal C}=
\left(\theta^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C},
\theta^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C},
\{(\theta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C},\lambda^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}=0)\}_{N\ge2}
\right)
\]
on every charge stratum used by the compact/wrapped Hall
correspondences.  A choice of simple wall transports \(\tau_i\) gives an
honest Weyl-equivariant orientation on the reduced quotient if and only
if the following two independent obstructions vanish.

\[
[c_o]=0\in H^2(\mathcal G_W;\underline{\mathbb F}_2)
\]
with a killing groupoid cochain
\(b\in C^1(\mathcal G_W;\underline{\mathbb F}_2)\) for which the
renormalized lifts
\(\widetilde\tau_w=(-1)^{b(w)}\tau_w\) satisfy
\(\widetilde\tau_i^{\,2}=1\) for the three simple reflections; and
\[
\omega_{i,\mathcal C}=0\in
H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{s_{\delta_i}\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\oplus
\bigoplus_{N\ge2}H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)
\]
for every simple reflection and every relevant charge stratum, with the
word defects obeying their natural torsor cocycle law.  Since the
type-II Weyl group has no braid relations among the three simple
reflections, the generator-square constraints are the only Coxeter
relation constraints after the projective cocycle is killed.  Killing
\([c_o]\) gives an action on the ordinary determinant line; killing the
\(\omega_{i,\mathcal C}\) gives an action on the quotient orientation
with its finite-stabilizer zero characters.  Neither condition is
implied by the Maass character \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The chosen transports over words in the generators define a central
\(\{\pm1\}\)-extension of the retained action groupoid precisely when
their composition defect is a \(2\)-cocycle
\[
w'^*\tau_w\circ\tau_{w'}=(-1)^{c_o(w,w')}\tau_{ww'}.
\]
Changing the word lifts by \((-1)^{b(w)}\) replaces \(c_o\) by
\(c_o+\delta b\).  Hence the projective determinant-line action becomes
an honest action on the ordinary orientation line exactly when
\([c_o]\) is zero and the chosen splitting is normalized on the
relations.  By Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle}, the
type-II Coxeter presentation is the free product of three copies of
\(\mathbb Z/2\).  Thus the only relation-level normalizations are
\(\widetilde\tau_i^{\,2}=1\) on a complete \(W\)-orbit; on a truncated
finite system this is the corresponding statement in the retained action
groupoid.

After the ordinary line action is honest, the quotient
null-trivializations form torsors under
\[
H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\oplus\bigoplus_{N\ge2}H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2).
\]
The difference between the transported trivialization and the chosen
trivialization on the reflected stratum is exactly
\(\omega_{i,\mathcal C}\).  Composition of transports gives the usual
torsor cocycle law
\(\omega_{ww',\mathcal C}=w'^*\omega_{w,\mathcal C}+
\omega_{w',\mathcal C}\).  Therefore vanishing on the retained
generators, together with the square coherences already imposed above,
propagates to every word in the retained action groupoid, and to every
word of \(W\) only after a complete orbit has been supplied.  Conversely,
any honest Weyl action on the reduced quotient orientation preserves the
chosen null-trivializations and zero finite characters, so both \(c_o\)
and all \(\omega_{i,\mathcal C}\) vanish after the corresponding choices.
The construction uses only determinant-line and quotient-torsor data, not
the scalar automorphic character.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Finite-stage Weyl cocycle over the quotient character
system]
\label{cor:finite-stage-weyl-cocycle-character-system}
Fix a finite compact/wrapped HN stage \(R\), a finite test set
\(\mathcal O_R\) of reduced charge strata closed under the simple
type-II wall transports retained at height \(R\), and a
quotient-orientation character system on \(\mathcal O_R\) in the sense of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-stage-quotient-orientation-character-system}.
Choose determinant-line lifts \(\tau_{i,R,\mathcal C}\) for the simple
type-II reflections whenever both \(\mathcal C\) and
\(s_{\delta_i}\mathcal C\) lie in \(\mathcal O_R\).  For words whose
intermediate strata remain in \(\mathcal O_R\), choose word lifts
\(\tau_{w,R,\mathcal C}\) and define
\[
w'^*\tau_{w,R,w'\mathcal C}\circ \tau_{w',R,\mathcal C}
=(-1)^{c_{o,R}(w,w';\mathcal C)}
\tau_{ww',R,\mathcal C}.
\]
Then \(c_{o,R}\) is a \(2\)-cocycle for the finite action groupoid
generated by these retained transports; on any genuine \(W\)-orbit it is
the corresponding group \(2\)-cocycle with values in locally constant
\(\mathbb F_2\)-functions on \(\mathcal O_R\).  Changing the word lifts by
a \(1\)-cochain changes \(c_{o,R}\) by a coboundary.  The
quotient-trivialization defect
\[
\omega_{w,R,\mathcal C}
\in
H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{w\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\oplus\bigoplus_{N\ge2}H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)
\]
satisfies
\[
\omega_{ww',R,\mathcal C}
=w'^*\omega_{w,R,\mathcal C}+\omega_{w',R,\mathcal C}.
\]
Thus the finite-stage Weyl lift exists on \(\mathcal O_R\) if and only
if \(c_{o,R}\) is killed by a cochain normalized on the relations
\(s_{\delta_i}^2=1\), and the defects \(\omega_{i,R,\mathcal C}\) vanish
for the three simple reflections.  A cofinal family of such finite-stage
splittings, compatible with the HN transition maps, is exactly the
Weyl-equivariant lift (O1)\(^+\) on the compact/wrapped sector.  A
non-zero \(c_{o,R}\), a failed square normalization, or a non-zero
\(\omega_{i,R,\mathcal C}\) at one finite stage obstructs (O1)\(^+\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first display is the definition of the composition defect for the
chosen word lifts.  Associativity of determinant-line composition gives
the cocycle identity.  Multiplying \(\tau_{w,R,\mathcal C}\) by
\((-1)^{b(w,\mathcal C)}\) replaces \(c_{o,R}\) by \(c_{o,R}+\delta b\),
so an honest determinant-line action is the same as a splitting of this
central extension, normalized on the Coxeter relations.  For the type-II
subgroup the only Coxeter relations are \(s_{\delta_i}^2=1\).

The quotient-orientation character system is a torsor under the displayed
\(H^1\)-groups.  The difference between the transported trivialization
and the chosen trivialization on the target stratum is therefore the
class \(\omega_{w,R,\mathcal C}\), and functoriality of transport gives
the displayed torsor cocycle law.  Vanishing on the retained simple
generators, together with the square normalizations, propagates to every
retained word in the finite action groupoid; on a genuine \(W\)-orbit
this is the free product \(C_2*C_2*C_2\).  Compatibility in \(R\) is
exactly the finite-stage inverse-system requirement in the compact/wrapped
certificate.  No Maass character or scalar normalization enters the
construction.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Semidirect wall-transport obstruction]
\label{cor:semidirect-wall-transport-obstruction}
Let
\[
G=W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II})
\]
and suppose (O1) has been supplied on the reduced quotient strata.  Let
\(\mathcal G_G\) be the action groupoid of the retained strata under the
chosen \(G\)-transports; on a complete \(G\)-orbit with constant
coefficients this reduces to ordinary group cohomology of \(G\).  An
extension of the type-II Weyl orientation transport from \(W\) to \(G\)
is an additional datum.  It exists on the reduced quotient orientation if
and only if the projective determinant-line cocycle for the chosen lifts
to \(\mathcal G_G\),
\[
c_o^G\in Z^2(\mathcal G_G;\underline{\mathbb F}_2),
\]
has trivial class in
\(H^2(\mathcal G_G;\underline{\mathbb F}_2)\), the chosen killing
cochain normalizes the Coxeter relations in \(W\) and the \(S_3\)-relations in
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\), and the quotient-torsor defects
\[
\omega_{g,\mathcal C}\in
H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{g\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\oplus\bigoplus_{N\ge2}H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)
\]
vanish for the chosen generators \(g\) of \(G\).  The \(S_3\)-part must
transport the full quotient package
\[
\left(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}},
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}},
\{(\beta^{E,N},\lambda^{E,N}=0)\}_{N\ge2}\right)
\]
between chamber-permuted strata.

Consequently the Maass values
\[
\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_{-2}-f_2})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2-f_3})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2+f_3})=+1
\]
are only automorphic target values.  They do not construct a Hall
orientation sign on the semidirect-product generators.  Without the
vanishing above, the manuscript asserts the Hall orientation character
only on \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\), under (O1), (O1)\(^+\), and (O2).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The proof is the same obstruction calculation as
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-quotient-orientation-obstruction}, with
\(\mathcal G_W\) replaced by \(\mathcal G_G\).  A projective action on the
determinant line is a central \(\mathbb F_2\)-extension of the retained
action groupoid, hence is classified by \([c_o^G]\).  On a complete
\(G\)-orbit this is the usual group-cohomology class, and a splitting must
respect all relations of the semidirect presentation, not only the three
generator squares in \(W\).  After the
ordinary determinant-line action is honest, the chosen quotient
trivializations remain torsors under the displayed \(H^1\)-groups; their
failure to be preserved is exactly \(\omega_{g,\mathcal C}\).  Vanishing
on a generating set, with the relation coherences, propagates through the
retained action groupoid, and to all of \(G\) only after a complete
\(G\)-orbit has been supplied.  The Maass character is a scalar
automorphic character and has no map to these determinant-line or
quotient-torsor classes.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rem:thm3-honest-status}
\label{rem:thm3-status}
\label{rem:thm3-deliverable}
The table values of \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on the six generators
(Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction}), the determinant
identity \(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\)
(Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification}), and the OP scalar
\(-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) (Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}) are
independent of the compact Hall hypotheses; they are imported or proved
under the cited source hypotheses, normalizations, and chamber
conventions.  The Pfaffian recognition (i), the orientation-character
identity (ii), and the categorical upgrade (iii) are conditional on
(O1), (O1)\(^+\), and (O2).  Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle}
identifies the strongest algebraic consequence of a supplied
Weyl-equivariant lift: the sign factors through the
\((\Z/2)^3\) abelianization of \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-quotient-orientation-obstruction} separates this
group-theoretic sign extension from the projective determinant-line and
quotient-torsor obstructions that must vanish before there is an honest
Weyl action on the reduced quotient orientation.
Open: (O1) for the reduced
\(E\)-quotiented Weyl-equivariant compact critical \(K3\times E\)
Hall/CoHA sector.  Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier},
Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, and
Borisov--Joyce--Bojko \cite{BorisovJoyce} cover the unreduced
\(\mathrm{Perf}(X)\), and \cite{JoyceUpmeier} covers shifted
symplectic stacks, but the reduced \(E\)-quotient with type-II
Weyl-equivariant lift is not in the literature; (O2) is the supplied
Pfaffian local normal form on type-II walls of that sector, not a
consequence of the automorphic product.  The local obstruction certificate
of Proposition~\ref{prop:o2-local-obstruction-certificate} names the
missing chart, splitting, invariant-unit, and rank-one normal-mode
computations.  The squared scalar branch
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) is orientation-forgetful;
rescaling \(\Delta_5\) by a nonzero scalar leaves \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\)
invariant.  The three type-II rows match Borcherds automorphic divisor
orders \(d_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{aut}}=1\) via \(f(nm,l)\) at
\((1,1,0),(0,1,1),(0,-1,0)\); the independent automorphic check at the
three chamber-permuting type-I roots yields divisor order \(0\) from the
explicit support of \(\phi_{0,1}\) \cite[\S2.2]{EZ:1}.
\end{remark}

\begin{openproblem}[Protected one-particle lift]
Construct, if it exists, a protected one-particle object with a
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\)-graded super-vector-space decomposition
$$
\mathcal H^{\mathrm{1p,ch}}
=\bigoplus_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
\mathcal H^{\mathrm{1p,ch}}_\gamma
$$
with protected superdimensions
$$
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H^{\mathrm{1p,ch}}_{(n,l,m)}}(-1)^F
=f(nm,l).
$$
The determinant construction uses only the virtual classes
\(\mathbb U_{n,l}\) and their signed dimensions.  The algebraic object
constructed from the same charge grading and the same signed
multiplicities is the Borcherds denominator algebra.  Such a lift would
still be weaker than the holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra,
because it would not by itself supply the collision law.
\end{openproblem}

\section{The normalized cusp form}

Freitag \cite{FREITAG:1}, Van der Geer \cite{VDGEER:1}, and Igusa
\cite{Igusa1962,Igusa1964II}: the
even-weight scalar subring is
$$M^{\mathrm{even}}_*(\Sp_4(\Z)) = \C[E_4,E_6,\Delta_{10},\Delta_{12}],$$
$$\mathrm{wt}(E_4,E_6,\Delta_{10},\Delta_{12})=(4,6,10,12).$$
$$\Delta_{10}=\Delta_5^2,\qquad
\mathrm{wt}(\Delta_5)=5,\qquad
\Delta_5|_5 g=\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\Delta_5.$$
$$\Delta_5 =
\prod_{\substack{a,b\in (\Z/2\Z)^2\\{}^t ab\equiv 0 \mod 2}}
\nu_{a,b},$$
$$\nu_{a,b}(z)=
\sum_{l\in\Z^2}\exp\bigl(\pi i(z[l+\tfrac12a]+{}^tbl)\bigr),
\qquad z[x]={}^txzx.$$

For $M = \begin{pmatrix} A & B\\ C & D\end{pmatrix}
\in \Sp_4(\Z)$, Maass's character \cite{MAASS:1}
$$\nu_{\Delta_5}:\Sp_4(\Z)\rightarrow \C^\times,\qquad
|\nu_{\Delta_5}|=1,$$
is determined on the standard generators by
$$\nu_{\Delta_5}\begin{pmatrix}0 & \Id_2\\
-\Id_2 & 0\end{pmatrix} = 1,$$ $$\nu_{\Delta_5}\begin{pmatrix}\Id_2 & B\\
0 & \Id_2\end{pmatrix} = (-1)^{b_1 + b_2 + b_3},$$
$$\nu_{\Delta_5}\begin{pmatrix}{}^tA^{-1} & 0\\
0 & A\end{pmatrix} = (-1)^{(1 + a_1 + a_4)(1 + a_2 + a_3) + a_1a_4}$$
with $A = \begin{pmatrix}a_1 & a_2\\
a_3 & a_4\end{pmatrix} \in \GL_2(\Z)$ and $B = \begin{pmatrix}b_1 &
b_2\\
b_2 & b_3\end{pmatrix} \in M_{2\times2}(\Z).$

$\Delta_5$ is a weight-$5$ form with character
$\nu_{\Delta_5}$, and $\Delta_5^2=\Delta_{10}$ is scalar.

For
$$Z=\begin{pmatrix}z_1&z_2\\z_2&z_3\end{pmatrix},$$
$$\Delta_5(Z) =
\sum_{\substack{n,l,m\equiv 1 \bmod 2\\4nm-l^2>0\\n,m>0}}
c_\Delta(n,l,m)\exp\bigl(\pi i(nz_1+lz_2+mz_3)\bigr),$$
with
$$c_\Delta(1,1,1)=64,\qquad c_\Delta(n,l,m)\in64\Z.$$

\begin{proposition}[Isotropic cusp coefficient]
$$1+\frac1{64}\sum_{t\geq1}c_\Delta(1+2t,1,1)q^t
=\prod_{k\geq1}(1-q^k)^9.$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$$\Delta_5(Z) =
\sum_{\substack{m>0\\m\equiv1\bmod2}}
\phi_{5,m}(z_1,z_2)\exp(\pi i m z_3).$$
$$\phi_{5,1}\in J_{5,\frac12}(\nu_{\Delta_5}).$$
$$\nu_{11}(z_1,z_2)=
\sum_{n\in\Z}(-1)^n
\exp\left(\frac{\pi i}{4}(2n+1)^2z_1+\pi i(2n+1)z_2\right).$$
$$\nu_{11} =
-q^{1/8}r^{-1/2}\prod_{n\geq1}
(1-q^{n-1}r)(1-q^nr^{-1})(1-q^n),$$
$$q=\exp(2\pi iz_1),\qquad r=\exp(2\pi iz_2).$$
$$\psi_{5,\frac12}=\eta(z_1)^9\nu_{11}(z_1,z_2),\qquad
\eta(z_1)=q^{1/24}\prod_{n\geq1}(1-q^n).$$
$$\frac1{64}\phi_{5,1}(z_1,z_2)=\psi_{5,\frac12}(z_1,z_2)
=-q^{1/2}r^{-1/2}\prod_{n\geq1}
(1-q^{n-1}r)(1-q^nr^{-1})(1-q^n)^{10}.$$
$$1+\frac1{64}\sum_{t\geq1}c_\Delta(1+2t,1,1)q^t
=\prod_{k\geq1}(1-q^k)^9.$$
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Massless divisor and determinant sign]
$$\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}
=\left\{\begin{pmatrix}a&0\\0&b\end{pmatrix}\mid
a,b\in\mathbb H_1\right\}.$$
Gritsenko--Cl\'ery \cite{GC}, $N=1$:
$$\operatorname{supp}\operatorname{div}(\Delta_5)
=\Sp_4(\Z)\cdot\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}},\qquad
\operatorname{mult}_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}}(\Delta_5)=1.$$
$$\mathcal M_{\mathrm{massless}}
:=\operatorname{supp}\operatorname{div}(\Delta_5),\qquad
\epsilon_{\det}:=\nu_{\Delta_5}.$$
$$\Delta_5|_5g=\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\Delta_5,\qquad
\Delta_5(s_{\delta_i}Z)=-\Delta_5(Z).$$
The displayed sign on the type-II diagonal reflections \(s_{\delta_i}\),
\(i=1,2,3\), is the Maass-character verification carried out in
Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction} below; the
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1\) line of that lemma is the input used
here.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Orientation line of the protected sector]
\label{def:orientation-line}
Let \(\mathcal C\) be a stable object in the reduced compact critical
Hall/CoHA sector envisaged in
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}, with derived
self-Ext line after cosection reduction
$$
\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)
\in\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak M^{or}_X).
$$
By an \emph{orientation line} of the protected sector is meant a line
bundle
$$
o_{\mathcal C}\in\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak M^{or}_X)
$$
together with the squaring isomorphism
$$
o_{\mathcal C}^{\otimes 2}
\;\simeq\;
\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C),
$$
fitting into a strong orientation datum compatible with the extension
correspondences of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.  This is the
existence frame for orientations on critical and \((-1)\)-shifted
symplectic moduli; on Calabi--Yau threefolds the orientation-data
formalism is Joyce--Song \cite{JoyceSong}, and on Calabi--Yau \(4\)-folds
it is the Borisov--Joyce / Oh--Thomas construction
\cite{BorisovJoyce}, \cite{OhThomasI}, \cite{OhThomasII}.  The
\(K3\times E\) case is neither of these: its reduced compact critical
sector is not constructed in this paper, and the existence of a
square-root line \(o_{\mathcal C}\) for that sector is one of the
unresolved data items of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.  No such line is
constructed here.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Polarization is independent of orientation]
\label{rem:gram-polarization-not-orientation}
\label{rem:bott-sign-normalization}
The identity
\[
B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)
\]
is the polarization identity for the quadratic Gram map
\(\Pi_X\).  It is independent of the parity split of a protected
cohomology representative and independent of the choice of an
orientation line.  Orientation data
enters later, when one tries to promote a determinant section to a
Pfaffian section and to compute its monodromy under wall reflections.
It does not change the Gram polarization.  In particular no
Bott-periodicity convention, Grothendieck--Witt sign convention, or
choice of Bott element is used to prove \(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\).  Such
conventions may rigidify an already constructed orientation theory; they
do not supply the lattice polarization, the reduced \(E\)-quotient
linearization, or the compact Pfaffian sign.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin identification]
\label{prop:bgn-identification}
By the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin product formula for
\(\phi_{0,1}\),
$$\mathcal D_X(Z)=\Delta_5(Z).$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The general Borcherds product mechanism is
\cite[Theorem~10.1]{Borcherds95}; no scalar normalization is taken from
that general theorem.  The exact genus-two specialization used here is
Gritsenko--Nikulin: \cite[Theorem~2.1 and Example~2.4, especially
(2.15)--(2.16)]{GNII} gives the monic product
$$D_5(Z)
=q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
GNII denotes this monic product by \(\Delta_5\).  This paper reserves
\(\Delta_5\) for the theta-constant normalization.  In that convention,
\cite[Theorem~4.1]{GN} gives
\[
D_5(Z)=64^{-1}\Delta_5(Z).
\]
Hence
$$64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=\Delta_5(Z).$$
$$\mathcal D_X(Z)=\Delta_5(Z).$$
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Normalization of the square root]
The constants in the square-root product are fixed by the following
chain:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.25\textwidth}p{0.62\textwidth}}
\hline
Object & Fixed value \\
\hline
Fourier variables &
\(q=e^{2\pi iz_1},\ r=e^{2\pi iz_2},\ s=e^{2\pi iz_3}\) \\
Borcherds input &
\(Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1}\) \\
Borcherds product normalization &
\(D_5^{\mathrm{mon}}=D_5^{\mathrm{GNII}}
=64^{-1}\Delta_5^{\theta}\), and this paper writes
\(\Delta_5=\Delta_5^{\theta}\) \\
Weight &
\(\mathrm{wt}\,\operatorname{Borch}_{\theta}(\phi_{0,1})=f(0,0)/2=5\) \\
Igusa leading coefficient &
\([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5=64\) \\
Monic product &
\(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5
=q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\prod(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}\) \\
Determinant normalization &
\(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5,\quad
v_0=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\) \\
Virtual inverse &
\(\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}
=64^{-1}q^{-1/2}r^{-1/2}s^{-1/2}\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)\) \\
BKM denominator &
\(\operatorname{den}(\autcor)=D_5(2Z)=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\) \\
Scalar square &
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}\);
in general \(Z^X_{\square}=C_{\square}\Delta_5^{-2}\), hence
\((\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}})^2=Z^X_{\square}/C_{\square}\) \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Borcherds--Gritsenko weight identity at \(N=1\)]
Let $\phi_{0,1}\in J_{0,1}^{\mathrm{weak}}$ be the weight-zero index-one
weak Jacobi form with Fourier expansion
$\phi_{0,1}(z_1,z_2)=\sum_{n,l}f(n,l)\,q^nr^l$.  The
theta-normalized Borcherds lift at \(N=1\) is \(\Delta_5\), and the
Borcherds weight reads
$$\operatorname{wt}(\Delta_5)=\frac{f(0,0)}{2}=5=\frac{c_1(0)}{2},$$
with $c_1(0):=f(0,0)=10$.  Since the weight is integral, no metaplectic
cover is needed for the weight factor.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The Borcherds singular-theta regularisation of \(\phi_{0,1}\) produces
a meromorphic Siegel modular form of weight \(f(0,0)/2\); at \(N=1\)
the paramodular group is \(\Sp_4(\Z)\) by Gritsenko--Nikulin
\cite{GN}.  The input Jacobi form has \(f(0,0)=10\)
(Eichler--Zagier \cite{EZ:1}, elliptic genus of K3), hence the output
weight is
\(5\).  Identifying
\(\operatorname{Borch}_{\theta}(\phi_{0,1})\) with \(\Delta_5\) via the
Igusa identification \((\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5)\) fixes
$\operatorname{wt}(\Delta_5)=5$.  Setting $c_1(0):=f(0,0)$ exhibits the
row $(N=1,\,\operatorname{wt}=5,\,c_1(0)=10)$ of the Gritsenko--Cl\'ery
catalogue \cite{GC}; the remaining integral and half-integral
Clery--Gritsenko rows are listed in \cite[Theorem 1.4]{GC}.  Integrality
\(\operatorname{wt}(\Delta_5)\in\Z\) means that no metaplectic cover is
required for the weight factor.  The Hodge automorphic line
\(\mathcal L^5\) remains nontrivial, and the Maass character
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) is a finite-order character of \(\Sp_4(\Z)\).
\end{proof}

\part{Physical charge and normal-ordered descent}

\section{D6--D2--D0 protected-index dictionary}

Only the OP/DT scalar branch requires an elliptically fibered K3 surface
with a section.  The Borcherds determinant above used only the universal
K3 elliptic genus.

Let $S$ be an elliptically fibered K3 surface
$$\pi:S\rightarrow \mathbb{P}^1$$
with a section $s_1$, and let $E$ be an elliptic curve.  Set
$$X=S\times E.$$
Let $F\in \mathrm{Pic}(S)$ be the fibre class and put
$$\beta_h=s_1+hF,\qquad h\geq 0.$$

Type IIA D6--D2--D0 charge:
$$\gamma(h,d,n)=(1;\,(\beta_h,d);\,n).$$
Write $\Omega_X(h,d,n)$ for the putative protected D6--D2--D0 index
attached to this charge in a compact physical realization.  The
microscopic trace is not constructed here; the desired datum would be:
$$
\stackrel{?}{\exists}\,\mathcal H_{\gamma(h,d,n)},\qquad
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_{\gamma(h,d,n)}}(-1)^F
=\Omega_X(h,d,n).
$$
$$\mathrm{Hilb}^n(X,(\beta_h,d))
=\{Y\subset X\mid [Y]=(\beta_h,d),\ \chi(\mathcal O_Y)=n\}.$$
$$E\curvearrowright X,\qquad (x,e')\mapsto (x,e+e').$$

\begin{lemma}[D6--D2--D0 Mukai--Gram dictionary]
\label{lem:mukai-vector-ideal-sheaf-sxe}
Let $X=S\times E$ with $S$ K3 and $E$ elliptic.  Let
$Y\subset X$ be a one-dimensional subscheme with class
$[Y]=(\beta,d)\in H_2(S,\Z)\oplus H_2(E,\Z)$ and
$\chi(\mathcal O_Y)=n\in\Z$.  Let
$\mathcal I_Y\in D^b(X)$ be its ideal sheaf.  Decompose the Mukai vector
$$
v_X(\mathcal I_Y)=\ch(\mathcal I_Y)\cdot\sqrt{\td(X)}
$$
against the K\"unneth basis
\(\Lambda_S\otimes\{1_E,\omega_E\}\) where
\(\Lambda_S=H^*(S,\Z)\) and \(\omega_E\in H^2(E,\Z)\) is the
fundamental class.  Then
$$
v_X(\mathcal I_Y)
=(1,\,0,\,1-d)\otimes 1_E
+(0,\,-\beta,\,-n)\otimes\omega_E.
$$
With
$$
P_Y=(1,0,1-d),\qquad Q_Y=(0,-\beta,-n),
$$
the Gram-degree triple is
$$
\left(\frac{Q_Y^2}{2},\,Q_Y\cdot P_Y,\,\frac{P_Y^2}{2}\right)
=\left(\frac{\beta^2}{2},\,n,\,d-1\right).
$$
In particular, for \(\beta=\beta_h=s_1+hF\) with
\(\beta_h^2=2h-2\),
\[
\Pi_X(Q_Y,P_Y)=(h-1,n,d-1).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Since \(X=S\times E\) is a Calabi--Yau threefold,
$$\ch(\mathcal I_Y)=1-\ch(\mathcal O_Y).$$
For a one-dimensional sheaf on a Calabi--Yau threefold,
\[
\ch_2(\mathcal O_Y)=\operatorname{PD}[Y],
\qquad
\int_X\ch_3(\mathcal O_Y)=\chi(\mathcal O_Y)=n.
\]
The Todd square root factorizes as
$$
\sqrt{\td(X)}
=\pi_S^*\sqrt{\td(S)}\,\pi_E^*\sqrt{\td(E)}
=\pi_S^*(1,0,1)\cup 1,
$$
since \(\sqrt{\td(E)}=1\) and \(\sqrt{\td(S)}=(1,0,1)\) in Mukai
notation on a K3 surface.  Decomposing the curve class,
the K3-vertical component \(\beta\times\{\mathrm{pt}\}\) contributes
\(\beta^\vee\otimes\omega_E\), while the elliptic component
\(d\{\mathrm{pt}\}\times E\) contributes \(d[\mathrm{pt}_S]\otimes 1_E\).
Thus
$$
\ch(\mathcal O_Y)
=(0,0,d)\otimes 1_E+(0,\beta,n)\otimes\omega_E.
$$
Multiplying
\[
1-\ch(\mathcal O_Y)
=(1,0,-d)\otimes 1_E+(0,-\beta,-n)\otimes\omega_E
\]
by \((1,0,1)\otimes1_E\) gives
\[
v_X(\mathcal I_Y)
=(1,0,1-d)\otimes1_E+(0,-\beta,-n)\otimes\omega_E,
\]
because \(\beta^\vee[\mathrm{pt}_S]=0\) on the K3 surface.

The Mukai pairing on \(\Lambda_S\) is
\[
(r,D,s)\cdot(r',D',s')=D\cdot D'-rs'-r's.
\]
Therefore
\[
\frac{Q_Y^2}{2}=\frac{\beta^2}{2},\qquad
Q_Y\cdot P_Y
=(-\beta)\cdot0-0(1-d)-1(-n)=n,
\]
and
\[
\frac{P_Y^2}{2}
=\frac{-2(1)(1-d)}{2}=d-1.
\]
For \(\beta=\beta_h\), \(\beta_h^2=2h-2\), this gives
\(\Pi_X(Q_Y,P_Y)=(h-1,n,d-1)\).
\end{proof}

The Gram-degree triple
\((Q^2/2,\,Q\cdot P,\,P^2/2)=(h-1,\,n,\,d-1)\)
identifies the Hilbert/PT charge with a triple in the Mukai lattice of
\(X\); this is the Gram-index data used by the Borcherds product and
by the OP normalization of Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square}.  The hypothesis
\(\beta_h^2=2h-2\) of Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square} is exactly the
\(Q^2/2=h-1\) line of this lemma.

\begin{proposition}[Reduced scalar quotient integration]
\label{prop:reduced-scalar-quotient-integration}
The reduced DT/PT side used in this paper is the coefficientwise scalar
Behrend-weighted quotient integration
$$
\mathbf{DT}^X_{n,(\beta,d)}
=
\int_{\mathrm{Hilb}^n(X,(\beta,d))/E}\nu_{\mathrm{Hilb}}\,de,
$$
and
$$
\mathsf P^X_{n,(\beta,d)}
=
\int_{P_n(X,(\beta,d))/E}\nu_P\,de
$$
for the stable-pair moduli space \(P_n(X,(\beta,d))\).  It lands in
numbers, coefficient by coefficient.  Oberdieck's reduced stable-pair
quotient invariant agrees with the reduced virtual-class incidence
definition, and his reduced DT/PT theorem identifies the two reduced
quotient series for nonzero K3 class \cite[Theorem 3(i)]{OberdieckReducedPT}.
This is scalar integration.  It is not a Hall product, not a CoHA
integration map, and not an orientation character.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Behrend's constructible function gives the weighted Euler
characteristic used in Donaldson--Thomas theory \cite{BEHREND},
\cite{DT}.  The \(E\)-action on \(X=S\times E\) forces the ordinary
unreduced invariant to vanish, so the reduced theory integrates over
the quotient by \(E\).  Bryan's Hilbert-scheme normalization and
Oberdieck's stable-pair normalization are exactly the quotient
Behrend-weighted Euler characteristics \cite{BRYAN},
\cite{OberdieckReducedPT}.  Oberdieck proves the quotient stable-pair
definition equals the reduced incidence invariant and proves the
reduced DT/PT comparison for nonzero K3 class.  These statements produce
integers indexed by \((\beta,d,n)\); no algebra object or primitive
projection is constructed.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[Protected D-brane index]
\label{conj:protected-d-brane-index}
For the D6--D2--D0 charge
$$\gamma(h,d,n)=(1;\,(\beta_h,d);\,n),$$
if such a compact physical Hilbert space is supplied, the conjectural
enumerative dictionary identifies its protected trace with the
Behrend-weighted Hilbert-scheme quotient invariant:
$$
\Omega_X(h,d,n)
:=\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_{\gamma(h,d,n)}}(-1)^F
\stackrel{\mathrm{phys}}{=}
\mathbf{DT}^X_{n,(\beta_h,d)}.
$$
This physical identification is not used in the scalar theorem below.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{definition}[Protected Hall integration criterion]
\label{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}
A protected Hall or critical CoHA integration map refining
Proposition~\ref{prop:reduced-scalar-quotient-integration} would have
to supply the following data before comparison with
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\):
an extension-closed compact Hall/CoHA sector for the reduced
\(E\)-quotient, oriented critical extension correspondences,
vanishing-cycle coefficient systems, HN-finite sector completions,
protected integration compatible with the completed Hall product and
wall crossing, a primitive projection, and a lifted Weyl action on the
oriented completed theory.

If these data exist, the test is rigid: protected primitives must have
signed dimensions
$$
\sdim\Prim_{(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l),
$$
their bracket must be the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin bracket, and the
induced orientation character must restrict on the type-II Weyl group as
$$
\epsilon_o|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}
=
\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}.
$$
General CoHA technology supplies a language for such conditions
\cite{KSCoHA}, \cite{DavisonMeinhardtCoHA}; it does not construct this
compact \(K3\times E\) datum.
\end{definition}


\begin{lemma}[Brauer-class parity criterion for Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbes]
\label{lem:p3-brauer-gerbe-vanishing}
Let \(\mathcal C\) be a protected Mukai charge on the reduced
\(K3\times E\) sector, and let
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) and
\(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) be the reduced Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe class and
the \(E\)-equivariant descent obstruction of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.  On any
projection-finite stratum on which:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a GRR/Stiefel--Whitney comparison identifies the reduced
orientation gerbe of the self-Ext complex with the numerical parity
class \(c_1(L)^2/2\bmod2\) of a K3 chamber polarization line \(L\), and
\item \(c_1(L)^2/2\equiv0\pmod2\), and
\item the \(E\)-descent parity
\(c_1(\mathrm{degree})\cup c_1(\mathrm{level})\) is even,
\end{enumerate}
one has
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=0,
\qquad
\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}=0
\]
on that stratum.  In particular this proves the claimed vanishing on
rank-two chambers satisfying the displayed parity and on HN strata whose
graded factors reduce to rank-one/rank-two pieces on which the ordinary
and quotient orientation classes have already vanished.  It does not
prove the length-one stable higher-rank case.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The BBDJS orientation gerbe of the reduced self-Ext complex is the
second Stiefel--Whitney class of the determinant line, equivalently the
mod-two Brauer class of the square-root gerbe
\cite{BBDJS2015}.  On a stratum satisfying the first hypothesis the
supplied GRR/Stiefel--Whitney comparison represents this class by
\[
\frac{c_1(L)^2}{2}\bmod2.
\]
The second hypothesis therefore gives
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=0\).  The equivariant Serre
spectral sequence for the free \(E\)-translation quotient identifies the
connected descent obstruction with
\(c_1(\mathrm{degree})\cup c_1(\mathrm{level})\bmod2\), so the third
hypothesis gives \(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}=0\).  Without the first
comparison, the displayed parity is only a numerical diagnostic, not a
proof of gerbe triviality.  Additivity of orientation
gerbes on HN direct sums, from the Joyce--Upmeier / Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier
multiplicative orientation formalism \cite{JoyceUpmeier,JoyceTanakaUpmeier},
then transports the vanishing to HN strata whose graded factors all lie
in the proved rank-one/rank-two sectors; off-diagonal self-Ext blocks
occur in dual pairs and contribute even Stiefel--Whitney class.  No
induction over a stable length-one higher-rank factor is used.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rem:p3-route-b-versus-hn}
Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-brauer-gerbe-vanishing} reads the parity off the
Chern integrand of the chamber polarization;
Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-higher-rank-pin-c-vanishing} reads it off the
HN-filtration data.  Both are reduction criteria: they agree with the
rank-one base case (P1) and with each other on the rank-two/HN-reducible
strata after the rank-one finite-data checks of (P1) have been
performed, but neither closes stable higher-rank length-one strata.
\end{remark}

\begin{openproblem}[Orientation monodromy character]
\label{op:orientation-monodromy-character}
The geometric orientation monodromy character
$$
\epsilon_o:W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\longrightarrow\{\pm1\},
$$
expected to satisfy
$$
\epsilon_o|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}
=
\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})},
$$
is not produced by normalizing \(\Delta_5\).  Multiplying \(\Delta_5\)
by a nonzero scalar leaves its Maass character unchanged.  The character
must instead be produced by transporting the square root of the
determinant line around the simple diagonal wall reflections; the
expected local model is Pfaffian, in the sense made precise as
hypothesis (O2) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}: a simple
real-root reflection reverses one oriented normal mode, so its square is
scalar while the square root changes sign.

\smallskip
\textup{(P1)} \emph{Rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum: ordinary Pin\(^c\)
input and quotient checks.}  On the rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\) of physical Mukai charge
\(\mathcal C=(1,\beta,n)\), the desired reduced orientation line
\(o^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\in\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C})\)
is reduced to four pieces of data: an ordinary Pin\(^c\) lift of the
cosection-reduced self-Ext frame bundle, a connected \(BE\)-equivariant
linearization class, finite-stabilizer gerbe classes on the small-orbit
strata, and the residual finite-stabilizer \(H^1\)-linearization
characters after those gerbes have been null-trivialized.  The standard
orientation technologies
\cite{BBDJS2015,JoyceUpmeier,JoyceTanakaUpmeier,CaoKoolMonavari}
provide the local Pin\(^c\) frame and sign-rigidification model used in
Lemma~\ref{lem:spin-lift-sign-fixing}.  They do not, without the
following quotient computations, construct the reduced
\(E\)-quotient orientation.  The ordinary obstruction class is
$$
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
:=w_2\bigl(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\bigr)
+\mathrm{cs}^{*}\,w_2\bigl(\det(\operatorname{coker}\,\mathrm{cs})\bigr)
\;\in\;H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)
$$
of the reduced orientation gerbe.  The connected quotient class has the
form
\[
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C}
=a_1(\mathcal C)u_1+a_2(\mathcal C)u_2
\in H^2(BE;\mathbb F_2),
\]
with \(u_1,u_2\) as in
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.  On the \(N=2\)
small-orbit stratum the finite residual is
\[
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}
=b_{20}(\mathcal C)x_1^2+b_{11}(\mathcal C)x_1x_2
+b_{02}(\mathcal C)x_2^2
\in H^2(BE[2];\mathbb F_2).
\]
After \(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0\), the chosen two-torsion
linearization has a degree-one character
\[
\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}
=\lambda_1(\mathcal C)x_1+\lambda_2(\mathcal C)x_2
\in H^1(BE[2];\mathbb F_2).
\]
Thus rank-one (O1) through the two-torsion small-orbit boundary is
proved exactly when
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=0,\qquad
a_1(\mathcal C)=a_2(\mathcal C)=0,\qquad
b_{20}(\mathcal C)=b_{11}(\mathcal C)=b_{02}(\mathcal C)=0,\qquad
\lambda_1(\mathcal C)=\lambda_2(\mathcal C)=0.
\]
The first equality is the ordinary Pin\(^c\) orientation calculation.
The remaining bits are quotient gerbe and linearization data.  The three
finite-sector bits \(r_1,r_2,r_3\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:rank-one-e2-linearization-obstruction} are
equivalent to the three coefficients \(b_{20},b_{11},b_{02}\), but they
do not see the connected \(BE\)-class
\(a_1u_1+a_2u_2\) or the degree-one finite character
\(\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}\).  Thus the three cyclic degree-two bits cannot
by themselves be promoted to a proof of rank-one \textup{(O1)}.  Rank-one
\textup{(O1)} through
the two-torsion boundary is proved only after the ordinary class, the
two connected coefficients, the three finite cyclic degree-two
residuals, and the finite degree-one character have all been computed to
vanish.  None of these vanishing statements is
implied by ordinary translation invariance or by the OP scalar square.
Full rank-one descent through all small-orbit strata also requires
\(\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}=0\) and the trivial \(H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)\)
linearization character for every even \(N\ge4\), with the
two-primary residual described in
Lemma~\ref{lem:even-finite-stabilizer-residuals}; the \(E[2]\) bits do
not imply those vanishings.
Higher-rank semistable strata remain open except where the HN criteria
below reduce them to already-oriented factors.

\smallskip
\textup{(P2)} \emph{Type-II diagonal reflections: wall-character formula
conditional on the orientation existence.}  Conditional on (P1) and on
the multiplicative orientation cocycle of Joyce--Upmeier
\cite{JoyceUpmeier} and Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} extending equivariantly across the reduced
\(E\)-quotient, and on the Pfaffian local model (O2) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}, equivalently
the three local calculations isolated in
Proposition~\ref{prop:o2-local-obstruction-certificate}, the induced
orientation character satisfies
\(\epsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})=-1=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})\),
\(i=1,2,3\), so \(\epsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).  The three
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3\) chamber-permuting reflections have Maass
value \(+1\), but Hall signs on them require a separately supplied
semidirect-product lift.  This is exactly conclusion (ii) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}, with the
explicit row-by-row calculation in
Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation}; conditional on (O1),
(O1)\(^+\), and (O2).

\smallskip
\textup{(P3)} \emph{Higher-rank obstruction.}
The required task is to compute the obstruction classes
$$
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2),
\qquad
\alpha^{E}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;H^2_E(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2),
$$
where \(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) is the Pin\(^c\)-lift
gerbe class of the reduced derived self-Ext frame bundle on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\), and \(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\)
is the equivariant-linearization obstruction to descent of the
orientation along the free \(E\)-translation quotient.  On the rank-one
stratum it should be computed, not inferred from the OP scalar, by a
direct Chern-class calculation in the \(E_2^{2,0}\)-term of the
equivariant Serre spectral sequence
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\to
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}/E\to BE\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.  One must then prove
their joint vanishing on the Harder--Narasimhan-completed semistable stack
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN}}_{\mathcal C}\).
The small-orbit gerbe contribution
\(\overline{\beta}^E_{\mathcal C}\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}(iv) from the
\(N\ge 2\) torsion locus
\(K3\times(E/E[N])\subset X\) is governed by the finite-stabilizer
criterion of Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing}: the band at
\(N=2\) is the Klein-four \(BE[2]\) (not cyclic \(B\mu_2\)), and
vanishing requires a trivial \(E[2]\)-equivariant linearization of the
orientation line, detected on the three nontrivial cyclic subgroups.
Granted the ordinary Pin\(^c\) gerbe vanishing, the connected
\(BE\)-linearization vanishing, and this finite-stabilizer vanishing,
(O1) would follow from the Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier}
multiplicative cocycle plus the supplied Pin\(^c\) lift; granted (O2),
the wall-character formula of (P2) would follow by
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}.  On
higher-rank semistable strata the joint vanishing of
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) and \(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) is
reduced by Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-higher-rank-pin-c-vanishing} to HN strata
whose graded factors are already oriented; stable higher-rank length-one
strata and even finite-stabilizer strata not covered by a trivial
linearization remain open.  The
Pin\(^c\)-lift program of \cite{JoyceUpmeier},
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, \cite{CaoKoolMonavari}, \cite{Bojko},
\cite{BBDJS2015} supplies the analytic technology on the
cosection-twisted reduced \(E\)-quotient; non-compact and Joyce--Song
extensions are Bojko \cite{Bojko}.

\smallskip
\textup{(P4)} \emph{Cosection-induced parity flip from \(\sigma_{K3}\):
\(\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{red}}=\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{std}}+1\); absorbed
into (O1) as a \(\mathbb Z/2\)-grading shift on \(o_{\mathcal C}\).}
The Maulik--Toda / Oberdieck reduced obstruction theory
\cite{MaulikTodaGV,OberdieckReducedPT} contracts the
PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form
\(\omega_{\mathfrak M}\) on \(\mathfrak M_{\mathcal C}(X)\) against the
cosection
\(\mathrm{cs}\colon\operatorname{Obs}_{\mathfrak M_{\mathcal C}}\to
\mathcal O_{\mathfrak M_{\mathcal C}}\) generated by Mukai dilation
along \(\sigma_{K3}\), and the restriction \(\omega_{\mathfrak M}^{\mathrm{red}}\)
to the cosection vanishing locus
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\hookrightarrow
\mathfrak M_{\mathcal C}\) is non-degenerate on the OP/DT
D6--D2--D0 stratum, with virtual dimension shifted by one,
\(\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{std}}_{\mathcal C}+1\).
Under the BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} Pin-to-Spin lift of
the BBDJS line of Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}, this dimension
shift propagates as a \(\mathbb Z/2\)-grading shift on the orientation
line:
$$
o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
\;=\;o^{\mathrm{std}}_{\mathcal C}\otimes\Pi,
$$
where \(\Pi\) is the parity-flip line generated by the cosection cokernel.
The strong orientation certificate \textup{(O1)} includes the coherence
datum that makes this shift commute with the extension correspondences of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion} and preserves
the Joyce--Upmeier multiplicative cocycle of (P2).  The Oberdieck monic
normalization \cite{OberdieckReducedPT} fixes the scalar parity branch,
and the Hall extension coherence is the corresponding \textup{(O1)}
residual.  The parity-flip is absorbed into (O1):
the strong orientation line
\(o_{\mathcal C}\) demanded by
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional} is, on the
reduced sector, \(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\), not the unreduced
BBDJS line, and the squaring isomorphism is to the reduced derived
self-Ext
\(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)
=\operatorname{cofib}(\sigma_{K3}\colon
\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)[-2]\to\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C))\).
Operationally this parity shift belongs to the reduced orientation
datum and to any eventual Berezinian convention for a compact
first-order object.  The overall minus in
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) is the scalar OP/DT branch
convention.  It may be compatible with a chosen fermionic grading, but
it is not evidence for the Hall orientation character.  The reflection
character \(\epsilon_o\) must be computed from monodromy of the
orientation line around the type-II walls.
The (P3) residual is the joint vanishing of
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}+\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) on the
HN-completed semistable stack with \(\mathrm{rk}\,\mathcal C\ge 2\) and
on the small-orbit \(BE[N]\) finite-stabilizer strata.
Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-higher-rank-pin-c-vanishing} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-brauer-gerbe-vanishing} give conditional reductions
for the HN-reducible and rank-two parity pieces;
Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing} gives the \(N=2\)
Klein-four detection criterion.  Stable higher-rank length-one strata
and nontrivial finite-stabilizer linearizations remain genuine open
obligations.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{lemma}[Connected and finite-stabilizer \(E\)-descent of the
orientation line]
\label{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}
Let \(\mathcal C\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) and let
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) be the cosection-reduced
critical Hall stack of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.  The
translation action of \(E\) on \(X=K3\times E\) lifts to an action on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\), free outside the
small-orbit locus
$$
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{small}}_{\mathcal C}
=\bigcup_{N\ge 2}\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\bigl(K3\times(E/E[N])\bigr)
\;\subset\;
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C},
$$
and on the free locus produces a quotient stack
\(\overline{\mathfrak M}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
=\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\big/E\).  Suppose the unreduced
orientation \(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) of (P1) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character} exists on the
free locus.  Its descent to a line
\(\overline{o}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
\in\operatorname{Pic}(\overline{\mathfrak M}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C})\)
is governed by the equivariant Serre spectral sequence
$$
E_2^{p,q}=H^p(BE;\,H^q(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2))
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H^{p+q}_E(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)
$$
attached to the fibration
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\to
\overline{\mathfrak M}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\to BE\).  The
connected \(E\)-quotient and the finite stabilizer strata have different
cohomology and must be treated separately.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] (\emph{Connected free \(E\)-descent.})
Topologically \(E^{\mathrm{top}}\simeq T^2\), hence
\[
BE\simeq BT^2\simeq K(\mathbb Z^2,2),
\qquad
H^*(BE;\mathbb F_2)=\mathbb F_2[u_1,u_2],
\quad |u_i|=2.
\]
Therefore
$$
H^1(BE;\mathbb F_2)=0,\qquad
H^2(BE;\mathbb F_2)=\mathbb F_2u_1\oplus\mathbb F_2u_2.
$$
In particular there is no connected-torus obstruction in bidegree
\[
E_2^{1,1}
=H^1(BE;\mathbb F_2)\otimes
H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)=0.
\]
The degree-two obstruction on the free locus has only the two standard
components
\[
E_2^{2,0}
=H^2(BE;\mathbb F_2)\otimes
H^0(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\]
and
$$
E_2^{0,2}
=H^0(BE;\,H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)).
$$
Thus the free-locus descent obstruction is a class
$$
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C}
\in H^2_E(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
$$
whose connected-torus part lies in
\(\mathbb F_2u_1\oplus\mathbb F_2u_2\), not in a rank-three
\(\langle\alpha^2,\alpha\beta,\beta^2\rangle\) group.
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (\emph{Rank-one free-locus criterion.})  On the
rank-one stratum
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\),
\(\mathcal C=(1,\beta,n)\), descent of
\(o^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\) through the free \(E\)-quotient is
equivalent to the vanishing of the two components in \textup{(i)}:
the ordinary reduced orientation gerbe in \(E_2^{0,2}\), and the
connected-torus equivariant linearization class in \(E_2^{2,0}\).
If a direct Chern-class calculation identifies the latter with a class
of the form
$$
c_1(\mathrm{degree})u_1+c_1(\mathrm{level})u_2
\in H^2(BE;\mathbb F_2),
$$
then the class vanishes exactly when those two mod-\(2\) coefficients
vanish.  The OP scalar normalization by itself does not prove this
equivariant linearization statement; it is a separate orientation
calculation.
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (\emph{Finite stabilizer descent.})  On
the small-orbit locus \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}(K3\times(E/E[N]))\)
the \(E\)-quotient is the stacky orbifold
\([\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}(K3\times(E/E[N]))/(E/E[N])]\)
banded by \(BE[N]\), not by \(B\mu_N\) unless a cyclic subgroup has
been chosen.  The orientation line may pick up a finite-stabilizer
descent class
$$
\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,S}
\;\in\;
H^2_{E[N]}(S;\mathbb F_2).
$$
Its point-stabilizer restriction is a class in
\(H^2(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)\) only after the mixed Borel terms, stabilizer
action on \(H^\bullet(S;\mathbb F_2)\), and spectral-sequence
differentials have vanished.
For \(N=2\),
$$
E[2]\simeq(\mathbb Z/2)^2,\qquad
H^*(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)=\mathbb F_2[x_1,x_2],
\quad |x_i|=1,
$$
so
\[
H^2(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)
=\mathbb F_2\langle x_1^2,x_1x_2,x_2^2\rangle.
\]
This rank-three group is the point-stabilizer reduction of the finite
two-torsion calculation; it is not the full Borel descent class and it is
not connected \(BE\).  If \(N\) is odd, the positive-degree
mod-\(2\) cohomology of \(BE[N]\) vanishes because \(E[N]\) has odd
order.  For even \(N\), the residual class is detected on the
\(2\)-primary part and must be computed stratum by stratum from the
equivariant linearization of the orientation line.  More precisely, if
\(2^a\parallel N\) and \(a\ge2\), then
\[
H^*\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
=\Lambda(x_1,x_2)\otimes\mathbb F_2[y_1,y_2],
\qquad |x_i|=1,\quad |y_i|=2,\quad x_i^2=0,
\]
so
\[
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_1^{(N)}y_1+A_{12}^{(N)}x_1x_2+A_2^{(N)}y_2.
\]
This is not determined by the \(N=2\) Klein-four vector.
\item[\textup{(iv)}] (\emph{Combined criterion.})  The orientation line
descends over the full reduced quotient only if the ordinary reduced
orientation gerbe, the connected-torus equivariant linearization class,
and every finite Borel class
\(\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,S}\) vanish on the relevant strata.
After each finite Borel class has been null-trivialized, the chosen stabilizer
linearization has a residual character
\[
\lambda^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}\in H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2),
\]
and the quotient orientation requires this character to be zero.
Translation invariance of the underlying ordinary line is not enough: a
fixed line can carry a non-trivial equivariant character.
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The cohomology calculation in \textup{(i)} is the standard classifying
space computation for a compact torus:
\[
BT^2=K(\mathbb Z^2,2),\qquad
H^*(BT^2;\mathbb F_2)=\mathbb F_2[u_1,u_2],\quad |u_i|=2.
\]
Hence \(H^1(BE;\mathbb F_2)=0\), and the bidegree
\((1,1)\) term in the equivariant Serre spectral sequence vanishes.
The only total-degree two terms on the free connected quotient are
\((2,0)\) and \((0,2)\), as displayed.  This proves the connected
separation.

For \textup{(ii)}, descent of a square-root line through a free group
quotient is exactly an equivariant linearization problem together with
the ordinary gerbe-trivialization problem.  The spectral sequence in
\textup{(i)} records these two classes.  A proposed rank-one
Chern-class formula is therefore a criterion: once the two coefficients
of \(u_1,u_2\) and the ordinary gerbe class vanish, the line descends on
that stratum.  The scalar identity
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP/DT}}=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}\) has no information about a
choice of \(E\)-equivariant linearization, so it cannot by itself prove
the criterion.

For \textup{(iii)}, the stabilizer of the \(N\)-fold small-orbit stratum
is the finite group \(E[N]\simeq(\mathbb Z/N)^2\).  At \(N=2\) this is
the Klein-four group.  Its mod-\(2\) cohomology is the polynomial ring
on the two degree-one character classes, hence its degree-two part has
basis \(x_1^2,x_1x_2,x_2^2\).  If \(N\) is odd, transfer kills
positive-degree \(\mathbb F_2\)-cohomology because \(|E[N]|=N^2\) is
invertible in \(\mathbb F_2\).  Even \(N\) reduces to its \(2\)-primary
stabilizer.  This proves the finite-stabilizer typing and separates it
from connected \(BE\).

Clause \textup{(iv)} is the standard descent criterion for a line on a
stack quotient: ordinary square-root gerbe, connected equivariant
linearization, finite-stabilizer Borel degree-two classes, and the residual
degree-one stabilizer characters must all vanish.  A line fixed as an
ordinary line can still carry a non-trivial character of the stabilizer
group, so ordinary translation invariance does not imply equivariant
descent.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Klein-four criterion for the small-orbit gerbe residual]
\label{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing}
Let \(\mathcal C\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) and adopt the notation of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.  The two-torsion
subgroup \(E[2]\subset E\) is the Klein-four group
\(\mathbb Z/2\times\mathbb Z/2\), generated by the three nontrivial
two-torsion points \(e_1,e_2,e_3\in E[2]\) (any two are independent).
The small-orbit stratum at \(N=2\) is
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}(K3\times(E/E[2]))\), banded
by \(BE[2]\), not \(B\mu_2\); the cohomological residual of
clause \textup{(iv)} of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction} at \(N=2\) is the
class
$$
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;
H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)
\;\cong\;(\mathbb Z/2)^3,
$$
with cohomology basis
$$
H^*(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)
\;=\;\mathbb Z/2[\,c_1(L_1),c_1(L_2)\,],
\quad
H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)
\;=\;\mathbb Z/2\langle c_1(L_1)^2\rangle
\oplus\mathbb Z/2\langle c_1(L_2)^2\rangle
\oplus\mathbb Z/2\langle c_1(L_1)\smile c_1(L_2)\rangle,
$$
where \(L_1,L_2\) are the two character lines of the dual
\(E[2]^{\vee}\simeq E[2]\), and the three nontrivial cyclic subgroups
\(\mu_2^{(i)}=\langle e_i\rangle\subset E[2]\), \(i=1,2,3\), restrict the
basis to the three generators of
\(H^2(B\mu_2^{(i)};\mathbb Z/2)\cong\mathbb Z/2\) componentwise.
Write
\[
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}
=b_{20}x_1^2+b_{11}x_1x_2+b_{02}x_2^2,
\qquad x_j=c_1(L_j),
\]
and let \(\tau_i\) be the degree-one generator of
\(H^*(B\mu_2^{(i)};\mathbb Z/2)\).  Define the three cyclic residual
bits \(r_i\in\mathbb Z/2\) by
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\mu_2^{(i)}}\!
\bigl(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}\bigr)=r_i\tau_i^2.
\]
With \(e_3=e_1+e_2\),
\[
r_1=b_{20},\qquad r_2=b_{02},\qquad
r_3=b_{20}+b_{11}+b_{02},
\]
hence
\[
b_{20}=r_1,\qquad b_{02}=r_2,\qquad
b_{11}=r_1+r_2+r_3.
\]
Thus the \(N=2\) finite-stabilizer residual vanishes if and only if the
three cyclic residual bits \(r_1,r_2,r_3\) vanish.  On the rank-one
D6--D2--D0 input \(\mathcal C=(1,\beta,n)\), the following hypotheses are
sufficient, and in the finite \(E[2]\)-sector necessary, for the
\(N=2\) residual to vanish and for the chosen \(E[2]\)-linearization to
be trivial:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(K1)}] (\emph{K\"unneth split.})  The reduced
orientation line factors as a tensor product
\(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=o_{K3}\otimes o_E\) on the protected
sector, where \(o_{K3}\) is the Pin\(^{c}\) orientation of the K3 PT
factor and \(o_E\) is the Pin\(^{c}\) orientation of the elliptic
fibration factor, by the K\"unneth factorization of the cosection-twisted
Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier multiplicative cocycle
\cite{JoyceUpmeier},\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\)
viewed as a relative Hilbert scheme over the elliptic base, and the
Cao--Kool--Monavari Pin\(^{c}\) lift on the K3 factor
\cite{CaoKoolMonavari}.
\item[\textup{(K2)}] (\emph{K3 factor.})  The action of \(E[2]\) on
\(X=K3\times E\) is fibrewise translation on the second factor and
trivial on the first.  The supplied factorwise equivariant lift on the
K3 orientation factor is required to be the trivial \(E[2]\)-lift; this
removes no elliptic finite-stabilizer obstruction.
\item[\textup{(K3)}] (\emph{Elliptic factor: finite gerbe and character
data.})
Translation by \(e_i\in E[2]\) fixes the underlying elliptic orientation
line \(o_E\) as an ordinary line.  This fixedness does not decide the
equivariant lift.  First one must compute the three degree-two gerbe
bits
\[
r_i(\mathcal C)
=\operatorname{res}_{\mu_2^{(i)}}(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C})/\tau_i^2
\in\mathbb Z/2,\qquad i=1,2,3.
\]
The degree-two vanishing hypothesis is
\[
r_1(\mathcal C)=r_2(\mathcal C)=r_3(\mathcal C)=0.
\]
After this vanishing has supplied a null-trivialized gerbe, the set of
\(E[2]\)-linearizations is an
\[
H^1(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)=\mathbb F_2\langle x_1,x_2\rangle
\]
torsor.  For a supplied linearization write its character as
\[
\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}=\lambda_1x_1+\lambda_2x_2,
\]
or, on the three cyclic inertia sectors,
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\mu_2^{(i)}}\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}
=\rho_i\tau_i,\qquad
\rho_1=\lambda_1,\quad \rho_2=\lambda_2,\quad
\rho_3=\lambda_1+\lambda_2 .
\]
The required trivial-linearization hypothesis is
\[
\rho_1(\mathcal C)=\rho_2(\mathcal C)=\rho_3(\mathcal C)=0.
\]
Equivalently, the Pin\(^{c}\) sign character
\[
w_1(o_E^{E[2]})\colon E[2]\longrightarrow\mathbb Z/2
\]
vanishes on \(e_1,e_2,e_3\).  This is a degree-one
equivariant-linearization hypothesis, distinct from the degree-two gerbe
bits \(r_i\), and not a consequence of ordinary translation invariance
alone.
\item[\textup{(K4)}] If \textup{(K1)},
\textup{(K2)}, and \textup{(K3)} hold, then the degree-two bits
\(r_i(\mathcal C)\) and the degree-one character bits
\(\rho_i(\mathcal C)\) vanish for every
\(\mu_2^{(i)}\subset E[2]\).  Since
\[
b_{20}=r_1,\qquad b_{02}=r_2,\qquad b_{11}=r_1+r_2+r_3,
\]
the three coefficients of
\(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}\) vanish, and therefore
$$
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0\;\in\;H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2).
$$
The additional equations \(\rho_i=0\) select the trivial point of the
\(H^1(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)\)-torsor of linearizations.
\end{enumerate}
Thus \(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0\) and the finite
\(E[2]\)-linearization is trivial under the stated hypotheses.
For odd \(N\), the finite-stabilizer obstruction vanishes
cohomologically by Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.
For even \(N\ge4\), the obstruction is detected on the \(2\)-primary
finite stabilizer and remains subject to the same equivariant
linearization calculation; it is not closed by ordinary translation
invariance.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The small-orbit stratum at \(N=2\) is the locus on which the
\(E\)-action factors through the quotient \(E\to E/E[2]\), so its
isotropy is exactly \(E[2]\) and the orbifold quotient
\([\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}(K3\times(E/E[2]))/(E/E[2])]\)
is banded by \(BE[2]\) (the inertia of the residual stabiliser),
\emph{not} by \(B\mu_2\).  Since \(E[2]\simeq(\mathbb Z/2)^2\) is the
Klein-four group, the cohomology \(H^*(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)\) has two
independent degree-one generators, whereas
\(H^*(B\mu_2;\mathbb F_2)\) has one.  The two stacks therefore cannot be
equivalent.  The mod-\(2\) cohomology is the polynomial ring on two
degree-one generators \(c_1(L_1),c_1(L_2)\) with
\(L_1,L_2\in\widehat{E[2]}\) the two characters (Cartan--Eilenberg
folklore for the cohomology of an elementary abelian \(2\)-group),
recovering \(H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\cong(\mathbb Z/2)^3\) as stated.

The three nontrivial cyclic subgroups \(\mu_2^{(i)}=\langle e_i\rangle\)
are detected as follows: writing \(E[2]\) additively with basis
\(\{e_1,e_2\}\) and \(e_3=e_1+e_2\), the inclusion
\(\mu_2^{(1)}\hookrightarrow E[2]\) restricts \(L_1\) to the sign
character of \(\mu_2^{(1)}\) and \(L_2\) to the trivial character; the
inclusion \(\mu_2^{(2)}\hookrightarrow E[2]\) restricts \(L_2\) to the
sign character of \(\mu_2^{(2)}\) and \(L_1\) to the trivial character;
the inclusion \(\mu_2^{(3)}\hookrightarrow E[2]\) restricts both
\(L_1,L_2\) to the sign character of \(\mu_2^{(3)}\), so \(c_1(L_1)\)
and \(c_1(L_2)\) restrict to the same generator and \(c_1(L_1)\smile
c_1(L_2)\) restricts to its square.  The three restriction maps are
therefore jointly injective on the rank-three space
\(H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\), so a class in \(H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\)
vanishes if and only if its image in each
\(H^2(B\mu_2^{(i)};\mathbb Z/2)\) vanishes.  This is the standard
Klein-four detection by cyclic restriction.

Equivalently, for
\(\beta=b_{20}x_1^2+b_{11}x_1x_2+b_{02}x_2^2\), the three restrictions
are
\[
\operatorname{res}_1(\beta)=b_{20}\tau_1^2,\qquad
\operatorname{res}_2(\beta)=b_{02}\tau_2^2,\qquad
\operatorname{res}_3(\beta)=(b_{20}+b_{11}+b_{02})\tau_3^2.
\]
This gives the displayed conversion between the coefficient vector
\((b_{20},b_{11},b_{02})\) and the cyclic residual vector
\((r_1,r_2,r_3)\).

\textup{(K1).}  The K\"unneth factorization
\(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=o_{K3}\otimes o_E\) is the underlying
splitting of the multiplicative orientation cocycle of
\cite{JoyceUpmeier},\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} along the product
factorization \(X=K3\times E\) on the protected sector, where the
moduli of stable pairs decompose as a relative Hilbert scheme over the
elliptic base.  The factorwise Pin\(^{c}\) lift on the K3 factor is a
supplied input, modeled on the BBDJS/Joyce--Upmeier and
Cao--Kool--Monavari orientation packages \cite{BBDJS2015,JoyceUpmeier,CaoKoolMonavari};
the elliptic ordinary factor is the orientation of the cotangent bundle
\(\Omega^1_E\), which is trivial of rank one and trivialized by the flat
translation-invariant one-form \(\mathrm dz\).

\textup{(K2).}  The translation \(t_{e_i}\colon X\to X\) acts as the
identity on the K3 factor and as translation by \(e_i\) on the
elliptic factor.  Pulling back along \(t_{e_i}\) does not move the K3
factor.  The trivial \(E[2]\)-lift on \(o_{K3}\) is therefore a supplied
factorwise linearization choice, not a consequence that settles the
elliptic quotient descent.

\textup{(K3).}  The cotangent bundle \(\Omega^1_E\) is trivial,
trivialized by \(\mathrm dz\); translation acts trivially on
\(\mathrm dz\).  This proves only fixedness of the underlying ordinary
line.  It does not determine the equivariant lift.  There are two
separate finite calculations: the degree-two gerbe residual
\(\operatorname{res}\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=r_i\tau_i^2\), and, only
after this residual has been null-trivialized, the degree-one character
\(\operatorname{res}\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}=\rho_i\tau_i\) of the
chosen line linearization.  Hypothesis \textup{(K3)} is the explicit
finite computation \(r_i=0\) and \(\rho_i=0\) for all three cyclic
inertia sectors.

\textup{(K4).}  Combining \textup{(K1)}, \textup{(K2)}, \textup{(K3)},
the three cyclic degree-two residuals and degree-one character bits
vanish.  The coefficient conversion above then gives
\(b_{20}=b_{11}=b_{02}=0\), hence
\(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0\in H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\); the
equations \(\rho_i=0\) give the trivial \(E[2]\)-linearization.  The
odd-\(N\) cases vanish for the cohomological reason of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.  Even-\(N\) cases
for \(N\ge4\) require the corresponding \(2\)-primary equivariant
linearization calculation.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Orbifold-stratum subtlety]
\label{rmk:bmu2-orbifold-stratum}
The K\"unneth factorization \textup{(K1)} is constructed on the smooth
locus of \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\); on the orbifold
stratum \(K3\times\{e_i\}\subset X\) it requires the orbifold extension
of the Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier multiplicative cocycle to the inertia
stack of the Klein-four banded quotient.  Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} provide the orientation technology for
finite-band quotient stacks.  In the present Klein-four case the
required check is concrete: the inertia decomposition into the three
nontrivial cyclic sectors must carry the same trivial equivariant
linearization.  Equivalently, the degree-two equalities
\(r_i(\mathcal C)=0\) and the degree-one equalities
\(\rho_i(\mathcal C)=0\) of clause \textup{(K4)} must both hold.  Once that is
verified, the
orbifold stratum introduces no additional obstruction beyond the
cyclic-sector criterion.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Two-torsion routes which do not replace the finite criterion]
\label{rmk:bmu2-three-additional-routes}
\label{lem:bmu2-small-orbit-vanishing}
\label{lem:bmu2-w1-vanishing}
\label{lem:bmu2-cohomological-computation}
\label{lem:bmu2-orbifold-lift}
\label{rmk:bmu2-cross-check}
\label{rem:bmu2-honest-status}
\label{rmk:bmu2-orbifold-lift-residual}
There are three natural attempts to turn the \(N=2\) small-orbit
calculation into a direct vanishing theorem.  They are useful checks, but
none replaces Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing} and
Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-stabilizer-o1-obstruction}.

\emph{Hyperelliptic route.}  One may try to identify the stabilizer with
the hyperelliptic involution \([-1]\) on \(E\) and prove vanishing from a
trivial action on Picard data.  This is not a theorem in the present
generality.  The action of \([-1]\) on \(\operatorname{Pic}^{0}(E)\) is
inversion, not pointwise triviality, and ordinary fixedness of the line
does not select the equivariant lift.  The route becomes valid only after
one supplies the actual \(E[2]\)-linearized orientation line and proves
that its degree-one character
\(\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}\in H^1(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)\) is zero.
That is precisely the \(\rho_i=0\) part of the finite criterion.

\emph{Wu-class route.}  A direct Stiefel--Whitney computation can identify
the degree-two gerbe class with the \(w_2\)-class of the finite
stabilizer representation, and Wu's formula expresses it as
\[
w_2=v_2+Sq^1v_1 .
\]
This gives an independent route to the bits
\((r_1,r_2,r_3)\) once the reduced tangent/self-Ext complex and its
\(E[2]\)-linearization have been constructed.  It still does not compute
the residual \(H^1(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)\)-character of the chosen
linearization.  Hence it can prove a degree-two gerbe vanishing, not
strong reduced orientation.

\emph{Orbifold Pin\(^c\) route.}  One can attempt to build the lift on
the inertia stack of the four \(E[2]\)-fixed sectors by combining the
K3 Pin\(^c\) package of Cao--Kool--Monavari \cite{CaoKoolMonavari}, the
Joyce--Upmeier/Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier orientation cocycle
\cite{JoyceUpmeier,JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, and To\"en's orbifold
Riemann--Roch \cite{ToenRRRoot}.  This is a legitimate conditional
construction target, not a completed proof here.  It requires an
inertia-stack Pin\(^c\) lift on each cyclic sector, an age-correction
parity calculation, multiplicative gluing across the smooth and
orbifold strata, and trivial residual character under the whole
Klein-four stabilizer.  The \(N=2\) age calculation does not imply the
higher even \(E[N]\) calculation; for \(N\ge4\) the mixed
two-primary class \(A_{12}^{(N)}x_1x_2\) and the degree-one characters
\(\lambda_i^{(N)}\) remain separate obstructions.

Thus the stable theorem in the manuscript is the finite
Klein-four criterion: degree-two gerbe bits and degree-one
linearization characters are both named and must both vanish.  The
three routes above are cross-checks or conditional construction
programmes for those entries.  They are not used as unconditional
vanishing theorems.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Rank-one two-torsion gerbe and linearization package]
\label{prop:rank-one-e2-linearization-obstruction}
On the rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)}\), assume the ordinary
reduced Pin\(^c\) orientation line has been constructed.  The remaining
\(N=2\) finite-stabilizer gerbe obstruction to descent of this line
through the small-orbit quotient is the vector of three degree-two bits
\[
r_i=\operatorname{res}_{\mu_2^{(i)}}(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C})/\tau_i^2
\in\mathbb Z/2,\qquad i=1,2,3.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(r_1,r_2,r_3)=(0,0,0).
\]
After this class has been null-trivialized, the triviality of the
\(E[2]\)-linearization is a separate degree-one question.  The set of
linearizations is an \(H^1(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)\)-torsor; for a supplied
linearization \(\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}\), write
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\mu_2^{(i)}}\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}
=\rho_i\tau_i .
\]
Trivial \(E[2]\)-linearization means
\((\rho_1,\rho_2,\rho_3)=(0,0,0)\).  The \(r_i\) are not the \(\rho_i\):
they live in different cohomological degrees.

\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(C)}] \emph{Cyclic-sector character, after
null-trivialization.}  For a genuine \(E[2]\)-linearized orientation line
on the inertia sector,
\[
\rho_i=\frac{1-\chi_i}{2},\qquad
\chi_i=\text{the scalar by which }e_i\text{ acts on }
o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}|_{I_{e_i}\mathfrak M}.
\]
This computes the degree-one linearization character, not the
degree-two gerbe class.
\item[\textup{(W)}] \emph{Stiefel--Whitney/Wu.}  The degree-two bit is the
coefficient of \(\tau_i^2\) in the equivariant reduced obstruction class:
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\mu_2^{(i)}}
w_2^{E[2]}\!\left(\mathbb T^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\right)
=r_i\tau_i^2,\qquad
w_2=v_2+Sq^1v_1,
\]
where \(\mathbb T^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) is the reduced virtual
tangent/self-Ext complex on the cyclic fixed sector and \(v_j\) are its
Wu classes.
\item[\textup{(P)}] \emph{Inertia-stack Pin\(^c\).}  The degree-two bit is
the Pin\(^c\) central holonomy corrected by the mod-\(2\) orbifold
Riemann--Roch age:
\[
r_i=
\operatorname{hol}_{\ker(\mathrm{Pin}^c\to SO)}
\!\left(\widetilde P^{\,\mathrm{red}}_{\mathrm{Pin}^c}
|_{I_{e_i}\mathfrak M}\right)(e_i)
+\operatorname{age}^{\mathrm{red}}_{e_i}
\pmod2.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Thus the rank-one two-torsion small-orbit sector is closed only after
both vectors vanish:
\[
(r_1,r_2,r_3)=(0,0,0),\qquad
(\rho_1,\rho_2,\rho_3)=(0,0,0).
\]
The present manuscript computes neither vector; the proposition is the
finite obstruction and linearization target, not a vanishing theorem.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing} identifies
\[
H^2(BE[2];\mathbb F_2)
=\mathbb F_2\langle x_1^2,x_1x_2,x_2^2\rangle
\]
and proves that restriction to the three cyclic subgroups
\(\mu_2^{(i)}=\langle e_i\rangle\) is jointly injective in degree two.
Hence \(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}\) vanishes if and only if its three
restrictions \(r_i\tau_i^2\) vanish.

For a line over the quotient stack, after the degree-two gerbe class has
been null-trivialized, the restriction to \(\mu_2^{(i)}\) is a
one-dimensional equivariant line on
\([I_{e_i}\mathfrak M/\mu_2^{(i)}]\).  The character \(\chi_i=\pm1\)
is trivial exactly when the degree-one coefficient \(\rho_i\) is zero;
this is the formula in \textup{(C)}.  The degree-two residual is a
different class.  It is the second Stiefel--Whitney obstruction of the
equivariant reduced tangent/self-Ext complex, and Wu's identity gives
\(w_2=v_2+Sq^1v_1\), giving \textup{(W)}.  Finally, a Pin\(^c\) lift of
the cyclic-sector frame records the central \(\mathbb Z/2\)-holonomy of
\(\ker(\mathrm{Pin}^c\to SO)\); orbifold Riemann--Roch contributes the
age correction on the fixed inertia sector.  This is \textup{(P)}.  The
formulae \textup{(W)} and \textup{(P)} compute the residual degree-two class
\(\operatorname{res}_{\mu_2^{(i)}}\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}\), while
\textup{(C)} computes the residual degree-one choice after that class has
been null-trivialized.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Even finite-stabilizer residuals beyond two torsion]
\label{lem:even-finite-stabilizer-residuals}
Let \(N\) be even and write \(2^a\parallel N\).  On the
\(N\)-fold small-orbit stratum of the reduced \(E\)-quotient, the
positive-degree mod-\(2\) finite-stabilizer obstruction is the
two-primary class
\[
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
\in H^2\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right).
\]
For \(a=1\) this is the Klein-four class
\(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing}.  For \(a\ge2\),
\[
H^*\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
=\Lambda(x_1,x_2)\otimes\mathbb F_2[y_1,y_2],
\qquad |x_i|=1,\quad |y_i|=2,\quad x_i^2=0,
\]
and therefore
\[
H^2\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
=\mathbb F_2\langle y_1,x_1x_2,y_2\rangle.
\]
Write
\[
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_1^{(N)}y_1+A_{12}^{(N)}x_1x_2+A_2^{(N)}y_2 .
\]
Let \(g_1,g_2\) be the standard generators of
\((\Z/2^a)^2\), put \(h_i=2^{a-1}g_i\), \(i=1,2\), and
\(h_3=h_1+h_2\).  For the three order-two cyclic subgroups
\(\langle h_i\rangle\),
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\langle h_1\rangle}\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_1^{(N)}\tau_1^2,\qquad
\operatorname{res}_{\langle h_2\rangle}\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_2^{(N)}\tau_2^2,
\]
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\langle h_3\rangle}\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=(A_1^{(N)}+A_2^{(N)})\tau_3^2 .
\]
The mixed coefficient \(A_{12}^{(N)}\) is invisible to all cyclic
restrictions, not only to the three order-two subgroups above.  It is
detected by the rank-two quotient
\((\Z/2^a)^2\twoheadrightarrow(\Z/2)^2\), which pulls the mixed class
\(\bar x_1\bar x_2\) back to \(x_1x_2\).
Therefore the three \(E[2]\) bits \(r_1,r_2,r_3\) do not determine the
even \(N\ge4\) residual.  Vanishing for \(N\ge4\) is a separate
\(2^a\)-primary equivariant-linearization calculation on the
small-orbit stratum.  After
\(\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}=0\), triviality of the chosen
two-primary linearization is a further degree-one condition:
\[
\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E,N}
=\lambda_1^{(N)}x_1+\lambda_2^{(N)}x_2
\in H^1\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
\]
must vanish.  This character is detected on the cyclic subgroups
generated by \(g_1\) and \(g_2\), not by the order-two subgroups
\(\langle h_i\rangle\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The odd part of \(E[N]\simeq(\Z/N)^2\) has order invertible in
\(\mathbb F_2\), so transfer identifies the positive-degree
\(\mathbb F_2\)-cohomology with that of the two-primary factor
\((\Z/2^a)^2\).  If \(a=1\), this is \(E[2]\) and the cohomology ring is
\(\mathbb F_2[x_1,x_2]\), \(|x_i|=1\), giving the Klein-four basis
\(\langle x_1^2,x_1x_2,x_2^2\rangle\).  If \(a\ge2\), the cyclic
calculation gives
\[
H^*(B\Z/2^a;\mathbb F_2)
\cong\Lambda(x)\otimes\mathbb F_2[y],
\qquad |x|=1,\quad |y|=2,\quad x^2=0.
\]
Kunneth for the product gives the degree-two basis
\(\langle y_1,x_1x_2,y_2\rangle\).

For the restriction formulas, restrict first to the order-two subgroup
\(\langle h_1\rangle=\langle2^{a-1}g_1\rangle\).  The degree-one class
\(x_1\in H^1(B\Z/2^a;\mathbb F_2)\) restricts to zero because the
generator \(h_1\) maps to \(2^{a-1}\equiv0\pmod2\) under the mod-two
character, while the degree-two cyclic extension class \(y_1\) restricts
to the generator \(\tau_1^2\in H^2(B\langle h_1\rangle;\mathbb F_2)\).
The same calculation holds for \(h_2\).  For
\(h_3=2^{a-1}(g_1+g_2)\), both \(y_1\) and \(y_2\) restrict to
\(\tau_3^2\), while \(x_1\) and \(x_2\) restrict to zero.  Hence
\(x_1x_2\) restricts to zero on all three order-two cyclic subgroups,
and the displayed formulas follow.

The quotient \((\Z/2^a)^2\twoheadrightarrow(\Z/2)^2\) identifies
\(H^1(B(\Z/2)^2;\mathbb F_2)\) with the span of \(x_1,x_2\); hence
\(\bar x_1\bar x_2\) inflates to \(x_1x_2\).  The mixed coefficient is
therefore a genuine rank-two equivariant-linearization obstruction.
It is invisible on every cyclic subgroup: for a cyclic subgroup of order
\(2\), the degree-one classes \(x_1,x_2\) restrict to zero as above; for
a cyclic subgroup of order \(2^b\) with \(b\ge2\), the restrictions of
\(x_1,x_2\) are scalar multiples of the single degree-one generator
\(x\), and \(x_1x_2\) restricts to a scalar multiple of \(x^2=0\) in
\(H^2(B\Z/2^b;\mathbb F_2)\).
This is a different stabilizer calculation from the \(N=2\) Klein-four
residual, so the vanishing of \((r_1,r_2,r_3)\) supplies no vanishing
theorem for \(N\ge4\).  Finally, when the degree-two class has vanished,
the residual two-primary linearisations are classified by
\[
H^1\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
=\mathbb F_2\langle x_1,x_2\rangle .
\]
The order-two subgroups generated by \(h_i=2^{a-1}g_i\) do not detect
this character, since \(x_j(h_i)=0\).  Triviality must be checked on
the full two-primary generators, for instance \(g_1,g_2\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Finite-stabilizer obstruction to \textup{(O1)}]
\label{cor:finite-stabilizer-o1-obstruction}
Fix a small-orbit stratum \(S\) of the reduced \(E\)-quotient with
stabilizer \(E[N]\).  Assume that the ordinary reduced square-root gerbe
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) and the connected free quotient
class \(\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C}\) have already been
null-trivialized on this stratum.  Then the finite-stabilizer part of
the strong reduced orientation \textup{(O1)} exists with trivial quotient
linearization if and only if the Borel descent class
\(\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,S}\) and the selected residual
character vanish.  After the Borel mixed terms, stabilizer action on
\(H^\bullet(S;\mathbb F_2)\), and spectral-sequence differentials have
been killed, this condition is computed by the following finite
point-stabilizer tuple.
\begin{enumerate}
\item If \(N\) is odd, there is no positive-degree mod-\(2\)
finite-stabilizer obstruction:
\[
H^{>0}(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)=0.
\]
\item If \(N=2\), the tuple is
\[
\mathfrak o^{E[2]}_{\mathcal C}
=
