\bigl(r_1,r_2,r_3;\rho_1,\rho_2,\rho_3\bigr),
\]
where
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\langle e_i\rangle}
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=r_i\tau_i^2,\qquad
\operatorname{res}_{\langle e_i\rangle}
\lambda^{E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=\rho_i\tau_i .
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\lambda^{E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0 .
\]
\item If \(N\) is even and \(2^a\parallel N\) with \(a\ge2\), the tuple is
\[
\mathfrak o^{E[N]}_{\mathcal C}
=
\bigl(A_1^{(N)},A_{12}^{(N)},A_2^{(N)};
\lambda_1^{(N)},\lambda_2^{(N)}\bigr),
\]
where
\[
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_1^{(N)}y_1+A_{12}^{(N)}x_1x_2+A_2^{(N)}y_2
\]
and
\[
\lambda^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}
=\lambda_1^{(N)}x_1+\lambda_2^{(N)}x_2
\in H^1(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2).
\]
\end{enumerate}
Thus the \(E[2]\) three-bit calculation proves only the point-stabilizer
reduction of the \(N=2\) degree-two gerbe vanishing.  It does not prove
the higher even
finite-stabilizer class \(A_{12}^{(N)}x_1x_2\), and it does not prove
the residual degree-one linearization character.  Any non-zero entry of
\(\mathfrak o^{E[N]}_{\mathcal C}\) obstructs \textup{(O1)} on that
small-orbit stratum.  No scalar automorphic character, Borcherds
divisor order, or OP/DT scalar square changes this finite quotient
obstruction.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
For a finite stabilizer \(G=E[N]\), the Borel descent spectral sequence
\[
E_2^{p,q}=H^p(BG;\,H^q(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};
\mathbb F_2))
\Longrightarrow
H_G^{p+q}(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\]
puts the finite square-root obstruction
\(\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,S}\) in total degree two.  After that
class is null-trivialized, linearizations of the resulting line form an
\(H^1(BG;\mathbb F_2)\)-torsor.  Hence descent with the trivial quotient
orientation is equivalent to the simultaneous vanishing of the degree-two
finite Borel class and the selected degree-one character.  The displayed
point-stabilizer formulas are reductions of this Borel statement after
the mixed terms and differentials vanish.  The odd case is transfer.  The
\(N=2\) case is
Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing} together with
Proposition~\ref{prop:rank-one-e2-linearization-obstruction}.  The
higher even case is Lemma~\ref{lem:even-finite-stabilizer-residuals}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Finite-stage quotient-orientation character system]
\label{prop:finite-stage-quotient-orientation-character-system}
Fix a finite HN height \(R\) in the compact/wrapped certificate of
Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate}.  Let
\(\mathsf{Str}^{or}_R\) be the finite set of reduced object, extension,
and flag strata of \(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\) on which
vanishing-cycle coefficients and orientation lines are pulled, pushed, or
compared.  For \(S\in\mathsf{Str}^{or}_R\), write
\(\mathcal C(S)\) for its charge label and
\(\mathcal N_R(S)\) for the finite stabilizers \(E[N]\) appearing on its
small-orbit components.

A finite-stage quotient-orientation character system is the datum
\[
\mathfrak Q^{or}_R
=
\left(
\{o_{R,S}\}_{S\in\mathsf{Str}^{or}_R},
\{\theta^{\mathrm{red}}_{R,S}\},
\{\theta^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{R,S}\},
\{\theta^{E,N}_{R,S},\,\lambda^{E,N}_{R,S}=0\}_{N\in\mathcal N_R(S)},
\{\mu^{or}_{R,e}\},
\{\Theta^{or}_{R,\mathrm{flag}}\}
\right).
\]
Here \(o_{R,S}^{\otimes2}\) is identified with the reduced determinant
line on object strata and with the corresponding pulled-back coefficient
determinant on extension and flag strata;
\(\theta^{\mathrm{red}}_{R,S}\) null-trivializes the ordinary reduced
gerbe, \(\theta^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{R,S}\) null-trivializes the connected
\(BE\)-class, and \(\theta^{E,N}_{R,S}\) null-trivializes the finite
Borel class
\[
\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{R,S}\in H^2_{E[N]}(S;\mathbb F_2).
\]
Its point-stabilizer restriction is a class
\(\beta^{E,N}_{R,S}\in H^2(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)\) only after the mixed
Borel terms, stabilizer action on \(H^\bullet(S;\mathbb F_2)\), and
spectral-sequence differentials have been killed.  After this finite
Borel class has been null-trivialized, the chosen
finite-stabilizer linearization has character
\[
\lambda^{E,N}_{R,S}\in H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2),
\]
and the quotient system selects the zero character.  The maps
\(\mu^{or}_{R,e}\) are the Thom--Sebastiani orientation transports along
the local-local, local/wrapped, and wrapped-wrapped correspondence
generators \(e\), and \(\Theta^{or}_{R,\mathrm{flag}}\) records their
two-step flag coherences.

Such a system exists on the finite stage if and only if every stratum
\(S\in\mathsf{Str}^{or}_R\) has
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{R,S}=0,\qquad
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{R,S}=0,
\]
and its finite-stabilizer obstruction tuple vanishes as follows:
\[
N\ \text{odd}:\quad H^{>0}(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)=0,
\]
\[
N=2:\quad
\bigl(r_1,r_2,r_3;\rho_1,\rho_2,\rho_3\bigr)=0,
\]
\[
2^a\parallel N,\ a\ge2:\quad
\bigl(A_1^{(N)},A_{12}^{(N)},A_2^{(N)};
\lambda_1^{(N)},\lambda_2^{(N)}\bigr)=0,
\]
with the notation of
Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-stabilizer-o1-obstruction}, and all
orientation-transport defects along the correspondence generators, flag
stacks, and \(R'\ge R\) transition maps vanish.  If the systems
\(\mathfrak Q^{or}_R\) exist for a cofinal family of finite stages and
are compatible with the transition maps, their inverse limit is exactly
the strong reduced orientation datum (O1) on the compact/wrapped Hall
sector.  Conversely, any (O1) datum restricts to such a compatible
finite-stage system.  No automorphic scalar, Borcherds divisor order, or
Maass target character detects any of the finite \(H^1(BE[N])\)
characters.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For each stratum \(S\), the ordinary and connected \(E\)-quotient parts
are the descent classes of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.  For every finite
small-orbit stabilizer \(E[N]\), the degree-two finite gerbe and the
residual degree-one character are precisely the obstruction tuple of
Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-stabilizer-o1-obstruction}.  Thus the displayed
stratumwise vanishings are necessary and sufficient for the coefficient
orientation line to descend with trivial finite-stabilizer character on
each object, extension, and flag stratum.

The remaining conditions are functorial, not cohomological.  A Hall
operation at height \(R\) is the pull--Thom--Sebastiani--push map attached
to a generator of \(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\).  The
orientation transports \(\mu^{or}_{R,e}\) must identify the descended
coefficient systems on the source and target of this generator.  The two
ways to compose such identifications over a two-step flag stack differ
by a finite defect; vanishing of all flag defects is exactly the strict
pentagon condition at height \(R\).  The same statement for successor
maps is the displayed transition compatibility.  Since the stage is
finite, these are finitely many equalities.  Passing to a cofinal inverse
system gives (O1), and restriction of (O1) to a finite height gives the
listed data.  The final sentence follows because the obstruction groups
are the displayed Borel-equivariant \(H^2\) and \(H^1\) groups, whereas a
scalar automorphic character is not a class in them.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Rank-one Pin-lift sign rigidification conditional on a supplied lift]
\label{lem:spin-lift-sign-fixing}
Assume the BBDJS Pin\(^c\) lift \cite{BBDJS2015} of the \(\SO\)-frame
bundle of
\(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\) on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)}\) has been constructed
after the ordinary reduced gerbe class has vanished.  Its underlying
\(\SO\)-bundle determines it only up to a global \(\mathbb Z/2\)
ambiguity
\(\eta_{\mathcal C}\in
H^0(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)};\mathbb Z/2)\), the
kernel of the surjection
\(\mathrm{Pin}^c\twoheadrightarrow\SO\) acting on global sections of the
lift.  On the rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum, this residual sign is
rigidified by the following data, jointly:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(S1)] the Joyce--Upmeier orientability cocycle
\cite{JoyceUpmeier}, \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} on Hall extension
correspondences, which imposes multiplicative compatibility when
rank-one factors are used as graded pieces of HN or direct-sum strata.
This is a compatibility constraint for extending signs beyond the
rank-one components; it is not a proof that the rank-one locus itself is
generated by one component under direct sum;
\item[(S2)] the requirement that, after the supplied comparison
\(\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}\), the Pfaffian section
\(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\) is read as a section of
\(\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5}\) and restricts at the unique
top-cohomology generator of the isotropic-cusp expansion to the monic
Borcherds normalization \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification}; equivalently, the leading
Fourier coefficient of \(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}\) at the
isotropic cusp \(\mathfrak c_\infty\) equals \(+1\) (positive
orientation, monic);
\item[(S3)] scalar consistency, after squaring, with the OP/DT scalar sign
\(C_{\square,X}=-4096\) of Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}, i.e.\
\((\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}})^{2}\!|_{\mathrm{rank\textnormal{-}one}}
=\Delta_5^{2}\) with positive leading coefficient
\(c_\Delta(1,1,1)^2=64^2=4096\), the absolute value of
\(C_{\square,X}\), and
the OP scalar sign \(\operatorname{sign}(C_{\square,X})=-1\) absorbed into the
fermionic shift \((-p_{\mathrm{DT}})^n\) of the OP/DT chamber, not into
the orientation line; this is a scalar compatibility check, not a
rigidifying input for \(\eta_{\mathcal C}\).
\end{enumerate}
Then, on any connected rank-one component for which the supplied
\(\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}\) identifies the Pfaffian section with the monic
cusp branch, the residual sign \(\eta_{\mathcal C}\) is fixed to \(+1\)
for that component.  This fixes a chosen global sign there.  It does not
prove that the same choice extends over all rank-one charge components,
over HN sums, or through the reduced \(E\)-quotient; those compatibilities
are part of \textup{(O1)} and \textup{(O1)}\(^+\), including the connected
\(BE\)-linearization and finite \(E[N]\)-residual vanishings.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The \(\mathrm{Pin}^c\twoheadrightarrow\SO\) sequence has kernel \(\mathbb Z/2\),
so on a connected component the global lift is unique up to multiplying
by a constant element of this kernel; on the disconnected components of
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)}\) (indexed by the
discrete Mukai-charge label \((1,\beta,n)\), connected within each
fixed charge by the Beauville--Mukai moduli construction
\cite{Mukai1984,Mukai1987,HuybrechtsLehn}) the ambiguity is the function
\(\eta\colon\pi_0\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}\to\{\pm 1\}\).

\emph{(S1)} fixes the multiplicative compatibility that any extension of
\(\eta\) to Hall direct-sum or HN correspondence strata must satisfy: by
Joyce--Upmeier
\cite[Theorem~5.1]{JoyceUpmeier}, the orientation cocycle on the
extension correspondence
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\times
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C'}\to
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C+\mathcal C'}\) is the Mukai
parity \((-1)^{\langle\mathcal C,\mathcal C'\rangle_{\mathrm{Mukai}}}\),
and the BBDJS Pin\(^c\) lift respects this cocycle by
\cite[\S5.4]{BBDJS2015} together with the cosection-twist compatibility
of \cite{CaoKoolMonavari}.  Hence an already supplied extension of
\(\eta\) must be multiplicative modulo the Mukai parity.  This does not
show that all rank-one charge components are generated by one component.

\emph{(S2)} fixes \(\eta\) on any connected component on which the
supplied \(\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}\) compares the Pfaffian section with the
monic cusp branch: the Pfaffian section is a section of
\(\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5}\), and
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification} together with the
square-root normalization table of
Remark~\textup{Normalization of the square root} require the leading
Fourier coefficient of \(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}\) at
\(\mathfrak c_\infty\) to be \(+1\) (the monic
\(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\) being the canonical Borcherds output).  The
coefficient \(64\) is the theta-normalization converting the monic
Borcherds product \(D_5\) to \(\Delta_5\); it is not the square of an
orientation line.  The orientation line chooses the sign of a supplied
first-order Pfaffian section, not the scalar prefactor.  This pins
\(\eta_{\mathcal C}\in\{+1,-1\}\) to a specific value on that component.

\emph{(S3)} verifies consistency: squaring an orientation line forgets
\(\eta\), so the only sign data surviving after squaring are
\((c_\Delta(1,1,1))^2=4096\) (positive, automatic) and the
fermionic-shift sign \(\operatorname{sign}(C_{\square,X})=-1\), which lives in
the OP/DT chamber of Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization} (the
\((-p_{\mathrm{DT}})^n\) factor) and does not constrain \(\eta\).  So
(S3) is consistent with (S2) but does not refine it.  Combining (S1)
and (S2), \(\eta_{\mathcal C}=+1\) on each supplied connected component
whose Pfaffian branch has been compared with the monic cusp branch; any
extension to other rank-one charge components or to HN sums remains a
separate orientation datum.

The choice is determinate once the ordinary lift and quotient
linearizations have been supplied.  This is the analogue, on the
cosection-twisted reduced \(K3\times E\) rank-one sector, of the BBDJS
Pin lift sign convention of \cite[\S5.4]{BBDJS2015} and the
Joyce--Upmeier rigidification by Pfaffian normalization data
\cite{JoyceUpmeier}.  It is not a proof that
\(\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C}\) or
\(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}\) vanishes.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rmk:sign-fixing-higher-rank}
The same data \textup{(S1)}, \textup{(S2)}, \textup{(S3)} rigidify
\(\eta_{\mathcal C}\) on a higher-rank semistable stratum only after the
Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe class \(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) of
\textup{(P3)} and the required quotient linearization classes have
already vanished.
\end{remark}


\begin{lemma}[HN-reducible Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe criterion]
\label{lem:p3-higher-rank-pin-c-vanishing}
Let \(\mathcal C\) be a higher-rank protected charge and let
\(\tau=(\mathcal C_1,\ldots,\mathcal C_\ell)\) be an HN-type of length
\(\ell\ge2\) in the reduced semistable stack.  On the corresponding
HN stratum, the reduced orientation gerbe satisfies
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}|_\tau
=\sum_i\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C_i}\bmod2,
\]
with off-diagonal self-Ext blocks contributing even class.  Therefore
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}|_\tau=0\) on every HN stratum whose
graded factors lie in the already-oriented rank-one sector or in a
rank-two sector covered by Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-brauer-gerbe-vanishing}.
If, in addition, the \(E\)-equivariant parity
\[\sum_i d_E(\mathcal C_i)\operatorname{rk}(\det\mathcal C_i)\]
is even, then the joint class
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}+\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) vanishes
on that HN stratum, subject to the finite-stabilizer criterion of
Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing} on any small-orbit boundary.
Stable higher-rank length-one HN strata are not covered by this lemma.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The HN stratification expresses a length-\(\ell\) stratum as an extension
stack over the product of the moduli of its graded factors.  The
Joyce--Upmeier and Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier multiplicative orientation
formalism \cite{JoyceUpmeier,JoyceTanakaUpmeier} identifies the
orientation gerbe of the direct-sum target with the tensor product of
the gerbes of the graded pieces.  The off-diagonal reduced self-Ext
blocks occur in dual pairs under the shifted-symplectic pairing, so
their Stiefel--Whitney contribution is even.  This gives the displayed
additivity formula.  The stated vanishing follows immediately when each
graded factor lies in a sector whose orientation gerbe has already been
trivialized.

The connected \(E\)-descent obstruction is computed by the equivariant
Serre spectral sequence of the free translation quotient; on an HN
stratum its parity is the sum of the elliptic rotation numbers of the
graded factors.  If that sum is even, the connected obstruction
vanishes.  The remaining torsion part is the small-orbit finite
stabilizer gerbe; the rank-one \(N=2\) detection criterion is isolated
in Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing}.  No induction on stable
higher-rank length-one factors is used.
\end{proof}


\section{Physical charge and normal-ordered Gram descent}
\label{sec:duality-principle}

The Hall charge is additive.  The Igusa degree is not.  This section
isolates the exact defect and removes it by normal ordering.  The result
is a lattice theorem, not yet a chain-level Hall strictification.

\begin{definition}[Dyonic Mukai lattice and quadratic Gram projection]
\label{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}
Let \(S\) be a complex K3 surface and put
\[
\La_S:=H^*(S,\Z)
=H^0(S,\Z)\oplus H^2(S,\Z)\oplus H^4(S,\Z),
\]
the Mukai lattice in the sense of
Mukai \cite{Mukai1984,Mukai1987}: even, unimodular, signature
\((4,20)\), rank \(24\), equipped with the Mukai pairing
\(\langle (r,c,s),(r',c',s')\rangle_{\mathrm{Muk}}=c\cdot c'-rs'-r's\).
The formal full-Mukai dyonic lattice is the additive abelian group
\[
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}:=\La_S\oplus\La_S,\qquad
c=(Q,P)\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}},
\]
graded electric \(\oplus\) magnetic.  Throughout the formulae below in
this paper,
\[
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}.
\]
In legacy lattice formulae below the
superscript \(\mathrm{phys}\) is only mnemonic for this formal even Mukai
sector \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\).  It is not the full four-dimensional
\(\mathcal N=4\) electric--magnetic charge lattice and not compact Hall
support.  It is the D6--D2--D0/OP branch on which the Mukai Gram map is
tested before imposing algebraicity, effectivity, stability, or
nonemptiness of compact Hall moduli.  For a chosen stability sector the
actual Hall support is a semigroup
\(\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}\subset\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{alg}}
\subset\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\); membership in that semigroup is not
proved by the formal lattice arithmetic.  The Gram-index lattice is
\[
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}:=\Z^3.
\]
The Gram map is the quadratic projection
\[
\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
(Q,P)\longmapsto\bigl(\tfrac{(Q,Q)}2,(Q,P),\tfrac{(P,P)}2\bigr).
\]
The bilinear obstruction to additivity of \(\Pi_X\) is the symmetric
cocycle
\[
B:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\times\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}
\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},\qquad
B(c,c')=\bigl((Q,Q'),(Q,P')+(Q',P),(P,P')\bigr),
\]
satisfying
\(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\) and
\(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\); \([B]=0\) in
\(H^2_{\mathrm{sym}}(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\)
via Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}.  The central extension
\[
\widehat\Gamma_X:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
(c,T)\star(c',T'):=\bigl(c+c',\,T+T'+B(c,c')\bigr),
\]
has the normal-ordered Gram homomorphism
\[
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T.
\]
It is the additive abelian group on which a Hall product graded by formal
charge and normal-ordered Gram invariants can be formulated.  A compact
Hall source must still restrict this formal group to its algebraic and
effective support.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}
The quadratic-projection identity
\(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\) expands
\((Q+Q',Q+Q')/2\), \((Q+Q',P+P')\), \((P+P',P+P')/2\).
Cohomologically the central extension is split
(\([B]=0\), Remark~\ref{rem:b-cocycle-status}), but the splitting
requires the quadratic primitive \(\Pi_X\), not a linear cochain.
Dyonic charges with distinct \((Q,P)\) but identical \((n,l,m)\) sit in
the same Gram sector; the Hall bracket distinguishes them through the
physical grading on \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) before passing to Gram
invariants.
\end{remark}

The preceding determinant was constructed in one cusp chamber.  Duality
does not preserve the displayed chamber inequalities in the same
coordinates; it transports the chamber, the Fourier expansion, and the
automorphic line together.  The invariant object is
$$
\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\in M_5(\Sp_4(\Z),\nu_{\Delta_5}),
$$
with cusp expansion
$$
\mathcal D_X|_{\mathfrak c_\infty}
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.
$$

For
$$Z=\begin{pmatrix}z_1&z_2\\z_2&z_3\end{pmatrix},$$
put
$$q=e^{2\pi iz_1},\qquad r=e^{2\pi iz_2},\qquad s=e^{2\pi iz_3}.$$
For
$$
T(n,l,m)=
\begin{pmatrix}n&l/2\\ l/2&m\end{pmatrix},
\qquad n,l,m\in\Z,
$$
put
$$
(T(n,l,m),Z)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=\operatorname{tr}(T(n,l,m)Z)=nz_1+lz_2+mz_3.
$$
Then
$$x^{(n,l,m)}=\exp(2\pi i(T(n,l,m),Z)_{\mathrm{tr}})
=q^nr^ls^m.$$

\begin{definition}[Gram-index notation]
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}:=\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}:=\Z^3,\qquad
\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\subset\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\subset\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}.
$$
Here \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\) is the cusp-positive semigroup and
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\) is the non-zero Jacobi-support locus.  This is
notation for Gram invariants and Fourier indices.  It is not the compact
Hall support; the formal dyonic lattice is
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\)
of Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}, and the Gram-index lattice is
the image of the quadratic projection
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\).  A Hall
algebra cannot be graded by \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\) directly because
\(\Pi_X\) is quadratic; the correct grading lattice is the central
extension
\(\widehat\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)
(Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}).  The grading on
\(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\) by \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\) is then the
normal-ordered image of a \(\widehat\Gamma_X\)-grading on a hypothetical
Hall source whose actual support lies in an algebraic/effective
semigroup.  The chain-level lift of this image is part of the open Hall
datum.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Gram matrix convention for protected charges]
Assume a protected charge grading with primitive electric-magnetic pair
\(Q,P\) in an even lattice.  Set
$$
n=\frac{(Q,Q)}2,\qquad l=(Q,P),\qquad m=\frac{(P,P)}2.
$$
Then
$$
\begin{pmatrix}(Q,Q)&(Q,P)\\ (P,Q)&(P,P)\end{pmatrix}
=2T(n,l,m),
$$
and the Gram discriminant is
$$
\det(2T(n,l,m))=4nm-l^2.
$$
The genus-two chemical potential \(Z\) pairs with the same matrix:
$$
\exp(2\pi i\,\operatorname{tr}(TZ))=q^nr^ls^m.
$$
Thus the Borcherds monomial records the Gram invariants of the protected
charge grading, once such a physical grading has been supplied.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By hypothesis the compactification charge lattice is even, so
\((Q,Q)/2\) and \((P,P)/2\) are integral and \((Q,P)\in\Z\).  The matrix
identity and its determinant are immediate.  The final equality is the
Fourier character attached to the chemical potential \(Z\).  The
Harvey--Moore and Dijkgraaf--Verlinde--Verlinde interpretation of this
Fourier character as a physical charge grading is additional physical
input \cite{HM}, \cite{DVV}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Formal additive even Mukai sector and Gram shadow]
\label{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice}
Let \(X=S\times E\), with \(S\) a K3 surface, and let
\[
\Lambda_S:=\widetilde H(S,\Z)
=H^0(S,\Z)\oplus H^2(S,\Z)\oplus H^4(S,\Z)
\]
with Mukai pairing
\[
(r,D,s)\cdot(r',D',s')=D\cdot D'-rs'-r's.
\]
In the formal even \(K3\times E\) Mukai sector, every class decomposes as
\[
v_X=P\otimes 1_E+Q\otimes\omega_E,\qquad Q,P\in\Lambda_S,
\]
where \(\int_E\omega_E=1\).  The formal additive dyonic lattice is
\[
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}:=\Lambda_S\oplus\Lambda_S,\qquad
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}},\qquad c=(Q,P).
\]
The superscript \(\mathrm{phys}\) is retained only as a mnemonic in older
formulas for this formal sector.
For exact triangles or Hall extensions inside a supplied algebraic
effective source sector the class \(c\) is additive.  The
Igusa variables are the Gram shadow
\[
\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
\Pi_X(Q,P)=\left(\frac{Q^2}{2},\,Q\cdot P,\,\frac{P^2}{2}\right).
\]
The map \(\Pi_X\) is an invariant map to Fourier/root degrees; it is not
the compact Hall support.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Formal primitive torsion-one lift of every Gram triple]
\label{lem:primitive-lift-every-gram-triple}
Suppose \(\Lambda_S\) contains two orthogonal hyperbolic planes
\[
U_1\oplus U_2
=\mathbb Ze_1\oplus\mathbb Zf_1\oplus
\mathbb Ze_2\oplus\mathbb Zf_2,
\]
with \(e_i^2=f_i^2=0\), \(e_i\cdot f_i=1\), and \(U_1\perp U_2\).
Then every Gram triple \((n,l,m)\in\mathbb Z^3\) has a primitive
saturated formal full-Mukai lift \(c=(Q,P)\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)
with
\[
\Pi_X(Q,P)=(n,l,m).
\]
One may take
\[
Q=e_1+nf_1,\qquad
P=lf_1+e_2+mf_2.
\]
For this displayed lift the standard wedge torsion invariant
\[
I(Q,P):=
\gcd\{\hbox{coordinates of }Q\wedge P
\hbox{ in a }\Z\hbox{-basis of }\bigwedge^2\Lambda_S\}
\]
is equal to \(1\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The hyperbolic-plane pairings give
\[
Q^2=2n,\qquad P^2=2m,\qquad Q\cdot P=l.
\]
Therefore \(\Pi_X(Q,P)=(n,l,m)\).  The sublattice
\(\mathbb ZQ+\mathbb ZP\subset\Lambda_S\) is primitive because the
coefficient matrix of \(Q,P\) in the ordered basis
\((e_1,f_1,e_2,f_2)\) contains the minor
\[
\det\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&1\end{pmatrix}=1
\]
using the \(e_1,e_2\) rows.  Hence the lift is primitive saturated.
Moreover
\[
Q\wedge P
=l\,e_1\wedge f_1+e_1\wedge e_2
+m\,e_1\wedge f_2+n\,f_1\wedge e_2
+nm\,f_1\wedge f_2 .
\]
The coefficient of \(e_1\wedge e_2\) is \(1\), so the gcd of all
coordinates of \(Q\wedge P\) is \(1\).  Thus \(I(Q,P)=1\) for the
displayed formal lift.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
The obstruction in the compact Hall problem is therefore not pointwise
existence of formal charge planes with a prescribed Igusa degree.
Every formal Borcherds degree has such a primitive saturated lift, and
the displayed lift is torsion-one in the wedge sense above.  This does
not prove algebraicity, effectivity, nonempty compact moduli, duality
orbit descent, or source-index descent.  The obstruction is functorial
compatibility with Hall addition and the primitive bracket.
No Nikulin orbit-uniqueness theorem, T-duality descent of protected
indices, or DVV primitive-sector formula is used here.  The lemma proves
only the displayed formal torsion-one lift.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Gram additivity defect]
\label{lem:gram-additivity-defect}
For \(c_i=(Q_i,P_i)\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\),
\[
\Pi_X(c_1+c_2)=\Pi_X(c_1)+\Pi_X(c_2)+B(c_1,c_2),
\]
where
\[
B(c_1,c_2)=
\bigl(Q_1\cdot Q_2,\ Q_1\cdot P_2+Q_2\cdot P_1,\ P_1\cdot P_2\bigr)
\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Expand
\[
\frac{(Q_1+Q_2)^2}{2},\qquad
(Q_1+Q_2)\cdot(P_1+P_2),\qquad
\frac{(P_1+P_2)^2}{2}.
\]
The three cross terms are exactly the three components of \(B(c_1,c_2)\).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Symmetric bilinear $2$-cocycle and on-the-nose
associativity of the Gram-corrected charge product]
\label{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}
Let \(S\) be a complex K3 surface and
\(\La_S=H^*(S,\Z)\) the Mukai lattice (even unimodular, signature
\((4,20)\)).  Let
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}:=\La_S\oplus\La_S\) and
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\),
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}:=\Z^3\), and let
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\),
\(B:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\times\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) be as in
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}}, namely, with
\(c=(Q,P)\),
\[
\Pi_X(Q,P)=\bigl(\tfrac{(Q,Q)}{2},\,(Q,P),\,\tfrac{(P,P)}{2}\bigr),
\qquad
B((Q,P),(Q',P'))=\bigl((Q,Q'),(Q,P')+(Q',P),(P,P')\bigr).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] \(B\) is symmetric and \(\Z\)-bilinear, and takes
integral values: \(B\in\Hom_\Z\!\bigl(S^2\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\bigr)\subset
\Hom_\Z\!\bigl(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\otimes_\Z
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\bigr)\).
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (Polarisation.)  \(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\) for every
\(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\).
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (Symmetric Hochschild $2$-cocycle.) \(B\) is
normalised, \(B(c,0)=B(0,c)=0\), and the additive coboundary
\[
(\delta B)(a,b,c):=B(b,c)-B(a+b,c)+B(a,b+c)-B(a,b)
\]
vanishes identically.  Hence
\([B]\in H^2_{\mathrm{sym}}\!\bigl(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\bigr)\) is well defined.
\item[\textup{(iv)}] (Star-associativity on the nose.) The product on
\(\widehat\Gamma_X:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\),
\[
(c,T)\star(c',T'):=\bigl(c+c',\,T+T'+B(c,c')\bigr),
\]
is associative and commutative; the unit is \((0,0)\) and the inverse
of \((c,T)\) is \((-c,\,-T+B(c,c))=(-c,\,-T+2\Pi_X(c))\).  Thus
\((\widehat\Gamma_X,\star)\) is an abelian group, and the sequence
\[
0\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\xrightarrow{T\mapsto(0,T)}
\widehat\Gamma_X\xrightarrow{\mathrm{pr}_1}
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\longrightarrow0
\]
is a central extension of abelian groups with cocycle \(B\).
\item[\textup{(v)}] (Normal-ordered Gram map.)  The map
\[
\overline\Pi_X:\widehat\Gamma_X\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T,
\]
is a homomorphism from \((\widehat\Gamma_X,\star)\) to the additive
group \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\).
\item[\textup{(vi)}] (Splitting; \([B]=0\).)  The Gram-shadow section
\(s:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\widehat\Gamma_X\), \(s(c):=(c,\Pi_X(c))\),
is a homomorphism for \(\star\); equivalently
\(B=-\delta\Pi_X\) in
\(B^2_{\mathrm{sym}}(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\),
where \((\delta\Pi_X)(c,c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')-\Pi_X(c+c')\).  In particular
\([B]=0\), the extension is split as an extension of abelian groups, and
\((c,T)\mapsto(c,T-\Pi_X(c))\) is an isomorphism
\(\widehat\Gamma_X\xrightarrow{\sim}
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) of abelian
groups carrying \(\star\) to componentwise addition.
\item[\textup{(vii)}] (Quadratic obstruction.)  \(B\) is not the
coboundary of any \emph{linear} \(1\)-cochain
\(L:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\): if
\(B(c,c')=L(c)+L(c')-L(c+c')\) for an additive \(L\), then setting
\(c'=c\) and using \textup{(ii)} gives \(2\Pi_X(c)=2L(c)-L(2c)=0\),
i.e.\ \(\Pi_X\equiv 0\), contradiction.  Trivialising \([B]\) requires the
quadratic refinement \(\Pi_X\); the defect is a polarization-correction
class, not a separate Heisenberg extension datum.
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Write \(c=(Q,P)\), \(c'=(Q',P')\), \(c''=(Q'',P'')\) with
\(Q,Q',Q'',P,P',P''\in\La_S\), and abbreviate
\((\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,):\La_S\times\La_S\to\Z\) by juxtaposition,
\(QQ'=(Q,Q')\), so that
\(B(c,c')=(QQ',\,QP'+Q'P,\,PP')\).

\smallskip\emph{(i) Symmetry, bilinearity, integrality.}
The components \(QQ'\) and \(PP'\) are the symmetric Mukai pairing on
\(\La_S\), so each is symmetric and \(\Z\)-bilinear.  The middle
component is the polarisation
\((c,c')\mapsto QP'+Q'P\) of the symmetric biadditive form
\((c,c')\mapsto QP'+Q'P\); swapping
\((Q,P)\leftrightarrow(Q',P')\) returns \(Q'P+QP'=QP'+Q'P\), so it is
symmetric, and \(\Z\)-bilinear in each slot by bilinearity of
\((\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,)\).  Integrality of every component follows from
the unimodular even structure on \(\La_S\).

\smallskip\emph{(ii) Polarisation.}
Set \(c'=c\): the cross terms reduce to
\(QQ\), \(QP+QP=2QP\), \(PP\), so
\(B(c,c)=(Q^2,2QP,P^2)=2\Pi_X(c)\).

\smallskip\emph{(iii) Cocycle.}
Bilinearity gives normalisation \(B(c,0)=B(0,c)=0\) immediately.  For
the cocycle identity, observe that any symmetric \(\Z\)-bilinear form
\(\beta:G\times G\to A\) on an abelian group \(G\) with values in a
trivial \(G\)-module \(A\) satisfies, by bilinearity in the first slot,
\[
\beta(a+b,c)=\beta(a,c)+\beta(b,c),
\qquad
\beta(a,b+c)=\beta(a,b)+\beta(a,c).
\]
Substituting into
\((\delta\beta)(a,b,c)=\beta(b,c)-\beta(a+b,c)+\beta(a,b+c)-\beta(a,b)\),
\[
(\delta\beta)(a,b,c)=
\beta(b,c)-\beta(a,c)-\beta(b,c)+\beta(a,b)+\beta(a,c)-\beta(a,b)=0.
\]
Applied componentwise to \(B\), this yields \(\delta B=0\).  Hence
\(B\in Z^2_{\mathrm{sym}}(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\).

\smallskip\emph{(iv) Associativity, identity, inverse.}
Compute the two bracketings of
\((c,T)\star(c',T')\star(c'',T'')\):
\begin{align*}
\bigl((c,T)\star(c',T')\bigr)\star(c'',T'')
&=\bigl(c+c'+c'',\,T+T'+T''+B(c,c')+B(c+c',c'')\bigr),\\
(c,T)\star\bigl((c',T')\star(c'',T'')\bigr)
&=\bigl(c+c'+c'',\,T+T'+T''+B(c',c'')+B(c,c'+c'')\bigr).
\end{align*}
The associator is the difference of the central components,
\(\mathrm{Ass}(c,c',c'')=B(c,c')+B(c+c',c'')-B(c',c'')-B(c,c'+c'')\),
which equals \(-(\delta B)(c,c',c'')=0\) by~(iii); equivalently, it
vanishes by bilinearity of \(B\).  Commutativity follows from symmetry
of \(B\).  The identity computation
\((c,T)\star(0,0)=(c,T+B(c,0))=(c,T)\) and the inverse computation
\((c,T)\star(-c,-T+B(c,c))=(0,B(c,c)-B(c,c))=(0,0)\) (using
\(B(c,-c)=-B(c,c)\) by bilinearity) finish the abelian-group structure.
That \(B\) is the cocycle of the displayed central extension is direct
from the formula for \(\star\) and normalisation \(B(c,0)=B(0,c)=0\).

\smallskip\emph{(v) Normal-ordered Gram map.}
Using Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect},
\begin{align*}
\overline\Pi_X((c,T)\star(c',T'))
&=\overline\Pi_X(c+c',T+T'+B(c,c'))\\
&=\Pi_X(c+c')-T-T'-B(c,c')\\
&=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')-T-T'\\
&=\overline\Pi_X(c,T)+\overline\Pi_X(c',T').
\end{align*}
Thus \(\overline\Pi_X\) is additive.

\smallskip\emph{(vi) Splitting.}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect},
\(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\), so
\[
s(c)\star s(c')
=(c+c',\,\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c'))=(c+c',\,\Pi_X(c+c'))=s(c+c').
\]
Thus \(s\) is a homomorphism, and
\(B(c,c')=\Pi_X(c+c')-\Pi_X(c)-\Pi_X(c')=-(\delta\Pi_X)(c,c')\) shows
\(B=-\delta\Pi_X\), so \([B]=0\).  The change of variables
\((c,T)\mapsto(c,T-\Pi_X(c))\) is bijective on the underlying set with
inverse \((c,T)\mapsto(c,T+\Pi_X(c))\), and carries
\(\star\) to componentwise addition:
\[
(c,T-\Pi_X(c))+(c',T'-\Pi_X(c'))
=(c+c',\,T+T'-\Pi_X(c)-\Pi_X(c'))
=(c+c',\,(T+T'+B(c,c'))-\Pi_X(c+c')),
\]
matching the change of variables applied to
\((c+c',T+T'+B(c,c'))=(c,T)\star(c',T')\).

\smallskip\emph{(vii) Quadratic obstruction.}
Suppose \(B=\delta L\) for some additive
\(L:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), i.e.\
\(B(c,c')=L(c)+L(c')-L(c+c')\).  Setting \(c'=c\),
\(B(c,c)=2L(c)-L(2c)\); but \(L\) additive gives \(L(2c)=2L(c)\), so
\(B(c,c)=0\), contradicting \(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\) for any
\(c=(Q,P)\) with \((Q,Q),(Q,P),(P,P)\) not all zero.  Hence no linear
trivialisation exists; the quadratic primitive \(\Pi_X\) is necessary.

\smallskip\emph{Scope of the chain-level claim.}
Clauses (i)--(vii) prove an ordinary set-level and \(H^0\)-level
polarization correction.  They do not prove that the protected Hall
chain complex has no higher associators.  In particular no acyclicity
of a bar complex \(B_*(\widehat\Gamma_X)\) is asserted: the bar
construction of a discrete abelian group records group homology, and
cannot be used to kill Stasheff coherences.  Chain-level strictness of
the Hall product therefore remains part of the orientation/coherence
hypotheses in Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}; what this lemma
supplies is only the explicit quadratic polarization correction
\(B=-\delta\Pi_X\) and the split degree monoid on which a later
cocycle-corrected descent can act.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rem:b-cocycle-status}
The preceding lemma records the additive degree correction.  It proves that
the Gram defect is the coboundary of the quadratic refinement
\(\Pi_X\), and that the corrected degree monoid is split.  Equivalently,
the cohomology class \([B]\in H^2_{\mathrm{sym}}(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\) is nontrivial as a class in linear cochains
because \(\Pi_X\) is genuinely quadratic, not linear; so \(B\) is not the
symmetric coboundary of any linear map
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\).  The class becomes
trivial only after passing to the quadratic refinement \(\Pi_X\), which is
exactly the polarization \(\Pi_X\to-\delta\Pi_X=B\) recorded above.  The
lemma does not
strictify the Hall chain complex.  A chain-level Hall product still
requires the multiplicative orientation, cyclic equivariance, and
associator data listed in
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}; absent those data the lift is
only \(A_\infty\)-coherent, and the obstruction is tracked by the
supplied cochain \(\Theta\), not by acyclicity of a group bar complex.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Normal-ordered Gram-corrected charge extension]
\label{def:gram-corrected-charge-extension}
Set
\[
\widehat\Gamma_X:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}.
\]
For \(c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) and
\(T,T'\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), define
\[
(c,T)\star(c',T')
:=(c+c',\,T+T'+B(c,c')).
\]
The section
\[
s:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\longrightarrow\widehat\Gamma_X,\qquad
s(c)=(c,\Pi_X(c))
\]
is additive for \(\star\).  The normal-ordered Gram map is
\[
\overline\Pi_X:\widehat\Gamma_X\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T.
\]
Thus the compact Hall object, if constructed, is graded upstairs by
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), or by the refinement
\(\widehat\Gamma_X\) after the normal-ordering counterterm is recorded.
The \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded Igusa object is obtained only
after normal-ordered Gram pushforward along \(\overline\Pi_X\), or by a
chain-level categorification of the same subtraction.
\end{definition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}(i),(iii),(iv), \(\star\) is
associative and commutative, the identity is \((0,0)\), and the inverse
of \((c,T)\) is \((-c,-T+B(c,c))\); the section \(s\) is the splitting
of clause~(vi).  Clause~(v) of the same lemma proves that
\(\overline\Pi_X\) is a homomorphism.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Strict fixed-lift raw Gram descent cannot realize the
type-II real-root strings]
\label{thm:raw-gram-descent-no-go}
Let
\[
P=\bigoplus_{c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}}P_c
\]
be a \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)-graded Lie superalgebra with
\[
[P_c,P_{c'}]\subset P_{c+c'}.
\]
Suppose a strict fixed-lift raw pushforward along the quadratic map
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) were a
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded Lie superalgebra structure on the
displayed bracket channels of chosen charge lifts.  Then every non-zero
bracket channel \([P_c,P_{c'}]\) contributing to that strict raw
pushforward must satisfy
\[
B(c,c')=0.
\]
For the type-II real simple roots of the Gritsenko--Nikulin algebra,
this condition is incompatible with the non-zero second real-root
strings \(2\delta_i+\delta_j\), \(i\ne j\).  Hence these type-II
real-root brackets cannot be obtained by strict fixed-lift raw
\(\Pi_X\)-descent.  They require the
normal-ordered extension
\(\widehat\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)
and the homomorphism \(\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If the raw pushforward is \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded, then a
non-zero bracket of classes of raw Gram degrees \(\Pi_X(c)\) and
\(\Pi_X(c')\) must land in raw Gram degree
\(\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')\).  But the upstairs bracket lands in physical
degree \(c+c'\), whose raw Gram shadow is
\[
\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c').
\]
Thus every non-zero bracket channel visible in a raw pushforward must
have \(B(c,c')=0\).

Let \(c_i,c_j\) be physical lifts of two distinct type-II real simple
root degrees \(\gamma_i,\gamma_j\), so
\[
\Pi_X(c_i)=\gamma_i,\qquad \Pi_X(c_j)=\gamma_j,
\qquad \gamma_i\ne0.
\]
The Gritsenko--Nikulin real simple roots have Cartan matrix
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
2&-2&-2\\
-2&2&-2\\
-2&-2&2
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The real-root string through distinct simple roots contains non-zero
brackets in degrees \(\gamma_i+\gamma_j\) and
\(2\gamma_i+\gamma_j\); this is the low-degree real-root information
recorded in Proposition~\ref{prop:low-degree-denominator-brackets}.
The first non-zero bracket would force
\[
B(c_i,c_j)=0.
\]
The second non-zero bracket is obtained by bracketing once more with
the \(c_i\)-degree generator, so raw Gram additivity would force
\[
B(c_i,c_i+c_j)=0.
\]
By bilinearity and polarization,
\[
B(c_i,c_i+c_j)=B(c_i,c_i)+B(c_i,c_j)
=2\Pi_X(c_i)+0=2\gamma_i.
\]
Since \(\gamma_i\ne0\) in the torsion-free lattice
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), this is non-zero.  Contradiction.

The contradiction uses the fixed chosen lifts \(c_i,c_j\) and the raw
quadratic map \(\Pi_X\).  It does not exclude special isolated
\(B\)-isotropic bracket channels, and it does not decide a mixed-lift
fibre-summed raw construction in which several lifts of a single Gram
degree are combined before taking brackets.  It excludes the strict
homogeneous fixed-lift raw pushforward needed by this proof.  The
normal-ordered extension removes exactly this obstruction because
\(\overline\Pi_X\) is additive on \(\widehat\Gamma_X\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
The remaining raw problem is the fibre-summed version: one may try to
sum several charge lifts over a fixed Gram degree before bracketing.
Theorem~\ref{thm:raw-gram-descent-no-go} neither proves nor disproves
such a construction.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Normal-ordered primitive recognition target]
The interface with the denominator algebra is therefore not the raw
map \(\Pi_X\).  It is the corrected route
\[
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}
\longrightarrow
\widehat\Gamma_X
\xrightarrow{\ \overline\Pi_X\ }
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}
\xrightarrow{\ \alpha\ }
\La^{2,1}_{II}.
\]
At chain level this becomes the descent
\(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:pi-descent-of-bracket}.  The primitive recognition
problem is to construct a protected primitive Hall algebra whose
normal-ordered descended bracket is the Borcherds--Kac bracket of
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\).  Raw Gram pushforward is not an admissible
recognition target.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Gram-index pairing]
For
$$\gamma=(n,l,m),\qquad \gamma'=(n',l',m'),$$
define
$$
\langle\gamma,\gamma'\rangle_{\mathrm{ind}}
=2(nm'+n'm)-ll'.
$$
The Gram discriminant is
$$
\Delta_{\mathrm{gram}}(\gamma)
=\langle\gamma,\gamma\rangle_{\mathrm{ind}}
=4nm-l^2.
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Chamber transport]
The pairing \(\langle\ ,\ \rangle_{\mathrm{ind}}\) is the pairing on
Gram invariants.  The order on \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\) is a Fock
polarization at one cusp.  A duality element transports this
polarization to the corresponding product chamber at the transported
cusp.
\end{remark}

\part{Denominator algebra and compact Dirac--Igusa realization}

\section{The exterior-square model of the automorphic group}

The form \(\Delta_5\) is an automorphic form on the Siegel space.  The
physical U-duality interpretation of the same arithmetic group is
external input from the \(K3\times E\) compactification; it is not needed
for the lattice calculation below.  The calculation records the
first-principles bridge from the Siegel variables to the type-IV
Lorentzian lattice on which the denominator algebra is written.
\(\Sp_4(\Z)\) is the arithmetic symmetry of the genus-two chemical
potential and of the invariant Gram plane on \(\Lambda^{3,2}\); it is not
asserted to be the full T-duality or U-duality group of the \(K3\times
T^2\) compactification, which is larger.

$$\La^4=\Z e_1\oplus\Z e_2\oplus\Z e_3\oplus\Z e_4.$$
$$g\in\SL_4(\Z):\qquad
\wedge^2g:\wedge^2\La^4\longrightarrow\wedge^2\La^4.$$
$$u\wedge v=(u,v)e_1\wedge e_2\wedge e_3\wedge e_4.$$
$$\bigl(\wedge^2\La^4,(\ ,\ )\bigr)\simeq \mathrm{II}_{3,3}.$$

Fix
$$q_0=e_1\wedge e_3+e_2\wedge e_4.$$
For $x,y\in\La^4$, define
$$-x\wedge y\wedge q_0
=B_{q_0}(x,y)e_1\wedge e_2\wedge e_3\wedge e_4.$$
$$\{g\in \SL(\La^4)\mid(\wedge^2g)q_0=q_0\}\simeq\Sp_4(\Z).$$

Set
$$\La^{3,2}=q_0^\perp\subset\wedge^2\La^4.$$
$$
f_1=e_1\wedge e_2,\quad
f_2=e_2\wedge e_3,\quad
f_3=e_1\wedge e_3-e_2\wedge e_4,\quad
f_{-2}=e_4\wedge e_1,\quad
f_{-1}=e_4\wedge e_3.
$$
$$(f_1,f_{-1})=(f_2,f_{-2})=-1,\qquad (f_3,f_3)=2.$$
$$\La^{3,2}\simeq\HypPlan\oplus\HypPlan\oplus[2],\qquad
\HypPlan=\begin{pmatrix}0&-1\\-1&0\end{pmatrix}.$$

$$\Hpl^{\IV}=
\{Z\in\Proj(\La^{3,2}\otimes\C)\mid (Z,Z)=0,\ (Z,\overline Z)<0\}.$$
$$\Hpl_+^{\IV}=
\{{}^t(z_2^2-z_1z_3,\ z_3,\ z_2,\ z_1,\ 1)z_0\in\Hpl^{\IV}
\mid \Imag z_1>0\}.$$
Writing $y_i=\Imag z_i$,
$$ (Z,\overline Z)<0\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad y_1y_3-y_2^2>0.$$
$$\Hpl_+^{\IV}\simeq
\left\{\begin{pmatrix}z_1&z_2\\z_2&z_3\end{pmatrix}\in\Hpl_2\right\}.$$

Let $\Orth_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+$ be the index-two subgroup preserving
$\Hpl_+^{\IV}$.  Its kernel on $\Hpl_+^{\IV}$ is $\{\pm\Id_5\}$, and
$$\Orth_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+=\{\pm\Id_5\}\SO_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+,$$
where $\SO_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+$ has real spin-norm $1$.  Put
$$\Orth(\La^{3,2})_+ = \Orth_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+ \cap \Orth(\La^{3,2})$$
and
$$\SO(\La^{3,2})_+=\SO_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+\cap\Orth(\La^{3,2}).$$

$$M=\begin{pmatrix}m_1&m_2\\m_2&m_3\end{pmatrix},$$
$$\wedge^2(g_0)
=\wedge^2\!\left(\begin{pmatrix}0 & \Id_2 \\ -\Id_2 & 0\end{pmatrix}\right)
= \begin{pmatrix}
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1\\
0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 0\\
0 & 0 & 1 & 0 & 0\\
0 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0\\
-1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0
\end{pmatrix},$$
$$\wedge^2(g_M)
=\wedge^2\!\left(\begin{pmatrix}\Id_2 & M\\ 0 & \Id_2\end{pmatrix}\right)
= \begin{pmatrix}1 & -m_1 & 2m_2 & -m_3 & m_2^2 - m_1 m_3\\
0 & 1 & 0 & 0 & m_3\\
0 & 0 & 1 & 0 & m_2\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 1 & m_1\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 1\end{pmatrix},$$
$$\wedge^2(g_A)
=\wedge^2\!\left(\begin{pmatrix}{}^tA^{-1} & 0\\0 & A\end{pmatrix}\right)
= \det(A)\begin{pmatrix}1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\
0 & a_1^2 & -2a_1a_2 & a_2^2 & 0\\
0 & -a_1a_3 & a_1a_4 + a_2a_3 & -a_2a_4 & 0\\
0 & a_3^2 & -2a_3a_4 & a_4^2 & 0\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 1\end{pmatrix}$$

\begin{lemma}
The exterior-square representation is
$$\wedge^2 :
\Sp_4(\Z)/\{\pm \Id_4\} \rightarrow \SO_+(\La^{3,2}) \simeq
\Orth(\La^{3,2})_+/\{\pm\Id_5\}.$$
For every $g\in\Sp_4(\Z)$,

  \[ \begin{tikzcd}
\Hpl_2 \arrow{r}{} \arrow[swap]{d}{} & \Hpl_2 \arrow{d}{} \\%
\Hpl_+^{\IV} \arrow{r}{g \wedge g}& \Hpl_+^{\IV}
\end{tikzcd}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The Pfaffian pairing is preserved by $\wedge^2\SL_4$.  The subgroup
fixing
$$q_0=e_1\wedge e_3+e_2\wedge e_4$$
is the group preserving the alternating form $B_{q_0}$, namely
$\Sp_4(\Z)$.  Its action preserves $q_0^\perp=\La^{3,2}$ and the displayed
component of the type-$\IV$ domain.  The kernel on $q_0^\perp$ is
$\{\pm\Id_4\}$.  The exceptional isomorphism
$\PSp_4(\R)\simeq \SO_{\R}(3,2)_+$ identifies the image with
$\SO_+(\La^{3,2})$.  The displayed matrices are the integral generators
on both sides.  Substitution of
$${}^t(z_2^2-z_1z_3,z_3,z_2,z_1,1)z_0$$
into the two actions produces the commutative square.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Automorphic duality datum]
$$G_{\mathrm{aut}}=\PSp_4(\Z)\simeq\SO_+(\La^{3,2}).$$
The virtual determinant \(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\) is not an invariant
scalar function on
$\Hpl_2$.  It is a section of the automorphic line
$$\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5}$$
with transformation law
$$
\Delta_5(g\cdot Z)
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\det(CZ+D)^5\Delta_5(Z),
\qquad
g=\begin{pmatrix}A&B\\ C&D\end{pmatrix}\in\Sp_4(\Z).
$$
The scalar square is a section of $\mathcal L^{10}$:
$$
\Delta_5^2(g\cdot Z)=\det(CZ+D)^{10}\Delta_5^2(Z).
$$
For every scalar-square branch,
$$
Z^X_{\square}(g\cdot Z)
=\det(CZ+D)^{-10}Z^X_{\square}(Z).
$$
\end{definition}

\section{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}

Fix the primitive hyperbolic sublattice
$$\La^{2,1} = \HypPlan \oplus [2] \simeq \Z f_2 \oplus \Z f_3 \oplus \Z
f_{-2} \subset \La^{3,2}$$
and its type-II sublattice
$$
\La^{2,1}_{II}=
\{mf_2+lf_3+nf_{-2}\in\La^{2,1}\mid m\equiv n\equiv0\pmod2\}.
$$

Change polarization on the same Gram-index lattice:
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\xrightarrow{\ \alpha\ }\La^{2,1}_{II},\qquad
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}.
$$
The cusp polarization gives the Fock determinant.  The denominator
polarization gives the Borcherds chamber.

Extend $\phi\in\Orth(\La^{2,1})$ by the identity on
$(\La^{2,1})^\perp$:
$$\Orth(\La^{2,1})\hookrightarrow\Orth(\La^{3,2}).$$
For the component-preserving subgroup attached to the positive cone
below,
$$\Delta_5\in M_5(\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+,\nu_{\Delta_5}).$$

For a primitive element $\alpha \in \La^{2,1}$ satisfying
$(\alpha,\alpha)>0$ and
$$(\alpha,\alpha)\mid 2(\La^{2,1},\alpha),$$
Kac reflection \cite{KAC:1}:
$$s_{\alpha}:x\mapsto x-2\frac{(x,\alpha)}{(\alpha,\alpha)}\alpha.$$
$$s_{\alpha}(\alpha)=-\alpha,\qquad
s_{\alpha}|_{\alpha^\perp}=\Id.$$
For $(\alpha,\alpha)=2$:
$$s_{\alpha}: x \mapsto
x - (x,\alpha)\alpha.$$

\begin{lemma}
Let $(\alpha,\alpha)=2$.  For
$$\delta_1=2f_2-f_3,\qquad
\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3,\qquad
\delta_3=f_3,$$
\cite[Theorem 2.1 and Section 4]{GN}; equivalently \cite[Section 5.1.1, case (t=1,II,0)]{GNII}.
$$\Delta_5(s_{\alpha}Z) = - \Delta_5(Z)$$
when $\alpha\in\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}$.  For
$$\alpha\in\{f_{-2}-f_2,\ f_2-f_3,\ f_2+f_3\},$$
$$\Delta_5(s_{\alpha}Z) = \Delta_5(Z)$$
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Let
$$\overline U=\wedge^2\begin{pmatrix}{}^tU^{-1}&0\\0&U\end{pmatrix},
\qquad U\in\GL_2(\Z).$$
Required reflections:
$$s_{f_{-2}-f_2}=-\overline{\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\1&0\end{pmatrix}},
\qquad
s_{f_3}=-\overline{\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix}},
\qquad
s_{f_2-f_3}=-\overline{\begin{pmatrix}1&-1\\0&-1\end{pmatrix}}.$$
Maass's character has value $-1$ on
$s_{\delta_i}$ and $+1$ on the three other reflection classes.
\end{proof}

\noindent The time-like cone is
$$\Cone(\La^{2,1}) = \{ x \in \La^{2,1}
\otimes \R | (x,x) < 0\}.$$
Let $\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+$ be the component for which
$$\Omega(\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+):=
\La^{2,1}\otimes\R+i\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+\subset\Hpl^{\IV}_+.$$
For
$$z=z_3f_2+z_2f_3+z_1f_{-2}\in\Omega(\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+),$$
the type $\IV$ point is
$$Z={}^t(z_2^2-z_1z_3,\ z_3,\ z_2,\ z_1,\ 1)z_0.$$
Let $\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+$ be the index-two subgroup fixing
$\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+$.  It acts discretely on
$$\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+/\R_{>0}.$$

For $(\alpha,\alpha)>0$,
$$\Hpl_{\alpha}=
\{\R_{>0}x\in\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+/\R_{>0}\mid (x,\alpha)=0\},$$
and
$$\Hpl_{\alpha,+}=
\{\R_{>0}x\in\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+/\R_{>0}\mid (x,\alpha)\leq0\}.$$
Let $W(\La^{2,1})$ be the subgroup generated by these positive-norm
reflections:
$$W(\La^{2,1})\subset\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+.$$


Nikulin's theorem for $\HypPlan\oplus[2]$ \cite{NIKULIN}:
$$\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+=W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}),$$
where $W^{(2)}$ is generated by reflections in square-$2$ vectors.
For $k>0$ put
$$\Delta^{(k)}(\La^{2,1})=
\{\delta\in\La^{2,1}\mid \delta\ \text{primitive},\
(\delta,\delta)=k,\ s_\delta\in\Orth(\La^{2,1})\}.$$
Each $\delta\in\Delta^{(2)}(\La^{2,1})$ has one of two divisibilities:
\begin{itemize}
\item Type I: $(\delta, \La^{2,1}) = \Z$
\item Type II: $(\delta, \La^{2,1}) = 2\Z$
\end{itemize}

The type sublattices are
$$\La^{2,1}_I=
\{mf_2+lf_3+nf_{-2}\in\La^{2,1}\mid m+l+n\equiv0\pmod2\},$$
and the already defined \(\La^{2,1}_{II}\).
Type I roots lie in $\La^{2,1}_I$; type II roots lie in
$\La^{2,1}_{II}$.  The reflection subgroups are normal, with indices
$$[W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}):W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_I)]=2,\qquad
[W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}):W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})]=6.$$

The chambers are
$$\Poly'=\bigcap_{\delta\in\Poly'_{prim}}\Hpl_{\delta,+},
\qquad \Poly'\in\{\Poly,\Poly_I,\Poly_{II}\},$$
with walls
$$\Poly_{prim}=\{f_2-f_3,\ f_{-2}-f_2,\ f_3\},$$
$$\Poly_{I,prim}=\{f_2-f_3,\ f_{-2}-f_2,\ f_2+f_3\},$$
$$\Poly_{II,prim}=\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}.$$
For
$$\Aut(\Poly')=\{g\in\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+\mid g\Poly'=\Poly'\},$$
$$\Aut(\Poly)=1,\qquad
\Aut(\Poly_I)=\langle s_{f_3}\rangle,\qquad
\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3,$$
with $\Aut(\Poly_{II})$ generated by
$s_{f_2-f_3}$ and $s_{f_{-2}-f_2}$.  The chamber decomposition is
$$\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+
\simeq W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1})
\simeq W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_I)\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_I)
\simeq W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II}).$$

\begin{lemma}[Multiplier restriction]
\label{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction}
\begin{itemize}
  \item for $w \in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_I)$ and $a \in \Aut(\Poly_{I})$,
  $$\Delta_5(w \cdot a Z) = \det(a) \Delta_5(Z)$$
  \item for $w \in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})$ and $a \in \Aut(\Poly_{II})$,
  $$\Delta_5(w \cdot a Z) = \det(w) \Delta_5(Z)$$
\end{itemize}
Equivalently,
\[
\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1,\qquad i=1,2,3,
\]
and
\[
\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_{-2}-f_2})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2-f_3})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2+f_3})=+1.
\]

\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Maass's multiplier formula for the product of the ten even theta
constants is recorded in \cite[(1.3)--(1.5)]{GN}, citing
\cite{MAASS:1}.  Under the exterior-square identification
\(\PSp_4(\Z)\simeq\SO_+(\La^{3,2})\), Gritsenko--Nikulin compute the
reflection values in \cite[Proposition~2.1]{GN} and the type-II chamber
restriction in \cite[Proposition~2.2]{GN}: it is \(-1\) on the three
type-II simple reflections and trivial on the three
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)-reflections.  This is a character computation, not
a normalization computation: multiplying \(\Delta_5\) by any nonzero
scalar leaves the displayed values unchanged.  Thus the six generator
values are
exactly
\[
\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1,\qquad
\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_{-2}-f_2})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2-f_3})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2+f_3})=+1.
\]
For the type-II chamber decomposition
\[
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II}),
\]
the first line says that the restriction to \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\)
is the determinant character, while the second says that the
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)-factor acts trivially.  The type-I statement is the
parallel restriction in the decomposition
\[
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_I)\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_I),
\]
where the nontrivial chamber automorphism contributes \(\det(a)\).
\end{proof}

Set
$$\Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+
= \R_{\geq 0} \delta_1 + \R_{\geq 0} \delta_2
+ \R_{\geq 0} \delta_3$$
and
$$\Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+^* = \{ x \in \La^{2,1} \otimes \R | (x,
\delta_i) \leq 0 \}.$$
For the finite-volume chamber $\Poly_{II}$, the dual cone obeys
$$\Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+^* \subset
\overline{\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+} \subset  \Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+.$$

The Weyl vector is determined by
$$ (\rho,\delta_i)=-\frac{(\delta_i,\delta_i)}{2}=-1,\qquad i=1,2,3.$$
$$(\delta_i,\delta_j) =
\begin{pmatrix}2 & -2 & -2\\-2 & 2 & -2\\-2 & -2 & 2\end{pmatrix}.$$
$$\rho = \frac{1}{2}\delta_1 + \frac{1}{2}\delta_2 + \frac{1}{2}\delta_3 = f_2 - \frac{1}{2}f_3 + f_{-2}.$$

Also
$$\rho \in
\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+ = \Cone(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+.$$

Fix
$$z = z_1 f_{-2} + z_2 f_3 + z_3 f_2
\in \La^{2,1} \otimes \R + i\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+
= \La^{2,1}_{II} \otimes \R + i\Cone(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+.$$
The dual lattice is
$$(\La^{2,1}_{II})^* = \Z \frac{1}{2} f_2 + \Z \frac{1}{2} f_3 + \Z \frac{1}{2} f_{-2} = \frac{1}{2}\La^{2,1}.$$

\begin{definition}[Gram-index degrees in the Weyl chamber]
\label{def:gram-index-degrees-weyl-chamber}
For $\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}$ set
$$\alpha(\gamma)=\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}
\in\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
With
$$z=z_1f_{-2}+z_2f_3+z_3f_2,$$
the character of the Gram-index degree is
$$x^\gamma=q^nr^ls^m=\exp(-\pi i(\alpha(\gamma),z)).$$
For $\gamma'=(n',l',m')$,
$$
(\alpha(\gamma),\alpha(\gamma'))
=-2\langle\gamma,\gamma'\rangle_{\mathrm{ind}},
\qquad
(\alpha(\gamma),\alpha(\gamma))=-2(4nm-l^2).
$$
Thus the Borcherds degree is the Lorentzian image of the Gram-index
grading.  The Weyl chamber and real walls are part of the
Gritsenko--Nikulin/Nikulin root datum.  The cusp polarization fixed in
Section \ref{sec:duality-principle} selects the corresponding product
expansion, and the active Jacobi support gives the nonzero visible
product exponents in that chamber.
$$E_0:=\rho.$$
$$q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}=\exp(-\pi i(\rho,z)).$$
$$\exp(-2\pi i(\alpha(\gamma),z)),\qquad
\exp(-2\pi i(\rho,z)).$$
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Active support and Borcherds cone]
In the standard cusp chamber, the active support is
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}
=\{\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\mid f(nm,l)\neq0\}.
$$
The inactive triples in $\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\setminus\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}$
are ordering data only; their product exponents are zero.  The product
does not prove absence of root spaces with zero signed superdimension.
The proof-grade Borcherds cone is the real cone generated by the active
positive Gram-index degrees after the Lorentzian degree map:
$$
\Cone_{\mathrm{Borch}}
:=\R_{\geq0}\,\alpha(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}})
\subset \La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\R.
$$
The real-root hyperplanes are the walls used by the denominator
identity in this polarization.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Active support gives the type-II chamber cone]
\label{lem:active-support-type-ii-cone}
For $\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}$,
$$
\alpha(\gamma)
=n\delta_1+m\delta_2+(n+m-l)\delta_3,
$$
with
$$n\ge0,\qquad m\ge0,\qquad n+m-l\ge0.$$
Consequently
$$
\Cone_{\mathrm{Borch}}
=\R_{\geq0}\delta_1+\R_{\geq0}\delta_2+\R_{\geq0}\delta_3.
$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The displayed decomposition is
$$
n(2f_2-f_3)+m(2f_{-2}-f_3)+(n+m-l)f_3
=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}.
$$
The effective chamber gives $n,m\ge0$.  Since
$\phi_{0,1}$ is weak of index one, $f(nm,l)\ne0$ implies
$4nm-l^2\ge-1$.  If $n=0$ or $m=0$, this gives $l^2\le1$, and the
boundary cases in $\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}$ give $l\le n+m$.  If
$n,m>0$ and $l\ge n+m+1$, then
$$
l^2\ge(n+m+1)^2
=4nm+(n-m)^2+2(n+m)+1>4nm+1,
$$
contradicting $l^2\le4nm+1$.  Hence $n+m-l\ge0$.
The reverse inclusion follows from the active triples
$$
(1,0,0),\qquad (0,0,1),\qquad (0,-1,0),
$$
whose degrees are $\delta_1+\delta_3$, $\delta_2+\delta_3$, and
$\delta_3$, and from the active triples
$$
(1,1,0),\qquad (0,1,1),
$$
whose degrees are $\delta_1$ and $\delta_2$.
\end{proof}

For $n,l,m \in \Z$ with $n \equiv m \equiv l \equiv 1 \mod 2$,
$n,m > 0$ and
$4nm - l^2 > 0$, set
$$a = (n-1) f_2 - \frac{l-1}{2} f_3 + (m-1) f_{-2},
\qquad
m(a) = -\frac{1}{64} c_\Delta(n,l,m).$$
\cite[Theorem 2.1]{GN}
$$\rho+a=nf_2-\frac l2f_3+mf_{-2},$$
and
$$\frac{1}{64}c_\Delta(n,l,m)\exp(\pi i (n z_1 + lz_2 + m z_3)) $$
$$= \frac{1}{64} c_\Delta(n,l,m)
\exp\left(- \pi i\left(nf_2-\frac{l}{2}f_3+mf_{-2}, z\right)\right)$$
$$= -m(a) \exp (-\pi i(\rho +a, z)),$$
with
$$a\in(\La^{2,1})^*=\frac{1}{2}\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
The normalization $c_\Delta(1,1,1)=64$ fixes $m(0)=-1$.  Since
$c_\Delta(n,l,m)\in64\Z$, all $m(a)$ are integral.  The inequality
$4nm-l^2>0$ implies
$$\rho+a\in \Cone(\La^{2,1})_+.$$

Let $\lambda=\rho+a$.  For nonzero coefficients in the chosen chamber,
$$\lambda\in(\La^{2,1}_{II})^*\cap\R_+\Poly_{II},\qquad
(\lambda,\delta_i)\leq0.$$
If $(\lambda,\delta_i)=0$, then
$$c_\lambda=-c_\lambda=0.$$
For nonzero terms, $(\lambda,\delta_i)<0$.  Since
$(\rho,\delta_i)=-1$,
$$(a,\delta_i)\leq0,\qquad
a\in\Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})^*_+.$$
$$a \in \R_{\geq 0} \Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+^* \cap
\overline{\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+} = \R_{\geq 0} \Poly_{II}.$$
The congruences $m\equiv n\equiv l\equiv1\pmod2$ imply
$$a\in 2(\La^{2,1})^*=\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
$$a=0\qquad\hbox{or}\qquad
a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}.$$


\begin{lemma}
$$\frac{1}{64}\Delta_5(Z)
=\displaystyle\sum_{w \in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})} \text{det}(w)( \exp(-\pi
i(w(\rho),z))- \sum_{a \in \La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}}
m(a)\exp(-\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)))$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Let $c_\lambda$ be the coefficient of $e^{-\pi i(\lambda,z)}$ in
$64^{-1}\Delta_5$.  The leading term has
$$\lambda=\rho,\qquad c_\rho=1.$$
The other exponents in the chosen chamber have
$$\lambda=\rho+a,\qquad
a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II},\qquad
c_{\rho+a}=-m(a).$$
Anti-invariance:
$$c_{w\lambda}=\det(w)c_\lambda.$$
If $\lambda$ lies on a simple wall, then
$$s_{\delta_i}\lambda=\lambda,\qquad c_\lambda=-c_\lambda=0.$$
Summing the signed Weyl translates proves the formula.
\end{proof}

The primitive isotropic rays of $\overline{\Poly_{II}}$ are generated by
$$2f_2,\qquad 2f_{-2},\qquad 2f_2-2f_3+2f_{-2}.$$
The group $\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3$ is transitive on these three
vectors.  For $a_0=2f_2$:

$$1 + \frac{1}{64} \sum_{t \geq 1} c_\Delta(1 + 2t, 1, 1)q^t = \displaystyle\prod_{k\geq 1} (1
- q^k)^9$$

In denominator notation,

$$ 1 - \sum_{t \geq 1} m(t a_0) q^t = \displaystyle\prod_{t\geq 1}
(1 - q^t)^{\tau(t a_0)},\qquad \tau(t a_0)=9\quad(t\geq1).$$

By $S_3$-symmetry,
$$\tau(ta)=9\qquad(t\geq1)$$
for every primitive isotropic ray
$$\Z_{>0}a\subset
\overline{\Poly_{II}}\cap\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
On isotropic rays, the coefficients $m(ta)$ are determined by the
eta-product expansion; the signed simple-root supermultiplicity is
\(\tau(ta)\).  The imaginary simple roots of $\autcor$ are these
isotropic and timelike rays in $\overline{\Poly_{II}}\cap\La^{2,1}_{II}$,
with multiplicities $\tau(a)$ on isotropic rays and $m(a)$ on
negative-norm rays \cite[Theorem 2.1]{GN}, \cite[(5.1), Section 5.1.1]{GNII}.


The real root datum is the wall set
$$\Poly_{II,prim}=\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}$$
with Gram matrix \cite[Theorem 4.1]{GN} (and \cite[Section 5.1.1, case (t=1,II,0)]{GNII} as secondary)

$$(\delta_i,\delta_j) = \begin{pmatrix}2 & -2 & -2\\-2 & 2 & -2\\-2 & -2 & 2\end{pmatrix}$$

\begin{definition}[Simple real roots and perturbative walls]
$$\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}=\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\},\qquad
\Delta^{re}=W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}},$$
$$
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{pert}}
=\bigcup_{\delta\in\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}}\Hpl_\delta.
$$
\end{definition}

\section{The denominator algebra}

$$A=((\delta_i,\delta_j))_{1\leq i,j\leq3}
=\begin{pmatrix}2&-2&-2\\-2&2&-2\\-2&-2&2\end{pmatrix}$$
$$A\ \hbox{symmetric generalized Cartan},\qquad
\bkm(A)\ \hbox{Kac--Moody}.$$
$$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}:=\autcor.$$
This is the target-internal algebraic denominator square root.  It is the
automorphic correction of $\bkm(A)$ constructed by
Gritsenko--Nikulin \cite[Sections~3--4]{GN}, with root spaces graded by the Gram-degree
map
$$
\gamma=(n,l,m)\longmapsto
\alpha(\gamma)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}.
$$
The Borcherds correction character in the coefficient chamber is
$$\mathcal C_{\mathrm{im}}(z)
=1-\sum_{a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}}
m(a)e^{-2\pi i(a,z)}.$$
$$e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}\mathcal C_{\mathrm{im}}(z).$$

Signed root-superdimension convention; Harvey--Moore is the external
physical interpretation \cite{HM}:
$$\smult(\alpha)
=\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha,\overline 0}
-\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha,\overline 1}.$$
Let \(\mathcal R\) be the root set of
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\), and let \(\mathcal R_+\) be the positive
root set in the \(\Poly_{II}\)-chamber.

\begin{definition}[Denominator Lie superalgebra]
For $\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}$ set
$$
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}
:=
\begin{cases}
\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C,&\gamma=0,\\
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(\gamma)},&\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R,\\
0,&\alpha(\gamma)\notin\mathcal R.
\end{cases}
$$
The zero degree is the Cartan subalgebra and is not governed by
\(f(0,0)\).  The bracket is the Borcherds--Kac--Moody bracket of
\(\autcor\):
$$
[\ ,\ ]:
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}
\otimes
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma'}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma+\gamma'}.
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Denominator algebra identity]
\label{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}
\label{thm:bracket-level-square-root}
The denominator Lie superalgebra has the following properties.
$$
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}
=\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},0}\oplus
\bigoplus_{\substack{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\\
\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R}}
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}
=\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},0}
\oplus\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}^{\mathrm{bulk}}
\oplus\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}^{\mathrm{cusp}},
\qquad
[\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma},\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma'}]
\subset \mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma+\gamma'},
$$
where
$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}^{\mathrm{bulk}}
=\bigoplus_{\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R,\,m(\gamma)>0}
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}$
records the $m>0$ Borcherds bulk and
$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}^{\mathrm{cusp}}
=\bigoplus_{\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R,\,m(\gamma)=0}
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}$
records the $m=0$ Weyl-chamber cusp boundary, in parallel with the
$\mathcal V=\mathcal V_{\mathrm{bulk}}\oplus\mathcal V_{\mathrm{cusp}}$
splitting at the determinant level above.
Its visible positive signed Gram-degree multiplicities are the K3 half-index
coefficients:
$$
\smult(\alpha(n,l,m))=f(nm,l)
\qquad((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}).
$$
Its Weyl--Kac--Borcherds denominator is
$$
\operatorname{den}(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}})
=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z).
$$
The theorem concerns the Borcherds denominator algebra.  A microscopic
BPS Hilbert space and its operator product require separate
construction.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Gritsenko--Nikulin \cite[Theorem 2.1, (2.1)--(2.3)]{GNII} construct $\autcor$ as the generalized
Borcherds--Kac--Moody superalgebra whose real simple roots are
$\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3$ and whose imaginary simple-root
multiplicities are read from the Borcherds correction character.  A
product exponent gives the signed multiplicity of a visible positive
root; the simple imaginary-root datum is Gritsenko--Nikulin's \(m(a)\)
for negative-norm \(a\) and \(\tau(a)\) on isotropic rays.  These are
different pieces of the denominator construction.  A
root-graded Lie superalgebra has
$$
[\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha},\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\beta}]
\subset\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha+\beta}.
$$
Here \(\alpha\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C\), and the addition
\(\alpha+\beta\) is linear inside the Cartan; this is the linear root
grading of a Borcherds--Kac superalgebra.  The Gram-degree map
\[
\gamma=(n,l,m)\longmapsto\alpha(\gamma)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}
\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C
\]
is the inverse correspondence of root indexing: it is additive in
\((n,l,m)\) and recovers the linear addition in
\(\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C\).  This linear additivity is the relevant
statement for the denominator algebra of \(\Delta_5\), where the grading
lattice is \(\La^{2,1}_{II}\) and \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}=\Z^3\) is the
Gram parametrization of that grading.  In a hypothetical Hall source,
the underlying lattice is the physical
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\), the Hall bracket is
graded by \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) (additive), and the
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\)-grading of the denominator algebra is the
\(\Pi\)-image, well defined modulo the cocycle \(B\) of
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}.  The denominator identity reads
$$
\frac1{64}\Delta_5(2Z)
=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)})^{\smult(\alpha)}.
$$
Comparing this with the Borcherds product gives
$$
\smult(\alpha(n,l,m))=f(nm,l)
\qquad((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}).
$$
\end{proof}

\section{Compact Dirac--Igusa realization problem}
\label{sec:compact-dirac-igusa-realization-problem}

The denominator algebra is the target.  A compact \(K3\times E\)
theory would be a source.  The distinction is between observables and
states.  The formal current envelope below is an observable algebra
attached to the imported Borcherds--Kac--Moody target; it is not a
compact BPS state space and it contains no Hall extension
correspondences.  Its target-side bar--cobar counit remains internal to
that observable algebra.  A genuine Dirac--Igusa realization must supply
the state-side Hall object, the orientation/Pfaffian line, the
normal-ordered Gram descent, and the chiral Koszul comparison before
one may identify its primitives with \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\).
Throughout this compact realization problem, \(S\) is a smooth complex
K3 surface and \(E\) is a smooth elliptic curve; singular K3 limits and
nodal or cuspidal elliptic degenerations belong to the boundary
certificate, not to the standing compact source datum.

\begin{definition}[Formal current envelope]
Let $E$ be the elliptic curve in $X=S\times E$.  Put
$$
\operatorname{Cur}_E(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}})
:=\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\otimes\mathcal O_E
$$
with the level-zero current bracket
$$
[a\otimes f,b\otimes g]=[a,b]\otimes fg.
$$
Its chiral enveloping algebra in the sense of Beilinson--Drinfeld
\cite{BD} is
$$
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}
:=U_E^{\mathrm{ch}}\!
\left(\operatorname{Cur}_E(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}})\right).
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Formal current envelope]
\label{prop:formal-current-envelope}
\label{thm:factorization-square-root}
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) is the formal completed ind
Beilinson--Drinfeld current envelope on \(E\) obtained from the
denominator Lie superalgebra.  Its constant-current Lie superalgebra is
\(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\), and the denominator of that
constant-current bracket is
$$
64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z).
$$
A compact \(E_3\)/Hall/chiral BPS realization requires additional
microscopic input.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
In the completed ind setting, the current construction sends a Lie
superalgebra to a Lie-* algebra on a smooth curve, and the chiral
enveloping construction sends a Lie-* algebra to a chiral algebra
\cite{BD}; equivalently, in vertex-algebra language, this is the
universal current vertex algebra at level zero \cite{KACVA}.  Constant
sections of
$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\otimes\mathcal O_E$ recover the original Lie
superalgebra.  The denominator statement is exactly
Theorem \ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Holomorphic \(E_3\) quantum upgrade]
The determinant and denominator results above are protected
Euler-characteristic statements.  The expected quantum upgrade does not
start from the scalar determinant.  It would start from a supplied
holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra on the Calabi--Yau threefold
$$
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X,\qquad X=K3\times E.
$$
By a holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra is meant here: a
factorization algebra on \(X\) in the sense of Costello--Gwilliam
(\cite{CostelloGwilliam1}, \cite{CostelloGwilliam2} esp.~vol.~II
\S10--11), locally constant in real directions and holomorphic in three
complex directions, whose factorization structure maps are governed by
holomorphic polydiscs in \(\C^3\); equivalently a factorization algebra
in the holomorphic \(E_3\)-operadic sense, together with whatever
homotopy/framing datum is required by the chosen operadic model.  No
identification with an \(SO(6)\) or \(SO(3)\) framed topological
operad is asserted here.  This symbol, and the placeholder
\(\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_3(X)\), denote the source object required in the
Calabi--Yau-to-chiral construction; they are not a constructed functor
evaluated on \(X\).
The candidate concrete realization, supplied as a conditional schema, is
the local protected observable algebra
\(\mathcal A_X(U)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}.
A compact holomorphic-Chern--Simons/BV model, if constructed with the
required descent, quantum master equation, and anomaly cancellation,
would be a candidate source for this datum in the completed charge
category.  Such a source also requires a chosen \(E_3\)-formality point,
a chain-level homotopy/framing datum for the chosen operadic model,
compact-support control, and
finite-stage HN quotients on which all operations are defined before
passing to the completed inverse system.

The curve-level BPS algebra would be obtained only after a supplied
chain-level specialization along the \(K3\)-direction.  Split the triple
identification into three named pieces, each carrying a separately
labelled comparison map:
\[
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X
\xrightarrow{\ \mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\ }
\mathcal F_X^{(0)}
\xrightarrow{\ \kappa_E\ }
\mathcal F_X^{(1)}
\xrightarrow{\ \pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\ }
(p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X.
\]
Here:
\(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\) is required to be a chain-level
K3-integration/factorization-pushforward datum along the
\(K3\)-fibration \(p_E:K3\times E\to E\), comparing the relevant
Beilinson--Drinfeld and Costello--Gwilliam models.  Its source category,
target category, support condition, charge grading, and functorial
transition squares are part of the supplied datum; its output
\(\mathcal F_X^{(0)}\) is intended to be a chiral algebra on \(E\)
(equivalently a factorization algebra on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)).
\(\kappa_E\) is the chiral-to-ordinary pushforward/formality comparison
\(\mathcal F_X^{(0)}\to\mathcal F_X^{(1)}\), not the source cobar
comparison \(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}\),
where \(\mathcal F_X^{(1)}\) is the candidate identification of the
chiral pushforward with the ordinary derived pushforward
\((p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) regarded as a sheaf-of-cochain factorization
algebra on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\); identification of
chiral and ordinary pushforward is the open chiral-Koszul comparison.
\(\pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\) is required to be the closing identification of
\(\mathcal F_X^{(1)}\) with \((p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) as
factorization data, comparing the Costello--Gwilliam push along a
proper holomorphic submersion with the topological pushforward; this
comparison is required to reduce to the standard projection-finite
comparison and is open in the wrapped sectors.  The convenient shorthand
\(\mathcal F_X\) refers to any one of \(\mathcal F_X^{(0)}\),
\(\mathcal F_X^{(1)}\), or \((p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) once
\(\kappa_E\) and \(\pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\) have been supplied.  Without
the chiral-Koszul comparison and the proper-pushforward identification,
the three names are distinct objects.
Restrictions to chambers, pushforwards to \(E\), and chiral Koszul
dualities are then operations on \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) and on its
\(E_1\)-chiral shadow \(\mathcal F_X\), not replacements for the
\(E_3\)-source.

After these data have been constructed, the required Igusa statement is
the pair of comparisons
$$
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X)
\stackrel{?}{\cong}
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5},
\qquad
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\stackrel{?}{\simeq}
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
$$
Here \(C_X\) is the source coalgebra later formalized in
Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-source-certificate}; in wrapped
degree it is attached to the hybrid object
\(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}\), not merely to the projection-finite
Ran shadow.  The first comparison would be the bracket theorem.  The
second would be the chiral Koszul theorem.  Both require microscopic data
beyond the scalar square and beyond the formal current envelope.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Compact holomorphic \(E_3\) source interface]
\label{def:compact-e3-source-interface}
Fix a stability sector \((\sigma,S)\) and the finite HN height
quotients of Proposition~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}.  A compact
holomorphic \(E_3\) source interface for \(X=K3\times E\) is not, by
itself, a compact quantum field theory.  It is the following finite-first
chain datum:
\[
\mathbb A_{X,\sigma,S}^{E_3}
=\left\{
\mathcal A_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{E_3},\,
\rho_{R'R},\,m_{\mathcal U,R},\,
S_R,\{-,-\}_R,\Delta_R^{\mathrm{BV}},\,
\eta_{\mathcal V,R},\omega_{\mathrm{QME},R},
\omega_{\mathrm{anom},R},\,
\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E,R}
\right\}_{R>0,\ R'\ge R}.
\]
Here \(\mathcal A_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{E_3}\) is a charge-supported
cochain-level holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization object with charges in
\(\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)\); \(\rho_{R'R}\) are transition maps for the
HN inverse system; \(m_{\mathcal U,R}\) are the structure maps attached to
disjoint holomorphic polydiscs \(\mathcal U\subset X\);
\(S_R,\{-,-\}_R,\Delta_R^{\mathrm{BV}}\) are the finite BV action,
antibracket, and BV Laplacian conventions used to formulate the finite
classical or quantum master equation; \(\eta_{\mathcal V,R}\) are
Cech--Weiss descent cochains for the chosen holomorphic-polydisc cover
\(\mathcal V\); \(\omega_{\mathrm{QME},R}\) and
\(\omega_{\mathrm{anom},R}\) are the finite QME and anomaly cocycles with
specified null-homotopies; and
\(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E,R}\) is the finite-stage K3-to-\(E\)
specialization datum, including source, target, support, charge grading,
wrapped-sector compatibility, and transition squares.  The interface is
required to carry:
\begin{enumerate}
\item descent, QME, and anomaly-cancellation witnesses at every finite
height \(R\), i.e.
\[
d_R S_R+\frac12\{S_R,S_R\}_R
\quad\hbox{or}\quad
d_R S_R+\frac12\{S_R,S_R\}_R+\hbar\Delta_R^{\mathrm{BV}}S_R
\]
is killed by the supplied finite homotopy
\(\omega_{\mathrm{QME},R}\), and the local anomaly cocycle is killed by
\(\omega_{\mathrm{anom},R}\), compatibly with \(\rho_{R'R}\);
\item a fixed \(E_3\)-formality point and a homotopy/framing witness for
the chosen holomorphic \(E_3\)-operadic model, treated as a chosen
torsor point rather than a canonical equality;
\item compatibility of \(m_{\mathcal U,R}\), specialization, and the
transition maps \(\rho_{R'R}\);
\item compact-support control and continuity for the HN inverse system,
with \(\mathcal A_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{E_3}\) a quotient by a
factorization ideal killing outputs of height \(>R\), and with every
structure map \(m_{\mathcal U,R}\) descended from higher stages;
\item the rule that the K3-to-\(E\) specialization is an ordinary
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)-factorization object only on the
projection-finite part; positive elliptic degree must be routed through
the hybrid wrapped datum of
Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate}.
\end{enumerate}
If all finite stages and transition maps are supplied, the completed
source is the inverse limit
\[
\mathcal A_{X}^{E_3}:=
\varprojlim_R\mathcal A_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{E_3}.
\]
This equation is a construction from the displayed finite data, not an
existence theorem for those data.
\end{definition}

\begin{openproblem}[Compact holomorphic \(E_3\) source]
\label{op:compact-e3-source}
Construct a nonempty interface
\(\mathbb A_{X,\sigma,S}^{E_3}\) in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-e3-source-interface}, and hence the completed
source object \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\), for \(X=K3\times E\).  A candidate
compact holomorphic-Chern--Simons/BV construction must prove, before any
comparison with \(\Delta_5\), the following finite-chain data:
\begin{enumerate}
\item descent for local observables on \(X\) and a quantum master
equation after compact charge completion;
\item anomaly cancellation, a fixed \(E_3\)-formality point in the
sense of Tamarkin--Kontsevich formality for \(E_n\)-operads
\cite{TamarkinLittleDisks,KontsevichOperadsMotives,LambrechtsVolicLittleDisks},
and a chain-level homotopy/framing datum for the chosen holomorphic
\(E_3\)-operadic model; compact-support control;
\item a finite-first sectorial completion compatible with
Harder--Narasimhan quotients, with all operations defined on finite
stages before completion;
\item the chain-level \(K3\)-to-\(E\) specialization
\(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\);
\item the projection-finite local sector and the hybrid wrapped repair
for positive elliptic degree;
\item a strong orientation, protected integration, and primitive
recognition certificate.
\end{enumerate}
Existing BV, CoHA, and chiral-algebra formalisms give the language for
these requirements.  They do not, by themselves, construct this compact
source for \(K3\times E\).  The external open data are: the
\(E_3\)-formality point (Tamarkin--Kontsevich formality at a chosen
associator, regarded here as a chosen torsor point
\cite{TamarkinLittleDisks,KontsevichOperadsMotives,LambrechtsVolicLittleDisks};
rationality of formality is open over \(\Q\) but known over \(\R\)), and the chain-level
homotopy/framing datum for the
chosen holomorphic \(E_3\)-operadic model; chain-level constructibility
for the candidate concrete realization
\(\mathcal A_X(U)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra} is open).
\end{openproblem}

\begin{remark}[Where the quantum comparison would live]
