Assume the source algebra \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\), the specialization
\(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\), a conilpotent coalgebra
\(C_X\) with supplied comparison
\[
b_X:C_X\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}),
\]
and a
quasi-isomorphism
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}
\]
have all been supplied.  Then \(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) is the place where the
protected primitive bracket and the chiral Koszul comparison must be
formulated.  Costello--Gwilliam locality explains why a holomorphic
quantum theory would produce factorization products before any trace or
determinant is taken \cite{CostelloRenormalization},
\cite{CostelloGwilliam1}, \cite{CostelloGwilliam2}; Beilinson--
Drinfeld chiral operations are the curve-level algebraic form of
collision maps \cite{BD}.  None of this is obtained from the scalar
square or from the denominator identity alone.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Pushforward, restriction, Koszul duality]
The second step is specialization, not inversion.  A restriction to a chamber
or sector is a restriction of \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) before, or of
\(\mathcal F_X\) after, the \(K3\)-specialization.  Pushforward along
\(p_E\) is the geometric notation for the same specialization.  A
compact Koszul theorem would require a supplied conilpotent coalgebra
\(C_X\), an identification
$$
C_X\stackrel{?}{\simeq} \bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}),
$$
and a further quasi-isomorphism
$$
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\stackrel{?}{\simeq}
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
$$
These are not procedures for reconstructing the holomorphic
\(E_3\)-source from the denominator alone.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Target-internal bar--cobar counit]
\label{prop:target-internal-bar-cobar-inversion}
Choose an augmented filtered model of the formal target
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) whose finite charge truncations lie in the
conilpotent chiral setting where Francis--Gaitsgory chiral Koszul
duality applies.  Then the target has its own bar--cobar counit:
\[
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E})
\longrightarrow
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
\]
The filtration used here is target-internal: it is the charge filtration
on the imported current envelope, together with the chosen augmentation.
It is not the source filtration \(F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,\bullet}\), and its
bar coalgebra is not \(C_{X,R}\).  Cf.\ Kac \cite{KACVA} for the
underlying vertex algebra structure, Beilinson--Drinfeld
\cite[\S3.7]{BD} for the chiral bar--cobar formalism, and
Francis--Gaitsgory \cite[Theorem~6.2.2]{FrancisGaitsgoryCKD} for chiral
Koszul duality in the conilpotent setting.  The counit reconstructs the already defined
target from its target bar coalgebra.  It is not the compact Koszul
comparison
\[
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\stackrel{?}{\simeq}
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}
\]
unless \(C_X\) has first been constructed from the compact
\(K3\times E\) factorization object and identified with
\(\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}})\).  The missing datum is the
source coalgebra, its collision coproduct, and the source comparison
map, not a homotopy inverse to the target-side counit.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Beilinson--Drinfeld bar--cobar formalism is an adjunction on chiral
algebras and conilpotent chiral coalgebras on the curve
\cite[\S3.7]{BD}.  Applying this formalism to the known target
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\), after choosing the displayed augmented
filtered model, produces a tautological counit map back to that target.
The finite charge filtration is used only to place this target
calculation in the conilpotent formal category.  No moduli stack of
compact objects, source collision coproduct, orientation system,
protected integration map, or primitive representative enters this
construction.  Those are precisely the extra data in
Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Source--target separation for the Koszul lane]
\label{lem:source-target-koszul-separation}
Fix a finite height \(R\).  The target counit
\[
\varepsilon_{\Delta,R}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R})
\longrightarrow
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}
\]
is a morphism internal to the imported current envelope.  A source
Koszul certificate is different data: it must first construct
\[
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}},\qquad
C_{X,R},\qquad
F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,\bullet},\qquad
\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}},
\]
from the finite hybrid correspondence category
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), its quotient functor \(Q_{E,R}\),
orientations, the eight-word two-step binary flag atlas, and the
separate higher colored configuration residual; only then may it compare
\[
b_{X,R}:C_{X,R}\simeq
\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
\bigl(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}},
\varepsilon_{X,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\bigr),
\qquad
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_{X,R}\simeq
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}.
\]
Thus setting \(C_{X,R}=\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R})\), or choosing a homotopy inverse to
\(\varepsilon_{\Delta,R}\), does not produce a source certificate.  It
sets the separation residual \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{sep}}_R\) to zero
only after an independent source construction of \(C_{X,R}\),
\(F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,\bullet}\), \(\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}\), and
\(b_{X,R}\) has been supplied and identified with the target-side model.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The domain of \(\varepsilon_{\Delta,R}\) contains only the target
augmentation, target charge filtration, and target chiral operations.  It
does not contain the rigidified wrapped prequotients, anchors, mixed
local/wrapped correspondences, quotient-after-correspondence functor,
orientation transport, protected integration, or primitive
representatives.  These are the data from which the source coalgebra and
collision coproduct are required to be built.  Therefore a target
bar--cobar inverse can be compared with a source coalgebra after that
coalgebra exists; it cannot define the source coalgebra or its primitive
restriction.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Chiral Koszul source certificate]
\label{def:chiral-koszul-source-certificate}
Fix \((\sigma,S,R)\), the finite HN support
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\), and the Gram image \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\).  Let
\[
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}
\]
denote the charge-truncation of the formal current envelope
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) to the finite set of Gram degrees
\(\Gamma_R^\Pi\).  A finite-stage chiral Koszul source certificate is a
datum
\[
\mathfrak K^{\mathrm{Kos}}_{X,R}
=
\left(
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}},
C_{X,R},
F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,\bullet},
\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}},
b_{X,R},
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}
\right)
\]
with the following properties.  Every entry is source-side finite data
except for the terminal comparison with the imported target
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}\).  In particular, neither
\(\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R})\) nor a
homotopy inverse to the target counit is allowed to define
\(C_{X,R}\), \(F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,\bullet}\), or
\(\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}\).  This is the source/target separation of
Lemma~\ref{lem:source-target-koszul-separation}.
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Source chiral object.}
\(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) is the finite hybrid
object of Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate}.
Its \(b_R=0\) part comes from the \(K3\)-specialized
\(E_3\)-source; its \(b_R>0\) part is present only through the rigidified
wrapped prequotient, the ordered two-sided mixed operations, the full
flag atlas, quotient-after-correspondence descent, and protected
integration.  Equivalently, the hybrid residual
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}\) has been trivialized at this height.  A
detached global Fock or Hecke factor does not supply this entry unless it
acts through the displayed mixed correspondences before the reduced
\(E\)-quotient.

\item \emph{Conilpotent chiral coalgebra.}
\(C_{X,R}\) is a coaugmented conilpotent chiral coalgebra on \(E\), with
coaugmentation \(\eta_R^C:k\to C_{X,R}\) and counit
\(\varepsilon_R^C:C_{X,R}\to k\), filtered by a finite increasing source
charge filtration
\[
0=F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,-1}\subset F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,0}
\subset\cdots\subset F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,N_R}=C_{X,R}
\]
whose associated graded pieces are finite dimensional in each
\(\Gamma_R^\Pi\)-degree.  Its reduced iterated coproduct is nilpotent on
each finite stage.  The chiral coproduct
\(\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}\) is the collision coproduct attached to the
finite Hall/factorization correspondences, including local-local,
all ordered local-wrapped, wrapped-wrapped, and eight-word flag stacks.
It is a finite pull-push construction on the collision correspondence
before \(Q_{E,R}\), and after quotient it satisfies the coalgebra
identities
\[
(\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}\otimes 1)\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}
=(1\otimes\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}})\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}},
\qquad
(\varepsilon_R^C\otimes1)\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}
=(1\otimes\varepsilon_R^C)\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}
=\mathrm{id}.
\]
For \(R'\ge R\) the transition map
\(\rho^C_{R'R}:C_{X,R'}\to C_{X,R}\) preserves the filtration and makes
the finite coproduct square commute:
\[
\begin{tikzcd}
C_{X,R'} \arrow[r,"\Delta_{R'}^{\mathrm{ch}}"]
\arrow[d,"\rho^C_{R'R}"']
& C_{X,R'}\otimes C_{X,R'}
\arrow[d,"\rho^C_{R'R}\otimes\rho^C_{R'R}"]\\
C_{X,R} \arrow[r,"\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}"']
& C_{X,R}\otimes C_{X,R}.
\end{tikzcd}
\]
This finite diagram is the source of the completed coproduct on
\(C_X=\varprojlim_R C_{X,R}\).  The coproduct is not transported from
\(\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R})\) along
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\), and no completed tensor statement is made
before these finite squares commute.

\item \emph{Bar comparison.}
There is a charge-preserving quasi-isomorphism of conilpotent chiral
coalgebras
\[
b_{X,R}:C_{X,R}
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
\bigl(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}},
\varepsilon_{X,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\bigr).
\]
It is compatible with primitive projection, the completed Hopf pairing,
the reduced \(E\)-quotient, and the normal-ordered descent
\(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\).  This is a source-side comparison map,
not the tautological bar construction of the target envelope.  Its target
is the reduced bar construction of the supplied augmented hybrid source
object, with length pieces generated by the augmentation ideal, not the bar
construction of \(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}\).

\item \emph{Cobar comparison with the target envelope.}
There is a charge-preserving quasi-isomorphism of augmented chiral
algebras
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_{X,R}
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}.
\]
On constant-current primitives, after the Hopf-radical quotient, this map
restricts to the primitive recognition morphism
\[
\iota_R^{\Prim}:
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}
(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}})
\longrightarrow
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\le R}.
\]
Here \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\le R}\) is the same finite
\(\Gamma_R^\Pi\)-truncation on constant currents.  The target is the
imported Beilinson--Drinfeld current envelope of the
Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator algebra.  The map does not construct the
compact source and is not obtained from the scalar square.  Its direction
is source-to-target.  A chosen homotopy inverse, if one exists after
localization or completion, is not part of the certificate and cannot be
used to define the source coalgebra or its primitive representatives.
The displayed primitive restriction is a condition on already supplied
source primitives after the closed Hopf-radical quotient.

\item \emph{Finite residual.}
The exact Koszul obstruction tuple at height \(R\) is
\[
\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{Kos},R}
=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{C}_{R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{fil}}_{R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{conil}}_{R},
\mathfrak o^{\Delta,\mathrm{ch}}_{R},
\{\mathfrak o^{C,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}\}_{R'\ge R},
\mathfrak o^{b}_{R},
\mathfrak o^{\Omega}_{R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{hyb}}_{R},
\mathfrak o^{\Pi}_{R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{sep}}_{R},
\mathfrak o^{\Prim}_{R}
\right).
\]
Here the finite coalgebra defects are
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{fil}}_{R}
:=
\left(
F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,-1},\
C_{X,R}/F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,N_R},\
\{d_C(F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,p})\to
C_{X,R}/F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,p}\}_{p},\
\{\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}(F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,p})\to
(C_{X,R}\otimes C_{X,R})/
\sum_{i+j\le p}F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,i}\otimes
F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,j}\}_{p}
\right),
\]
\[
\overline\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}
:=\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}
-\bigl((\eta_R^C\varepsilon_R^C)\otimes\mathrm{id}
+\mathrm{id}\otimes(\eta_R^C\varepsilon_R^C)\bigr),
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{conil}}_{R}
:=(\overline\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}})^{N_R+1},
\]
\[
\mathfrak o^{\Delta,\mathrm{ch}}_{R}
:=
\left(
(\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}\otimes1)\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}
-(1\otimes\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}})\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}},
(\varepsilon_R^C\otimes1)\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}-\mathrm{id},
(1\otimes\varepsilon_R^C)\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}-\mathrm{id}
\right),
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak o^{C,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}
:=
\left(
(\rho^C_{R'R}\otimes\rho^C_{R'R})\Delta_{R'}^{\mathrm{ch}}
-\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}\rho^C_{R'R},\
\{\rho^C_{R'R}(F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R',p})\to
C_{X,R}/F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,p}\}_{p}
\right).
\]
Here \(d_C\) is the finite-stage coalgebra differential, and a displayed
map to a quotient is zero exactly when the corresponding subobject
inclusion holds.
The entries record, respectively: existence of the source coalgebra;
bounded exhaustive source filtration; conilpotence of the reduced
iterated coproduct; finite collision-coproduct construction with
coassociativity and counit; transition-strict compatibility of
\((C_{X,R},F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,\bullet},\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}})\); the bar
quasi-isomorphism \(b_{X,R}\); the cobar quasi-isomorphism
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\); compatibility with the hybrid
local/wrapped operations, meaning
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}=0\); compatibility with normal-ordered descent and
the reduced \(E\)-quotient; source/target separation, meaning that the
source coalgebra, filtration, coproduct, and bar comparison are supplied
before the target comparison and are not reconstructed from the target
counit; and the primitive restriction after the closed Hopf-radical
quotient.  A full Koszul certificate is the compatible vanishing and
trivialization of \(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\) for all \(R\), followed
by passage to the HN inverse limit.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Canonical finite source-bar coalgebra]
\label{prop:canonical-source-bar-coalgebra}
Fix \(R\) and assume the finite hybrid residual
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}\) vanishes, with the transition and
properness data of
Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate}.  Assume
also that the finite hybrid stage supplies an integer \(N_R\) such that
every nonzero ordered word of non-vacuum hybrid inputs of total HN height
\(\le R\) has length at most \(N_R\).  Equivalently, the HN height is
positive on every non-vacuum colour which survives in the reduced bar
construction; if this bounded-length condition fails, the filtration and
conilpotence residuals below are not killed.  Finally assume a supplied
augmentation
\(\varepsilon_{X,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\colon
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\to k\mathbf 1\), and write
\[
\overline{\mathcal F}_{X,R}
:=\ker(\varepsilon_{X,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}).
\]
Under these hypotheses
there is a canonical source-side choice of the finite coalgebra in
Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-source-certificate}:
\[
C^{\mathrm{bar}}_{X,R}
:=
\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
\bigl(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}},
\varepsilon_{X,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\bigr).
\]
This is the reduced chiral bar coalgebra of the supplied hybrid source,
not the bar coalgebra of
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}\).  Equivalently, its length \(p\)
summand is generated by ordered \(p\)-fold inputs from the augmentation
ideal \(\overline{\mathcal F}_{X,R}\) whose total HN height is \(\le R\),
with all outputs of height \(>R\) set to zero:
\[
C^{\mathrm{bar}}_{X,R}
=k\mathbf 1\oplus
\bigoplus_{1\le p\le N_R}
\bar B^{\mathrm{ch},p}_E
\bigl(\overline{\mathcal F}_{X,R}\bigr).
\]
The finite source filtration is the bar-length filtration
\[
F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,p}C^{\mathrm{bar}}_{X,R}
:=
k\mathbf 1\oplus
\bigoplus_{1\le j\le p}
\bar B^{\mathrm{ch},j}_E
\bigl(\overline{\mathcal F}_{X,R}\bigr),
\qquad
0\le p\le N_R,
\]
where \(N_R\) is the supplied bounded-length constant.  The
coaugmentation is the inclusion of the vacuum summand and the counit is
projection to that summand.  For a homogeneous bar generator
\(x=[x_1|\cdots|x_p]\), the
collision coproduct is
\[
\Delta_R^{\mathrm{bar}}(x)
=\mathbf 1\otimes x+x\otimes\mathbf 1
+\sum_{i=1}^{p-1}
[x_1|\cdots|x_i]\otimes[x_{i+1}|\cdots|x_p],
\]
with the displayed cuts realized by the corresponding finite collision
and flag pull-push maps in
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\).  The eight-word flag coherences and
the four-input pentagon give coassociativity; the vacuum collision flags
give the counit identities; and, for the reduced coproduct obtained by
removing the two vacuum terms, the bar-length filtration gives
\[
\bigl(\overline\Delta_R^{\mathrm{bar}}\bigr)^{N_R+1}=0.
\]
Thus, after replacing \(C_{X,R}\) by
\(C^{\mathrm{bar}}_{X,R}\), the finite residuals
\[
\mathfrak o^C_R,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{fil}}_R,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{conil}}_R,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\Delta,\mathrm{ch}}_R
\]
vanish.  The bar comparison \(b_{X,R}\) may be chosen to be the identity
of
\(\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}},
\varepsilon_{X,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}})\).
For \(R'\ge R\), let
\[
\tau^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}:
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R'}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\]
be the finite hybrid transition.  Define the source coalgebra transition
\[
\rho^{\mathrm{bar}}_{R'R}:=
\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\tau}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R})
\quad\text{followed by the height-\(R\) truncation.}
\]
Here \(\overline{\tau}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}\) is the induced map on
augmentation ideals.
Then \(\rho^{\mathrm{bar}}_{R'R}\) preserves the bar-length filtration.
The transition residual
\(\mathfrak o^{C,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}\) vanishes exactly when the finite
hybrid transition functor carries ordered collision flags, quotient
compatibilities, and the bar-length filtration at height \(R'\) to the
corresponding data at height \(R\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The construction applies the Beilinson--Drinfeld chiral bar construction
to the already supplied source chiral object
\(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\).  Since the finite HN
quotient kills charges of height \(>R\), and since non-vacuum words have
length bounded by \(N_R\), only finitely many non-vacuum bar lengths
occur.  The reduced bar construction has a vacuum
coaugmentation, a projection counit, and the standard deconcatenation
coproduct.  In the present correspondence model, each deconcatenation is
implemented by cutting the ordered collision flag; admissibility of the
pull-push maps and Thom--Sebastiani transport are part of
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}=0\).  The associativity and pentagon
axioms for the finite flag stacks are precisely the equality of the two
iterated cut maps.  Hence the displayed coproduct is coassociative and
counital.  The reduced coproduct sends a word of length \(p\) to tensor
words whose individual lengths are \(<p\); after at most \(p\) reduced
iterations every branch has length one, and the next reduced coproduct is
zero.  Since \(p\le N_R\), the \((N_R+1)\)-fold reduced iterate is zero.
The construction of \(\rho^{\mathrm{bar}}_{R'R}\) is functorial from
\(\tau^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}\), and the displayed transition square is
exactly the assertion that this functorial bar map respects the finite
collision flags after quotient and truncation.  The construction has used
only the source hybrid correspondence category, not the target current
envelope.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Remaining source-to-target cobar obstruction]
\label{cor:source-bar-remaining-cobar-obstruction}
Under the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:canonical-source-bar-coalgebra}, the source
coalgebra, finite filtration, collision coproduct, conilpotence, and bar
comparison are no longer the Koszul obstruction.  A cobar
quasi-isomorphism to the target still requires two independent finite
assertions.

First, the supplied hybrid source must itself lie in the
Beilinson--Drinfeld/Francis--Gaitsgory bar--cobar domain.  Thus it must be
augmented and placed in the completed or coderived conilpotent category in
which the source-internal counit
\[
\varepsilon^{\mathrm{src}}_{\mathrm{bar},R}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C^{\mathrm{bar}}_{X,R}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\]
is a quasi-isomorphism.  This is a source-internal assertion about the
supplied hybrid object, not the target counit.

Second, one must construct a source-to-target chiral algebra
quasi-isomorphism
\[
\vartheta_R:
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}.
\]
If both assertions hold, then
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C^{\mathrm{bar}}_{X,R}
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}
\]
is the composite
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}
:=
\vartheta_R\circ
\varepsilon^{\mathrm{src}}_{\mathrm{bar},R}.
\]
Equivalently, the following triangle commutes in the finite homotopy
category:
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}
=\vartheta_R\circ
\varepsilon^{\mathrm{src}}_{\mathrm{bar},R}.
\]
For this source-bar model the exact finite defects are
\[
\mathfrak o^{\varepsilon,\mathrm{src}}_R
:=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{aug}}_R,\
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{FG}}_R,\
H^\bullet\operatorname{Cone}
(\varepsilon^{\mathrm{src}}_{\mathrm{bar},R})
\right),
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak o^\vartheta_R
:=
\left(
d_{\Delta}\vartheta_R-\vartheta_R d_{\mathrm{hyb}},\
\vartheta_R\mu_R^{\mathrm{hyb}}
-\mu_{\Delta,R}(\vartheta_R\otimes\vartheta_R),\
\vartheta_R\eta_R^{\mathrm{hyb}}-\eta_{\Delta,R},\
\vartheta_R\circ\tau^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}
-\pi^\Delta_{R'R}\circ\vartheta_{R'},\
H^\bullet\operatorname{Cone}(\vartheta_R),\
\vartheta_R|_{\Prim}-\iota_R^{\Prim}
\right).
\]
Thus
\[
\mathfrak o^\Omega_R
:=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{\varepsilon,\mathrm{src}}_R,\
\mathfrak o^\vartheta_R
\right)
\]
is the surviving cobar residual.  Its vanishing is exactly the assertion
that the source bar-cobar counit is admissible and a quasi-isomorphism
and that the compact hybrid source is quasi-isomorphic, with transition
and primitive compatibility, to the imported denominator current
envelope.

Thus the finite source-bar construction kills the coalgebra part of
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\) after the hybrid source is supplied, but
it does not identify compact primitives with the imported
Gritsenko--Nikulin current envelope.  That identification remains a
source-to-target theorem, not a target-internal counit.  No homotopy
inverse to
\(\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R})\to
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R}\)
enters this construction.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proposition}[Consequence of the chiral Koszul source certificate]
\label{prop:chiral-koszul-source-certificate-consequence}
Assume the finite-stage certificates
\(\mathfrak K^{\mathrm{Kos}}_{X,R}\) are supplied for all \(R\), with
compatible transition maps, in particular with
\(\mathfrak o^{C,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}=0\) for every \(R'\ge R\).  Assume
also the Koszul Mittag--Leffler condition: \(R^1\varprojlim=0\) for the
inverse systems of source coalgebras, completed chiral bar and cobar
constructions, target truncations, and the cones of \(b_{X,R}\) and
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\) \cite[\S3.5]{WeibelHA}.  Then the inverse limit
\[
C_X:=\varprojlim_R C_{X,R}
\]
is a completed pro-conilpotent chiral coalgebra attached to the hybrid
compact source, conilpotent on every finite HN quotient, and the maps
\(b_{X,R}\) and
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\) induce
\[
b_X:C_X\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}),
\qquad
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
\]
This identifies the supplied source cobar algebra with the formal target
current envelope.  It does not construct the \(E_3\)-source, the hybrid
wrapped Hall correspondences, the orientation line, the primitive
recognition data, or \(C_X\) itself from the target-internal counit.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The inverse limit exists by the transition compatibility, bounded
exhaustive finite charge filtration, finite coassociative and counital
collision coproduct, and continuity hypotheses in the certificate.  The
coradical filtration is finite on every \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\)-truncation and
continuous in the HN completion; the limit is therefore pro-conilpotent,
with finite-stage conilpotence preserved.  The coproduct on \(C_X\) is the
inverse limit of the finite \(\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}\).  The
quasi-isomorphisms \(b_{X,R}\) and \(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\) commute
with the transition maps.  The Koszul Mittag--Leffler condition kills
the \(R^1\varprojlim\) obstruction on their cones, hence these compatible
finite quasi-isomorphisms pass to completed quasi-isomorphisms.  Without
that exactness one obtains only a compatible pro-quasi-isomorphism.  The
final sentence is the
definition of the certificate: the source object, mixed correspondences,
orientation, primitive presentation, and source/target-separation datum
are separate entries of \(\mathfrak K_X\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Locality]
In a compact realization, the required local object would be a
finite-stage holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra on \(X\), and its
\(K3\)-specialization would be a finite-stage chiral factorization
algebra on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\).  This assertion is local only for
projection-finite sectors over \(E\).  The automorphic product is a
protected global trace after charge completion, wall-chamber choice, and
summation over compact \(K3\)-modes.  Duality monodromy, elliptic-degree
wrapping, and the Borcherds chamber are therefore global features of the
trace.  They do not replace the local factorization maps on disjoint
opens.
Singular \(K3\) surfaces and nodal or cuspidal elliptic curves require
the boundary degeneration certificate; the Ran-local statement here is
the smooth-\(S\), smooth-\(E\) compact-stage assertion.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Projection-finite, wrapped, and hybrid Ran strata]
\label{def:projection-finite-wrapped-sectors}
Let \(p_E:K3\times E\to E\) be projection.  A compact Hall or chiral
sector is projection-finite over \(E\) if every object \(A\) in it
satisfies
\[
p_E(\operatorname{Supp}A)\subset F
\]
for some finite subset \(F\subset E\).  A one-dimensional sector is
wrapped over \(E\) if its curve class has positive elliptic degree, i.e.
if the pushforward of its one-cycle to \(E\) is \(b[E]\) with \(b>0\).
For such one-dimensional Hall sectors write
\[
b(A)=\deg (p_E)_*[\operatorname{Supp}_1 A]\in\Z_{\ge0}.
\]
The same letter \(b(\gamma)\) denotes the elliptic-degree component of a
charge \(\gamma\).  Then projection-finite objects have \(b(A)=0\), while
wrapped objects have \(b(A)>0\).

The hybrid base used below is a finite-stage coloured correspondence
base, not an ordinary Ran space with one scalar attached.  At height
\(R\), after the certificate below is supplied, an object consists of a
finite projection-local support \(F\subset E\), finitely many wrapped
colours \(\eta_j\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{wr}}\), and rigidified wrapped
objects \(W_j\) carrying anchor values
\(\lambda_{\eta_j,R}(W_j)\in E\).  Its arrows are generated by finite
collisions of \(F\), by extension of local colours, by mixed
local/wrapped correspondences, and by wrapped/wrapped correspondences.
The notation \(\operatorname{Ran}^{\mathrm{hyb}}(E)\) denotes this
finite-coloured system through the inverse system in \(R\).  Its
underlying degree shadow is the displayed disjoint union
\[
\operatorname{Ran}^{\mathrm{hyb}}(E)
=\bigsqcup_{b\ge0}\operatorname{Ran}(E)_{[b]},
\qquad
\operatorname{Ran}(E)_{[b]}:=\operatorname{Ran}(E)\times\{b\}.
\]
The stratum \(b=0\) is the ordinary finite-support Ran stratum.  A
stratum \(b>0\) records finite local collision points together with a
global wrapped elliptic leg of degree \(b\); it is not an assertion that
the wrapped support is finite over \(E\).
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Projection-to-\(E\) support-locality obstruction]
\label{lem:projection-e-support-locality-obstruction}
\label{lem:elliptic-degree-locality-obstruction}
Let \(C\subset K3\times E\) be a one-dimensional subscheme whose curve
class has positive elliptic degree:
\[
(p_E)_*[C]=b[E],\qquad b>0.
\]
Then \(p_E(C)=E\).  In particular, \(C\) is not localized at finitely
many points of \(E\), and it is not contained in \(p_E^{-1}(U)\) for any
proper open \(U\subsetneq E\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If \(p_E(C)\) were zero-dimensional, then the pushforward of the
one-cycle \([C]\) to the curve \(E\) would vanish.  This contradicts
\((p_E)_*[C]=b[E]\) with \(b>0\).  Hence \(p_E(C)\) is a
one-dimensional closed subset of the irreducible curve \(E\), since
\(p_E\) is proper, and therefore \(p_E(C)=E\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Naive Ran locality misses the elliptic-degree direction]
\label{cor:ranE-locality-misses-elliptic-degree}
A support-local factorization algebra on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\),
defined only by separating supports over disjoint opens of \(E\), sees
the projection-finite sector.  It does not by itself realize the full
\(s\)-direction of the Igusa product.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The variable \(s\) is the Borcherds variable corresponding to the
OP elliptic-degree direction in Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}.
By Lemma~\ref{lem:projection-e-support-locality-obstruction}, positive
elliptic degree projects onto all of \(E\).  Such objects cannot be
separated by choosing disjoint opens in \(E\).  Therefore ordinary
support-local factorization on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) has no
locality mechanism for the wrapped elliptic-degree sector.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Finite hybrid local/wrapped factorization certificate]
\label{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate}
Fix \((\sigma,S,R)\) as in
Definition~\ref{def:compact-e3-source-interface}.  A finite-stage hybrid
local/wrapped factorization certificate is a datum
\[
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
=
\left(
\mathcal C_{\sigma,S,\le R},\,
b_R,\,
\mathcal F_{R}^{\mathrm{loc}},\,
\mathcal G_{R}^{\mathrm{wr}},\,
\mathfrak E_R^{\mathrm{loc}},\,
\mathfrak E_R^{\mathrm{hyb}},\,
\mathfrak E_R^{\mathrm{wr}},\,
\mathfrak{Flag}_R^{\mathrm{hyb}},\,
\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R,\,
\lambda_R,\,
Q_{E,R},\,
\theta^Q_R,\,
o_R,\,
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}
\right)
\]
with the following finite data and axioms.  Every stack, sheaf,
operation, and coherence named below lives at the fixed height \(R\); the
inverse limit appears only after all finite stages and transition maps
have been supplied.
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Finite Hall stage and elliptic degree.}
\(\mathcal C_{\sigma,S,\le R}\) is a supplied extension-closed finite
charge-support HN quotient of the candidate compact Hall category, under
the finite-type hypothesis \textup{[K3\(\times\)E-fin]}, with finite-type
charge substacks
\(\mathfrak M_{\gamma,R}\) for
\(\gamma\in\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)\), vanishing-cycle coefficients
\(\Phi_{\gamma,R}\), and orientation lines \(o_{\gamma,R}\).  The map
\[
b_R:\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)\longrightarrow \Z_{\ge0}
\]
is the elliptic-degree component.  Write
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{loc}}=\{\alpha\mid b_R(\alpha)=0\}\) and
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{wr}}=\{\eta\mid b_R(\eta)>0\}\).  The ideal of height
\(>R\) is already killed at this stage, and all operations below are
understood to be zero when their output has height \(>R\).  The map
\(b_R\) is additive on extensions that remain in the quotient:
\[
b_R(0)=0,\qquad
b_R(\gamma+\gamma')=b_R(\gamma)+b_R(\gamma')
\]
whenever \(\gamma,\gamma',\gamma+\gamma'\in
\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)\); if the sum has height \(>R\), the
corresponding operation is zero in the finite quotient.

\item \emph{Projection-finite local sector.}  For \(U\subset E\) open and
\(\alpha\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{loc}}\),
\[
\mathcal M_{\alpha,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U)
=
\left\{
A\in\mathfrak M_{\alpha,R}\ \middle|\
p_E(\operatorname{Supp}A)\subset U
\right\}
\]
is supplied as an open substack of \(\mathfrak M_{\alpha,R}\), and
\[
\mathcal F_{\alpha,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U)
:=
H_*^{\mathrm{BM}}\!\left(
\mathcal M_{\alpha,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U),
\Phi_{\alpha,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}\otimes o_{\alpha,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}
\right).
\]
The direct sum over \(\alpha\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{loc}}\) is
\(\mathcal F_R^{\mathrm{loc}}(U)\).  For disjoint opens this is an ordinary
projection-finite Ran factorization object.

\item \emph{Wrapped prequotient sector and rigidification.}  For
\(\eta\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{wr}}\), a prequotient stack
\[
\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}
\xrightarrow{\ \rho_{\eta,R}\ }
\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}
\subset\mathfrak M_{\eta,R}
\]
is supplied, together with a fixed origin \(0_E\in E\) and an
\(E\)-equivariant anchor
\[
\lambda_{\eta,R}:\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}\longrightarrow E,
\qquad
\lambda_{\eta,R}(t\cdot W)=t+\lambda_{\eta,R}(W),
\]
where \(+\) is the group law on \(E\) with respect to the chosen origin.
The origin \(0_E\) is part of the supplied datum and is fixed once globally
in the certificate; a different choice of origin shifts \(\lambda_{\eta,R}\)
by a constant and the anchor descends to a \(\mathrm{Pic}^0(E)\)-torsor whose
zero point is the fixed datum.  Its objects have support dominating \(E\).
The pair \((\rho_{\eta,R},\lambda_{\eta,R})\) is a supplied
rigidification, not a canonical construction.  A natural candidate is the
normalized determinant
\[
\lambda(A)=\det Rp_{E,*}A\otimes\mathcal O_E(-\chi(A)\cdot 0_E)
\in \operatorname{Pic}^0(E)\simeq E .
\]
This candidate has translation weight \(\chi(A)\):
\[
\lambda(t\cdot A)=\lambda(A)+\chi(A)t .
\]
Thus it gives the required unit-weight anchor only on strata where this
weight has been rigidified, divided by a chosen finite cover, or replaced
by an equivalent Abel--Jacobi/framing datum.  In particular, on
\(\chi(A)=0\) strata it does not by itself remember the relative
\(E\)-position.  The anchor residual is therefore a typed finite datum,
not a name:
\[
\mathfrak o^\lambda_R=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{\lambda,\mathrm{ex}}_R,\
\mathfrak o^{\lambda,\mathrm{unit}}_R,\
\mathfrak o^{\lambda,\mathrm{loss}}_R,\
\mathfrak o^{\lambda,\mathrm{multi}}_R,\
\mathfrak o^{\lambda,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}
\right).
\]
These components assert, respectively, existence of the rigidified
prequotient and anchor; unit translation law, possibly after a specified
finite cover; losslessness of the anchor on the relative \(E\)-position
needed by wrapped correspondences; compatibility of the input,
intermediate, and output anchors on mixed and wrapped flag stacks; and
compatibility under successor HN transitions.  The certificate requires
the chosen anchor, its translation law, and the vanishing of all components
of \(\mathfrak o^\lambda_R\) as finite data.  Put
\[
\mathcal G_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}
:=
H_*^{\mathrm{BM}}\!\left(
\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}},
\Phi_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}\otimes o_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}
\right),
\qquad
\mathcal G_R^{\mathrm{wr}}:=\bigoplus_{\eta\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{wr}}}
\mathcal G_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}.
\]
If no such prequotient memory is supplied, the wrapped part of the
certificate is absent.

\item \emph{Local, mixed, and wrapped extension correspondences.}  For
disjoint opens
\((U_i)\subset E\), local charges \(\alpha_i\), and wrapped charges
\(\eta,\eta_1,\eta_2\), the finite stage contains correspondences
\[
\prod_i\mathcal M_{\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U_i)
\xleftarrow{\ p\ }
\mathfrak E_{\alpha_1,\ldots,\alpha_r,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U_1,\ldots,U_r)
\xrightarrow{\ q\ }
\mathcal M_{\sum_i\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}\!\left(\bigcup_iU_i\right),
\]
\[
\prod_i\mathcal M_{\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U_i)
\times\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}
\xleftarrow{\ p\ }
\mathfrak E_{\alpha_1,\ldots,\alpha_r;\eta,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
(U_1,\ldots,U_r)
\xrightarrow{\ q\ }
\mathcal M_{\eta+\sum_i\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}},
\]
and
\[
\mathcal M_{\eta_1,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}
\times\mathcal M_{\eta_2,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}
\xleftarrow{\ p\ }
\mathfrak E_{\eta_1,\eta_2,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}
\xrightarrow{\ q\ }
\mathcal M_{\eta_1+\eta_2,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}.
\]
The second display is only the one-sided shorthand.  Since Hall
convolution is ordered, the datum contains, for every ordered mixed word
with local inputs on both sides of one wrapped input, correspondences
\[
\prod_{i\in I_-}\mathcal M_{\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U_i)
\times\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}
\times
\prod_{j\in I_+}\mathcal M_{\beta_j,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(V_j)
\xleftarrow{\ p\ }
\mathfrak E_{\alpha_-;\eta;\beta_+,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
((U_i),(V_j))
\xrightarrow{\ q\ }
\mathcal M_{\eta+\sum_{i\in I_-}\alpha_i+
\sum_{j\in I_+}\beta_j,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}.
\]
The displayed mixed correspondence above is the case \(I_+=\varnothing\).
The case \(I_-=\varnothing\) is the right local action on a wrapped
input.  Both are part of the certificate.  Similarly
\(\mathfrak E_{\eta_1,\eta_2,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}\) is ordered in
\((\eta_1,\eta_2)\); no symmetry of wrapped inputs is assumed unless an
extra symmetry datum is supplied.
The middle stacks classify exact triangles or exact sequences with the
displayed associated graded pieces.  They are constructed in the
unreduced \(E\)-equivariant theory, with proper-support or compact-support
witnesses for \(q\), admissibility witnesses for \(p^*\) and \(q_!\) on
the chosen vanishing-cycle/Borel--Moore theory, and Thom--Sebastiani
identifications for the coefficient systems.  For every generator
\(e\) among the local-local, ordered mixed, and wrapped-wrapped
correspondences, write
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop}}_{e,R},\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{adm}}_{e,R},\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{TS}}_{e,R}
\]
for the defects of proper-support, pull-push admissibility, and
Thom--Sebastiani compatibility.  Their aggregate defects in the three
families are
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{LL}}_R,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{mix}}_R,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{WW}}_R.
\]
They vanish exactly when all pull-push maps used below are honest
finite-stage operations, not formal correspondences without a defined
pushforward.  The mixed stacks use the
anchor \(\lambda_{\eta,R}\) to remember the relative position between the
finite local supports \(U_i\) and the wrapped leg; replacing this memory
by a scalar Fock coefficient is not this datum.  The wrapped-wrapped
stacks are likewise anchored: before quotienting they carry the map
\[
\mathfrak E_{\eta_1,\eta_2,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}
\longrightarrow E\times E\times E,\qquad
\xi\longmapsto
\bigl(\lambda_{\eta_1,R}(W_1),
\lambda_{\eta_2,R}(W_2),
\lambda_{\eta_1+\eta_2,R}(W)\bigr),
\]
where \(W_1,W_2,W\) are the two inputs and the output of \(\xi\).  The
finite correspondence keeps this relation, not only the total degree
\(b_R(\eta_1+\eta_2)\).

These object stacks, extension stacks, and flag stacks generate a finite
\(E\)-equivariant correspondence category
\[
\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R.
\]
Its objects are the finitely many local and rigidified wrapped charge
stacks at height \(R\).  Its arrows are generated by the displayed
correspondences, with composition by derived fibre product and with every
summand of height \(>R\) identified with zero.  The flag stacks below are
the specified \(2\)-morphisms witnessing equality of the two composites.
The finite operation
maps are the displayed pull-push maps
\[
\mu_R^\bullet=q_!\circ\operatorname{TS}_R^\bullet\circ p^*,
\]
namely
\[
\mu_{\alpha_1,\ldots,\alpha_r,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}:
\bigotimes_i\mathcal F_{\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U_i)
\longrightarrow
\mathcal F_{\sum_i\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}\!\left(\bigcup_iU_i\right),
\]
\[
\mu_{\alpha_1,\ldots,\alpha_r;\eta,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}:
\bigotimes_i\mathcal F_{\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U_i)
\otimes\mathcal G_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal G_{\eta+\sum_i\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{wr}},
\]
and
\[
\mu_{\eta_1,\eta_2,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}:
\mathcal G_{\eta_1,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}\otimes
\mathcal G_{\eta_2,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal G_{\eta_1+\eta_2,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}.
\]
Equivalently, the unreduced finite hybrid object at height \(R\) is the
correspondence-module functor
\[
\mathcal B_R^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}:
\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\longrightarrow \mathrm{Ch}_{\mathbb C}
\]
sending
\[
\mathcal M_{\alpha,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U)\longmapsto
\mathcal F_{\alpha,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U),\qquad
\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}\longmapsto
\mathcal G_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}},
\]
and sending a generator
\(e=(X\xleftarrow p\mathfrak E_e\xrightarrow qY)\) to
\[
\mathcal B_R^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}(e)
=q_!\circ\operatorname{TS}_{e,R}\circ p^*.
\]
This functor is defined only after the properness/admissibility defects
above vanish.  The reduced finite object is the quotient-after-
correspondence module
\[
\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{hyb}}
:=Q_{E,R}\mathcal B_R^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}.
\]
The two-sided mixed correspondences give, in the same notation,
\[
\mu_{\alpha_-;\eta;\beta_+,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}:
\bigotimes_{i\in I_-}\mathcal F_{\alpha_i,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U_i)
\otimes\mathcal G_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}
\otimes
\bigotimes_{j\in I_+}\mathcal F_{\beta_j,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(V_j)
\longrightarrow
\mathcal G_{\eta+\sum_i\alpha_i+\sum_j\beta_j,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}.
\]
An output with at least one wrapped input is wrapped.  The mixed
correspondence is also required to record the surviving terms in
\(\operatorname{RHom}(A,W)\) and \(\operatorname{RHom}(W,A)\) for local
\(A\) and wrapped \(W\); replacing it by a scalar global mode loses this
data.

\item \emph{Full flag associativity and coherence.}  Write
\(\mathrm L\) for a projection-finite local input and \(\mathrm W\) for a
rigidified wrapped input.  For every word
\[
w=(\epsilon_1,\epsilon_2,\epsilon_3)\in\{\mathrm L,\mathrm W\}^3
\]
and every compatible ordered triple of charges and local opens, the datum
contains a two-step flag stack
\[
\mathfrak{Flag}^{w}_{\xi_1,\xi_2,\xi_3,R}
\]
classifying filtrations with the prescribed associated graded pieces.
Here \(\mathfrak E_{\xi_i,\xi_j,R}\) means the corresponding ordered
local-local, mixed local/wrapped, or wrapped-wrapped extension stack from
the previous clause.  The flag stack carries comparison maps to the two
iterated correspondence fibre products
\[
\mathfrak E_{\xi_1,\xi_2,R}
\times_{\mathcal M_{\xi_1+\xi_2,R}}
\mathfrak E_{\xi_1+\xi_2,\xi_3,R},
\qquad
\mathfrak E_{\xi_2,\xi_3,R}
\times_{\mathcal M_{\xi_2+\xi_3,R}}
\mathfrak E_{\xi_1,\xi_2+\xi_3,R}.
\]
The eight words
\[
\mathrm{LLL},\ \mathrm{LLW},\ \mathrm{LWL},\ \mathrm{WLL},
\mathrm{LWW},\ \mathrm{WLW},\ \mathrm{WWL},\ \mathrm{WWW}
\]
are all part of the datum.  In the mixed and wrapped words the flag stack
retains the input, intermediate, and output anchors before quotienting by
\(E\).  The two parenthesizations give the same map in the finite
quotient:
\[
\mu_{\xi_1+\xi_2,\xi_3,R}
\circ(\mu_{\xi_1,\xi_2,R}\otimes 1)
=
\mu_{\xi_1,\xi_2+\xi_3,R}
\circ(1\otimes\mu_{\xi_2,\xi_3,R}).
\]
Here \(\mu\) means one of the displayed local, mixed, or wrapped maps.
The equality is required after vanishing cycles, Thom--Sebastiani
transport, orientation signs, and the quotient by height \(>R\).
Equivalently, the two pull-push maps are induced by the same
Borel--Moore class on the corresponding two-step flag stack.  This is a
finite-stage coherence axiom; no associativity is imported from the
completed inverse limit.
The defect class of this equality for the word \(w\) is denoted
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{assoc}}_{w,R}.
\]
The certificate requires \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{assoc}}_{w,R}=0\) for all
eight words, with the chosen \(2\)-morphisms satisfying the usual
four-input pentagon on the finite flag-of-flags stacks.
This eight-word atlas is the binary associativity subcertificate.  Full
hybrid factorization still requires the higher colored configuration
atlas, units, symmetry or ordering conventions, refinement maps, descent,
and overlap coherences for all finite HN windows.  None of these follows
from the eight displayed length-three words.

\item \emph{Reduced \(E\)-quotient order.}  All stacks and
correspondences above are \(E\)-equivariant before quotienting.  Let
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\) and
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{hyb}}_R\) denote the finite
unreduced and reduced correspondence bicategories generated by these
stacks, correspondences, and flag diagrams.  The quotient datum first
supplies a pseudofunctor between these bicategories, with coherent
\(2\)-morphisms for composition, base-change, and Thom--Sebastiani
transport.  Applying vanishing-cycle Borel--Moore chains, with the
orientation lines included, gives the finite correspondence module
categories \(\mathsf{BM}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\) and
\(\mathsf{BM}^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{hyb}}_R\).  The symbol \(Q_{E,R}\)
denotes the induced supplied functor
\[
Q_{E,R}:
\mathsf{BM}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R
\longrightarrow
\mathsf{BM}^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{hyb}}_R
\]
from the finite unreduced equivariant vanishing-cycle/Borel--Moore
category generated by the stacks above to the finite reduced category.
It is not only a map on object stacks.
It is allowed only after the local, wrapped, and mixed extension
correspondences have been formed and the chosen rigidification has either
descended or has been integrated out with a specified reduced kernel.
For every generator \(e\) of
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), the quotient package contains the
reduced correspondence \(\overline e\), the quotient maps from \(e\) to
\(\overline e\), admissibility witnesses for
\(\overline p^*\) and \(\overline q_!\), proper-support witnesses for
\(\overline q\), and orientation-descent isomorphisms for the coefficient
systems.  If the anchor is integrated out rather than descended, the
datum also contains the reduced kernel \(K_{\lambda,R}\) and its
compatibility with composition.  The quotient construction is therefore a
functor on the finite correspondence category, not a quotient of the
object spaces followed by a new Hall product.
For each operation \(\mu_R^\bullet=q_!\operatorname{TS}p^*\) the datum
contains a specified comparison isomorphism
\[
\theta^Q_{\mu,R}:\;
Q_{E,R}q_!\operatorname{TS}p^*
\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
\overline q_!\overline{\operatorname{TS}}\,\overline p^*
\bigl(Q_{E,R}^{\boxtimes k}\bigr),
\]
which is compatible with the flag-stack coherences.  The finite-stabilizer
gerbe classes needed for the orientation line must vanish on every stack
entering these squares.  For each two-step flag, the two composites of
\(\theta^Q_{\mu,R}\) agree with the descended flag \(2\)-morphism; for
\(R'\ge R\), the transition functors commute with \(Q_{E,R}\) through a
specified natural isomorphism.  A quotient-first construction is not this
datum.
The four quotient residuals are
\[
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{form}}_R,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{adm}}_R,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{flag}}_R,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}.
\]
They record, respectively, existence of the functor \(Q_{E,R}\) on the
finite correspondence category, admissibility/properness after quotient,
compatibility with all flag \(2\)-morphisms, and compatibility with HN
transition maps.  The certificate requires their vanishing and chosen
null-homotopies.

\item \emph{Protected integration and the Igusa \(s\)-direction.}  The
finite stage carries a protected integration map
\[
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}:
Q_{E,R}\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\longrightarrow
\C[\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}]_{\le R}
\]
where the subscript denotes the image of the finite \(h_S\)-box.  The map
is compatible with the three reduced products
\(\overline\mu_R^\bullet\), coproducts, primitive projection, and
transition maps.  This means a chain-level character of the finite
reduced correspondence algebra, not only the assignment of an
\(s\)-degree.  Let \(m_{\Gamma,R}\), \(\Delta_{\Gamma,R}\), and
\(P_{\Gamma,R}^{\Prim}\) denote the finite target multiplication,
coproduct, and primitive projector on the chosen decategorified monomial
model.  The integration defects are
\[
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{ch}}_R:=I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}d_R,
\]
\[
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{prod}}_{w,R}:=
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}\overline\mu^w_R
-m_{\Gamma,R}(I_R^{\mathrm{prot}})^{\otimes k},
\qquad w\in\{\mathrm L,\mathrm W\}^k,
\]
\[
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{co}}_R:=
\Delta_{\Gamma,R}I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}
-(I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}\otimes I_R^{\mathrm{prot}})\overline\Delta_R,
\qquad
\mathfrak o^{I,\Prim}_R:=
P_{\Gamma,R}^{\Prim}I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}
-I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}P_R^{\Prim}.
\]
They are required to vanish, compatibly with \(Q_{E,R}\), the orientation
trivializations, and transitions in \(R\).  Equivalently, for every
reduced operation \(\overline\mu_R^w\) and homogeneous inputs \(x_i\) of
charges \(\gamma_i\),
\[
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}
\bigl(\overline\mu_R^w(x_1,\ldots,x_k)\bigr)
=
\prod_i I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}(x_i)
\]
whenever the product is defined at height \(R\); if the output charge has
height \(>R\), both sides are zero in the finite quotient.  If a
homogeneous class \(x\) has charge \(\gamma\), and
\(\mathcal F_{\gamma,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) denotes the corresponding local
or wrapped summand, then every nonzero monomial in
\(I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}(Q_{E,R}x)\) has \(s\)-degree \(b_R(\gamma)\):
\[
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}(Q_{E,R}x)
\in
s^{\,b_R(\gamma)}\C[q^{\pm1},r^{\pm1}]
\]
under the OP/Borcherds variable convention of
Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}.  More precisely,
\(I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}\) is homogeneous for the full Gram label
\(\overline\Pi_X(\gamma)=(n,l,m)\), and the displayed condition records
the elliptic degree \(m=b_R(\gamma)\).  Thus positive powers of the
Igusa \(s\)-variable can only come from the wrapped colour \(b_R>0\).
This is a source-support condition, not a consequence of the target
product.  If a target window contains a degree with \(m>0\), and in
particular the test degree \(\delta_2\leftrightarrow(0,1,1)\), the finite
stage must contain a wrapped source summand mapping to that degree under
\(\overline\Pi_X\).  Otherwise the coefficient lies outside the verified
compact source image.
For products, the displayed character law and additivity of \(b_R\) give
\[
s^{b_R(\gamma_1+\cdots+\gamma_k)}
=
\prod_i s^{b_R(\gamma_i)}
\]
inside the finite HN quotient.  Hence the \(s\)-direction is coupled to
the actual local/wrapped operation, not appended as an external Fock
determinant.
For \(R'\ge R\), let
\(\tau^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}\) be the unreduced finite hybrid transition,
let
\[
\bar\tau^{\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}:
Q_{E,R'}\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R'}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\longrightarrow
Q_{E,R}\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\]
be the induced reduced chain map, and let \(\pi^\Gamma_{R'R}\) be the
induced truncation of the monomial target.
The integration transition defect is
\[
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}:=
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}\bar\tau^{\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}
-\pi^\Gamma_{R'R}I_{R'}^{\mathrm{prot}}Q_{E,R'}.
\]
It is required to vanish.  Thus protected integration is compatible
with the HN inverse system, not merely with one finite trace.
The coefficient of a monomial \(q^nr^ls^{b_R(\gamma)}\) is a protected
finite-stage trace coefficient.  Equality of these coefficients with the
Borcherds exponents \(f(nm,l)\), and the primitive
Borcherds--Kac--Moody bracket test, are additional recognition
requirements, not part of the definition.

\item \emph{Hybrid residual tuple.}
The exact finite obstruction tuple for the hybrid lane is
\[
\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}
=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{stage}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{\lambda}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{corr},\mathrm{LL}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{corr},\mathrm{mix}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{corr},\mathrm{WW}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{LL}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{mix}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{WW}}_R,\,
\{\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{assoc}}_{w,R}\}_{w\in\{\mathrm L,\mathrm W\}^3},\,
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{col}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{form}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{adm}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{flag}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R},\,
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{ch}}_R,\,
\{\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{prod}}_{w,R}\}_{w},\,
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{col}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{co}}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{I,\Prim}_R,\,
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R},\,
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{\mathrm{hyb},R'R}
\right).
\]
These entries record finite HN existence, anchor rigidification,
local-local correspondences, all ordered mixed correspondences,
wrapped-wrapped correspondences, properness/admissibility and
Thom--Sebastiani validity for the pull-push operations, the eight-word
two-step binary flag coherence, the higher colored configuration
residual, quotient formation/admissibility/flag and transition descent,
chain/product/colored-refinement/coproduct/primitive integration laws, integration
transition compatibility, and HN transition compatibility.  A finite
hybrid certificate means the compatible vanishing and trivialization of
this tuple for every \(R'\ge R\).  Without
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}=0\), the notation
\(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) names an obstruction
problem, not a source object.
The entry \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{col}}_R\) records the higher colored
configuration atlas, unit and vacuum maps, symmetry or ordering
conventions, refinement maps, descent, and overlap coherences not detected
by the eight length-three words.  If this entry is not supplied, vanishing
of the remaining binary terms gives only the two-step Hall/module
certificate, not a full hybrid factorization object.
The entry \(\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{col}}_R\) records compatibility of
protected integration with the higher colored configuration atlas and its
refinement maps; binary product compatibility does not imply this
colored-refinement integration law.

\item \emph{Finite HN completion.}  The construction is made only for
charges in \(\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)\).  For \(R'\ge R\), transition
maps
\[
\tau^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}:
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R'}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\]
must be induced by functors
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'}\to
\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\) compatible with all three kinds of
correspondences, with the flag associativity constraints, with the
rigidifying anchors, with \(Q_{E,R}\), with the comparison isomorphisms
\(\theta^Q_R\), and with protected integration.  They preserve elliptic
degree: if a homogeneous
summand of charge \(\gamma'\) at height \(R'\) maps to a nonzero summand
of charge \(\gamma\) at height \(R\), then
\[
b_R(\gamma)=b_{R'}(\gamma').
\]
The transition residual
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{\mathrm{hyb},R'R}\) is the joint defect of
object truncation, correspondence base-change, flag/pentagon coherence,
anchor compatibility, and the induced chain map
\[
\bar\tau^{\mathrm{hyb}}_{R'R}:
\mathcal B_{R'}^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{hyb}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{hyb}} .
\]
\end{enumerate}
When all finite stages and transitions have been supplied, the completed
hybrid object is
\[
\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}
:=
\varprojlim_R\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}.
\]
It is the charge-completed hybrid source specified by those finite
certificates over \(\operatorname{Ran}^{\mathrm{hyb}}(E)\).  Its
restriction to
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)_{[0]}\) is ordinary projection-finite Ran
factorization.  Its \(b>0\) strata are wrapped modules acted on by the
local sector through the mixed Hall correspondences.  This inverse-limit
formula is a construction from the displayed finite certificates; it is
not an existence theorem for those certificates.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Finite consequences of the hybrid certificate]
\label{prop:hybrid-certificate-scope}
Assume the finite-stage data of
Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate} are
supplied for all \(R\), with compatible transition maps.  Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(b=0\) restriction is an ordinary support-local factorization
object on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\);
\item every operation with a wrapped input lands in a wrapped stratum;
\item the displayed ordered mixed maps, including the two-sided maps
\(\mu_{\alpha_-;\eta;\beta_+,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\), define the only
available Hall actions of projection-finite insertions on wrapped
elliptic-degree sectors in
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\) before the reduced \(E\)-quotient;
\item vanishing of the properness/admissibility defects
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{LL}}_R\),
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{mix}}_R\), and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{WW}}_R\) makes the Borel--Moore
pull-push functor \(\mathcal B_R^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}\) and its reduced
quotient \(\mathcal B_R^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{hyb}}\) well-defined;
\item vanishing of the eight classes
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{assoc}}_{w,R}\) gives an associative finite-stage
reduced Hall product after vanishing cycles, orientations, HN quotienting,
the quotient functor, and the comparison isomorphisms
\(\theta^Q_{\mu,R}\);
\item a protected trace or primitive bracket obtained from this object is
compatible with reduced \(E\)-integration only through the specified
\(Q_{E,R}\)-compatibility isomorphisms, their flag coherences,
finite-stabilizer conditions, and the vanishing of the integration
defects
\(\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{ch}}_R\),
\(\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{prod}}_{w,R}\),
\(\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{col}}_R\),
\(\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{co}}_R\), and
\(\mathfrak o^{I,\Prim}_R\), compatibly with
\(\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}=0\);
\item for homogeneous
\(x\in Q_{E,R}\mathcal F_{\gamma,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\),
\[
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}(x)\in
s^{b_R(\gamma)}\C[q^{\pm1},r^{\pm1}],
\]
hence the positive \(s\)-direction cannot be supplied by the
projection-finite Ran stratum; on products this law is multiplicative
because \(b_R\) is additive inside the finite quotient.
\end{enumerate}
A decoupled global Fock or Hecke factor without
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), anchored mixed correspondences,
proper pull-push operations, the eight-word two-step binary flag atlas
with the higher colored residual \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{col}}_R\),
quotient residuals, and
protected-integration residuals may reproduce a
determinant-level product, but it does not define the local-wrapped
primitive brackets needed for recognition of \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The first two assertions are built into the elliptic-degree stratification
and Lemma~\ref{lem:projection-e-support-locality-obstruction}.  The third
assertion is the definition of the mixed operation maps: before the
reduced quotient they are the only displayed operations remembering
relative \(E\)-position between finite local support and a wrapped leg,
including the left and right ordered actions.  The properness assertion is
exactly the vanishing of the generator-wise proper-support,
admissibility, and Thom--Sebastiani defects.  The flag assertion is
exactly the eight-word two-step binary flag axiom transported through
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), with higher colored factorization
kept in the separate residual \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{col}}_R\).  The
quotient assertion is the quotient-order
axiom, the coherent comparison isomorphism \(\theta^Q_{\mu,R}\), and the
vanishing of the quotient residuals.  The last statement is the degree
law and character property in the protected integration clause, together
with the vanishing of the named integration defects and their transition
residual.
No compact source object, orientation system, quotient functor, or
protected integration map is constructed in this proposition.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[No quotient-first universal hybrid repair]
\label{cor:no-quotient-first-hybrid-repair}
Fix \(R\).  A candidate finite correspondence category for the
wrapped sector gives the source object
\(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) only if it contains the
unreduced local, wrapped, and ordered mixed source stacks of
Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate}, their
anchors, the eight-word flag atlas, the quotient functor \(Q_{E,R}\)
formed after those correspondences, the comparison maps
\(\theta^Q_{\mu,R}\), and protected integration with all entries of
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}\), including its transition entries,
trivialized.  A quotient of object stacks formed before the mixed and
wrapped correspondences, or a determinant/Fock category carrying only
the trace degree \(s^{b_R}\), does not define the hybrid source.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:projection-e-support-locality-obstruction}, a positive
elliptic-degree sector is not a finite-support Ran sector.  The only
displayed mechanism retaining its relative \(E\)-position is the
rigidified wrapped prequotient with anchor, together with the unreduced
mixed and wrapped correspondences.  If one quotients first, these
anchors are no longer available as source data for
\(\mathfrak E_R^{\mathrm{hyb}}\), the two-sided maps
\(\mu_{\alpha_-;\eta;\beta_+,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\), or the flag
\(2\)-morphisms.  Then \(Q_{E,R}\), \(\theta^Q_{\mu,R}\), and the
product, coproduct, primitive, and transition integration residuals are
not defined as finite source data.  A scalar determinant or Fock trace
can record coefficients after decategorification; it cannot supply the
correspondence-level primitive brackets required by the certificate.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[\textup{(O2)}/hybrid compatibility obstruction]
\label{prop:o2-hybrid-compatibility-obstruction}
Fix a finite HN height \(R\) and one of the three type-II simple walls.
Under the degree map
\(\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}\) the wall labels are
\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\hbox{wall} & (n,l,m) & \hbox{elliptic-degree shadow}\\
\hline
\delta_1=2f_2-f_3 & (1,1,0) & m=0\\
\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3 & (0,1,1) & m=1\\
\delta_3=f_3 & (0,-1,0) & m=0 .
\end{array}
\]
A finite compact construction which claims both the hybrid source
\(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate} and the
type-II Pfaffian wall model of
Definition~\ref{def:type-ii-pfaffian-wall-certificate} must supply a
compatibility package at the same height \(R\).  It consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a wall object \(x_{\delta_i,R}\) in the finite local or rigidified
wrapped moduli used by
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), mapping to Gram degree
\(\delta_i\);
\item a finite restriction of the unreduced hybrid deformation theory to
the wall object, producing a self-Ext complex \(K^E_{\delta_i,R}\);
\item a quotient-compatible comparison diagram
\[
\begin{tikzcd}
\mathsf{BM}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R
  \arrow[r,"\ell_{\delta_i,R}"]
  \arrow[d,"Q_{E,R}"']
&
K^E_{\delta_i,R}
  \arrow[r,"\operatorname{split}_{\delta_i,R}"]
  \arrow[d,"Q^K_{\delta_i,R}"]
&
K^{E,\mathrm{tan}}_{\delta_i,R}\oplus
K^{E,\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R}
  \arrow[d,"Q^{\mathrm{tan}}_{\delta_i,R}\oplus Q^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R}"]
\\
\mathsf{BM}^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{hyb}}_R
  \arrow[r,"\overline\ell_{\delta_i,R}"']
&
K^{\mathrm{red}}_{\delta_i,R}
  \arrow[r,"\overline{\operatorname{split}}_{\delta_i,R}"']
&
K^{\mathrm{tan}}_{\delta_i,R}\oplus
K^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R},
\end{tikzcd}
\]
where the bottom row is the reduced wall chart of
Proposition~\ref{prop:o2-local-obstruction-certificate};
\item an invariant normal Pfaffian unit and rank-one normal model
\[
\operatorname{Pf}(K^{\mathrm{nor}}_{\delta_i,R})
=\upsilon_{\delta_i,R}u_{\delta_i,R},\qquad
s_{\delta_i}(\upsilon_{\delta_i,R})=\upsilon_{\delta_i,R},
\]
after the quotient orientation trivializations used by \(Q_{E,R}\);
\item protected integration compatibility:
if \(\operatorname{pf}_{\delta_i,R}\) is the local Pfaffian class of the
normal crossing, then every nonzero monomial of
\[
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}\bigl(Q_{E,R}\operatorname{pf}_{\delta_i,R}\bigr)
\]
is supported on the full monomial \(q^nr^ls^m\) for the displayed Gram
label \((n,l,m)\), and the quotient-oriented Pfaffian sign is preserved
under \(s_{\delta_i}\).  This support and sign equality is compatible
with the transition residual \(\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}\).
\end{enumerate}
Equivalently, the finite residual
\[
\mathfrak O^{\mathrm{O2/hyb}}_{\delta_i,R}
=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{wall}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Ext}\text{-}\mathrm{split}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{unit}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rank}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{atlas,comp}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{atlas,bdy}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{atlas,ov}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{wall}}_{\delta_i,R},
\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{wall}}_{\delta_i,R}
\right)
\]
must be trivialized.  The \(\delta_2\) row has \(m=1\), hence its wall
object cannot be supplied by the projection-finite Ran stratum alone.
It must pass through the rigidified wrapped prequotient and the ordered
mixed correspondences before the reduced \(E\)-quotient.  A local
rank-one chart detached from
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), or a Fock/Hecke factor carrying only
the scalar \(s\)-degree, does not make this residual vanish.  For O2 this
compatibility must be imposed as a wall atlas: at finite height \(R\),
each retained component and boundary stratum of \(\Hpl_{\delta_i}\) needs
a chart of the above form, and the normal Pfaffian units, tangent/normal
splittings, quotient orientations, and protected integration maps must
agree on chart overlaps.  A single generic chart computes only a local
sign.
The atlas entries record, respectively, charts on every retained wall
component, charts on retained boundary strata, and agreement of normal
Pfaffian units, tangent/normal splittings, quotient orientations, and
protected integration maps on chart overlaps, compatibly with HN
transitions.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The three Gram labels are the inverse calculation recorded in the
type-II root section:
\[
\delta_1\leftrightarrow(1,1,0),\qquad
\delta_2\leftrightarrow(0,1,1),\qquad
\delta_3\leftrightarrow(0,-1,0).
\]
The local Pfaffian proposition requires a reduced wall chart, a reduced
self-Ext complex, a tangent/normal splitting, an invariant normal unit,
and \(N_{\delta_i}^{\mathrm{Pf}}=1\).  The hybrid certificate requires
unreduced local, wrapped, and ordered mixed correspondences, followed
only then by \(Q_{E,R}\) and by protected integration.  If both claims
are claims about the same compact source, the wall complex must be the
localization of the finite hybrid deformation theory and its splitting,
unit, quotient descent, and protected trace must commute with the hybrid
operations.  The displayed diagram and residual tuple are precisely this
finite compatibility requirement.

For \(\delta_2\) the target monomial has \(s\)-degree one.  By
Lemma~\ref{lem:projection-e-support-locality-obstruction}, positive
elliptic degree is not supported at finitely many points of \(E\).
Thus an ordinary projection-finite Ran object cannot supply the wall
object whose local Pfaffian class integrates to the \(\delta_2\) label.
The wrapped prequotient, its anchor, the mixed correspondences, and the
quotient-after-correspondence functor are not optional decoration; they
are the data needed even to state the compatibility of the local Pfaffian
calculation with the hybrid \(s\)-direction.
\end{proof}

\begin{openproblem}[Hybrid wrapped factorization]
\label{op:hybrid-wrapped-factorization}
Construct the finite-stage certificates
\(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate} and prove
that their inverse limit exists in the completed Hall/factorization
category.  The exact obstruction is the simultaneous construction of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the compact extension-closed category and stability/HN sector whose
local and wrapped moduli are finite type in bounded \(h_S\)-height;
\item a rigidified wrapped prequotient
\(\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr,rig}}\to
\mathcal M_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}\) retaining relative \(E\)-position
without inserting a positive elliptic-degree object at a finite Ran point;
\item local-local, all ordered two-sided local-wrapped, and
wrapped-wrapped extension stacks
with admissible vanishing-cycle pull-push functors and proper-support
witnesses for the \(q\)-maps, equivalently vanishing of
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{LL}}_R\),
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{mix}}_R\), and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{prop},\mathrm{WW}}_R\);
\item Thom--Sebastiani-compatible strong orientations on all three kinds
of correspondences and on the eight-word two-step binary flag atlas,
proving the displayed parenthesization identities and the four-input
pentagon in finite HN quotients, with higher colored factorization kept as
a separate obligation;
\item descent through the reduced \(E\)-quotient after forming
correspondences, including the finite-stabilizer gerbe checks and the
\(Q_{E,R}\)-compatibility isomorphisms, with
\(\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{form}}_R=
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{adm}}_R=
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{flag}}_R=
\mathfrak o^{Q,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}=0\);
\item protected integration whose decategorified trace sends elliptic
degree \(b\) to \(s^b\), recovers the Igusa \(s\)-direction
coefficientwise, vanishes on the chain/product/coproduct/primitive
defects \(\mathfrak o^{I,\bullet}_R\), has
\(\mathfrak o^{I,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}=0\) for all \(R'\ge R\), and whose
primitive bracket passes the Borcherds--Kac--Moody presentation test.
\end{enumerate}
Equivalently, one must trivialize
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}\) for every finite HN height \(R\),
including the quotient, integration, and HN transition components for
every \(R'\ge R\).
Until these six items are supplied, \(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) is a
finite categorical datum whose existence remains open, not a compact QFT
constructed in this paper and not a detached determinant factor.
Ordinary disjoint-open factorization on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) is only
the projection-finite \(b=0\) part.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{openproblem}[Normal-ordered descent of the protected bracket]
\label{op:pi-descent-of-bracket}
Let \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\),
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\),
\(B:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\times\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}
\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) be as in
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}.  Suppose a Hall lift
\(\widetilde P_X\) of the protected primitive algebra is supplied with a
\(\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}\)-graded bracket, for a supplied
semigroup
\(\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}\subset\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{alg}}\subset
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\).  Construct a
cocycle-corrected descent \(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\) categorifying the
normal-ordered homomorphism
\(\overline\Pi_X:\widehat\Gamma_X\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\).  The raw
Hall bracket
is concentrated in additive charge \(c+c'\) inside the supplied effective
support, whose raw Gram shadow is
\[
\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c').
\]
The coefficient category, central translations, Hochschild cocycle
\(B_{\mathrm{ch}}\), and cochain
\(\Theta_\Pi(c)=\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c)}\) are those of
Definition~\ref{def:normal-ordering-coefficient-dg-category}.  The datum
\(\Theta_\Pi\) must lift the lattice identity
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_\Pi=B
\]
to the chain identity
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_\Pi=B_{\mathrm{ch}}
\]
in the Picard dg groupoid of central translations.  Its triple
homotopies must be compatible with the Hall extension correspondences,
the Joyce--Upmeier orientation cocycle, the Hopf pairing, the reduced
\(E\)-quotient, the finite fibre products over
\(\overline\Pi_X\), the completed HN tensor topology, and the
\(S^1\)-action on the cyclic complex.  Without such a lift, the raw
bracket has the wrong Gram degree and the ordinary pushforward along
\(\Pi_X\) is not a recognition target.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{definition}[Normal-ordering coefficient dg category]
\label{def:normal-ordering-coefficient-dg-category}
Fix a finite HN quotient \(R\) of the protected Hall sector, before
passing to the inverse limit.  Let
\[
\mathsf{Ch}_{k,R,E}^{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}
\]
be the dg category of \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded complexes of
protected vanishing-cycle sheaves after the cosection-reduced
\(E\)-quotient, with differential preserving the Gram degree and with
support projected to the finite test window of the stage.  The transition
functors for \(R'\ge R\) are required to be strict continuous maps for the
HN filtration.  They define the completed separated dg category
\[
\mathsf{Ch}_{k,\widehat{\mathrm{HN}},E}^{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}
:=\varprojlim_R
\mathsf{Ch}_{k,R,E}^{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}.
\]
Every completed tensor product in this section is taken in this topology:
\[
V\widehat{\otimes}W:=\varprojlim_R(V_R\otimes W_R)
\]
for compatible finite stages.  No tensor product or coproduct is formed
directly on an unfiltered infinite direct sum.
For \(\eta\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) define the central translation
dg autoequivalence
\[
(\mathsf T_\eta V)_\gamma:=V_{\gamma+\eta},
\qquad
d_{\mathsf T_\eta V}=d_V .
\]
Then
\(\mathsf T_0=\mathrm{id}\) and
\(\mathsf T_\eta\mathsf T_{\eta'}=\mathsf T_{\eta+\eta'}\) strictly.
Let
\(\mathsf{Pic}^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\) denote the
Picard dg groupoid generated by these translations and their chain
homotopies.

For formal charges \(c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\) put
\[
B_{\mathrm{ch}}(c,c'):=\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}.
\]
This is the translation-valued Hochschild \(2\)-cocycle representing the
normal-ordering defect.  A chain-level normal-ordering datum is a
normalized \(1\)-cochain
\[
\Theta_\Pi(c)=\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c)}
\in
C^1_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\!
\bigl(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};
\mathsf{Pic}^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\bigr)
\]
together with natural quasi-isomorphisms
\[
\vartheta_{c,c'}:
\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c)}
\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c')}
\mathsf T_{\Pi_X(c+c')}
\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_\Pi=B_{\mathrm{ch}}.
\]
The translation cochain itself is formal once the finite coefficient dg
category exists.  The non-formal datum is its realization on the compact
Hall correspondence targets, with orientation, quotient, cyclic, and HN
transition compatibility.
For a finite \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)-supported complex
\(V=\bigoplus_cV_c\), the uncompleted shorthand is
\[
(\overline\Pi_{*,\mathrm{fin}}^{\Theta}V)_\gamma
=\prod_{\Pi_X(c)=\gamma}V_c,
\]
with the product finite.  Its product and bracket structure is transported
by the \(\Theta_\Pi\)-quasi-isomorphisms.  Thus a raw bracket output in
charge \(c+c'\), whose Gram shadow is \(\Pi_X(c+c')\), is read after
\(\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}\) in degree
\[
\Pi_X(c+c')-B(c,c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c').
\]
At a finite stage the actual coefficient object is defined on
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\).  If
\[
V_R=\bigoplus_{(c,T)\in\widehat\Gamma_R} (V_R)_{(c,T)}
\]
is a finite \(\widehat\Gamma_R\)-graded complex, set
\[
(\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta}V_R)_\gamma
=
\prod_{\substack{(c,T)\in\widehat\Gamma_R\\
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\gamma}} (V_R)_{(c,T)}.
\]
This product is finite; when the fibre is empty it is \(0\).  The
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)-graded formula above is only the special
case \(T=0\) before the counterterm has been recorded.  For a compatible
inverse system \(V=\varprojlim_R V_R\), the completed descent is
\[
(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}V)_\gamma
:=
\varprojlim_R(\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta_R}V_R)_\gamma .
\]
Thus a product over a fibre of \(\overline\Pi_X\) means an inverse limit
of finite fibre products.  The notation is not a licence to multiply over
an uncontrolled infinite fibre.  Products, brackets, coproducts, pairings,
and radical quotients after \(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\) are defined
only when their finite-stage maps commute with the transition maps and
are continuous for the displayed HN completion.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Finite Picard normal-ordering lift]
\label{lem:finite-picard-normal-ordering-lift}
Fix a finite HN stage \(R\) for which the coefficient dg category of
Definition~\ref{def:normal-ordering-coefficient-dg-category} and the
finite set \(\widehat\Gamma_R\) are supplied.  Put
\[
\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{\mathrm{phys}}(c):=\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c)}
\qquad(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}})
\]
and, after the counterterm \(T\) has been recorded,
\[
\widehat\Theta_{\Pi,R}(c,T)
:=\mathsf T_{-\overline\Pi_X(c,T)}
=\mathsf T_{T-\Pi_X(c)}
\qquad ((c,T)\in\widehat\Gamma_R).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] \(B_{\mathrm{ch},R}(c,c')=\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}\) is a
normalized Hochschild \(2\)-cocycle in the Picard dg groupoid of central
translations, and
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{\mathrm{phys}}=B_{\mathrm{ch},R}.
\]
\item[\textup{(ii)}] \(\widehat\Theta_{\Pi,R}\) is a strict Picard
character on every allowed finite normal-ordered charge channel
\((c,T)\star(c',T')\in\widehat\Gamma_R\):
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\widehat\Theta_{\Pi,R}=0.
\]
Equivalently, the \(\widehat\Gamma_R\)-grading has already absorbed the
Gram defect, and \(\overline\Pi_X\) is additive on \(\widehat\Gamma_X\).
\item[\textup{(iii)}] If the successor transition
\(\rho_{R^+R}\) is the degree-truncation map of
\textup{(D0-F)} and commutes with central translations, then the finite
fibre square \textup{(NO1)} commutes for every finite
\(\widehat\Gamma_{R^+}\)-graded complex \(V_{R^+}\).
\end{enumerate}
Thus the Picard part of normal ordering is formal after the finite
coefficient dg category is supplied.  What is not formal is the action of
these translations on Hall pull-push correspondences, orientation lines,
cyclic complexes, and the product/coproduct/pairing transition maps.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The translation functors satisfy
\(\mathsf T_\eta\mathsf T_{\eta'}=\mathsf T_{\eta+\eta'}\) and
\(\mathsf T_0=\mathrm{id}\) strictly.  Therefore
\[
(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{\mathrm{phys}})(c,c')
=\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c)-\Pi_X(c')+\Pi_X(c+c')}
=\mathsf T_{B(c,c')},
\]
by Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect}.  The same bilinear cocycle
identity for \(B\) gives \(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}B_{\mathrm{ch},R}=0\), and
normalization follows from \(B(c,0)=B(0,c)=0\).

For \(\widehat\Theta_{\Pi,R}\), compute with
\((c,T)\star(c',T')=(c+c',T+T'+B(c,c'))\):
\[
\begin{aligned}
&-\overline\Pi_X(c,T)-\overline\Pi_X(c',T')
+\overline\Pi_X((c,T)\star(c',T'))\\
&\qquad
=-\Pi_X(c)+T-\Pi_X(c')+T'
+\Pi_X(c+c')-T-T'-B(c,c')=0.
\end{aligned}
\]
Hence its Hochschild boundary is the identity translation.

Finally, the fibre of
\(\overline\Pi_X:\widehat\Gamma_R\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) over a fixed
\(\gamma\) is finite because \(\widehat\Gamma_R\) is finite.  Since
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\subset\widehat\Gamma_{R^+}\), the two composites in
\textup{(NO1)} both first select the finite summands with
\(\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\gamma\) and then kill exactly those summands not
lying in \(\widehat\Gamma_R\).  Commutation with central translations
identifies the coefficient maps.  Thus the square commutes.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Kunneth-pure multiplicative orientation criterion]
