\label{lem:explicit-multiplicative-orientation-cocycle}
Adopt the notation of
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice} and
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}.  Suppose a
projection-finite Kunneth-pure substack of the reduced compact
protected derived moduli stack of \(K3\times E\) is supplied, closed
under the Hall extension correspondences under consideration.  Suppose
also that on this substack:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the full self-Ext determinant admits a functorial Kunneth
decomposition, including the cross terms for direct sums;
\item the elliptic factor carries a chosen Costello--Li flat
trivialization compatible with the reduced \(E\)-quotient
\cite{CostelloLiBCOV,CostelloLiOpenClosedBCOV};
\item the K3 factors carry supplied Joyce--Upmeier
multiplicative orientation isomorphisms with strict pentagon; and
\item these choices are \(S^1\)-equivariant on the cyclic complexes.
\end{enumerate}
Then the tensor product of these supplied data gives multiplicative
orientation isomorphisms
\[
\mu_{c,c'}:o_{c+c'}\xrightarrow{\sim}o_c\otimes o_{c'}
\]
on that Kunneth-pure sector, natural for the restricted Hall
correspondences and compatible with the reduced \(E\)-quotient.
No assertion is made here for the full compact or wrapped
\(K3\times E\) protected sector.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Conditional tensor product.}
On the supplied Kunneth-pure substack, the full self-Ext determinant
has the assumed factorization into K3 factors and the flat elliptic
factor, including all direct-sum cross terms.  Tensor the supplied
factorwise Joyce--Upmeier multiplicative orientation maps with the
chosen Costello--Li trivialization
\cite{CostelloLiBCOV,CostelloLiOpenClosedBCOV} on the elliptic factor.  This gives
the displayed maps \(\mu_{c,c'}\) on precisely that restricted sector.


Naturality, the strict pentagon, and reduced-
\(E\)-compatibility follow from the corresponding supplied properties
on the factors.  The \(S^1\)-statement is exactly the assumed
equivariance of the factorwise cyclic data.

The proof uses no global product decomposition of the full compact
moduli stack and no projection formula for wrapped branes.  Therefore it
proves (O) only on the explicitly supplied Kunneth-pure sector.  The
full compact/wrapped orientation problem remains the open obligation
recorded in Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Conditional orientation comparison]
\label{rem:pin-c-gerbe-mult-orientation}
The criterion above explains how a multiplicative orientation would
factor after one has already supplied the projection-finite Kunneth-pure
sector and all factorwise orientation data.  It does not construct the
reduced compact \(K3\times E\) orientation gerbe, its cyclic
equivariance, or its HN-completed higher-rank extension.  Those remain
part of the Dirac--Igusa realization certificate.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[PTVV--Joyce normal-ordered descent of the primitive bracket;
certificate and obstruction]
\label{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}
Adopt the notation of Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice} and
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice}: formal lattice
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\), Gram shadow
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}=\Z^3\),
symmetric quadratic cocycle
\(B(c,c')=(Q\!\cdot\!Q',\,Q\!\cdot\!P'+Q'\!\cdot\!P,\,P\!\cdot\!P')\)
satisfying \(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\).  Suppose:
In the Hall-geometric clauses below, quantifiers over charges mean charges
in the supplied effective support or in the finite normal-ordered support
of the relevant stage.  The formal lattice \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\)
is only the ambient bookkeeping lattice; it is not asserted to be fully
realized by compact moduli.
At each finite stage the theorem uses the supplied normal-ordered
refinement of the primitive layer,
\[
\widetilde P_R=
\bigoplus_{(c,T)\in\widehat\Gamma_R}\widetilde P_{R,(c,T)},
\]
whose bracket lands in
\[
[\widetilde P_{R,(c,T)},\widetilde P_{R,(c',T')}]
\subset
\widetilde P_{R,(c,T)\star(c',T')}.
\]
The no-overcount residual of
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate} is required to vanish, so
these labels refine rather than duplicate the \(c\)-graded primitive
source.  The completed object is the inverse limit of these finite
normal-ordered stages.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(P)] \emph{(PTVV host.)}  The protected primitive layer
\(\widetilde P_X=\bigoplus_c\widetilde P_{X,c}\) is realized as
\(\widetilde P_X=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)\) for an oriented
critical Hall/factorization object \(\mathcal F_X\) on a
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic derived moduli stack
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\) of compactly supported B-branes on \(K3\times E\)
in the sense of
Pantev--Toen--Vaquie--Vezzosi \cite{PTVV2013} (cf.\ the local schema of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}), graded by
supplied algebraic/effective charge
\(c\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}\subset
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{alg}}\subset\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\), with reduced
\(E\)-quotient compatible with the projection
\(p_E:K3\times E\to E\) of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.  The
factorization product on \(\mathcal F_X\) is \(A_\infty\) (homotopy
\(E_3\)): the BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} Thom--Sebastiani isomorphism on
disjoint d-critical charts is a derived natural isomorphism, and
downstream consumption acts on the \(H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}\)
truncation, on which the bracket descends strictly.  Strict \(E_3\)
rectification of the protected chain-level product is a separate
residual obligation: it would require coherent strictification of the
Massey--Saito/BBDJS Thom--Sebastiani product together with the
multiplicative orientation cocycle.  It is not used by the denominator
identity or the primitive-recognition theorem, which consume only the
strict \(H^0\)-level Lie superalgebra.  The binary Hall operations are
represented, before the reduced quotient, by
correspondences
\[
\mathfrak M_{X,c}\times\mathfrak M_{X,c'}
\xleftarrow{\ p_{c,c'}\ }
\mathfrak E_{c,c'}
\xrightarrow{\ q_{c,c'}\ }
\mathfrak M_{X,c+c'},
\]
and the two parenthesizations of a triple product are compared on the
two-step flag stack
\(\mathfrak{Flag}_{a,b,c}\).  These correspondences are part of the
input; the Borcherds product does not construct them.
\item[(E)] \emph{(Reduced \(E\)-quotient and completion.)}
The Hall correspondences, orientation lines, Hopf pairing, and central
translation functors \(\mathsf T_\eta\) are constructed before quotienting
by translations of \(E\), then descend to the cosection-reduced
\(E\)-quotient and to the sectorial HN inverse system.  In particular
\(\mathsf T_\eta\) commutes with the reduced \(E\)-quotient, with HN
completion, and with the local-local, wrapped-wrapped, and mixed
local/wrapped extension correspondences of
Open Problem~\ref{op:hybrid-wrapped-factorization}.  The completed
primitive object is the inverse limit of finite stages:
\[
P_X^\Pi=\varprojlim_R P_{R}^{\Pi},\qquad
P_X^\Pi\widehat{\otimes}P_X^\Pi
=\varprojlim_R(P_R^\Pi\otimes P_R^\Pi).
\]
The maps \(m_R\), \([\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_R\), \(\Delta_R\),
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_R\), and
\(\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta}\) commute with all transition maps.  Thus
every product over a fibre of \(\overline\Pi_X\), and every completed
tensor product used by the Hopf structure, is the inverse limit of finite
operations.  This is a hypothesis; it is not a formal consequence of the
lattice homomorphism \(\overline\Pi_X\).
\item[(O)] \emph{(\(S^1\)-equivariant multiplicative orientation cocycle.)}
The collection \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) is an \(S^1\)-equivariant
multiplicative orientation cocycle on \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic
stacks satisfying the strict pentagon.  Concretely: an orientation
datum \(\{o_c\}_{c\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}}\) in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} is supplied with
\emph{Joyce--Upmeier multiplicative isomorphisms} \cite{JoyceUpmeier}
\[
\mu_{c,c'}\,:\;o_{c+c'}\;\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\;o_c\otimes o_{c'},
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
satisfying the strict cocycle pentagon
\(\mu_{c+c',c''}\circ\mu_{c,c'}=\mu_{c,c'+c''}\circ\mu_{c',c''}\)
on the Cartesian extension correspondence, compatible with the
reduced \(E\)-quotient and with the HN/sectorial completion of
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}, and \emph{equivariant
under the loop-rotation \(S^1\)-action on the cyclic complex of
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\)}.  This last condition lifts the orientation
cocycle from a Hochschild trivialization to a \emph{cyclic}
trivialization, and is exactly the kind of orientation technology
Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} supply once the reduced compact
sector and its cyclic model have been constructed.  The
\(S^1\)-equivariance is not inferred from the scalar determinant; it is
an input on the Hall side.
Equivalently, the collection \(\{o_c\}\) is an \(S^1\)-equivariant
multiplicative section of the determinant gerbe over the moduli of
objects in the protected sector.
\item[(\(\Theta\))] \emph{(Cocycle-corrected degree shifts.)}
A coherent family of central degree-shift data is supplied on the
primitive bracket targets in the coefficient dg category of
Definition~\ref{def:normal-ordering-coefficient-dg-category}.  The chain
representative of the Gram defect is the normalized translation-valued
Hochschild \(2\)-cocycle
\[
B_{\mathrm{ch}}(c,c'):=\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}
\in
Z^2_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\!
\bigl(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};
\mathsf{Pic}^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\bigr).
\]
A normalized \(1\)-cochain
\[
\Theta_\Pi\in
C^1_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\!
\bigl(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};
\mathsf{Pic}^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\bigr),
\qquad
\Theta_\Pi(c)=\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c)}
\]
is supplied with coherent natural quasi-isomorphisms
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_\Pi=B_{\mathrm{ch}}.
\]
The formula for \(\Theta_\Pi\) is the formal central translation
cochain.  The hypothesis is stronger: these translations must act on the
actual Hall correspondence targets and must be compatible with the
orientation, reduced quotient, cyclic model, and finite HN transitions.
Equivalently, for every pair \(c,c'\) the raw bracket target of Gram
degree \(\Pi_X(c+c')\) is translated by
\(\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}\) to the additive Gram degree
\(\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')\).  For triples \(a,b,c\), the two composites over
\(\mathfrak{Flag}_{a,b,c}\),
\[
(\vartheta_{a,b}\otimes 1)\circ\vartheta_{a+b,c},
\qquad
(1\otimes\vartheta_{b,c})\circ\vartheta_{a,b+c},
\]
agree after the Hall associator, Thom--Sebastiani transport, and
orientation signs.  Their quotient in
\(\pi_1\mathsf{Pic}^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\) is the
triple obstruction
\[
\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}(a,b,c)
:=
\bigl[(\vartheta_{a,b}\otimes 1)\circ\vartheta_{a+b,c}\bigr]
-
\bigl[(1\otimes\vartheta_{b,c})\circ\vartheta_{a,b+c}\bigr],
\]
with the Hall associator and orientation transport inserted in the
middle.  Hypothesis \((\Theta)\) requires
\(\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}(a,b,c)=0\) for every two-step Hall flag.
On degrees this is exactly
\[
B(a,b)+B(a+b,c)=B(b,c)+B(a,b+c),
\]
i.e. \(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}B_{\mathrm{ch}}=0\), but the displayed equality is
required as a chain homotopy, not only as a lattice identity.
\item[(F)] \emph{(Frobenius pairing.)}  The protected Hall bracket
\([\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]\) and the protected Hopf pairing
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle\) on \(\widetilde P_X\) (the latter
furnished by the squaring isomorphism
\(o_c^{\otimes 2}\simeq\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} and the PTVV \cite{PTVV2013}
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form on
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\), trivialized along the reduced \(E\)-quotient via
the Costello--Li flat Calabi--Yau pairing
\cite{CostelloRenormalization,CostelloLiBCOV,CostelloLiOpenClosedBCOV}) satisfy the
graded-Frobenius identity
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle=0
\]
for homogeneous \(x,y,z\in\widetilde P_X\) of additive formal charges
\(c_x,c_y,c_z\) with \(c_x+c_y+c_z=0\).  After applying
\(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\) the same identity is imposed for the
transported bracket \([\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_\Theta\).
\item[(Cyc)] \emph{(Negative-cyclic lift.)}
The Hochschild cochain \(\Theta_\Pi\) has an \(S^1\)-equivariant lift
\(\Theta_\Pi^{-}\) in the negative-cyclic complex of the protected Hall
sector, and the lifted equation
\[
(b+uB_{\mathrm C})\Theta_\Pi^{-}=B_{\mathrm{ch}}^{-}
\]
holds, where \(B_{\mathrm C}\) is the Connes operator and
\(B_{\mathrm{ch}}^{-}\) is a negative-cyclic representative whose
forgetful image in Hochschild cochains is \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}\).  The
forgetful map sends the cyclic equation to the Hochschild equation in
\((\Theta)\), so the cyclic lift is a refinement, not a replacement, of
normal ordering.
\end{enumerate}
Then, writing \(P_X^\Pi:=\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\widetilde P_X\), for
finite normal-ordered labels \((c,T)\), \((c',T')\) whose summands are
supplied, the finite-stage normal-ordered lift of the raw
physical-charge bracket
\[
[\widetilde P_{R,(c,T)},\widetilde P_{R,(c',T')}]
\subset
\widetilde P_{R,(c,T)\star(c',T')}
\]
induces, after passage to the compatible inverse limit, a
cocycle-corrected Gram-graded bracket
\[
[\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_\Theta:
(P_X^\Pi)_{\overline\Pi_X(c,T)}
\otimes
(P_X^\Pi)_{\overline\Pi_X(c',T')}
\longrightarrow
(P_X^\Pi)_{\overline\Pi_X(c,T)+\overline\Pi_X(c',T')}.
\]
Thus \(B\) is not erased; it is the coherent degree-shift by which the
raw target \(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\) is transported to
the additive normal-ordered Gram target
\(\overline\Pi_X((c,T)\star(c',T'))\).  This object
\[
P_X^\Pi
\]
is therefore a \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded Lie superalgebra at
the stated \(H^0\) level, and hypothesis~(1b) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition} is satisfied with the
\(\Theta\)-corrected descent.

If the finite-fibre HN topology of (E), \((\Theta)\), its triple
coherence, (F), (Cyc), and radical ideal/coideal stability are not
supplied, the minimal computable obstruction is the finite-HN inverse
system of classes
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}}
:=
\left\{
\mathfrak o_{\Theta,R'R}^{\mathrm{fib}},
\mathfrak o_{\Theta,R'R}^{m},
\mathfrak o_{\Theta,R'R}^{\Delta},
\mathfrak o_{\Theta,R'R}^{\langle\, ,\,\rangle}
\right\}_{R'\ge R},
\]
where \(\rho_{R'R}\) is the source transition,
\(\rho^\Pi_{R'R}\) is the descended primitive transition, and these are
the finite Hom-space defects
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta,R'R}^{\mathrm{fib}}
:=
\rho^\Pi_{R'R}\overline\Pi_{R',*}^{\Theta_{R'}}
-
\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta_R}\rho_{R'R},
\]
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta,R'R}^{m}
:=
\rho^\Pi_{R'R}m_{R'}^{\Theta}
-
m_R^{\Theta}(\rho^\Pi_{R'R}\otimes\rho^\Pi_{R'R}),
\qquad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta,R'R}^{\Delta}
:=
(\rho^\Pi_{R'R}\otimes\rho^\Pi_{R'R})\Delta_{R'}^{\Theta}
-
\Delta_R^{\Theta}\rho^\Pi_{R'R},
\]
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta,R'R}^{\langle\, ,\,\rangle}
:=
\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_R
(\rho^\Pi_{R'R}\otimes\rho^\Pi_{R'R})
-
\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_{R'},
\]
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{Hoch}}
:=[B_{\mathrm{ch}}-d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_\Pi]
\in
HH^2_{\mathrm{red},E}
\bigl(\widetilde P_X^{\mathrm{br}};
\mathsf{Pic}^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\bigr),
\]
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{tri}}
:=[\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}]
\in
HH^3_{\mathrm{red},E}
\bigl(\widetilde P_X^{\mathrm{br}};
\pi_1\mathsf{Pic}^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\bigr),
\]
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{Jac}}
:=[\operatorname{Jac}_{\Theta}]
\in
C^3_{\mathrm{CE},\mathrm{red},E}
\bigl(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\widetilde P_X;
\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\widetilde P_X\bigr),
\]
\[
\mathfrak o_F
:=\bigl[
(x,y,z)\mapsto
\langle[x,y]_{\Theta},z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x||y|}\langle y,[x,z]_{\Theta}\rangle
\bigr]
\in
C^3_{\mathrm{cyc},\mathrm{red},E}
\bigl(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\widetilde P_X;k\bigr),
\]
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{cyc}}
:=[B_{\mathrm{ch}}^{-}-(b+uB_{\mathrm C})\Theta_\Pi^{-}]
\in
HC^{-\,2}_{\mathrm{red},E}
\bigl(\widetilde P_X^{\mathrm{br}};
\mathsf{Pic}^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\bigr),
\]
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad}}
:=
\bigl(
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad,Lie}},
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad,coid}}
\bigr),
\]
defined on the HN-completed reduced \(E\)-quotient of the protected
bracket category, where
\[
P_X^\Pi=\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\widetilde P_X,\qquad
\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi
=\{r\in P_X^\Pi\mid \langle r,w\rangle=0\ \text{for all }w\in P_X^\Pi\}.
\]
The two components are
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad,Lie}}
:=\bigl[
(x,r,z)\mapsto
\langle[x,r]_{\Theta},z\rangle
\bigr]
\in
\Hom_{\mathrm{red},E}
\bigl(P_X^\Pi\otimes\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi\otimes P_X^\Pi,k\bigr),
\]
and, for the quotient map
\(\bar q_\Pi:P_X^\Pi\to P_X^\Pi/
\overline{\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi}\),
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad,coid}}(r)
:=
(\bar q_\Pi\widehat{\otimes}\bar q_\Pi)\Delta_\Theta(r),
\qquad r\in\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi .
\]
Here \(\Delta_\Theta\) is the descended completed Hopf coproduct.  The
condition
\(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad,coid}}=0\) says exactly that
\[
\Delta_\Theta(\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi)
\subset
\overline{\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi\widehat{\otimes} P_X^\Pi
+P_X^\Pi\widehat{\otimes}\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi}.
\]
Here \(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}}\) is the assertion that
\(\overline\Pi_{*}^{\Theta}\), the transported product, the transported
coproduct, and the pairing are strict morphisms of the finite HN inverse
system; its vanishing is what makes the completed fibre products and
\(\widehat{\otimes}\)-operations well defined.  The class
\(\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}(a,b,c)\) is the difference of the two
triple composites over
\(\mathfrak{Flag}_{a,b,c}\), and
\(\operatorname{Jac}_{\Theta}\) is the signed Jacobiator of the transported
bracket.  The Hochschild shadow is computed on homogeneous charges by the
explicit formula for \(B(c,c')\); the triple shadow is the displayed
cocycle identity for \(B\), hence zero at the lattice level; the cyclic
component is computed by applying \(B_{\mathrm C}\) to the chosen cyclic
orientation representative.  The class
\(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad}}\) vanishes exactly when the Hopf
radical is both a Lie ideal for the transported bracket and a coideal for
the completed descended coproduct.  Closedness of the radical in the HN
topology is still a separate topological hypothesis.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (The coefficient category).}
The coefficient system for normal ordering is the Picard dg groupoid of
central translations of
\(\mathsf{Ch}_{k,\widehat{\mathrm{HN}},E}^{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}}\), as in
Definition~\ref{def:normal-ordering-coefficient-dg-category}.
That definition constructs \(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\) as the inverse
limit of the finite fibre products
\((\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta}V_R)_\gamma\).  The finite-transition part
of hypothesis (E), encoded by
\(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}}=0\), is what permits the
transported product, coproduct, and pairing to pass from finite stages to
the completed HN object.
With the convention
\((\mathsf T_\eta V)_\gamma=V_{\gamma+\eta}\), applying
\(\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}\) to a raw target of degree
\(\Pi_X(c+c')\) displays it in degree
\[
\Pi_X(c+c')-B(c,c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c').
\]
Thus \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}(c,c')=\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}\) is the exact
translation-valued Hochschild \(2\)-cocycle measuring failure of raw
Gram additivity.

\emph{Step 2 (The boundary equation).}
For the standard additive Hochschild differential on normalized
cochains,
\[
(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_\Pi)(c,c')
=\Theta_\Pi(c)+\Theta_\Pi(c')-\Theta_\Pi(c+c').
\]
The underlying degree of the translation
\(\Theta_\Pi(c)=\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c)}\) gives
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_\Pi(c,c')
=-\Pi_X(c)-\Pi_X(c')+\Pi_X(c+c')=B(c,c').
\]
Hypothesis \((\Theta)\) is precisely the statement that this arithmetic
boundary is represented by actual central translation
quasi-isomorphisms on the protected Hall bracket targets.

\emph{Step 3 (Triples, Jacobi, and Frobenius).}
For three charges \(a,b,c\), the two ways of translating the target of
a two-step bracket differ by
\[
B(a,b)+B(a+b,c)-B(b,c)-B(a,b+c)
=-d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}B(a,b,c)=0
\]
by Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}.  The supplied pentagon
homotopies in \((\Theta)\) lift this equality from degrees to the Hall
chain category: the obstruction is precisely
\(\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}(a,b,c)\).  If it vanishes, the
normal-ordered product is associative on \(H^0\), and the supercommutator
bracket inherits the Jacobi identity from the upstairs Hall bracket.  The
corresponding signed Jacobiator is
\[
\operatorname{Jac}_{\Theta}(x,y,z)
=[x,[y,z]_{\Theta}]_{\Theta}
-[[x,y]_{\Theta},z]_{\Theta}
-(-1)^{|x||y|}[y,[x,z]_{\Theta}]_{\Theta};
\]
its degree shadow is zero by the same cocycle identity, and its chain
class is the image of the Hall associator and
\(\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}\).  Hypothesis (F) is then the separate
vanishing of
\[
\mathfrak o_F(x,y,z)
=\langle[x,y]_{\Theta},z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x||y|}\langle y,[x,z]_{\Theta}\rangle.
\]
It is not implied by the degree calculation.

\emph{Step 4 (Orientation, reduced quotient, and radical quotient).}
Hypothesis (O) transports the orientation lines through the same
extension correspondences used by the Hall product; hypothesis (E)
asserts that the translation action, orientation transport, and mixed
local/wrapped correspondences descend through the reduced
\(E\)-quotient and HN completion.  Let
\(\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi\) be the radical of the descended Hopf
pairing.  The exact obstruction to Lie-ideal stability is
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad,Lie}}(x,r,z)
=\langle[x,r]_{\Theta},z\rangle,\qquad r\in\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi .
\]
If (F) holds, this expression equals
\(-(-1)^{|x||r|}\langle r,[x,z]_{\Theta}\rangle=0\), so the radical is a
Lie ideal.  This does not prove coideal stability.  Let
\(\bar q_\Pi:P_X^\Pi\to
P_X^\Pi/\overline{\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi}\).  The exact coideal
obstruction is
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad,coid}}(r)
=
(\bar q_\Pi\widehat{\otimes}\bar q_\Pi)\Delta_\Theta(r).
\]
Its vanishing is equivalent to
\(\Delta_\Theta(r)\) lying in the completed sum
\[
\overline{\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi\widehat{\otimes} P_X^\Pi
+P_X^\Pi\widehat{\otimes}\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi}.
\]
Closedness of \(\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi\) in the Hall topology remains a
separate input.  Only after ideal, coideal, and closedness conditions does
the quotient carry the same \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded Hopf--Lie
structure.

\emph{Step 5 (Cyclic lift and obstruction).}
The Hochschild construction controls the displayed \(H^0\) bracket.
For the full chain-level descent, the degree-shift cochain must be
fixed by loop rotation.  This is exactly hypothesis (Cyc):
\((b+uB_{\mathrm C})\Theta_\Pi^{-}=B_{\mathrm{ch}}^{-}\).  If such a
negative-cyclic lift is absent, or if the finite-HN topology,
triple/Jacobi/Frobenius/radical coherence fails, the seven classes
displayed in the theorem are the obstruction.  They are minimal for this
model: vanishing of \(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}}\) is equivalent
to the finite-fibre descent and completed tensor operations commuting with
the HN inverse system; vanishing of
\(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{Hoch}}\) is equivalent to existence of
the degree-shift trivialization on bracket targets; vanishing of
\(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{tri}}\) is equivalent to compatibility of
that trivialization with the two-step Hall flag correspondences;
vanishing of \(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{Jac}}\) is the Jacobi
compatibility of the transported bracket; vanishing of \(\mathfrak o_F\)
is the Frobenius/Hopf invariance of the transported bracket; vanishing
of \(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{cyc}}\) is equivalent to choosing the
trivialization compatibly with the \(S^1\)-equivariant orientation data;
and vanishing of \(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad}}\), together with
closedness in the HN topology, is the condition for passage to the Hopf
radical quotient.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Finite verification diagrams for normal ordering]
\label{prop:finite-normal-ordering-verification-diagrams}
Fix a successor arrow \(R^+\to R\) in the cofinal HN subsystem of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate}}.  Let
\(P_R^\Pi=\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta_R}\widetilde P_R\) be a finite
normal-ordered primitive stage, with transition
\(\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}:P_{R^+}^\Pi\to P_R^\Pi\).  A supplied finite system kills
the seven normal-ordering obstructions of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}} at this successor arrow
exactly when the following finite maps commute, or are supplied with the
displayed null-homotopies, in the indicated finite Hom complexes.

\textup{(NO1) Finite fibres.}
\[
\begin{tikzcd}
V_{R^+} \arrow[r,"\overline\Pi_{R^+,*}^{\Theta_{R^+}}"]
\arrow[d,"\rho_{R^+R}"']
& \overline\Pi_{R^+,*}^{\Theta_{R^+}}V_{R^+}
\arrow[d,"\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}"]\\
V_R \arrow[r,"\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta_R}"']
& \overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta_R}V_R .
\end{tikzcd}
\]
This is \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{fib}}_{\Theta,R^+R}=0\); it says that
fibre products over \(\overline\Pi_X\) are finite before completion and
transition-compatible before the inverse limit is taken.

\textup{(NO2) Product, coproduct, pairing.}
\[
\begin{tikzcd}
P_{R^+}^\Pi\otimes P_{R^+}^\Pi
\arrow[r,"m_{R^+}^{\Theta}"]
\arrow[d,"\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}\otimes\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}"']
& P_{R^+}^\Pi \arrow[d,"\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}"]\\
P_R^\Pi\otimes P_R^\Pi
\arrow[r,"m_R^{\Theta}"']
& P_R^\Pi
\end{tikzcd}
\qquad
\begin{tikzcd}
P_{R^+}^\Pi
\arrow[r,"\Delta_{R^+}^{\Theta}"]
\arrow[d,"\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}"']
& P_{R^+}^\Pi\otimes P_{R^+}^\Pi
\arrow[d,"\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}\otimes\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}"]\\
P_R^\Pi
\arrow[r,"\Delta_R^{\Theta}"']
& P_R^\Pi\otimes P_R^\Pi .
\end{tikzcd}
\]
Together with
\[
\langle\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}x,\rho^\Pi_{R^+R}y\rangle_R
=\langle x,y\rangle_{R^+},
\]
these are
\(\mathfrak o^{m}_{\Theta,R^+R}=
\mathfrak o^{\Delta}_{\Theta,R^+R}=
\mathfrak o^{\langle\, ,\,\rangle}_{\Theta,R^+R}=0\).

\textup{(NO3) Hochschild and negative-cyclic equations.}
For every finite charge pair \(c,c'\in\widehat\Gamma_{R^+}\), the
Hochschild boundary and its cyclic refinement are the finite equations
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_{\Pi,R}(c,c')=B_{\mathrm{ch},R}(c,c'),
\qquad
(b+uB_{\mathrm C})\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}=B_{\mathrm{ch},R}^{-}.
\]
They kill
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Hoch}}_{\Theta,R}\) and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{\Theta,R}\).  The second equation is imposed
in the negative-cyclic complex; it is not obtained by forgetting to
Hochschild cochains.

\textup{(NO4) Triple flag.}
For every two-step finite Hall flag over \(\mathfrak{Flag}_{a,b,c,R}\),
the two translated products must agree after inserting the Hall associator
and orientation transport:
\[
(\mathsf A_{a,b,c}\circ(\vartheta_{a,b}\otimes1)\circ
\vartheta_{a+b,c})
-
((1\otimes\vartheta_{b,c})\circ\vartheta_{a,b+c})=0.
\]
This is the finite representative of
\(\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}(a,b,c)\).  Its degree shadow is the
bilinear identity for \(B\); the chain equality is additional data.

\textup{(NO5) Jacobi.}
The transported bracket must have zero finite Jacobiator
\[
\operatorname{Jac}_{\Theta,R}(x,y,z)=0
\]
for all homogeneous \(x,y,z\in P_R^\Pi\).

\textup{(NO6) Frobenius.}
The finite Frobenius defect
\[
\mathfrak o_{F,R}(x,y,z)=
\langle[x,y]_{\Theta},z\rangle_R
+(-1)^{|x||y|}\langle y,[x,z]_{\Theta}\rangle_R
\]
must vanish.

\textup{(NO7) Hopf radical.}
Finally, for
\(\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi=\{r\in P_R^\Pi\mid
\langle r,w\rangle_R=0\ \forall w\in P_R^\Pi\}\) (equivalently the
two-sided radical when the finite Hopf pairing is graded symmetric) and
\(\bar q_{\Pi,R}:P_R^\Pi\to
P_R^\Pi/\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi\), one must have both
\[
\langle[x,r]_{\Theta},z\rangle_R=0
\qquad
(x,z\in P_R^\Pi,\ r\in\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi)
\]
and the finite coideal square
\[
\begin{tikzcd}
\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi \arrow[r,"\Delta_R^\Theta"]
\arrow[d,"0"']
& P_R^\Pi\otimes P_R^\Pi
\arrow[d,"\bar q_{\Pi,R}\otimes\bar q_{\Pi,R}"]\\
0 \arrow[r]
& (P_R^\Pi/\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi)
\otimes(P_R^\Pi/\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi).
\end{tikzcd}
\]
These are the finite Lie-ideal and coideal parts of
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rad}}_{\Theta,R}=0\).  Closedness of the inverse
limit radical is the additional HN topological assertion that the kernels
\(\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi\) form a transition-compatible closed subsystem.

Consequently, if \textup{(NO1)--(NO7)} hold for every successor arrow and
the non-successor transition maps are their composites, the inverse limit
kills
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}},\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{Hoch}},\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{tri}},\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{Jac}},\quad
\mathfrak o_F,\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{cyc}},\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad}}.
\]
If one displayed finite diagram fails, its homotopy class is the surviving
obstruction.  Neither non-degeneracy of the pairing nor the scalar
Borcherds determinant removes \textup{(NO3)}, \textup{(NO6)}, or the
coideal part of \textup{(NO7)}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{lemma}[Hopf--Frobenius certificate and obstruction]
\label{lem:F-frobenius-from-hopf-nondegeneracy}
Adopt hypotheses (P) and (O) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}, and grant
the Hopf-pairing/radical hypothesis of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}: the protected Hopf pairing
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle\) on the protected primitive layer
\(\widetilde P_X=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)\) is
non-degenerate after the standard radical quotient.  Non-degeneracy
alone does not imply the graded Frobenius identity.  The missing datum is
the vanishing of the trilinear obstruction
\[
\mathfrak o_F(x,y,z):=
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle,
\qquad
x\in\widetilde P_{X,c_x},\
y\in\widetilde P_{X,c_y},\
z\in\widetilde P_{X,c_z},\quad c_x+c_y+c_z=0,
\]
viewed as a class
\[
\mathfrak o_F\in
C^3_{\mathrm{cyc}}
\bigl(\widetilde P_X;\,k\bigr)
\]
after the reduced \(E\)-quotient and radical quotient.  Hypothesis (F)
of Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} is equivalent to
\(\mathfrak o_F=0\).  It is supplied, for example, by the CY-\(3\)
Serre-functor criterion of Lemma~\ref{lem:F-frobenius-from-cy-serre}.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (Exact defect).}
For homogeneous \(x,y,z\) with \(c_x+c_y+c_z=0\), the displayed cochain
\(\mathfrak o_F(x,y,z)\) is precisely the left side of the
graded-Frobenius identity.  Hence hypothesis (F) is equivalent, by
definition, to \(\mathfrak o_F=0\) after the reduced \(E\)-quotient and
the chosen radical quotient.  No determinant or non-degeneracy statement
alone forces this vanishing.

\emph{Step 2 (What non-degeneracy detects).}
After quotienting by the radical, non-degeneracy identifies a bilinear
operation \(D(x,y)\) with the functional
\(z\mapsto\langle D(x,y),z\rangle\).  Thus if the Frobenius defect is
known to vanish after pairing against every \(z\), non-degeneracy forces
the corresponding operation-level defect to vanish in the quotient.
This is detection, not construction: the cyclic or Serre-functor input
must still supply the equality being detected.

\emph{Step 3 (Radical consequence).}
Let
\[
\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi
=\{r\mid \langle r,w\rangle=0\ \text{for all }w\}.
\]
If \(\mathfrak o_F=0\), then for every \(r\in\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi\)
\[
\langle[x,r],z\rangle
=-(-1)^{|x||r|}\langle r,[x,z]\rangle=0.
\]
Therefore \(\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi\) is a Lie ideal.  The assertion
that it is closed and is also a coideal is the separate Hopf-radical
hypothesis in Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.  Equivalently,
the coproduct must separately satisfy
\[
(\bar q_\Pi\widehat{\otimes}\bar q_\Pi)\Delta_\Theta(r)=0
\qquad(r\in\operatorname{Rad}_X^\Pi),
\]
with \(\bar q_\Pi\) the quotient by the closed radical.  Lemma
\ref{lem:F-frobenius-from-cy-serre} is one conditional source for
\(\mathfrak o_F=0\); it is not a source for coideal stability unless the
cyclic/Serre datum is also proved compatible with the Hopf coproduct.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Finite Hopf-adjointness radical test]
\label{lem:finite-hopf-adjointness-radical-test}
Let \(P_R^\Pi\) be a finite normal-ordered primitive stage with transported
product \(m_R^\Theta\), coproduct \(\Delta_R^\Theta\), and graded
symmetric Hopf pairing \(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_R\).  Let
\[
\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi
=\{r\mid \langle r,w\rangle_R=\langle w,r\rangle_R=0
\ \text{for all }w\in P_R^\Pi\}.
\]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(H1)}] \(m_R^\Theta\) and \(\Delta_R^\Theta\) are adjoint for
the finite Hopf pairing:
\[
\langle m_R^\Theta(x,y),z\rangle_R
=
\langle x\otimes y,\Delta_R^\Theta z\rangle_R
\qquad(x,y,z\in P_R^\Pi),
\]
with the tensor pairing induced from \(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_R\).
\item[\textup{(H2)}] The induced tensor pairing on
\[
(P_R^\Pi/\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi)\otimes
(P_R^\Pi/\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi)
\]
is non-degenerate.
\end{enumerate}
Together with the supplied finite Hopf pairing, coproduct, and radical
matrices, this is the algebraic finite-stage test for \textup{(NO7)}.
Then the finite coideal square in \textup{(NO7)} commutes:
\[
(\bar q_{\Pi,R}\otimes\bar q_{\Pi,R})\Delta_R^\Theta(r)=0
\qquad(r\in\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi).
\]
If, in addition, the finite Frobenius defect \(\mathfrak o_{F,R}\)
vanishes, then \(\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi\) is also a Lie ideal for the
transported bracket.  Thus finite \textup{(NO7)} is killed by
\(\mathfrak o_{F,R}=0\) plus Hopf adjointness and finite quotient
non-degeneracy.  The closed inverse-limit radical still requires the
transition-compatible closedness condition of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For \(r\in\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi\) and \(x,y\in P_R^\Pi\),
Hopf adjointness gives
\[
\bigl\langle x\otimes y,\Delta_R^\Theta(r)\bigr\rangle_R
=\langle m_R^\Theta(x,y),r\rangle_R=0,
\]
because \(r\) lies in the right radical.  Hence the class
\((\bar q_{\Pi,R}\otimes\bar q_{\Pi,R})\Delta_R^\Theta(r)\) pairs to zero
against every elementary tensor in the quotient.  By finite
non-degeneracy of the quotient tensor pairing, the class itself is zero.
This is exactly the coideal square of \textup{(NO7)}.

If \(\mathfrak o_{F,R}=0\), then for \(r\in\operatorname{Rad}_R^\Pi\)
\[
\langle[x,r]_\Theta,z\rangle_R
=-(-1)^{|x||r|}\langle r,[x,z]_\Theta\rangle_R=0
\]
for every \(x,z\), so \([x,r]_\Theta\) lies in the radical.  This is the
finite Lie-ideal half.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Negative-cyclic route to the normal-ordering cochain]
\label{prop:negative-cyclic-normal-ordering-route}
Assume, in addition to hypothesis \textup{(P)} of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}, that the protected Hall sector
has a cyclic model \(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}\) with mixed complex
\((C_*(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}),b,B_{\mathrm C})\), a cyclic class
\(\varpi_X\) representing the PTVV form, and a Connes-contraction
cochain \(\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X\) satisfying
\[
(b+uB_{\mathrm C})(\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X)=B_{\mathrm{ch}}^{-},
\]
where \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}^{-}\) is a negative-cyclic lift whose Hochschild
image is \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}\), and \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}\) maps to the
Gram-defect cocycle \(B\) under the Loday--Quillen--Tsygan comparison
\[
HC^2_{\mathrm{strict}}\longrightarrow HH^2
\]
\cite{LodayQuillen1984}, \cite{Tsygan1983},
\cite[\S2]{LodayCyclicHomology}.  If the induced two-step flag
homotopies have \(\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}=0\), then the cochain
\(\Theta_\Pi^{-}:=\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X\) supplies the
negative-cyclic part of \textup{(Cyc)} and the Hochschild part of
hypothesis \((\Theta)\).  It supplies none of the Frobenius identity, the
finite-HN topology, or the Hopf-radical ideal/coideal condition.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
After forgetting to Hochschild cochains, the displayed equation becomes
\(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_\Pi=B_{\mathrm{ch}}\), whose degree shadow is
\(B\), and the cocycle identity \(\delta B=0\) gives the degree shadow of
the triple pentagon.  The actual Hall flag coherence is still the
vanishing of \(\operatorname{Pent}_{\Theta}\).  This route is a second
construction of the \(\Theta\)-datum once the cyclic model and the
triple homotopies are available.  It is not a consequence of (P) alone.
It does not assert compatibility of fibre products over
\(\overline\Pi_X\) with the HN transitions, and it contains no information
about the completed coproduct on a radical element.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Comparison of the two proofs]
\label{rem:cyclic-vs-orientation-step4}
\([B]=[B_{\mathrm{ch}}]\) under the Loday--Quillen--Tsygan comparison
\(HC^*_{\mathrm{strict}}\to HH^*\) of \cite{LodayQuillen1984},
\cite{Tsygan1983}, \cite[\S2]{LodayCyclicHomology}, with witnessing
cochains \(\Theta\) (PTVV--Joyce) and
\(\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X\) (cyclic homology), whenever the cyclic model
and comparison cochain are supplied.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Status of the descent criterion]
\label{rem:ptvv-joyce-pi-status}
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} is a conditional descent
criterion.  Its inputs are the PTVV host (P), the reduced quotient and
HN completion (E), including finite-fibre compatibility of
\(\overline\Pi_{*}^{\Theta}\) and continuity of \(\widehat{\otimes}\), the
supplied \(S^1\)-equivariant multiplicative orientation cocycle (O), the
degree-shift cochain \(\Theta\), the Frobenius pairing (F), the
negative-cyclic lift (Cyc), and Hopf-radical stability.
Lemma~\ref{lem:explicit-multiplicative-orientation-cocycle}
constructs (O) only on a supplied projection-finite Kunneth-pure sector;
it does not construct the full compact or wrapped reduced
\(K3\times E\) protected sector.  Thus the remaining obligations are
geometric and chain-level: construct (P), (E), and (O) beyond the
Kunneth-pure sector including the HN/higher-rank extension, prove that
the supplied \(\Theta\) identifies the raw Gram defect \(B\) with
canonical degree shifts in the protected primitive bracket, kill
\(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}}\), \(\mathfrak o_F\), and prove
closed Hopf-radical coideal stability.  The
scalar Borcherds determinant and the denominator algebra do not discharge
these obligations.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Graded Frobenius identity from CY-3 Serre functor]
\label{lem:F-frobenius-from-cy-serre}
Suppose that the protected observable algebra
\(\mathcal A_X\) of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}, after the
reduced \(E\)-quotient and the Costello--Li flat trivialization
\cite{CostelloRenormalization,CostelloLiBCOV,CostelloLiOpenClosedBCOV}
along the elliptic factor, is realized
as a Calabi--Yau \(A_\infty\)-category of dimension \(d=3\),
i.e.~it carries a Serre functor \(S\simeq[3]\) and a
non-degenerate cyclically invariant pairing
\[
\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_S
:\Hom_{\mathcal A_X}(X,Y)\otimes
\Hom_{\mathcal A_X}(Y,X[3])\longrightarrow k,
\]
in the sense of Kontsevich--Soibelman \cite{KSCoHA} (cyclic
\(A_\infty\)-structure) and PTVV
\cite{PTVV2013}/BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} (orientation data realising the
shift \([3]\) on the moduli of objects of \(\mathcal A_X\)).  Let
\(\widetilde P_X\subset H_*(\mathcal A_X)\) be the protected primitive
subspace, equipped with the Hall bracket \([\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]\) and
the Hopf pairing \(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle\) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.  Suppose, moreover, that at
every finite HN stage the primitive Hall bracket is represented by the
antisymmetrisation of the finite product \(m_{2,R}\), the cyclic trace
descends through the reduced \(E\)-quotient, and the trace, pairing, and
primitive projection commute with the transition maps.  Then the graded
Frobenius identity holds:
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle=0,
\qquad x,y,z\in\widetilde P_X\ \mathrm{homogeneous},
\]
i.e.~hypothesis (F) of Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} is met.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (Serre pairing and cyclic trace).}
A CY-\(d\) \(A_\infty\)-category \(\mathcal A_X\) is, by
\cite{KSCoHA} (\S~10), an \(A_\infty\)-category equipped with a
quasi-isomorphism \(S\xrightarrow{\sim}[d]\) of bimodules and a
non-degenerate cyclically symmetric pairing
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_S\) on
\(\Hom_{\mathcal A_X}(-,-)\), of total degree \(-d\).  Equivalently,
there is a chain-level cyclic trace
\(\tr_S:\Hom_{\mathcal A_X}(X,X)\to k[-d]\) satisfying
\(\tr_S(f\circ g)=(-1)^{|f|\cdot|g|}\tr_S(g\circ f)\) for composable
homogeneous \(f,g\) (loc.~cit., Lemma~10.2.4).  PTVV
\cite{PTVV2013} produce the underlying \((-d)\)-shifted symplectic
form on \(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\); BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} extend the
orientation/d-critical datum that realises \(S\simeq[d]\) at chain
level on the perfect-complex moduli.  Costello--Li
\cite{CostelloRenormalization,CostelloLiBCOV,CostelloLiOpenClosedBCOV}
flat trivialization along the elliptic
factor reduces \(d=4\) to \(d=3\), so the discussion takes \(d=3\) and the
identification \(\langle x,y\rangle=\tr_S(x\cdot y)\), where
\(\cdot\) is the cup product on the protected primitive subspace.

\emph{Step 2 (Frobenius from cyclic invariance).}
Specialise to homogeneous primitives \(x,y,z\in\widetilde P_X\) and
expand the Hall bracket as the graded commutator
\([x,y]=x\cdot y-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}y\cdot x\) (the bracket on
primitives in a connected graded Hopf algebra is the antisymmetrised
product, as part of the primitive Lie-superalgebra structure assumed in
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}).  Then
\begin{align*}
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
&=\tr_S\bigl((x\cdot y-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}y\cdot x)\cdot z\bigr)\\
&=\tr_S(x\cdot y\cdot z)-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\tr_S(y\cdot x\cdot z).
\end{align*}
Cyclic invariance of \(\tr_S\) applied to the second term gives
\(\tr_S(y\cdot x\cdot z)=(-1)^{|y|\cdot(|x|+|z|)}\tr_S(x\cdot z\cdot y)\),
and applied to the first gives
\(\tr_S(x\cdot y\cdot z)=(-1)^{|x|\cdot(|y|+|z|)}\tr_S(y\cdot z\cdot x)\).
Substituting and re-collecting,
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle=
-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\tr_S\bigl(y\cdot(x\cdot z-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|z|}z\cdot x)\bigr)
=-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle,
\]
which is (F).

\emph{Step 3 (Finite-stage chain-level lift).}
The cyclic trace \(\tr_S\) is a strict invariant on the
\(A_\infty\)-homotopy category by \cite{KSCoHA}, \S~10.2; on
\(d\)-critical thickenings it lifts to perfect-complex chain level by
\cite{BBDJS2015} (the cyclic structure on the vanishing-cycle dg
algebra) and PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} (the shifted symplectic form
descends to the cotangent complex of \(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\)).  By the
finite-stage hypotheses, this cyclic trace, the product, the pairing, and
the primitive projector all descend through the reduced \(E\)-quotient and
commute with HN transitions.  The identity of Step~2 therefore holds at
each finite \(R\) and passes to the completed protected primitive
subspace \(\widetilde P_X\).  A cyclic trace on an auxiliary model would
not prove the Frobenius identity for the Hall bracket unless these
finite-stage compatibilities were supplied.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
Lemma~\ref{lem:F-frobenius-from-cy-serre} derives (F) from the
CY-\(3\) Serre functor of \(\mathcal A_X\), parallel to the derivation
through the squaring isomorphism
\(o_c^{\otimes 2}\simeq\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} and the Hopf pairing of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.  Both derivations meet at
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle=\tr_S(\,\cdot\,\cdot\,\cdot\,)\), the
BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} cyclic upgrade of the PTVV
\cite{PTVV2013} \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form, and produce the same
sign convention \((-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\) on the Gram degree
\(c_x+c_y+c_z=0\).  It proves only \(\mathfrak o_F=0\); it does not
prove \(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}}=0\), coideal stability of the
Hopf radical, a no-extra-relations theorem, or PBW compatibility.  It is
therefore one input to the full Dirac--Igusa realization certificate, not
a substitute for it.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Finite normal-ordering closure criterion]
\label{prop:finite-normal-ordering-closure-criterion}
Fix a successor arrow \(R^+\to R\).  Suppose a finite Hall--Dirac atlas
\(\mathfrak A_R\) and its successor transition are supplied through the
normal-ordering lane, and suppose the following finite data hold.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(N1)}] The coefficient dg categories, central translations,
and degree-truncation transitions satisfy
Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-picard-normal-ordering-lift}.
\item[\textup{(N2)}] The Joyce--Kontsevich--Soibelman pull-push product,
coproduct, and finite Hopf pairing are strictly compatible with the
successor transition after \(\Theta_\Pi\)-transport.
\item[\textup{(N3)}] The \(S^1\)-equivariant lift
\(\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}\) satisfies
\[
(b+uB_{\mathrm C})\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}=B_{\mathrm{ch},R}^{-},
\]
and its Hochschild shadow is
\(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_{\Pi,R}=B_{\mathrm{ch},R}\).
\item[\textup{(N4)}] The two translated products over every finite
two-step Hall flag agree after inserting the Hall associator and
Joyce--Upmeier orientation transport.
\item[\textup{(N5)}] The transported bracket is the graded commutator of
the finite product on \(H^0\), so the Jacobiator is the image of the
associator and the \(\Theta\)-pentagon.
\item[\textup{(N6)}] The finite cyclic trace satisfies the CY-\(3\)
Serre-functor criterion of
Lemma~\ref{lem:F-frobenius-from-cy-serre}; equivalently
\(\mathfrak o_{F,R}=0\).
\item[\textup{(N7)}] The finite Hopf pairing is product-coproduct adjoint,
its quotient tensor pairing is non-degenerate, and the radical kernels
are preserved by the successor transition, as in
Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-hopf-adjointness-radical-test}.
\end{enumerate}
Then the finite normal-ordering diagrams \textup{(NO1)--(NO7)} of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-normal-ordering-verification-diagrams}
commute at the arrow \(R^+\to R\).  Hence the seven finite obstruction
classes
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{top}}_{\Theta,R^+R},\quad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Hoch}}_{\Theta,R},\quad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tri}}_{\Theta,R},\quad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Jac}}_{\Theta,R},\quad
\mathfrak o_{F,R},\quad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{\Theta,R},\quad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rad}}_{\Theta,R}
\]
vanish at that finite stage.  Conversely, the first failed item among
\textup{(N1)--(N7)} is the corresponding obstruction component unless an
independent finite null-homotopy for the same \textup{(NO)} diagram is
supplied.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-picard-normal-ordering-lift}, \textup{(N1)}
kills the finite fibre square \textup{(NO1)} and the Hochschild part of
\textup{(NO3)}.  Hypothesis \textup{(N2)} is exactly the product,
coproduct, and pairing square \textup{(NO2)}.  Hypothesis \textup{(N3)}
kills the negative-cyclic part of \textup{(NO3)}, as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:negative-cyclic-normal-ordering-route}.  Hypothesis
\textup{(N4)} is \textup{(NO4)}.  Under \textup{(N5)}, associativity and
\textup{(NO4)} imply the finite Jacobi identity, so \textup{(NO5)}
vanishes.  Hypothesis \textup{(N6)} is exactly \textup{(NO6)} by
Lemma~\ref{lem:F-frobenius-from-cy-serre}.  Finally,
Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-hopf-adjointness-radical-test} proves the coideal
part of \textup{(NO7)}, while \textup{(NO6)} proves the Lie-ideal part.
Transition preservation of the finite radical kernels is the finite
closedness condition needed before passing to the inverse limit.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Unitarity]
This paper uses the protected index, the virtual determinant, and
the Borcherds denominator algebra.  A holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization
algebra in cochains is part of the open Dirac--Igusa realization
certificate, not a positive Hilbert-space construction already in hand.  Negative
coefficients \(f(nm,l)\) record an odd excess in a protected supertrace
or in a \(K_0\)-representative; actual parity dimensions require an
additional Hilbert-space or denominator-algebra parity datum.  If the
untwisted compactification is unitary, the statement that survives the
twist is right-moving cohomology, protected integration, and the signed
index.  Reflection positivity is not a hypothesis of the Borcherds
denominator theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Cyclotomic-spectrum construction of the multiplicative
orientation cocycle; alternative source for hypothesis (O) of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}}]
\label{lem:cyclotomic-multiplicative-orientation}
Let \(\mathcal F_X\) be the protected observable algebra of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}},
graded by supplied algebraic/effective charge
\(c\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}\subset
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{alg}}\subset\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\), and let
\(\{o_c\}_{c\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}}\) be the orientation lines of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:orientation-line}}.  Suppose:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(C1)}] \emph{(Cyclotomic host.)} Each charged sector
\(\mathcal F_{X,c}\) is realised as a connective cyclotomic spectrum
in the sense of Nikolaus--Scholze \cite{NikolausScholze}; the
\(p\)-typical cyclotomic structure map
\(\varphi_p:\mathcal F_{X,c}\to(\mathcal F_{X,c})^{tC_p}\) is the
Frobenius inherited from the chiral product on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\).  Equivalently, the underlying spectrum
\(HH(\mathcal F_{X,c})\) carries the natural \(S^1\)-action by the
Connes operator \(B\) of Goodwillie \cite{Goodwillie1985}, with
genuine \(S^1\)-fixed points
\(HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c}):=HH(\mathcal F_{X,c})^{hS^1}\).
\item[\textup{(C2)}] \emph{(Determinant track.)} The orientation line
\(o_c\) lifts to a unit
\(\widehat o_c\in\pi_0HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c})\) representing the
graded determinant
\(\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)^{1/2}\) of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:orientation-line}} in the \(S^1\)-equivariant
periodic Picard groupoid, in the sense of
Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier}.
\item[\textup{(C3)}] \emph{(Strict tensor compatibility.)} The
external product on \(\{\mathcal F_{X,c}\}\) is symmetric monoidal as
a map of cyclotomic spectra,
\(\mathcal F_{X,c}\boxtimes\mathcal F_{X,c'}\to\mathcal F_{X,c+c'}\),
intertwining \(\varphi_p\) on each side.
\end{enumerate}
Then there exists a multiplicative orientation cocycle
\[
\mu_{c,c'}\,:\;o_{c+c'}\;\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\;o_c\otimes o_{c'},
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
with the following properties:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] (Strict pentagon.)
\(\mu_{c+c',c''}\circ\mu_{c,c'}=\mu_{c,c'+c''}\circ\mu_{c',c''}\) as
maps of \(HC^-\)-modules, with no higher coherence remainder.
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (\(S^1\)-equivariance.) Each \(\mu_{c,c'}\) is
an \(S^1\)-equivariant map of cyclotomic spectra; the Connes operator
\(B\) intertwines source and target.
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (PTVV compatibility.) The Tate construction
\((-)^{tC_p}\) carries \(\mu_{c,c'}\) to a comparison of Frobenius
twists \(\mathcal F_{X,c}^{(p)}\otimes\mathcal F_{X,c'}^{(p)}\to
\mathcal F_{X,c+c'}^{(p)}\) compatible with the PTVV \cite{PTVV2013}
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form on \(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\), in the
sense that \(\mu_{c,c'}\) restricts on the underlying graded
determinants to the symplectic-Lagrangian comparison map of
\cite{JoyceUpmeier}.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, hypothesis (O) of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}} is satisfied, and the
construction of \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) is independent of the Costello--Li
flat Calabi--Yau pairing and of any K\"unneth decomposition of
\(\mathcal F_X\) along \(K3\times E\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (Construction of \(\mu_{c,c'}\) in \(HC^-\)).}  Apply the
\(S^1\)-fixed-points functor \((-)^{hS^1}\) to the symmetric monoidal
external product of (C3): the resulting map
\[
HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c})\otimes HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c'})
\;\longrightarrow\;
HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c+c'})
\]
is a strict map of \(\mathbb E_\infty\)-algebras in cyclotomic spectra
by Nikolaus--Scholze \cite[Cor.~II.1.7, Thm.~II.6.9]{NikolausScholze},
since \((-)^{hS^1}\) is lax symmetric monoidal and the cyclotomic
Frobenius \(\varphi_p\) is itself symmetric monoidal.  Take
\(\widehat o_c\) and \(\widehat o_{c'}\) as in (C2); their product
under this map lifts the right-hand side of the desired isomorphism
\(o_c\otimes o_{c'}\), and divides the lift \(\widehat o_{c+c'}\) of
\(o_{c+c'}\) to define
\(\mu_{c,c'}:=\widehat o_{c+c'}\cdot
(\widehat o_c\boxtimes\widehat o_{c'})^{-1}\).  The Connes operator
\(B\) acts trivially on units of \(\pi_0\), so \(\mu_{c,c'}\) is
\(S^1\)-equivariant on the nose.

\emph{Step 2 (Strict pentagon from \(\mathbb E_\infty\)-associativity).}
The pentagon
\(\mu_{c+c',c''}\circ\mu_{c,c'}=\mu_{c,c'+c''}\circ\mu_{c',c''}\) is
the \(\pi_0\)-shadow of the strict associator of the
\(\mathbb E_\infty\)-algebra structure on \(\bigoplus_c HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c})\)
in cyclotomic spectra.  Strictness follows because Nikolaus--Scholze
\cite[Thm.~I.1.13]{NikolausScholze} present the cyclotomic
\(\infty\)-category as a strict \(\mathbb E_\infty\)-monoidal limit
along the Frobenius diagram; the homotopy-coherent pentagon
collapses to an on-the-nose identity at the level of
\(\pi_0\)-units.  No higher coherence datum is required, because
\(\pi_0HC^-\) is a discrete commutative monoid and units satisfy strict
associativity in any commutative monoid.

\emph{Step 3 (\(S^1\)-equivariance built in).}  By construction
\(HC^-=HH^{hS^1}\) is the genuine \(S^1\)-fixed-points spectrum, so
every map produced by Step~1 is \(S^1\)-equivariant.  The Connes
operator \(B\) is the generator of the \(S^1\)-action on \(HH\)
\cite{Goodwillie1985}, and \(B\) acts as a derivation on \(HC^-\);
it kills \(\pi_0\)-units, hence kills \(\mu_{c,c'}\) as a higher
homotopy.

\emph{Step 4 (Tate-construction comparison with PTVV).}  Apply
\((-)^{tC_p}\) to the equation defining \(\mu_{c,c'}\).  The
Frobenius \(\varphi_p\) intertwines source and target by (C1) and (C3),
so \(\mu_{c,c'}^{tC_p}\) is the comparison of Frobenius twists
\(\mathcal F_{X,c}^{(p)}\otimes\mathcal F_{X,c'}^{(p)}\to
\mathcal F_{X,c+c'}^{(p)}\).  Restrict to the underlying graded
determinants: the symplectic structure on
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\) of PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} is the
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form whose square root is \(o_c\)
\textup{(Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line})}; under
\((-)^{tC_p}\) this form is sent to the Tate-Frobenius pairing on
\(\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)^{(p)}\), which by
Joyce--Upmeier \cite[multiplicative orientation
construction]{JoyceUpmeier} agrees with the
symplectic-Lagrangian comparison map.  Compatibility (iii) follows.

The data \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) is a multiplicative
orientation cocycle satisfying (i)--(iii), so hypothesis (O) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} holds.  The construction
factors through the cyclotomic-spectrum machinery of Nikolaus--Scholze
\cite{NikolausScholze} and the Connes-\(B\) calculus of
Goodwillie \cite{Goodwillie1985}; it does not invoke Costello--Li
chiral pairings, K\"unneth decompositions of \(\mathcal F_X\) along
\(K3\times E\), or any compactness datum beyond (C1)--(C3).  \qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
Hypotheses (C1), (C2), (C3) are open for \(K3\times E\): (C1) asks
\(\mathcal F_{X,c}\) to carry a cyclotomic structure in the
Nikolaus--Scholze sense \cite{NikolausScholze}; (C2) asks orientation
lines to lift to \(\pi_0HC^-\) units, refining
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}; (C3) asks symmetric monoidality
of \(\{\mathcal F_{X,c}\}\) at the cyclotomic level.  The cocycle
\(\mu_{c,c'}\) is built from the Hochschild--cyclic machinery of
\(\mathcal F_X\) alone, supplying an alternative construction of
hypothesis (O) disjoint from the Costello--Li flat Calabi--Yau pairing
and from any K\"unneth decomposition.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Sectorial Hall truncation]
\label{def:sectorial-hall-truncation}
Suppose an extension-closed compact Hall category graded by the additive
formal lattice \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice}, with actual
charges in a supplied algebraic/effective support semigroup, together with
the Gram map \(\Pi_X\), a stability/HN/support datum
\(\sigma=(Z_\sigma,\mathcal P_\sigma)\), and semistable stacks
\(\mathfrak M_{\sigma,S,c}^{ss}\) for
\(c\in\Gamma_{X,\sigma}^{\mathrm{eff}}\subset
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{alg}}\subset\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\).
Fix a strict
sector \(S\subset\C^\times\) of angular width \(<\pi\), with no active
semistable ray on its boundary.  Choose \(\vartheta\) so that
$$
h_S(c):=\Re(e^{-i\vartheta}Z_\sigma(c))>0
$$
on every nonzero semistable class with central charge in \(S\).
For \(R>0\), set
$$
F_{\sigma,S}(R)
=\{c\mid \mathfrak M_{\sigma,S,c}^{ss}\ne\varnothing,\
0<h_S(c)\le R\},
$$
and
$$
\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)
=\left\{c_1+\cdots+c_k\ \middle|\
c_i\in F_{\sigma,S}(R),\
\sum_i h_S(c_i)\le R\right\}.
$$
If an oriented critical Hall object
\(\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}\) has been constructed, put
$$
\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{>R}
=\prod_{h_S(c)>R}\mathcal H_{\sigma,S,c}^{or},
\qquad
\mathsf F_R\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}
=\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}/\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{>R}.
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Conditional finite charge-support Hall quotient]
\label{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}
A nonzero additive heart cannot have finite nonzero charge support in
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\).  The pushed-forward active support
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\subset\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) is not additive.
The finite charge-support Hall object is therefore not a finite
active-support heart.

Assume the support property, the
HN property, finite type of the
semistable stacks in bounded \(h_S\)-height, and the oriented critical
Hall correspondences.  Then \(F_{\sigma,S}(R)\) and
\(\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)\) are finite,
\(\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{>R}\) is a two-sided Hall ideal, and
\(\mathsf F_R\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}\) is a finite charge-support
Hall quotient.
The compact sectorial Hall object is the completed inverse system
$$
\widehat{\mathcal H}_{\sigma,S}^{or}
=\varprojlim_R\mathsf F_R\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}.
$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If a heart contains an object of nonzero charge \(c\), it contains
all finite direct sums of that object, hence all charges \(kc\).
Since \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\) is torsion-free, the charge support is
infinite.  Also \((0,-1,0)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\), while
\((0,-2,0)\notin\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\), so active support is not
additive.

For semistable classes in \(S\), the strict-sector condition gives
\(h_S(c)\ge \kappa|Z_\sigma(c)|\) for some \(\kappa>0\).  The support
property and discreteness of the numerical lattice make
\(F_{\sigma,S}(R)\) finite.  The function \(h_S\) is positive and
additive on extensions in the sector; hence HN sums of total height
\(\le R\) form a finite set and the subspace of height \(>R\) is a
two-sided Hall ideal.  The inverse limit is the \(h_S\)-adic Hall
completion.  This supplies the charge-index finiteness part of the
finite Hall package; the full certificate also includes finite-type
d-critical substacks, finite-dimensional protected cohomology, and
proper/admissible pull-push geometry.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[First-order Dirac--Igusa \(D_0\)-certificate]
\label{def:first-order-d0-certificate}
Fix a stability/HN sector \((\sigma,S)\) as in
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:sectorial-hall-truncation}}.  The certificate
operates under two explicit standing hypotheses:
\begin{itemize}
\item[\textup{[K3$\times$E-fin]}] \emph{Finite-type semistable substacks
at bounded HN height.}  For every \(R>0\), the substack of
\(\sigma\)-semistable objects in \(\mathsf{D}^b(\mathrm{Coh}(K3\times E))\)
of HN height \(\le R\) and active charge in
\(F_{\sigma,S}(R)\) is of finite type over \(\mathbb C\).
K3-surface finite-wall and HN technology motivates this hypothesis; the
\(K3\times E\) threefold case is not in the cited literature and is taken
as part of the supplied datum.
\item[\textup{[ML]}] \emph{Mittag--Leffler descent for the HN inverse
system.}  The transition maps \(\rho_{R'R}\) of clauses (D0-F)--(D0-S) below
satisfy \(\lim^1=0\) on every finite \(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\)-supported
piece.  Equivalently, the inverse system is uniformly surjective on each
finite charge slice; the completed Dirac--Igusa state is then a Lie object
in the strict sense rather than only a pro-Lie object.
\end{itemize}
The recognition theorem of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}} reads as
a strict isomorphism only after both hypotheses are granted.  If [ML] fails,
the recognition statement weakens to a pro-comparison.

Write
\(\Gamma_R^{HN}:=\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)\).  For
\(c\in\Gamma_R^{HN}\), put
\[
\mathcal T_R(c)=
\left\{
\sum_{1\le i<j\le k}B(c_i,c_j)\ \middle|\
c=c_1+\cdots+c_k,\ c_i\in F_{\sigma,S}(R),\
\sum_i h_S(c_i)\le R
\right\}.
\]
The empty decomposition is allowed for \(c=0\), giving \(T=0\).
The finite normal-ordered support at height \(R\) is
\[
\widehat\Gamma_R=
\{(c,T)\mid c\in\Gamma_R^{HN},\ T\in\mathcal T_R(c)\}
\subset\widehat\Gamma_X,
\qquad
\Gamma_R^\Pi:=\overline\Pi_X(\widehat\Gamma_R)
\subset\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}.
\]
The label \(T\) is not an extra brane charge and not a new moduli
factor.  It is finite normal-ordering coefficient data attached to an HN
word, equivalently a central-translation label for the coefficient
system.  The same underlying total charge \(c\) may appear with several
such labels before a no-overcount theorem is supplied.  Thus
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\) is finite coefficient-system data; functorial
descent of these labels through the finite Hall correspondences is part
of the \(D_0\)-certificate.
The coefficient label must also be lossless.  For a label \((c,T)\), let
\(\mathcal W_R(c,T)\) be the finite set of HN words whose normal-ordering
label is \((c,T)\), let \(\mathcal H^{or}_{R,w}\) denote the iterated
extension-correspondence object attached to \(w\), and let
\(\mathcal H^{or}_{R,(c,T)}\) be the summand labelled by \((c,T)\) when
the finite source kernel is supplied.  The no-overcount residual
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{no}}_{R,c,T}:=
\operatorname{Cone}\!\left(
\bigoplus_{w\in\mathcal W_R(c,T)}\mathcal H^{or}_{R,w}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal H^{or}_{R,(c,T)}
\right)
\]
is an object of the finite derived category of source coefficient
complexes.  Its acyclicity records that the normal-ordering labels
neither duplicate nor lose source summands.  It is finite-stage source
data, not a consequence of the lattice identity for \(\overline\Pi_X\).

For nonzero \(\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), set the finite
target exponent
\[
a_\Delta(\gamma)=
\begin{cases}
f(nm,l),&\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}},\\
0,&\gamma\notin\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}.
\end{cases}
\]
Fix also a proper height
\[
h_\Delta:\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\longrightarrow\Z_{\ge0},
\qquad
h_\Delta(n,l,m)=|n|+|l|+|m|
  \]
on the Gram-index lattice.  The \(D_0\) bookkeeping also fixes a
nondecreasing cofinal target-window schedule
\[
N_R^\Delta\in\Z_{\ge0},\qquad
R'\ge R\Rightarrow N_{R'}^\Delta\ge N_R^\Delta,\qquad
\sup_R N_R^\Delta=\infty .
\]
This schedule is finite-window bookkeeping, not a relation between HN
height and automorphic height.  To make each transition-obstruction
stage a finite datum, fix a cofinal discrete subsystem
\[
\mathcal R=\{R_0<R_1<R_2<\cdots\}\subset\mathbb R_{>0},
\qquad R_\nu\to\infty,
\]
and take all inverse limits below over \(\mathcal R\).  Cofinality does
not change the completed HN object or the target exhaustion; the
finite-type substack and proper-correspondence assertions are the
separate geometric entries of the same certificate.  For
\(R=R_\nu\) write \(R^+=R_{\nu+1}\).  Transition maps for non-successor
arrows are composites of the successor maps.  Thus the independent
transition obstruction at a stage is a finite obstruction, not an
infinite product of defects over all larger heights.  In what follows,
\(R\) denotes an element of this cofinal subsystem.

Define the finite target and test windows
\[
\Gamma_{\Delta,R}
:=\{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\setminus\{0\}\mid
h_\Delta(\gamma)\le N_R^\Delta\},
\qquad
\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}
:=(\Gamma_R^\Pi\setminus\{0\})\cup\Gamma_{\Delta,R}.
\]
\[
\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}:=\Gamma_R^\Pi\cap\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}
:=(\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\setminus\{0\})\cup\Gamma_{\Delta,R}.
\]
The superscript \(+\) denotes the cusp-positive Pfaffian half; the full
Borcherds--Kac--Moody double also has the opposite root spaces and is
tested separately in the primitive-recognition theorem.
Write
\[
A_R:=\{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\mid a_\Delta(\gamma)\ne0\},
\qquad
Z_R:=\{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\mid a_\Delta(\gamma)=0\}.
\]
The inclusion \(A_R\subset\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\) is not built into the target
schedule; it is a finite source-coverage residual tested below.
The set \(\widehat\Gamma_R\), and hence
\(\Gamma_R^\Pi\), \(\Gamma_{\Delta,R}\), and
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\), is finite by
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation} and properness of
\(h_\Delta\).  Cofinality of \(N_R^\Delta\) makes the target windows
exhaust \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\setminus\{0\}\).  For \(R'\ge R\) the
inclusions
\[
\widehat\Gamma_R\subset\widehat\Gamma_{R'},\qquad
\Gamma_R^\Pi\subset\Gamma_{R'}^\Pi,\qquad
\Gamma_{\Delta,R}\subset\Gamma_{\Delta,R'}
\]
hold.  A first-order Dirac--Igusa \(D_0\)-certificate for
\(X=K3\times E\) is the choice of the schedule \(N_R^\Delta\) above,
together with a compatible inverse system of finite-stage
state/observable packages
\[
D_{0,R}=
\bigl(\mathcal H^{or}_{R},\mathcal F_{R}^{D_0},K_R^\Pi,
P_R^\Pi,m_R,\Delta_R,[\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_R,I_R^{\mathrm{prot}},
\Theta_{\Pi,R},\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-},\mathfrak D_{X,R},
\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},R},\operatorname{pf}_{X,R},\iota_R^{obs}\bigr),
\qquad R\in\mathcal R,
\]
together with successor transition maps whose composites give every
non-successor arrow.  If the transition residuals below vanish and the
composite transition identities hold, the inverse limit is denoted
\[
D_0(X;\sigma,S)=
\bigl(\widehat{\mathcal H}^{or}_{\sigma,S},
\mathcal F_X^{D_0},K_X^\Pi,P_X^\Pi,\mathfrak D_X,
\Theta_\Pi,\Theta_\Pi^{-},\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},X},
\operatorname{pf}_X,\iota_X^{obs}\bigr).
\]
The clauses are the following.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(D0-F)}] \emph{Finite-stage maps and transitions.}
At height \(R\), all state, observable, primitive, Pfaffian, and
comparison data are defined on the finite support
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\) and its Gram image \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\).  The stage
carries Hall product, coproduct, primitive bracket, and protected
integration maps
\[
m_R,\qquad \Delta_R,\qquad [\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_R,\qquad
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}},
\]
and a charge-preserving observable comparison
\[
\iota_R^{obs}:\mathcal F_R^{D_0}\longrightarrow
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
\]
For the successor arrow \(R^+\to R\) there are transition maps
\[
\rho^H_{R^+R}:\mathcal H^{or}_{R^+}\to\mathcal H^{or}_{R},\qquad
\rho^F_{R^+R}:\mathcal F_{R^+}^{D_0}\to\mathcal F_R^{D_0},\qquad
\rho^K_{R^+R}:K_{R^+}^\Pi\to K_R^\Pi,\qquad
\rho^P_{R^+R}:P_{R^+}^\Pi\to P_R^\Pi,
\]
and compatible maps \(\rho^{\mathrm{Pf}}_{R^+R}\) on Pfaffian lines.  These
maps are degree-truncation maps: after projection to
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\), \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\), and
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\), all summands of HN height \(>R\) are zero.
For a non-successor \(R'\ge R\), the map \(\rho_{R'R}\) is the composite
of the successor maps.  Let
\(\pi^{\Delta}_{R^+R}\) denote the finite target truncation on
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) and on
\(\C[\Gamma_{\Delta,R^+}]\to\C[\Gamma_{\Delta,R}]\).  The transition residual
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{R^+R}
\]
is the finite tuple of defect maps, in the corresponding finite Hom
spaces over \(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\), asserting compatibility of
\(\rho_{R^+R}\) with
\[
m,\quad \Delta,\quad [\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,],\quad I^{\mathrm{prot}},
\quad \Theta_\Pi,\quad \Theta_\Pi^{-},\quad \mathfrak D,\quad \iota^{obs},
\quad \operatorname{pf}.
\]
For example it includes the defects
\[
\rho^F_{R^+R}m_{R^+}-m_R(\rho^F_{R^+R}\otimes\rho^F_{R^+R}),\qquad
\rho^P_{R^+R}[\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_{R^+}
-[\,\rho^P_{R^+R}(\cdot),\rho^P_{R^+R}(\cdot)\,]_R,
\]
\[
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}\rho^F_{R^+R}
-\pi^\Delta_{R^+R}I_{R^+}^{\mathrm{prot}},\qquad
\iota_R^{obs}\rho^F_{R^+R}
-\pi^\Delta_{R^+R}\iota_{R^+}^{obs},\qquad
\rho^K_{R^+R}\mathfrak D_{X,R^+}
-\mathfrak D_{X,R}\rho^K_{R^+R},\qquad
\rho^{\mathrm{Pf}}_{R^+R}(\operatorname{pf}_{X,R^+})
-\operatorname{pf}_{X,R}.
\]
The certificate requires
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{R^+R}=0\) for every successor arrow.  The
zero means a chosen finite equality or null-homotopy in the indicated Hom
complex.  Non-successor compatibility is then the corresponding composite
equality; if non-successor maps are recorded separately, the evident
cocycle identity for \(R''\ge R'\ge R\) is also part of the finite
transition datum.  These equalities are finite-stage data, not formal
consequences of the inverse-limit notation.

\item[\textup{(D0-S)}] \emph{State object; conditional datum, open
construction.}
A certificate supplies an oriented critical Hall/factorization inverse
system whose completed state side is
\[
\widehat{\mathcal H}^{or}_{\sigma,S}
=\varprojlim_R\mathsf F_R\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}
\]
formed first on the finite HN quotients of
Definition~\ref{def:sectorial-hall-truncation}.  Each finite quotient
carries finite-type semistable substacks, extension correspondences,
vanishing-cycle coefficients, orientation lines, Hall product and
coproduct maps, and protected integration.  All products, coproducts,
brackets, pairings, and comparison maps are defined on the finite
quotients and are continuous for the inverse limit.  This clause is a
conditional datum; Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}
proves only the finite-first formal shape once the Hall object and the
HN/support hypotheses are supplied.

\item[\textup{(D0-Q)}] \emph{Reduced quotient and orientation obstruction
classes; conditional trivializations.}
Let \(\mathsf{St}_R\) be the finite stable-stratum index set in the
chosen finite-type atlas at height \(R\).  For every
\(\mathcal C\in\mathsf{St}_R\), with stable stratum
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{st}}_{R,\mathcal C}\subset\mathcal H_R^{or}\), the
certificate includes the computed obstruction
tuple
\[
\mathfrak o^{or}_{R,\mathcal C}=
\left(
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{R,\mathcal C},\
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{R,\mathcal C},\
\{(\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{R,\mathcal C},
\lambda^{E,N}_{R,\mathcal C})\}_{N\in\mathcal N_R(\mathcal C)}
\right),
\]
where
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{R,\mathcal C}
\in H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{R,\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2),
\qquad
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{R,\mathcal C}
\in H^2(BE;\mathbb F_2),
\]
and
\[
\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{R,\mathcal C}
\in H^2_{E[N]}(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{st}}_{R,\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\]
is present for each finite stabilizer \(E[N]\) appearing at height \(R\).
Its point-stabilizer restriction is a class
\(\beta^{E,N}_{R,\mathcal C}\in H^2(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)\) only after the
mixed Borel terms, stabilizer action on stratum cohomology, and
spectral-sequence differentials have vanished.  After
\(\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{R,\mathcal C}\) has been null-trivialized, the
certificate also records the finite linearization character
\[
\lambda^{E,N}_{R,\mathcal C}\in H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)
\]
and requires the zero character.  The certificate supplies
null-trivializations of all degree-two classes and zero finite
degree-one characters, compatible with the transition maps.  These are
exactly the ordinary reduced gerbe, connected \(BE\)-linearization,
finite-stabilizer gerbe, and finite-stabilizer \(H^1\)-character
obstructions of Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.  Their
vanishing gives the reduced quotient and orientation line needed for the
\(D_0\) Pfaffian.  Equivalently, (D0-Q) supplies the finite-stage
quotient-orientation character system of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-stage-quotient-orientation-character-system}
for the local, wrapped, mixed, and flag strata at height \(R\).  It does
not compute the Weyl monodromy character; that is the separate content of
(O1)\(^+\) and (O2) in
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}.

\item[\textup{(D0-C)}] \emph{Charge completion; proved lattice input.}
The finite quotients are graded by the normal-ordered charge extension
\[
\widehat\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
(c,T)\star(c',T')=(c+c',T+T'+B(c,c')),
\]
and the observable Gram degree is
\[
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T.
\]
A semistable one-particle generator of charge \(c\) is placed in
\((c,0)\); composite HN words are labelled by the corresponding
\((c,T)\in\widehat\Gamma_R\).  Thus \(T=0\) is not asserted for every
normal-ordered composite.
The bracket of homogeneous states satisfies
\[
[\widetilde P_{X,(c,T)},\widetilde P_{X,(c',T')}]
\subset
\widetilde P_{X,(c,T)\star(c',T')}.
\]
At height \(R\) this statement is read inside \(\widehat\Gamma_R\), with
targets of height \(>R\) killed by the quotient.  The finite-support
assertion follows from Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}; the
additivity of \(\overline\Pi_X\) follows from
Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}; no chain-level Hall
strictification is claimed by this lattice statement.

\item[\textup{(D0-O)}] \emph{State/observable interface; imported target,
conditional source.}
A certificate supplies, at finite height \(R\), source observable shadows
\(\mathcal F_R^{D_0}\).  Their compatible inverse limit
\(\mathcal F_X^{D_0}\) is obtained from
\(\widehat{\mathcal H}^{or}_{\sigma,S}\) by the supplied
\(K3\)-to-\(E\) specialization and, in positive elliptic degree, by a
hybrid wrapped repair.  It is a source object.  The target observable
algebra is the target current envelope
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:formal-current-envelope}.  The interface is a
charge-preserving comparison morphism
\[
\iota_X^{obs}:\mathcal F_X^{D_0}\longrightarrow
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}
\]
whose constant-current primitive restriction is
\[
\iota_X^{\Prim}:
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}
(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X^{D_0})
\longrightarrow
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}.
\]
The target side is imported from Gritsenko--Nikulin; the source and the
comparison morphism are conditional data.  The finite observable residual
\[
\mathfrak o^{obs}_R
\]
is the finite tuple of defects measuring whether \(\iota_R^{obs}\) is a
morphism for the finite product, coproduct, primitive bracket, protected
trace, and constant-current primitive comparison after projection to
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\).  Here
\(m_{\Delta_5},\Delta_{\Delta_5},[\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_{\Delta_5}\), and
\(\operatorname{tr}_{\Delta_5}\) denote the corresponding finite target
operations induced from \(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\).  Thus
\(\mathfrak o^{obs}_R\) includes
\[
\iota_R^{obs}m_R-m_{\Delta_5}(\iota_R^{obs}\otimes\iota_R^{obs}),
\qquad
\Delta_{\Delta_5}\iota_R^{obs}-(\iota_R^{obs}\otimes\iota_R^{obs})\Delta_R,
\]
\[
\iota_R^{\Prim}([x,y]_R)-[\iota_R^{\Prim}x,\iota_R^{\Prim}y]_{\Delta_5},
\qquad
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}-\operatorname{tr}_{\Delta_5}\iota_R^{obs}.
\]
The certificate requires \(\mathfrak o^{obs}_R=0\).  This is a finite
comparison with the imported observable target.  It is not the
presentation-level primitive isomorphism, injectivity, surjectivity, or
no-extra-relations theorem; those belong to the full recognition
certificate.  No target truncation, target bar--cobar counit, or
homotopy inverse to \(\iota_R^{obs}\) is allowed to define
\(\mathcal F_R^{D_0}\).  The source object is supplied first, and the
arrow points source-to-target.

\item[\textup{(D0-N)}] \emph{Exact normal-ordered descent; conditional
finite-topology, Hochschild, triple, Jacobi, Frobenius, cyclic, and radical
trivializations.}
At finite height \(R\), the datum \(\Theta_{\Pi,R}\) is the central
translation cochain
\[
\Theta_{\Pi,R}(c)=\mathsf T_{-\Pi_X(c)}
\]
in the coefficient dg category of
Definition~\ref{def:normal-ordering-coefficient-dg-category}, and
\(\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}\) is its negative-cyclic lift.  For
\((c,T),(c',T')\in\widehat\Gamma_R\), it gives coherent degree-shift
quasi-isomorphisms
\[
\Theta_{(c,T),(c',T')}:
\Pi_X(c+c')-T-T'-B(c,c')
\longrightarrow
\bigl(\Pi_X(c)-T\bigr)+\bigl(\Pi_X(c')-T'\bigr)
\]
on primitive bracket targets.  Equivalently,
\(\Theta_\Pi\) categorifies the equality
\[
\overline\Pi_X((c,T)\star(c',T'))
=\overline\Pi_X(c,T)+\overline\Pi_X(c',T')
\]
and turns the upstairs physical Hall bracket into a
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded bracket after
\(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\).  This is exactly the conditional input of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}; constructing
\(\Theta_\Pi\) on the reduced compact/wrapped sector is open.
The finite coefficient pieces are
\[
(\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta}V_R)_\gamma
=
\prod_{\substack{(c,T)\in\widehat\Gamma_R\\
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\gamma}}(V_R)_{(c,T)},
\]
and this product is finite.  For the successor arrow \(R^+\to R\), the
transition maps must
commute with these finite fibre products, with \(m_R^\Theta\), with
\(\Delta_R^\Theta\), and with the finite pairing.  The corresponding
transition defect is
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{top}}_{\Theta,R^+R}
=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{fib}}_{\Theta,R^+R},
\mathfrak o^{m}_{\Theta,R^+R},
\mathfrak o^{\Delta}_{\Theta,R^+R},
\mathfrak o^{\langle\, ,\,\rangle}_{\Theta,R^+R}
\right),
\]
with the components defined in
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}.  Its vanishing is the finite
statement that the completed fibre products and
\(\widehat{\otimes}\)-operations exist as inverse limits.
Equivalently, with
\[
B_{\mathrm{ch},R}(c,c'):=\mathsf T_{B(c,c')},
\]
the certificate supplies trivializations
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta_{\Pi,R}=B_{\mathrm{ch},R},
\qquad
(b+uB_{\mathrm C})\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}=B_{\mathrm{ch},R}^{-},
\]
and the triple and Jacobi coherences of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}.  Thus the finite-stage
obstruction classes
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{top}}_{\Theta,R^+R},\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Hoch}}_{\Theta,R},\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tri}}_{\Theta,R},\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Jac}}_{\Theta,R},\qquad
\mathfrak o_{F,R},\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{\Theta,R},\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rad}}_{\Theta,R}
\]
vanish in the finite-topology, Hochschild, triple-coherence,
Chevalley--Eilenberg, cyclic-Frobenius, negative-cyclic, and Hopf-radical
ideal/coideal groups displayed there.  The radical class is read as the
ordered pair
\((\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rad,Lie}}_{\Theta,R},
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rad,coid}}_{\Theta,R})\).  Equivalently, every
successor arrow must satisfy the finite tests
\textup{(NO1)--(NO7)} of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-normal-ordering-verification-diagrams}.
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-normal-ordering-closure-criterion} records
the finite closure proved by the preceding finite tests: the
Picard/Hochschild and finite-fibre parts are formal after the coefficient
dg category and degree-truncation topology are supplied, while the cyclic
lift, two-step flag coherence, Frobenius trace, and Hopf-adjoint radical
tests remain source-side data.

\item[\textup{(D0-D)}] \emph{First-order object; conditional.}
There are perfect finite-stage \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\)-graded supercomplexes
\(K_R^\Pi\), compatible under \(\rho^K_{R^+R}\), with finite-dimensional
parity pieces.  At each finite stage there is a \(\Z/2\)-odd skew-adjoint
first-order operator/algebra
\[
\mathfrak D_{X,R}:K_R^\Pi\longrightarrow K_R^\Pi
\]
whose primitive symbol is the finite normal-ordered Hall bracket on
\(P_R^\Pi\).  The successor transition compatibility
\[
\rho^K_{R^+R}\mathfrak D_{X,R^+}
