=\mathfrak D_{X,R}\rho^K_{R^+R}
\]
is one component of \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{R^+R}=0\).  The inverse
limits are
\[
K_X^\Pi=\varprojlim_R K_R^\Pi,\qquad
\mathfrak D_X=\varprojlim_R\mathfrak D_{X,R}.
\]
Their protected primitive cohomology is
\[
P_X^\Pi
=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}
(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X^{D_0}),
\]
and the primitive symbol of \(\mathfrak D_X\) is the normal-ordered Hall
bracket.  The term
``first-order'' means the Pfaffian/primitive object before scalar
squaring; it does not assert an analytic Dirac operator on an already
constructed Hilbert space.

\item[\textup{(D0-Pf)}] \emph{Pfaffian line, finite support, and
normalization; conditional datum, imported automorphic target.}
For every \(R\) there is a Pfaffian line
\(\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},R}\) attached to \(\mathfrak D_{X,R}\) and to the
finite reduced orientation line of the stage, with a finite squaring
isomorphism
\[
\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},R}^{\otimes2}\simeq
\mathscr L_{\det,R}.
\]
The successor maps \(\rho^{\mathrm{Pf}}_{R^+R}\) commute with these square
isomorphisms, as part of
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{R^+R}=0\), and identify the inverse limit
with a Pfaffian line
\[
\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},X},\qquad
\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},X}^{\otimes2}\simeq
\mathscr L_{\det,X},
\]
attached to \(\mathfrak D_X\) and the orientation line on the
state object, together with a normalized section
\(\operatorname{pf}_{X,R}\) at height \(R\) and
\(\operatorname{pf}_X=\varprojlim_R\operatorname{pf}_{X,R}\).  Let
\(x^\gamma=q^nr^ls^m\) for \(\gamma=(n,l,m)\).  Projected to the finite
monomial span of \(\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\), the Borcherds-cusp
product formula below is not a construction of the compact source.  It is
the finite determinant calculation after the primitive spaces, the
first-order block decomposition, and the Pfaffian line have been
supplied.  For \(\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\) write
\(P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}:=P^\Pi_{R,\gamma}\), and for
\(\gamma\notin\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\) set \(P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}=0\).  For a
homogeneous primitive mode in cusp-positive degree
\(\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\), the elementary two-term Pfaffian/Koszul
block is the skew block
\[
J_{\gamma}=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1-x^\gamma\\
-(1-x^\gamma)&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
acting on
\(P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}\oplus(P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma})^\vee[1]\); its Pfaffian
contribution, with the supplied Pfaffian orientation convention, is
\((1-x^\gamma)^{\sdim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}}\).  Equivalently, an even
basis vector contributes \((1-x^\gamma)\), an odd basis vector contributes
\((1-x^\gamma)^{-1}\), and the exponent is
\(\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar0}
-\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar1}\).  Thus the
expansion is
\[
\operatorname{pf}_{X,R}|_{\mathfrak c_\infty}
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{\substack{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\\ \gamma\ne0}}
(1-x^\gamma)^{\sdim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}}.
\]
The Pfaffian half is not the full BKM double: it records the
cusp-positive product factors.  Negative root representatives and the
Cartan/imaginary completion enter the Lie recognition statement after the
primitive bracket and pairing are supplied.  Write
\[
p^{\bar0}_{R,\gamma}:=\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar0},\qquad
p^{\bar1}_{R,\gamma}:=\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar1}.
\]
The finite-stage support, signed-parity, and leading-coefficient defects
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{supp}}_{R,\gamma}:=
\begin{cases}
P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma},& a_\Delta(\gamma)=0,\\
0,&a_\Delta(\gamma)\ne0,
\end{cases}
\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{par}}_{R,\gamma}
:=p^{\bar0}_{R,\gamma}-p^{\bar1}_{R,\gamma}
-a_\Delta(\gamma)\in\mathbb Z,
\]
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{lead}}_R:=\operatorname{lc}_{\mathfrak c_\infty}
(\operatorname{pf}_{X,R})-64\in\mathbb C
\]
are required to satisfy
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{supp}}_{R,\gamma}=
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{par}}_{R,\gamma}=0
\quad(\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}),
\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{lead}}_R=0 .
\]
The support residual is an actual super-vector-space residual, not only a
\(K_0\) class: its vanishing excludes invisible even--odd cancelling
primitive pieces in target-zero degrees.  The parity residual is a signed
superdimension residual; the Borcherds product fixes this integer, not a
canonical split of the nonzero multiplicity into even and odd compact
states.  For a fixed \(R\), these residuals decide only the supplied
finite test window.  The inclusion of active target degrees in the source
image is itself a residual condition, not a consequence of the automorphic
product.  Thus the target windows do not prove compact source coverage;
they test it inside the source-covered finite stages.  If the residuals
vanish compatibly for all \(R\), and the cofinal windows are
source-covered, the limit section has the prescribed
expansion
\[
\operatorname{pf}_X|_{\mathfrak c_\infty}
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{\sdim P^\Pi_{X,\gamma}},
\]
with
\[
\sdim P^\Pi_{X,(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l).
\]
No source-window theorem is asserted here.  The schedule
\(N_R^\Delta\) is an external finite target test; it becomes a source
coverage theorem only after the supplied finite Hall stages prove
\(A_R\subset\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\) compatibly in \(R\).
The equality of the resulting product with \(\Delta_5\) is imported from
the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin product.  The compact parity pieces
realizing these signed dimensions are conditional data, not a consequence
of the scalar OP square.  No source computation of the primitive
exponents is claimed here.  The equalities
\(\sdim P^\Pi_{X,(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l)\) are part of the supplied
\(D_0\)-certificate, tested against the imported Borcherds product.  A
source computation would derive these signed dimensions from the compact
Hall correspondences, orientation data, and protected integration before
comparison with the target denominator algebra.  A section-level statement
\(\operatorname{pf}_X=\Delta_5\) also requires a supplied isomorphism from
the Pfaffian line \(\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},X}\) to the pullback of the
automorphic weight-five line, compatible with the cusp trivialization and
the squaring maps.  The finite product formula alone is only a recognition
test after such line-comparison data have been supplied.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Chamber dependence and wall-crossing]
\label{rem:chamber-conditional-wall-crossing}
The certificate is indexed by a Bridgeland-type supplied stability/HN sector
\((\sigma,S)\), in the K3-surface lineage of
\cite{BridgelandK3Stability,BayerMacriProjectivity}.  The lattice cocycle
\(B(c,c')\) is chamber-independent: it
records only Mukai pairings of fixed lattice vectors.  The compact
Hall/factorization side \(D_0(X;\sigma,S)\) is chamber-dependent: the
finite-type semistable substacks change under wall-crossing, and the
Kontsevich--Soibelman wall-crossing formula relates Hall counts in
adjacent chambers.

If the certificate
\(D_0(X;\sigma,S)\) is supplied in chamber \(\sigma\), then the
normal-ordered map \(\overline\Pi_X\) remains a homomorphism and the
recognition target is \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\) provided the chamber
identifications hold for the OP/DT scalar import of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:op-normalization}}; that the chosen
\(\sigma\) lies in the OP/DT chamber, or that the wall-crossing transport
is compatible with \(\overline\Pi_X\), is a separate conjectural input.
The manuscript does not assert chamber-independence of the recognition
target; that is an open conjecture.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Finite Pfaffian window obstruction]
\label{prop:finite-pfaffian-window-obstruction}
Fix \(R\in\mathcal R\), and put
\[
A_R:=\{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\mid a_\Delta(\gamma)\ne0\},
\qquad
Z_R:=\{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\mid a_\Delta(\gamma)=0\}.
\]
For any supplied finite source package \(D_{0,R}\), vanishing of
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{supp}}_{R,\gamma}\) and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{par}}_{R,\gamma}\) on
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\) is equivalent to the two finite conditions
\[
P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}=0\quad(\gamma\in Z_R),
\qquad
\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+},\quad
p^{\bar0}_{R,\gamma}-p^{\bar1}_{R,\gamma}=a_\Delta(\gamma)
\quad(\gamma\in A_R).
\]
In particular every active target degree in the cofinal window must
already occur in the source image:
\[
A_R\subset\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+} .
\]
The strongest object constructed from the automorphic input alone at
this stage is the finite \(K_0\)-Pfaffian shadow
\[
[\mathsf P_{\Delta,R}^{K_0}]
:=\sum_{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}}
a_\Delta(\gamma)[\C_\gamma]
\in
K_0\!\left(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\text{-graded }
\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}}\right)
\]
and the finite formal section
\[
\operatorname{pf}^{K_0}_{\Delta,R}
:=
64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}}
(1-x^\gamma)^{a_\Delta(\gamma)} .
\]
This shadow is a target invariant.  It is not a compact Hall object, not
a Pfaffian line on the reduced quotient, and not a first-order operator.
For \(\gamma\in A_R\), the pair of compact parity dimensions is not
determined by the shadow: adding a finite vector space \(W_\gamma\) in
both parities replaces
\[
(P^\Pi_{R,\gamma,\bar0},P^\Pi_{R,\gamma,\bar1})
\quad\text{by}\quad
(P^\Pi_{R,\gamma,\bar0}\oplus W_\gamma,
 P^\Pi_{R,\gamma,\bar1}\oplus W_\gamma)
\]
and leaves the finite product, support test, signed-parity test, and
leading coefficient unchanged.  Thus compact parity pieces on the
cofinal target windows are extra source data.  They cannot be constructed
from \(\Delta_5\), from the denominator product, or from the OP scalar
square.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
If \(\gamma\in Z_R\), the support residual is
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{supp}}_{R,\gamma}=P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}\); its vanishing
is exactly the first displayed condition.  If \(\gamma\in A_R\) and
\(\gamma\notin\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\), the convention
\(P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}=0\) gives
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{par}}_{R,\gamma}=-a_\Delta(\gamma)\ne0\).  Hence
vanishing forces \(\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\), and then the parity
residual is exactly
\[
p^{\bar0}_{R,\gamma}-p^{\bar1}_{R,\gamma}-a_\Delta(\gamma)=0.
\]
This proves the equivalence and the active-window coverage.

The finite formal section is obtained by applying the
superdeterminant formula to the \(K_0\)-class
\([\mathsf P_{\Delta,R}^{K_0}]\).  This construction takes place in the
Grothendieck group of finite graded super vector spaces.  It contains no
extension correspondences, no orientation line, and no skew-adjoint
finite operator.  Finally, the replacement by
\(W_\gamma\oplus\Pi W_\gamma\) has zero class in \(K_0\), so it does not
change \(p^{\bar0}_{R,\gamma}-p^{\bar1}_{R,\gamma}\) or any product
depending only on signed superdimension.  The actual parity pieces are
therefore invisible to the finite Pfaffian shadow.
\end{proof}

\begin{openproblem}[Source computation of the Igusa exponents]
\label{op:source-computation-igusa-exponents}
Derive the equalities
\[
\sdim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}=a_\Delta(\gamma),
\qquad
\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+},
\]
from the compact Hall correspondences, orientation data, quotient descent,
and protected integration at finite height \(R\), before comparison with
the imported Borcherds product.  The present certificate only tests a
supplied source object against the target exponents.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{definition}[Finite Hall source kernel and downstream normal-ordering
package]
\label{def:finite-hall-source-kernel}
Fix \(R\in\mathcal R\).  A finite Hall source kernel at height \(R\) is
first the following source-side geometric datum, before normal-ordering,
protected integration, or comparison with the Borcherds target:
\[
\mathfrak S^{\mathrm{geom}}_R=
\bigl(
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c},\Phi_{R,\widehat c},
\mathfrak E_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'},
p_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'},q_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'},
o_{R,\widehat c},\mu^{or}_{R}
\bigr)_{\widehat c,\widehat c'\in\widehat\Gamma_R}.
\]
The finite source package used by the \(D_0\)-certificate is
\[
\mathfrak S_R=
\bigl(
\mathfrak S^{\mathrm{geom}}_R,
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}},
\Theta_{\Pi,R},\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}
\bigr).
\]
Only \(\mathfrak S^{\mathrm{geom}}_R\) is the common finite geometric
kernel.  The protected integration map and the normal-ordering cochains
are downstream finite data; they are part of the certificate, not
consequences of the geometric kernel alone.  The requirements are finite
and source-internal.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(S0)}] The finite direct sum of protected cohomology groups
has a supplied unit, counit, multiplication, and coproduct, making it a
finite graded bialgebra object before primitives are taken.  The counit is
denoted \(\epsilon_R\), the coproduct \(\Delta_R\), and
\[
\Prim_R:=\ker\bigl(\Delta_R-(1\otimes\mathrm{id})
-(\mathrm{id}\otimes1)\bigr)\cap\ker(\epsilon_R)
\]
is the finite primitive subobject.
\item[\textup{(S1)}] Each
\(\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c}\) is a finite-type d-critical stack with
compactly supported BBDJS vanishing-cycle complex
\(\Phi_{R,\widehat c}\), orientation line \(o_{R,\widehat c}\), and
finite-dimensional protected cohomology.
\item[\textup{(S2)}] For every product whose target charge remains in
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\), the extension correspondence
\[
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c}\times\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c'}
\xleftarrow{\ p_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}\ }
\mathfrak E_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}
\xrightarrow{\ q_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}\ }
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c\star\widehat c'}
\]
is admissible for vanishing-cycle pull-push, proper on the protected
support used by \(I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}\), and equipped with the oriented
Thom--Sebastiani transport \(\mu_R^{or}\).  If
\(\widehat c\star\widehat c'\notin\widehat\Gamma_R\), the projected
correspondence is declared zero in the finite quotient.
\item[\textup{(S3)}] The two-step extension stacks carry the usual flag
associativity isomorphisms, and the coproduct correspondences are
admissible in the same Borel--Moore or compact-support formalism.
\item[\textup{(S3')}] The multiplication and coproduct satisfy the finite
bialgebra compatibility diagram after vanishing-cycle pull-push and
orientation transport.  Consequently the supercommutator of two primitives
is again primitive at this finite stage.
\item[\textup{(S4)}] The added normal-ordering cochains
\(\Theta_{\Pi,R}\), \(\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}\) act on the actual finite
correspondence targets, not merely on the lattice labels.
\end{enumerate}
For a successor arrow \(R^+\to R\), a transition-compatible family of
kernels also includes truncation morphisms on stacks, extension stacks,
coefficient complexes, orientations, and protected integration maps,
with non-successor maps defined as their composites.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Finite \(D_0\) Hall source package from a supplied kernel]
\label{prop:finite-d0-hall-source-construction}
A supplied finite Hall source kernel \(\mathfrak S_R\) determines the
finite state-side Hall object, its primitive bracket, and the justified
first-order differential shadow as follows.

First set
\[
\mathcal H^{or}_{R,\widehat c}
:=
\mathrm H_c^\bullet
(\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c},
\Phi_{R,\widehat c}\otimes o_{R,\widehat c}),
\qquad
\mathcal H^{or}_{R}:=
\bigoplus_{\widehat c\in\widehat\Gamma_R}
\mathcal H^{or}_{R,\widehat c}.
\]
This is finite-dimensional because \(\widehat\Gamma_R\) is finite and
\textup{(S1)} imposes finite protected cohomology on each summand.  The
Hall product and coproduct are the finite pull-push maps
\[
m_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}
=
q_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c',!}\,
\operatorname{TS}^{or}_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}\,
p_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}^*,
\]
\[
\Delta_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}
=
p_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c',!}\,
(\operatorname{TS}^{or}_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'})^{-1}\,
q_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}^*,
\]
with zero output when the target charge leaves \(\widehat\Gamma_R\).
The two-step flag isomorphisms in \textup{(S3)} give associativity and
coassociativity at this finite height; their failure is exactly the finite
flag component of the \(D_0\) residual.

Let \(P_R\subset\mathcal H_R^{or}\) be the primitive part for
\(\Delta_R\), and put
\[
P_R^\Pi:=\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta_R}P_R .
\]
The normal-ordering cochain in \textup{(S4)} transports the supercommutator
of \(m_R\) to a finite \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\)-graded bracket
\[
[\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_{\Theta,R}:
P^\Pi_{R,\gamma}\otimes P^\Pi_{R,\gamma'}
\longrightarrow P^\Pi_{R,\gamma+\gamma'} .
\]
If the finite Jacobi diagram \textup{(NO5)} holds, this is a finite Lie
superalgebra bracket.  Equivalently, it determines the Chevalley--Eilenberg
first-order differential
\[
d_{\mathrm{CE},R}:
C^\bullet_{\mathrm{CE}}(P_R^\Pi)
\longrightarrow
C^{\bullet+1}_{\mathrm{CE}}(P_R^\Pi),
\]
the unique degree-one derivation whose quadratic part is dual to
\([\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_{\Theta,R}\).  The identity
\(d_{\mathrm{CE},R}^2=0\) is exactly the finite Jacobi identity with the
Koszul signs.  This is the first-order differential justified by the
finite Hall source core.  It is not yet the protected Dirac operator
\(\mathfrak D_{X,R}\), and it carries no Pfaffian line, unless the extra
Dirac/Pfaffian data of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-d0-atlas-parity-obstruction} are supplied.

For a transition-compatible family \(\mathfrak S_{R^+}\to\mathfrak S_R\),
the specified truncation morphisms induce
\[
\rho^H_{R^+R}:\mathcal H^{or}_{R^+}\to\mathcal H^{or}_{R},\qquad
\rho^P_{R^+R}:P^\Pi_{R^+}\to P^\Pi_R .
\]
They are morphisms of finite Hall objects precisely when the product,
coproduct, pairing, integration, and normal-ordering squares
\textup{(NO1)--(NO7)} commute.  Thus the source kernel constructs the
finite Hall source and names the exact residuals obstructing its passage
to a \(D_{0,R}\)-stage.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The direct sum is finite by finiteness of \(\widehat\Gamma_R\) and the
finite-dimensionality imposed in \textup{(S1)}.  The BBDJS
Thom--Sebastiani isomorphism, transported through the orientation
isomorphisms, identifies the vanishing-cycle coefficients on the source
of the correspondence with the coefficient system on the target.  The
properness/admissibility in \textup{(S2)} therefore makes the displayed
pull-push maps defined.  The zero convention for charges outside
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\) is exactly the finite charge-support Hall quotient
convention.
The two-step flag isomorphisms in \textup{(S3)} identify the two
parenthesized pull-push composites, hence give associativity and the
dual coproduct coherence at height \(R\).  Clause \textup{(S0)} supplies
the finite unit, counit, multiplication, and coproduct, and defines
primitives as the displayed kernel.  Clause \textup{(S3')} supplies the
finite bialgebra compatibility diagram, so the supercommutator of two
primitives is again primitive.  The normal-ordering cochain acts on the
actual correspondence targets by \textup{(S4)}, so it transports the
bracket to the additive \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\)-degree.  Finally, the
Chevalley--Eilenberg differential is the standard derivation dual to a
Lie superalgebra bracket; its square is the Jacobiator with the Koszul
signs.  The transition assertion is the same pull-push naturality applied
to the supplied truncation morphisms.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Cofinal target-window \(K_0\) parity shadow]
\label{prop:cofinal-target-window-parity-model}
For every \(R\in\mathcal R\), the target exponents construct a canonical
minimal finite super-vector-space model on the test window:
\[
\mathsf P^{\min}_{\Delta,R,\gamma}:=
\begin{cases}
\C^{a_\Delta(\gamma)}\ \hbox{in parity }\overline0,
&a_\Delta(\gamma)>0,\\
\C^{-a_\Delta(\gamma)}\ \hbox{in parity }\overline1,
&a_\Delta(\gamma)<0,\\
0,&a_\Delta(\gamma)=0,
\end{cases}
\qquad
\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}.
\]
It satisfies
\[
[\mathsf P^{\min}_{\Delta,R}]
=
\sum_{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}}
a_\Delta(\gamma)[\C_\gamma]
=[\mathsf P_{\Delta,R}^{K_0}]
\]
and gives the formal Pfaffian section
\(\operatorname{pf}^{K_0}_{\Delta,R}\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-pfaffian-window-obstruction}.

Let \(P_R^{\Pi,+}:=P_R^\Pi|_{\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}}\) be the cusp-positive
primitive source half constructed from a finite Hall source kernel.  On
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\), vanishing of
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{supp}}_{R,\gamma}\) and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{par}}_{R,\gamma}\) is equivalent to the
Grothendieck equality
\[
[P_R^{\Pi,+}|_{\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}}]
=
[\mathsf P^{\min}_{\Delta,R}]
\]
together with active-window source coverage
\[
\{\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\mid a_\Delta(\gamma)\ne0\}
\subset\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}
\]
and actual vanishing of source primitive spaces in all target-zero
degrees.  This equality upgrades to an isomorphism of graded super vector
spaces
\[
P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}\simeq
\mathsf P^{\min}_{\Delta,R,\gamma}
\qquad(\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+})
\]
if and only if the no-hidden-cancellation condition
\[
\min\{\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\overline0},
\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\overline1}\}=0
\]
holds for every active \(\gamma\) in the test window.  Without that extra
source condition, one may add \(W_\gamma\oplus\Pi W_\gamma\) in any active
degree without changing the Pfaffian product, the signed parity residual,
or the leading coefficient.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The definition of \(\mathsf P^{\min}_{\Delta,R,\gamma}\) gives signed
dimension \(a_\Delta(\gamma)\) in every test degree and no vector space
when \(a_\Delta(\gamma)=0\).  Hence its Grothendieck class is the
displayed finite \(K_0\)-Pfaffian shadow.  The equivalence between
vanishing residuals, active-window source coverage, and the stated
\(K_0\)-equality is exactly
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-pfaffian-window-obstruction}, with the
support residual remembering actual source spaces in target-zero degrees.
For an active \(\gamma\), two finite super vector spaces of signed
dimension \(a_\Delta(\gamma)\) are isomorphic to the minimal model
precisely when one parity has dimension zero.  Adding
\(W_\gamma\oplus\Pi W_\gamma\) changes neither signed dimension nor any
superdeterminant depending only on signed dimension.  This proves the
last assertion.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Finite Hall--Dirac atlas and parity-lift obstruction]
\label{prop:finite-d0-atlas-parity-obstruction}
Fix \(R\in\mathcal R\).  The finite Hall source core is constructed from
the source kernel of Definition~\ref{def:finite-hall-source-kernel} by
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-d0-hall-source-construction}.  A genuine
construction of the full finite stage \(D_{0,R}\), including the Dirac
operator and Pfaffian line, is equivalent to supplying in addition a
finite Hall--Dirac atlas
\[
\mathfrak A_R=
\bigl(
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c},\mathfrak E_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'},
\Phi_{R,\widehat c},o_{R,\widehat c},\mu^{or}_{R},
\mathcal F_R^{D_0},\Theta_{\Pi,R},\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-},\iota_R^{obs},
K_R^\Pi,\mathfrak D_{X,R},
\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},R},\ell_R
\bigr)
\]
with the following data.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(A1)}] \emph{Finite extension-closed d-critical source.}
For each \(\widehat c=(c,T)\in\widehat\Gamma_R\) there is a finite-type
d-critical stack
\(\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c}\) with compactly supported BBDJS
vanishing-cycle coefficient complex
\(\Phi_{R,\widehat c}\).  The finite union
\(\mathfrak M_R=\coprod_{\widehat c\in\widehat\Gamma_R}
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c}\) is closed under those extensions whose
charge remains in \(\widehat\Gamma_R\).  Thus for
\(\widehat c,\widehat c'\), with
\(\widehat c\star\widehat c'\in\widehat\Gamma_R\), there is a finite-type
extension correspondence
\[
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c}\times\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c'}
\xleftarrow{\ p_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}\ }
\mathfrak E_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}
\xrightarrow{\ q_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}\ }
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c\star\widehat c'} ,
\]
and the correspondence is empty after projection to the quotient when the
target charge leaves \(\widehat\Gamma_R\).  The two-step extension stacks
for triples in \(\widehat\Gamma_R\) satisfy the usual flag associativity
isomorphisms.
\item[\textup{(A2)}] \emph{Orientation square and quotient
linearization.}
There are orientation lines
\[
o_{R,\widehat c}^{\otimes2}
\simeq
\det\mathrm{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}
(\mathcal C_{\widehat c},\mathcal C_{\widehat c})
\]
on the finite strata, Thom--Sebastiani orientation isomorphisms
\(\mu^{or}_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}\) over the extension
correspondences, and zero quotient-linearization characters for every
finite stabilizer appearing in the reduced \(E\)-quotient.  Equivalently
the classes \(\mathfrak o^{or}_{R,\mathcal C}\) of \textup{(D0-Q)}
vanish with chosen finite trivializations.
\item[\textup{(A3)}] \emph{Finite Hall operations, normal ordering, and
protected integration.}
The maps \(p_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}\) and
\(q_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}\) are admissible for vanishing-cycle
pull-push and proper on the support used by the protected trace.  The
resulting Joyce--Kontsevich--Soibelman pull-push operations define
\[
m_R,\qquad \Delta_R,\qquad [\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]_R,\qquad
I_R^{\mathrm{prot}},
\]
and the source observable shadow \(\mathcal F_R^{D_0}\), normal-ordering
cochains \(\Theta_{\Pi,R}\), \(\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}\), and comparison map
\(\iota_R^{obs}\) are defined source-first.  They satisfy the finite flag,
coproduct, trace, observable-comparison, Hochschild, and negative-cyclic
diagrams required in \textup{(D0-F)}, \textup{(D0-O)}, and
\textup{(D0-N)}.
\item[\textup{(A4)}] \emph{Finite first-order complex.}
There is a perfect \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\)-graded supercomplex \(K_R^\Pi\) and
an odd skew-adjoint first-order endomorphism
\[
\mathfrak D_{X,R}:K_R^\Pi\to K_R^\Pi
\]
whose primitive symbol on
\[
P_R^\Pi=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}
(\overline\Pi_{R,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_R^{D_0})
\]
is the Hall bracket of \textup{(A3)}.
\item[\textup{(A5)}] \emph{Pfaffian square.}
On the reduced finite quotient
\(\mathfrak Q_R:=(\mathfrak M_R/E)^{\mathrm{red}}\) there is a determinant
line \(\mathscr L_{\det,R}\) attached to \(K_R^\Pi\), a square root
\[
\eta_R:\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},R}^{\otimes2}
\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\mathscr L_{\det,R},
\]
and a finite section \(\operatorname{pf}_{X,R}\) whose leading coefficient
at the Borcherds cusp is \(64\).
\item[\textup{(A6)}] \emph{Parity lift on the positive Pfaffian test window.}
For every \(\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\) there are actual compact
primitive super-vector spaces
\[
P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}
=P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar0}\oplus P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar1}
\]
with
\[
\ell_R(\gamma)=
\bigl(\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar0},
\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar1}\bigr),
\]
such that \(P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma}=0\) for \(a_\Delta(\gamma)=0\), and
\[
\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar0}
-\dim P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar1}
=a_\Delta(\gamma)
\]
for \(a_\Delta(\gamma)\ne0\).  This includes the active-window source
coverage \(A_R\subset\Gamma_R^{\Pi,+}\).
\item[\textup{(A7)}] \emph{Successor transition diagrams.}
For \(R^+\to R\) there are truncation maps on the stacks, extension
stacks, coefficient complexes, first-order complexes, and Pfaffian lines
such that
\[
\begin{tikzcd}
\mathfrak E_{R^+,\widehat c,\widehat c'}
 \arrow[r,"q_{R^+}"] \arrow[d,"\tau^E_{R^+R}"']
&
\mathfrak M_{R^+,\widehat c\star\widehat c'}
 \arrow[d,"\tau^M_{R^+R}"]
\\
\mathfrak E_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}
 \arrow[r,"q_R"']
&
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c\star\widehat c'}
\end{tikzcd}
\qquad
\begin{tikzcd}
\mathfrak E_{R^+,\widehat c,\widehat c'}
 \arrow[r,"p_{R^+}"] \arrow[d,"\tau^E_{R^+R}"']
&
\mathfrak M_{R^+,\widehat c}\times
\mathfrak M_{R^+,\widehat c'}
 \arrow[d,"\tau^M_{R^+R}\times\tau^M_{R^+R}"]
\\
\mathfrak E_{R,\widehat c,\widehat c'}
 \arrow[r,"p_R"']
&
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c}\times
\mathfrak M_{R,\widehat c'}
\end{tikzcd}
\]
commute after projection to the finite quotient, and the induced diagrams
for \(\rho^K_{R^+R}\mathfrak D_{X,R^+}\),
\(\rho^{\mathrm{Pf}}_{R^+R}\eta_{R^+}\), and
\(\rho^{\mathrm{Pf}}_{R^+R}(\operatorname{pf}_{X,R^+})\) commute.  The
finite tuple of failures of these diagrams is denoted
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{atlas}}_{R^+R}\); it is one source-level
realization of the transition residual
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{R^+R}\).
\end{enumerate}

If \(\mathfrak A_R\) is supplied and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{atlas}}_{R^+R}=0\), then the pull-push operations,
orientation square, first-order operator, Pfaffian line, and parity lift
construct the finite package \(D_{0,R}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate}.  Conversely, every
constructed \(D_{0,R}\) gives such finite atlas data after forgetting to
the finite support and reduced quotient.  Thus the missing object is not
the target determinant; it is the finite atlas \(\mathfrak A_R\) and its
successor-compatible trivializations.

Moreover the two remaining Pfaffian ambiguities are exact.  The
Pfaffian square-root choices for a fixed determinant line are empty unless
\([\mathscr L_{\det,R}]\) is divisible by \(2\) in
\(\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak Q_R)\); when nonempty, their isomorphism
classes form a torsor under \(\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak Q_R)[2]\), with
the \(H^1(\mathfrak Q_R;\mathbb F_2)\) local-system shadow used in the
finite-stabilizer orientation tests.  For an active degree
\(\gamma\in A_R\), the compact parity lifts form the affine monoid
\[
\mathscr P_R(\gamma)
=
\{(u,v)\in\Z_{\ge0}^2\mid u-v=a_\Delta(\gamma)\},
\qquad
(u,v)\mapsto(u+t,v+t).
\]
The finite \(K_0\)-Pfaffian shadow fixes only the difference \(u-v\).
The no-hidden-cancellation condition
\[
\min(u,v)=0
\]
would select the unique minimal lift
\[
(u,v)=
\begin{cases}
(a_\Delta(\gamma),0),&a_\Delta(\gamma)>0,\\
(0,-a_\Delta(\gamma)),&a_\Delta(\gamma)<0,
\end{cases}
\]
but this is an extra source axiom.  It is not implied by
\(\Delta_5\), by the denominator algebra, by the OP scalar square, or by
equality in \(K_0\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Given \(\mathfrak A_R\), clauses \textup{(A1)}--\textup{(A3)} are exactly
the finite Joyce--Kontsevich--Soibelman Hall pull-push construction with
BBDJS vanishing-cycle coefficients and Joyce--Upmeier orientation
transport.  Finiteness of the index set makes all sums and products
finite, and the two-step flag isomorphisms are precisely the associativity
and coproduct-coherence diagrams.  Clause \textup{(A4)} gives
\textup{(D0-D)}.  Clause \textup{(A5)} gives the finite Pfaffian square
and the leading coefficient condition in \textup{(D0-Pf)}.  Clause
\textup{(A6)} is exactly the vanishing of the support and parity residuals
on \(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\), with active-window coverage as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-pfaffian-window-obstruction}.  Clause
\textup{(A7)} gives the successor compatibility diagrams; their failure
is the displayed finite residual \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{atlas}}_{R^+R}\),
which maps into \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{R^+R}\).  Hence the data
assemble to \(D_{0,R}\).  The converse is tautological: a constructed
finite \(D_{0,R}\) already contains the finite source stacks,
correspondences, coefficient systems, operator, Pfaffian line, and parity
pieces named above, after restriction to its finite support.

The assertion about square roots is the elementary Picard-group
classification: a line \(L\) admits a square root iff its class lies in
\(2\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak Q_R)\); the set of square roots, when
nonempty, is acted on simply transitively by \(2\)-torsion line bundles.
Passing to \(\mathbb F_2\)-local systems gives the
\(H^1(\mathfrak Q_R;\mathbb F_2)\) shadow.  Finally
\(\mathscr P_R(\gamma)\) is the set of nonnegative integer solutions to
one linear equation \(u-v=a_\Delta(\gamma)\).  Adding \((t,t)\) preserves
the \(K_0\) class and all product exponents.  Therefore signed dimension
does not determine compact parity pieces unless the extra condition
\(\min(u,v)=0\) is supplied.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Finite \(D_0\)-certificate: proved, imported,
conditional, and open parts]
\label{thm:first-order-d0-certificate}
This first-order certificate separates finite objects obtained from
supplied kernels and atlases from the open existence of those kernels and
atlases.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(lattice/finite bookkeeping, conditional on supplied HN support)}]
For every \(R\in\mathcal R\), the
normal-ordered support
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\), its image \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\), the target window
\(\Gamma_{\Delta,R}\), the ambient test window
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\), and the positive Pfaffian test window
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate} are finite; by
cofinality of the target-window schedule, the windows
\(\Gamma_{\Delta,R}\) exhaust
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\setminus\{0\}\).  The lattice charge completion
\(\widehat\Gamma_X\) and the normal-ordered homomorphism
\(\overline\Pi_X\) exist and are additive, by
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}.
The exhaustion statement is target-side only; it does not assert that
every target degree lies in the image of the supplied finite Hall support.
\item[\textup{(imported)}] The target observable algebra
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\), its constant-current denominator algebra
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\), and the product
\[
64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=\Delta_5
\]
are supplied by the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin theorem and
Proposition~\ref{prop:formal-current-envelope}.
\item[\textup{(finite source package from supplied kernel)}] If, at height \(R\), a
finite Hall source kernel \(\mathfrak S_R\) in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:finite-hall-source-kernel} is supplied, then
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-d0-hall-source-construction} determines the
finite state object \(\mathcal H_R^{or}\), the Hall product, coproduct,
primitive bracket, normal-ordered finite primitive algebra \(P_R^\Pi\),
successor transition maps, and the Chevalley--Eilenberg first-order
differential \(d_{\mathrm{CE},R}\) justified by the finite bracket.  This
is finite algebra obtained from supplied source data at height \(R\).  It
is not yet the protected
Dirac operator \(\mathfrak D_{X,R}\) and carries no Pfaffian line unless
the extra Dirac/Pfaffian atlas data are supplied.  Independently, the
cofinal target exponents construct the minimal finite target-window
parity model
\(\mathsf P^{\min}_{\Delta,R}\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:cofinal-target-window-parity-model}; comparison
with actual compact source primitives is exactly the support/parity and
no-hidden-cancellation test recorded there.
\item[\textup{(finite residual)}] Once the finite Hall--Dirac atlas
\(\mathfrak A_R\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-d0-atlas-parity-obstruction} is supplied,
including the finite semistable stacks, extension correspondences,
vanishing-cycle pull-push maps, protected integration maps, source
comparison, first-order complex, Pfaffian square, and compact parity
lifts at height \(R\), the obstruction tuple recorded by the finite-stage
\(D_0\) certificate is the vanishing, with compatible trivializations, of
\[
\mathfrak O_{D_0,R}:=
\left(
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{R^+R},\
\{\mathfrak o^{or}_{R,\mathcal C}\}_{\mathcal C\in\mathsf{St}_R},\
\mathfrak o^{obs}_R,\
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{top}}_{\Theta,R^+R},\
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Hoch}}_{\Theta,R},\
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tri}}_{\Theta,R},\
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Jac}}_{\Theta,R},\
\mathfrak o_{F,R},\
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{\Theta,R},\
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rad}}_{\Theta,R},\
\{\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{no}}_{R,c,T}\}_{(c,T)\in\widehat\Gamma_R},\
\{\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{supp}}_{R,\gamma}\}_{\gamma\in
\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}},\
\{\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{par}}_{R,\gamma}\}_{\gamma\in
\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}},\
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{lead}}_R
\right).
\]
These classes are typed in
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate}, the no-overcount label
paragraph following \(\widehat\Gamma_R\), and
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}.  They are not determined by
\(\Delta_5\), by the denominator algebra, or by the OP scalar square.
Vanishing here means chosen null-trivializations in the displayed finite
obstruction groups or complexes, compatible with the successor transition
\(R^+\to R\) and hence with its composites; a numerical zero in a
Grothendieck group is not such a trivialization.
The Pfaffian part has the sharp finite consequence recorded in
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-pfaffian-window-obstruction}: active target
degrees in \(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\) must lie in the source image, but
the compact parity dimensions themselves remain extra source data.
\item[\textup{(conditional)}] If a tuple satisfying
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate} is supplied, then it
supplies hypothesis \textup{(D0)} of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}.  Its primitive
bracket is compatible with normal-ordered descent on the nose:
\[
[P^\Pi_{X,\gamma},P^\Pi_{X,\gamma'}]_{\Theta}
\subset P^\Pi_{X,\gamma+\gamma'},
\qquad \gamma,\gamma'\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\]
and its Pfaffian section has the formal cusp expansion
\[
\operatorname{pf}_X|_{\mathfrak c_\infty}
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)},
\]
which the imported Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin theorem identifies with
the normalized \(\Delta_5\) product at \(\mathfrak c_\infty\).  This is
not a section-level equality in the automorphic line; that conclusion
requires the supplied Pfaffian-to-automorphic comparison
\(\iota_{\mathrm{aut}}\) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}.
\item[\textup{(usage certificate)}] Every use of \textup{(D0)} in
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional} factors through
one of the displayed clauses of
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate}: finite state and
transition data through \textup{(D0-F)}--\textup{(D0-S)}, reduced
orientation descent through \textup{(D0-Q)}, source/observable comparison
through \textup{(D0-O)}, normal-ordered grading through \textup{(D0-C)}
and \textup{(D0-N)}, the protected first-order complex through
\textup{(D0-D)}, and the Pfaffian target windows, support residuals,
signed parity exponents, and leading coefficient through
\textup{(D0-Pf)}.
\item[\textup{(open)}] The compact state-side construction of
\(\widehat{\mathcal H}^{or}_{\sigma,S}\), the finite Hall source kernels
\(\mathfrak S_R\), the finite Hall--Dirac atlases
\(\mathfrak A_R\), the finite-stage hybrid wrapped object
\(\mathcal F_R^{D_0}\), the obstruction trivializations
\(\mathfrak O_{D_0,R}=0\) and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{atlas}}_{R^+R}=0\), the compatible inverse system,
the Pfaffian line on the reduced compact quotient, and the compact parity
pieces
\(P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar0}\), \(P^{\Pi,+}_{R,\gamma,\bar1}\) on
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\), including vanishing in target-zero degrees,
are not constructed in this paper.  The target \(K_0\)-shadow supplies
only the signed differences; it does not trivialize the Pfaffian
square-root torsor or select a compact parity lift.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For fixed \(R\), the set \(F_{\sigma,S}(R)\) is finite by
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}.  Since \(h_S\) is positive on
active semistable charges, the length of a decomposition
\(c=c_1+\cdots+c_k\) with \(\sum_i h_S(c_i)\le R\) is bounded.  Hence only
finitely many sums \(\sum_{i<j}B(c_i,c_j)\) occur, so
\(\widehat\Gamma_R\) and \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\) are finite.
The function \(h_\Delta(n,l,m)=|n|+|l|+|m|\) is proper on the lattice
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), so \(\Gamma_{\Delta,R}\) is finite.  Since
\(\sup_RN_R^\Delta=\infty\), the union over all \(R\) is
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\setminus\{0\}\).  Thus
\(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\) is finite.  If \(R'\ge R\), then
\(F_{\sigma,S}(R)\subset F_{\sigma,S}(R')\) and every decomposition of
height \(\le R\) is also a decomposition of height \(\le R'\); this gives
the displayed inclusions of \(\widehat\Gamma_R\), \(\Gamma_R^\Pi\), and
\(\Gamma_{\Delta,R}\).
Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension} gives associativity of
\(\star\) and
\(\overline\Pi_X((c,T)\star(c',T'))=
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)+\overline\Pi_X(c',T')\).  The imported item is
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification} together with
Theorem~\ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:formal-current-envelope}.

Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-d0-hall-source-construction} is the finite
source package determined by the displayed source kernel: the Hall vector
spaces are compactly supported vanishing-cycle cohomologies, the product
and coproduct are the finite pull-push maps, the primitive bracket is the
normal-ordered supercommutator, and the first-order CE differential is
the standard derivation dual to that finite Lie bracket.
Proposition~\ref{prop:cofinal-target-window-parity-model} constructs the
minimal target-window parity model directly from the finite exponent
function \(a_\Delta\), and identifies the exact extra condition needed to
compare it with the compact source primitives.

The residual tuple \(\mathfrak O_{D_0,R}\) is a collection of already
typed obstructions.  The transition component records compatibility in
the finite inverse system.  The quotient-orientation component is the
criterion of Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.  The
observable component records that the source/target comparison respects
the finite product, coproduct, bracket, trace, and primitive comparison.
The next seven are the finite-topology, Hochschild, triple, Jacobi,
Frobenius, negative-cyclic, and Hopf-radical ideal/coideal obstruction
classes of Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}; the final three state exactly
the finite target coverage, absence of invisible zero-target primitive
support, signed Pfaffian multiplicity, and cusp-leading normalization
required in the Pfaffian line.  Their vanishing is therefore necessary
for the finite stage to be a \(D_0\)-stage, and, once the finite stacks,
correspondences, first-order complex, comparison map, and Pfaffian line
have been supplied, is precisely the extra trivialization data demanded by
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate}.

Assume the \(D_0\)-certificate.  Clause \textup{(D0-F)} gives the finite
stages and transition maps.  Clause \textup{(D0-S)} gives the HN-completed
state object on which the Hall operations are defined.  Clause
\textup{(D0-Q)} supplies the reduced quotient and orientation line used in
the Pfaffian construction.  Clause \textup{(D0-C)} places operations in the
corrected charge extension.  Clause \textup{(D0-N)} supplies the
chain-level shift categorifying the additivity of
\(\overline\Pi_X\); hence the descended primitive bracket is
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded.  Clause \textup{(D0-O)} supplies the
source observable shadow and comparison map.  Clauses \textup{(D0-D)} and
\textup{(D0-Pf)} supply the first-order object and its Pfaffian line.  The
support, signed-superdimension, target-window exhaustion, and
leading-coefficient conditions in \textup{(D0-Pf)}, combined with the
imported Borcherds product, give the normalized
\(\Delta_5\) cusp expansion for \(\operatorname{pf}_X\).

It remains to check the stated usage certificate in
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}.  Step 1 uses
only the supplied first-order object, the normal-ordered primitive
multiplicities, and the leading Pfaffian normalization; these are
\textup{(D0-D)} and \textup{(D0-Pf)}.  Step 2 uses the imported
Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin product, not a compact construction.  Step
3 uses the Pfaffian cusp normalization from \textup{(D0-Pf)} and the
imported Oberdieck--Pixton scalar normalization.  Step 5 uses only the
supplied chiral protected first-order theory and its decategorification,
supplied by \textup{(D0-F)}--\textup{(D0-Pf)}.  Step 4 is independent of \(D_0\)
except for the existence of the Pfaffian object; its signs come from
(O1), (O1)\(^+\), and (O2).  Thus the certificate implies every use of
\textup{(D0)} and no stronger compact existence claim is made.

The final item is a status statement: none of the source-side objects or
trivializations named there is constructed by the lattice calculation, by
the denominator algebra, or by the scalar OP square.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Dirac--Igusa realization certificate]
\label{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum}
A compact realization of the Igusa square root is a
Dirac--Igusa realization certificate
$$
\mathfrak K_X=(L_X,H_X,O_X,D_X,R_X).
$$
Its first-order truncation is the \(D_0\)-certificate of
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate}.  The full certificate
adds the orientation-monodromy, chiral Koszul, and primitive-recognition
data needed to identify the compact state-side algebra with the
Gritsenko--Nikulin target.  It is not a consequence of the Borcherds
product, the scalar Oberdieck--Pixton square, the target current envelope,
the target bar--cobar counit, or the existence of orientation lines alone.
It is the list of data whose construction would turn the virtual
determinant \(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\) into a compact first-order protected
realization.  The five entries have the following meanings.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\((L_X)\)] \emph{Local charge and \(E_3\) host.}
This entry consists of the formal dyonic Mukai lattice
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\), the algebraic/effective Hall support inside
it, the Gram map
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), and the
cocycle \(B\) of
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect}.  The Hall category is graded by
the supplied algebraic/effective charge support, not by
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) itself.
\((L_X)\) also includes the normal-ordered extension
\[
\widehat\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T,
\]
and the primitive saturated lifts of
Lemma~\ref{lem:primitive-lift-every-gram-triple}.  Finally, it includes
a supplied charge-completed holomorphic
\(E_3\)-factorization algebra, denoted \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\), on
\(X=K3\times E\), finite-first after the sectorial HN quotients of
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}.  A compact
holomorphic-Chern--Simons/BV construction, if it satisfies descent, the
quantum master equation, and anomaly cancellation in the completed charge
category, is a candidate source for this datum.  The datum also includes
a fixed \(E_3\)-formality point, a chain-level homotopy/framing datum
for the chosen operadic model, compact-support control, and continuity
of the \(E_3\) operations across
the finite HN inverse system.

\item[\((H_X)\)] \emph{Hybrid \(K3\)-to-\(E\) factorization shadow.}
This entry consists of a supplied finite-first
K3-to-\(E\) source interface in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-e3-source-interface}, a chain-level
specialization \(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\), and named comparison
maps \(\kappa_E\) (chiral-Koszul) and \(\pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\)
(proper-pushforward identification), with the triple zigzag
$$
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X
\xrightarrow{\ \mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\ }
\mathcal F_X^{(0)}
\xrightarrow{\ \kappa_E\ }
\mathcal F_X^{(1)}
\xrightarrow{\ \pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\ }
(p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X
$$
of equivalences in the projection-finite sectors.  In the wrapped
elliptic-degree sectors, the required filling is the finite-HN inverse
system whose limit is the hybrid object
\(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:hybrid-wrapped-factorization-certificate}.  Thus
\((H_X)\) includes the hybrid Ran base
\(\operatorname{Ran}^{\mathrm{hyb}}(E)\), projection-finite local
sectors \(\mathcal F_{\alpha,R}^{\mathrm{loc}}(U)\), rigidified wrapped
prequotient sectors \(\mathcal G_{\eta,R}^{\mathrm{wr}}\) with anchors
\(\lambda_{\eta,R}\), finite correspondence categories
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), and the three finite operation
families
\[
\mu_R^{\mathrm{loc}},\qquad
\mu_R^{\mathrm{hyb}},\qquad
\mu_R^{\mathrm{wr}},
\]
where \(\mu_R^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) includes the ordered two-sided mixed maps
\(\mu_{\alpha_-;\eta;\beta_+,R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\).  It also includes the
eight-word two-step binary flag atlas in the finite HN quotients, the
higher colored residual \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{col}}_R\), the
properness/admissibility residuals which make
\(\mathcal B_R^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}\) an actual correspondence-module
functor, the quotient operation \(Q_{E,R}\) applied only after the
extension correspondences are formed, the quotient comparison
isomorphisms \(\theta^Q_{\mu,R}\), and protected integration maps
\(I_R^{\mathrm{prot}}\) whose homogeneous \(s\)-degree is the elliptic
degree \(b_R\).  Equivalently,
\[
\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}=0
\]
for every finite height \(R\), compatibly with transition maps.  The
orientation lines used in these hybrid pull-push operations are the local
coefficient part of \((O_X)\); the Weyl-equivariant monodromy package
\((\mathrm{O1})^+\) and the type-II wall package \((\mathrm{O2})\) are
additional data.  A global Fock/Hecke sector is acceptable here only if
it is represented by the rigidified wrapped prequotients and acts through
the mixed maps \(\mu_R^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) before the reduced
\(E\)-quotient.  These equivalences and wrapped-sector data are part of
the datum, not operations constructed from the determinant.

\item[\((O_X)\)] \emph{Oriented compact Hall object and Weyl
orientation character.}
This entry consists of an oriented compact Hall factorization object
\(\mathcal H_X\)
graded by supplied effective charges \(c\) in the formal dyonic lattice,
with finite-type sectorial
moduli stacks and extension correspondences
$$
\mathfrak M_c^\sigma\times\mathfrak M_{c'}^\sigma
\xleftarrow{\ p_{c,c'}\ }
\mathfrak E_{c,c'}^\sigma
\xrightarrow{\ q_{c,c'}\ }
\mathfrak M_{c+c'}^\sigma,
$$
perfect reduced obstruction theories or critical
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structures, vanishing-cycle coefficients,
orientation lines with chosen square roots, Thom--Sebastiani orientation
transport coherent for triple extensions, and protected integration maps
compatible with HN completion and wall crossing.  The orientation entry
also includes the exact quotient-descent package.  For every charge
stratum \(\mathcal C\) used by the Hall correspondences one must specify
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
=w_2\!\left(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}
(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\right)
+\mathrm{cs}^{*}w_2\!\left(\det(\operatorname{coker}\mathrm{cs})\right)
\in H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2),
\]
\[
\alpha^{E,\mathrm{free}}_{\mathcal C}
=a_1(\mathcal C)u_1+a_2(\mathcal C)u_2
\in H^2(BE;\mathbb F_2),
\]
and, for every finite-stabilizer stratum \(S\) with stabilizer \(E[N]\),
\[
\widetilde\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,S}
\in H^2_{E[N]}(S;\mathbb F_2).
\]
The point-stabilizer class
\[
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,S}\in H^2(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)
\]
is used only after the mixed Borel terms, the stabilizer action on
\(H^\bullet(S;\mathbb F_2)\), and the Borel spectral-sequence
differentials have vanished.  One must prove these Borel classes, and
then their point-stabilizer restrictions, vanish on the corresponding
free and small-orbit strata.  At \(N=2\), after this restriction,
\[
\beta^{E,2}_{\mathcal C,S}
=b_{20}x_1^2+b_{11}x_1x_2+b_{02}x_2^2
\in H^2(BE[2];\mathbb F_2),
\]
with \(E[2]=\langle e_1,e_2\rangle\), \(e_3=e_1+e_2\), and
\[
\operatorname{res}_{\langle e_i\rangle}
\beta^{E,2}_{\mathcal C,S}=r_i(\mathcal C,S)\tau_i^2,
\qquad
(b_{20},b_{11},b_{02})
=(r_1,r_1+r_2+r_3,r_2).
\]
Thus the finite two-torsion residual vanishes exactly when
\(r_1=r_2=r_3=0\), but the full quotient descent also requires
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=0\) and
\(a_1(\mathcal C)=a_2(\mathcal C)=0\).  After this degree-two
two-torsion class vanishes, the chosen \(E[2]\)-linearization has a
degree-one character
\[
\lambda_{\mathcal C}^{E[2]}
=\lambda_1x_1+\lambda_2x_2\in H^1(BE[2];\mathbb F_2),
\]
and the quotient orientation requires \(\lambda_1=\lambda_2=0\).
Odd \(N\) finite stabilizers
have no positive-degree mod-\(2\) obstruction; even \(N\ge4\) is
detected on the \(2\)-primary stabilizer
\((\Z/2^a)^2\), \(2^a\parallel N\), where for \(a\ge2\)
\[
H^*\!\left(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2\right)
=\Lambda(x_1,x_2)\otimes\mathbb F_2[y_1,y_2],
\qquad |x_i|=1,\quad |y_i|=2,\quad x_i^2=0,
\]
\[
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C,(2)}
=A_1^{(N)}y_1+A_{12}^{(N)}x_1x_2+A_2^{(N)}y_2 .
\]
The mixed coefficient \(A_{12}^{(N)}\) is not detected by cyclic
restrictions; after this degree-two class vanishes, the residual
\(H^1(B(\Z/2^a)^2;\mathbb F_2)\)-linearization character must also
vanish.  Thus the even \(N\ge4\) residual remains part of the descent
datum; it is not implied by the \(E[2]\) vector.  The Hall
atlas must include local-local, wrapped-wrapped, and
mixed local/wrapped extension correspondences before quotienting by the
translation action of \(E\);
quotienting first forgets the relative \(E\)-position needed by mixed
convolution.  If a lifted action of
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) on the oriented completed Hall object is
supplied, its finite-stage obstruction is first the projective
determinant-line cocycle on the retained action groupoid
\(\mathcal G_R\):
\[
[c_{o,R}]\in H^2(\mathcal G_R;\underline{\mathbb F}_2).
\]
Only on a complete \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\)-orbit with constant
coefficients does this reduce to
\[
[c_o]\in H^2\!\left(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II});\mathbb F_2\right).
\]
The relevant groupoid or group class must vanish, the generator lifts
must satisfy \(s_{\delta_i}^2=1\), and the full quotient package,
including the zero finite characters \(\lambda^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}=0\),
must be transported with zero
\[
H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{s_{\delta_i}\mathcal C};\mathbb F_2)
\oplus\bigoplus_{N\ge2}H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)
\]
torsor defect, as in
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-quotient-orientation-obstruction}.  Only then does
the induced orientation character \(\epsilon_o\) satisfy
\[
\epsilon_o|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}
=\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}.
\]
Constructing the domain of this comparison and the character
\(\epsilon_o\) is part of the datum.  The comparison is a geometric
orientation-monodromy condition on the Hall side; it requires computing
the determinant-line signs on the three type-II simple reflections and
checking the reflection relations.  It is not obtained by choosing the
scalar normalization of \(\Delta_5\).

\item[\((D_X)\)] \emph{Normal-ordered descent and chiral Koszul
comparison.}
This entry consists of the chain-level normal-ordering package
\[
\mathsf{Ch}_{k,\widehat{\mathrm{HN}},E}^{\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}},
\quad
\{\mathsf T_\eta\}_{\eta\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}},
\quad
B_{\mathrm{ch}},
\quad
\Theta_\Pi,\Theta_\Pi^{-},
\quad
\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X,
\]
as in Definition~\ref{def:normal-ordering-coefficient-dg-category} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}.  The protected primitives are
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded only after applying
\(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\).  Their bracket is induced from the
upstairs \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)-graded Hall bracket by translating
the raw target degree
\[
\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')
\]
through \(\mathsf T_{B(c,c')}\), hence by shifting the displayed Gram
degree by \(-B(c,c')\).  The datum includes the triple-coherence
pentagon over the two-step Hall flag stacks, Jacobi compatibility of the
transported bracket, the \(S^1\)-equivariant negative-cyclic lift
\[
(b+uB_{\mathrm C})\Theta_\Pi^{-}=B_{\mathrm{ch}}^{-},
\]
and compatibility with the Joyce--Upmeier orientation cocycle, the
graded Frobenius identity, the completed Hopf pairing, and the reduced
\(E\)-quotient.  Equivalently, the seven obstruction classes
\[
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}},\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{Hoch}},\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{tri}},\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{Jac}},\quad
\mathfrak o_F,\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{cyc}},\quad
\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad}}
\]
of Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} vanish on every finite HN
quotient and compatibly in the inverse limit, with
\(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{top}}\) enforcing finite-fibre descent
and completed tensor/coproduct continuity, and with
\(\mathfrak o_{\Theta}^{\mathrm{rad}}\) read as the Lie-ideal and coideal
pair.  The finite-stage tests are the seven diagrams
\textup{(NO1)--(NO7)} of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-normal-ordering-verification-diagrams}.
The finite closure criterion
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-normal-ordering-closure-criterion} separates
the formal Picard normal-ordering lift from the non-formal Hall
correspondence, cyclic trace, and Hopf-radical compatibilities.
Before this descent, the
protected primitives of \(\mathcal F_X\) are graded by the upstairs
additive normal-ordered labels \((c,T)\), not by a Gram triple.  The
comparison with \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)}\) is made after
passing to \((n,l,m)=\overline\Pi_X(c,T)\); the shorthand
\(\Pi_X(c)\) is legitimate only on labels with \(T=0\).
\((D_X)\) also includes the full chiral Koszul source certificate of
Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-source-certificate}.  Thus, at every
finite HN height \(R\), one must supply a conilpotent chiral coalgebra
\(C_{X,R}\) attached to the hybrid source
\(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\), a finite source
charge filtration \(F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,\bullet}\), the collision
coproduct \(\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}}\), a charge-preserving bar comparison
$$
b_{X,R}:C_{X,R}\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
\bigl(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}}\bigr),
$$
and a chiral cobar quasi-isomorphism
$$
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_{X,R}
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E,\le R},
$$
compatibly in \(R\), and the Koszul Mittag--Leffler exactness hypothesis
of Proposition~\ref{prop:chiral-koszul-source-certificate-consequence}.
In the inverse limit this gives
$$
b_X:C_X\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}),
\qquad
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
$$
The target-internal counit
\(\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E})\to\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) does not
supply \(C_X\), \(b_X\), or \(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}\).  These are
source-side compact data.  Their finite residual is the vanishing of
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\) in every finite HN quotient, including
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), the assertion that the finite hybrid
source has been built with all correspondences, quotient, and integration
laws, \(\mathfrak o^{\Delta,\mathrm{ch}}_R\) and
\(\mathfrak o^{C,\mathrm{tr}}_{R'R}\), the finite collision-coproduct and
transition-continuity assertions, the Koszul
\(R^1\varprojlim=0\) condition for the source coalgebras, completed
bar/cobar systems, target truncations, and cones of \(b_{X,R}\) and
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\), \(\mathfrak o^\Omega_R\), the split
cobar residual
\[
\mathfrak o^\Omega_R
=
(\mathfrak o^{\varepsilon,\mathrm{src}}_R,\mathfrak o^\vartheta_R)
\]
of Corollary~\ref{cor:source-bar-remaining-cobar-obstruction}, and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{sep}}_R\), the assertion that the source coalgebra,
filtration, collision coproduct, bar comparison, and primitive restriction
were supplied independently of the target counit.

\item[\((R_X)\)] \emph{Primitive recognition.}
This entry is a primitive recognition certificate
\(\Pi_{\mathrm{rec}}\) for
$$
P_X^\Pi:=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X).
$$
This certificate is not a determinant datum and is not the
Gritsenko--Nikulin target itself.  It consists of a source-side
Gram-descended Lie superalgebra structure on \(P_X^\Pi\), the parity split
of each homogeneous primitive piece, compact representatives for the real
and imaginary simple-root fibres of the Gritsenko--Nikulin presentation,
verification of the Borcherds--Kac defining relations in the protected
Hall bracket, the completed Hopf pairing, generation by the simple
primitives and the Cartan, a no-extra-relations theorem, completed PBW
compatibility, and identification of the source Hopf radical with the
standard Gritsenko--Nikulin/Kac radical after completion.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Primitive recognition certificate; no source construction]
\label{prop:compact-igusa-realization-criterion}
\label{thm:primitive-recognition}
\label{thm:microscopic-hall-drinfeld-criterion}
Let \(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5}=(H,I,p,\alpha_i,(\ ,\ ))\) be the imported
Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds--Cartan superdatum for the automorphic
correction.  Thus
\[
H=\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C,\qquad
\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}\subset\La^{2,1}_{II}\subset H,
\]
the three \(\delta_i\) are even real simple roots, and
\[
((\delta_i,\delta_j))_{1\le i,j\le3}
=
\begin{pmatrix}2&-2&-2\\-2&2&-2\\-2&-2&2\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The remaining fibres of \(I\to H^*\) are the imaginary simple-root
fibres with the Gritsenko--Nikulin parity split
\(\mu_{\overline0}(a),\mu_{\overline1}(a)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:imaginary-simple-roots}.  The degree map is
\[
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}
=n\delta_1+m\delta_2+(n+m-l)\delta_3.
\]
Let \(\widehat{\mathfrak F}(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\) be the completed free
Lie superalgebra generated by the even Cartan \(H\) and by
parity-homogeneous generators \(e_i,f_i\), \(i\in I\), with
\(|e_i|=|f_i|=p(i)\) and \(\deg e_i=\alpha_i\),
\(\deg f_i=-\alpha_i\).  Let \(J_{\mathrm{BK}}\) be the closed
Borcherds--Kac ideal generated by the Cartan, Chevalley, real Serre,
orthogonality, and super sign relations.  After quotienting by the
standard radical of the completed invariant pairing one obtains the
target denominator algebra
\[
G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})
=\widehat{\mathfrak F}(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})/
\overline{J_{\mathrm{BK}}+\operatorname{Rad}_{\mathrm{GN}}}
=\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}
=\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}.
\]
Here \(\operatorname{Rad}_{\mathrm{GN}}\) denotes the preimage in the
completed presentation of the standard radical.
This target-side statement is imported from the Gritsenko--Nikulin/Kac
construction; it is not a compact Hall construction.

Suppose a compact Hall/factorization construction supplies a completed
\(\widehat\Gamma_X\)-graded primitive Hall Lie superalgebra
\[
\widetilde P_X=\prod_{\widehat c\in\widehat\Gamma_X}
\widetilde P_{X,\widehat c},
\qquad
[\widetilde P_{X,\widehat c},\widetilde P_{X,\widehat c'}]
\subset \widetilde P_{X,\widehat c\star\widehat c'},
\]
and a completed Hopf pairing.  Its normal-ordered Gram descent is
\[
P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{raw}}
=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X)
=\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\widetilde P_X
\]
and
\[
P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}
=P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{raw}}/
\overline{\operatorname{Rad}\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_X}.
\]
Assume the following source-side presentation data are supplied.  None of
these data is inferred from the Borcherds product, from the determinant,
or from signed dimensions alone.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(S1)] \emph{Charge and normal-ordered descent.}
The chain-level descent \(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\) categorifies the
normal-ordered homomorphism
\[
\overline\Pi_X:\widehat\Gamma_X\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T,
\]
of Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}.  For
\(\widehat c=(c,T)\) and \(\widehat c'=(c',T')\),
\[
\overline\Pi_X(\widehat c\star\widehat c')
=\overline\Pi_X(\widehat c)+\overline\Pi_X(\widehat c'),
\]
so the descended bracket is a \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded bracket:
\[
[\widetilde P_{X,\widehat c},\widetilde P_{X,\widehat c'}]
\subset\widetilde P_{X,\widehat c\star\widehat c'}
\xrightarrow{\ \overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\ }
P^{\Pi,\mathrm{raw}}_{X,\overline\Pi_X(\widehat c)+\overline\Pi_X(\widehat c')}.
\]
Equivalently, the raw quadratic shadow
\(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\) has been corrected by the
\(\Theta\)-degree shift before comparison with the denominator algebra.
Each descended homogeneous parity piece is finite dimensional.  The
construction of \((\Theta)\), the orientation datum (O), and the
chain-level Frobenius compatibility is exactly the compact content of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent},
Open Problem~\ref{op:pi-descent-of-bracket}, and
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.

\item[(S2)] \emph{Cartan and root-degree matching.}
There is an even Cartan identification
\[
\iota_H:P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,0}\xrightarrow{\sim}
\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C.
\]
The degree map \(\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}\) identifies the
descended Gram grading with the Gritsenko--Nikulin root grading after
applying \(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\).  The upstairs Hall bracket
remains \(\widehat\Gamma_X\)-graded; only the descended object is
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded.

\item[(S3)] \emph{Simple primitive representatives and parities.}
For every simple-root index \(i\in I\) of
\(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5}\), the compact source supplies parity-homogeneous
primitive representatives
\[
e_i^X\in P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,\alpha_i},\qquad
f_i^X\in P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,-\alpha_i},\qquad
h_i^X\in P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,0}
\]
with \(|e_i^X|=|f_i^X|=p(i)\) and \(h_i^X=\iota_H^{-1}(\alpha_i)\).  The
representatives preserve the real/imaginary distinction, the multiplicity
fibres, and the parity map.  The real representatives for
\(\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\) are even.  For each imaginary simple root
\(a\), the supplied representatives have dimensions
\[
\dim\langle e_i^X:\alpha_i=a,\ p(i)=0\rangle=\mu_{\overline0}(a),
\qquad
\dim\langle e_i^X:\alpha_i=a,\ p(i)=1\rangle=\mu_{\overline1}(a)
\]
with the same convention for the negative representatives.
The negative representatives belong to the supplied BKM double and its
independent negative primitive half.  They are not constructed or tested by
the cusp-positive Pfaffian support residuals of \textup{(D0-Pf)}.

\item[(S4)] \emph{Borcherds--Kac relations in the Hall bracket.}
In the protected Hall/factorization bracket these representatives satisfy
the Borcherds--Kac defining relations for \(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5}\):
\[
[h,h']=0,\qquad
[h,e_i^X]=(h,\alpha_i)e_i^X,\qquad
[h,f_i^X]=-(h,\alpha_i)f_i^X,
\]
\[
[e_i^X,f_j^X]=\delta_{ij}h_i^X,
\]
the real Serre relations
\[
(\operatorname{ad}e_i^X)^{1-2(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)/(\alpha_i,\alpha_i)}
e_j^X=
(\operatorname{ad}f_i^X)^{1-2(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)/(\alpha_i,\alpha_i)}
f_j^X=0
\]
for real \(i\) and \(i\neq j\), the Borcherds orthogonality relations
\[
(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)=0\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
[e_i^X,e_j^X]=[f_i^X,f_j^X]=0,
\]
and the super sign rule.  In the real rank-three subsystem
\((\delta_i,\delta_j)=-2\) for \(i\neq j\), so the real Serre exponent is
\(3\); the first brackets \([e_i^X,e_j^X]\) are not forced to vanish.
For the primitive isotropic simple roots
\[
a_{ij}:=\delta_i+\delta_j,\qquad i<j,
\]
the source representatives
\(u^{+,X}_{ij,r}\in P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,a_{ij}}\) and
\(u^{-,X}_{ij,r}\in P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,-a_{ij}}\),
\(1\le r\le9\), satisfy the orthogonality and Chevalley zero relations
with the two adjacent real roots,
\[
[e_i^X,u^{+,X}_{ij,r}]=[e_j^X,u^{+,X}_{ij,r}]
=[f_i^X,u^{+,X}_{ij,r}]=[f_j^X,u^{+,X}_{ij,r}]=0,
\]
with the analogous negative-root relations, and for the complementary
root \(\{i,j,k\}=\{1,2,3\}\) the real-string relations
\[
(\operatorname{ad}e_k^X)^5u^{+,X}_{ij,r}=0,\qquad
(\operatorname{ad}f_k^X)^5u^{-,X}_{ij,r}=0.
\]
These are relation checks in the compact bracket.  They are not
consequences of the equality \(\sdim=f(nm,l)\).

\item[(S5)] \emph{Completed Hopf pairing and radical quotient.}
The completed Hopf pairing on the positive and negative primitive halves
is continuous for the Hall completion, homogeneous for the
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-grading, invariant for the bracket and
coproduct, and has closed homogeneous radical
\[
\operatorname{Rad}_X
=\{x\mid \langle x,y\rangle_X=0\ \text{for all }y\}
\]
which is a Lie ideal and a coideal.  After quotienting by
\(\overline{\operatorname{Rad}_X}\), the source radical quotient is the
same as the Gritsenko--Nikulin/Kac quotient by
\(\overline{\operatorname{Rad}_{\mathrm{GN}}}\).  Equivalently, on every
finite-height saturated set of roots the positive-negative pairing
matrices have the same parity-block ranks as the target invariant
pairing matrices, their kernels are carried by the transition maps, and
the inverse-limit kernel is exactly \(\operatorname{Rad}_X\).  At every
finite stage one has
\[
[P^\Pi_{R},\operatorname{Rad}_{X,R}]
\subset \operatorname{Rad}_{X,R},
\qquad
\Delta_R(\operatorname{Rad}_{X,R})
\subset
\operatorname{Rad}_{X,R}\otimes P^\Pi_R
+P^\Pi_R\otimes\operatorname{Rad}_{X,R},
\]
and the completed statement is obtained by inverse limit and closure.
The radical rank is computed from these matrices and kernel maps; it is
not read from the signed determinant.  Equality of ranks alone is not a
Hopf quotient theorem without the Lie-ideal, coideal, closedness, and
transition-compatibility assertions.

\item[(S6)] \emph{No extra relations.}
The Hall primitive algebra satisfies a no-extra-relations theorem: if
\[
\pi:\widehat{\mathfrak F}(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})
\longrightarrow P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}
\]
is the continuous map determined by the displayed representatives, then
\[
\ker\pi=
\overline{J_{\mathrm{BK}}+\operatorname{Rad}_{\mathrm{GN}}}.
\]
Equivalently, the induced map
\(G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\to P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}\) is injective.  This
is required finite stage by finite stage: for every saturated finite root
window \(W\), the restricted map \(\pi_W\) has kernel
\[
\ker\pi_W
=
\bigl(\overline{J_{\mathrm{BK}}+\operatorname{Rad}_{\mathrm{GN}}}\bigr)_W
\]
after projection to \(W\), and these kernel identifications commute with
the HN transition maps.  A comparison of signed dimensions or a
determinant identity is not this theorem.

\item[(S7)] \emph{Generation.}
\(P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}\) is topologically generated by
\(P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,0}\) and the simple primitive representatives
\(e_i^X,f_i^X\).

\item[(S8)] \emph{Completed PBW.}
A completed PBW theorem holds for \(P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}\): the PBW
filtration on its enveloping algebra is transported to the PBW filtration
on \(U(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})\), the associated graded finite-height
pieces agree with the target pieces, and the finite-height PBW bases form
a closed inverse system in the chosen completion.  Concretely, for every
finite saturated window \(W\), the associated graded map
\[
\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{PBW}}U(P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}})_W
\longrightarrow
\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{PBW}}U(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})_W
\]
is an isomorphism, the transition maps preserve the PBW filtration
strictly, and inverse limits are taken in the same HN topology as
Definition~\ref{def:normal-ordering-coefficient-dg-category}.  Target PBW
does not transfer to the compact source until these finite-stage
isomorphisms are supplied.

\item[(S9)] \emph{Exact completion.}
The inverse limit is exact on the saturated finite root windows used
above: the transition maps are strict for the HN topology, images are
closed, and passage to the completed quotient by the radical commutes with
finite-window kernels, cokernels, PBW associated gradeds, and root-space
parity pieces.  Equivalently, no new relation, generator, radical element,
or parity-cancelling summand appears only after completion; equivalently,
the relevant \(\lim^1\) terms vanish on these finite root-window
systems.

\item[(S10)] \emph{Full parity dimensions.}
The full root-space parity dimensions in \(P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}\)
agree with those of \(G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\), not only their
differences.  For every nonzero \(\gamma\) with
\(\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R\),
\[
\dim P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,\gamma,\overline p}
=d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{\gamma,\overline p},
\qquad
d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{\gamma,\overline p}
:=\rootmult_{\overline p}(\alpha(\gamma))
\qquad(p=0,1).
\]
Thus the source must match two integers in every root degree; equality of
their difference is not enough.
In the first timelike channel \(\gamma=(1,1,1)\),
Proposition~\ref{prop:delta123-presentation-count} gives
\[
d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{(1,1,1),\overline0}=29,\qquad
d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{(1,1,1),\overline1}=93.
\]
These are presentation-level target dimensions, not an inference from
\(29-93=-64\).
If \(\alpha(\gamma)\) is not a target root and \(\gamma\neq0\), the
corresponding source piece is zero after the radical quotient.  On active
positive Gram degrees this implies
$$
\sdim P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l).
$$
\end{enumerate}
Then
$$
P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}
\cong
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}
=\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}
$$
as Gram-graded Lie superalgebras, and its Weyl--Kac--Borcherds
denominator is \(64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\).  If in addition the chiral
Koszul source certificate of
Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-source-certificate} is supplied,
including the Koszul Mittag--Leffler exactness hypothesis of
Proposition~\ref{prop:chiral-koszul-source-certificate-consequence}, then
$$
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X\simeq\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
$$
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The simple primitive representatives define a continuous homomorphism
$$
\pi:\widehat{\mathfrak F}(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})
\longrightarrow P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}.
$$
\textup{(S1)} and \textup{(S2)} make this a homomorphism of the descended
Gram-graded completions.  \textup{(S3)} fixes the real and imaginary
simple generators with their parities and multiplicity fibres.
\textup{(S4)} puts \(J_{\mathrm{BK}}\) in the kernel.  \textup{(S5)}
identifies the compact Hopf radical with the Gritsenko--Nikulin/Kac
radical, so \(\pi\) descends to
\[
G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\longrightarrow P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}.
\]
\textup{(S7)} gives surjectivity.  \textup{(S6)} gives injectivity after
the completed radical quotient.  \textup{(S8)} gives the PBW-compatible
finite-height identifications, and \textup{(S9)} says that the completed
inverse limit is exact for the kernels, radicals, and PBW associated
gradeds under discussion.  \textup{(S10)} rules out hidden
zero-superdimension root spaces and cancelling ideals invisible to the
determinant.  Hence the descended map
is an isomorphism of Gram-graded Lie superalgebras.  The denominator
statement is
Theorem~\ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}.  The chiral statement is
Proposition~\ref{prop:chiral-koszul-source-certificate-consequence}; it
uses the supplied \(C_X\), \(b_X\), \(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}\), and the
Koszul Mittag--Leffler exactness hypothesis of that proposition, not the
target-internal bar--cobar counit.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Cofinal finite-window primitive-recognition certificate]
\label{def:cofinal-primitive-recognition-certificate}
A finite set \(W\subset Q_+\setminus\{0\}\) is
\emph{downward saturated} if
\[
0<\beta'\leq\beta,\qquad \beta\in W,\qquad
\beta-\beta'\in Q_+
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\beta'\in W .
\]
Thus every positive presentation word whose total degree lies in \(W\)
uses only positive degrees already in \(W\).  For the full BKM double,
each finite certificate below is triangular: positive and negative
letters are separately restricted to \(W_\nu\) and \(-W_\nu\), mixed
Chevalley and pairing checks are made only for the supplied letters in
\(W_\nu\cup(-W_\nu)\cup\{0\}\), and words whose total degree enters the
window only by cancellation are deferred to the exact-completion clause
below.
A cofinal finite-window
primitive-recognition certificate for \(P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}\) is an
increasing sequence of finite downward-saturated windows
\[
W_1\subset W_2\subset\cdots,\qquad
\bigcup_\nu W_\nu=\mathcal R_+,
\]
together with the following finite data for every \(W_\nu\), compatible
under \(W_\nu\subset W_{\nu+1}\).

\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(R1)}] \emph{Representatives and parities.}
All simple-root representatives \(e_i^X,f_i^X,h_i^X\) whose roots lie in
\(W_\nu\) are supplied in the compact source, with the
Gritsenko--Nikulin parity fibres
\(\mu_{\overline0}(a),\mu_{\overline1}(a)\) for imaginary simple roots
and even real representatives for \(\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\).

\item[\textup{(R2)}] \emph{Relations.}
The Cartan, Chevalley, real Serre, Borcherds orthogonality, and super
sign relations are checked for every relation whose displayed source and
target degrees lie in \(W_\nu\cup(-W_\nu)\cup\{0\}\).  Downward
saturation makes this a finite relation check for all positive
presentation words of total degree in \(W_\nu\).

\item[\textup{(R3)}] \emph{Full finite parity dimensions.}
For every \(\beta\in W_\nu\), the compact root space after the source
radical quotient has the two target dimensions
\[
\dim P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,\beta,\overline p}
=\rootmult_{\overline p}^{\mathrm{GN}}(\beta),
\qquad p=0,1,
\]
and the corresponding non-root degrees in the finite test window have
zero source piece.  This is a two-integer equality in each degree, not a
signed-superdimension equality.

\item[\textup{(R4)}] \emph{Hopf pairing and radical.}
The positive-negative pairing matrices between \(W_\nu\) and
\(-W_\nu\) are written in parity blocks.  Their kernels agree with the
Gritsenko--Nikulin/Kac invariant-pairing kernels, are stable under all
finite brackets whose degrees remain in the window, are coideals for the
finite coproduct, and are carried to the next window by the transition
maps.  The inverse-limit radical is the closure of these finite kernels.

\item[\textup{(R5)}] \emph{No extra relations.}
Let
\[
\pi_\nu:\widehat{\mathfrak F}(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})_{\le W_\nu}
\longrightarrow P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,\le W_\nu}
\]
be the finite presentation map obtained by projecting to words whose
letters lie in the triangular finite span generated by
\(W_\nu\cup(-W_\nu)\cup\{0\}\).  The certificate
requires the finite kernel equality
\[
\ker\pi_\nu=
\bigl(\overline{J_{\mathrm{BK}}+\operatorname{Rad}_{\mathrm{GN}}}\bigr)_{\le W_\nu}.
\]
This is the no-extra-relations theorem in finite form.

\item[\textup{(R6)}] \emph{Generation.}
Every source primitive root space in \(W_\nu\cup(-W_\nu)\), after the
finite radical quotient, is generated by the Cartan and the supplied
simple-root representatives through brackets whose intermediate positive
degrees stay in \(W_\nu\).

\item[\textup{(R7)}] \emph{Completed PBW compatibility.}
The PBW filtrations on the finite enveloping spans agree:
\[
\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{PBW}}U(P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}})_{\le W_\nu}
\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{PBW}}U(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})_{\le W_\nu},
\]
and the transition maps \(W_{\nu+1}\to W_\nu\) preserve the filtration
strictly.  The completed PBW statement is the inverse-limit statement for
this compatible finite system.

\item[\textup{(R8)}] \emph{Exact triangular completion.}
Words whose total degree lies in the finite test window only through
positive-negative cancellation are not added as extra finite generators.
They are controlled by exact completion: the transition maps are strict,
images are closed, and passage to the inverse limit commutes with the
finite kernels, cokernels, radicals, PBW associated gradeds, and parity
pieces supplied in \textup{(R3)--(R7)}.  Equivalently, the relevant
\(\lim^1\) terms vanish for these triangular finite-window systems.
\end{enumerate}
The certificate is finite at each \(\nu\), but it is not numerical: it
contains representatives, relation verifications, pairing matrices,
kernel equalities, and PBW transition data.  The Borcherds product and
the OP scalar square provide none of these source-side objects.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Global recognition is exactly the cofinal certificate]
\label{prop:global-recognition-cofinal-certificate}
Assume \textup{(S1)}--\textup{(S4)} of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.  Then the remaining global
source-side assertions \textup{(S5)}--\textup{(S10)} are supplied by a
