cofinal finite-window primitive-recognition certificate in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:cofinal-primitive-recognition-certificate}.  Under
that certificate,
\[
P_X^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}\cong\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}
\]
as completed Gram-graded Lie superalgebras.  Conversely, any proposed
global proof of this isomorphism, with the chosen
Gritsenko--Nikulin presentation and source Hopf pairing, must restrict to
such finite certificates on every downward-saturated window.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For a fixed \(W_\nu\), \textup{(R1)} and \textup{(R2)} define the finite
presentation map and put the Borcherds--Kac relation ideal in its kernel.
\textup{(R4)} identifies the compact finite Hopf radical with the target
radical and makes the quotient a finite Hopf Lie-superalgebra quotient.
\textup{(R5)} gives injectivity of the induced target map on the window,
while \textup{(R6)} gives surjectivity.  Thus the source and target
primitive Lie superalgebras agree on \(W_\nu\).

\textup{(R3)} rules out zero-superdimension source summands and wrong
parity lifts invisible to the determinant.  \textup{(R7)} says that the
finite isomorphisms are compatible with PBW associated gradeds and with
the chosen HN/window transition maps.  \textup{(R8)} is the exact
triangular completion clause.  Since the windows are cofinal and
the radical in \textup{(R4)} is the closure of the finite kernels, passing
to the inverse limit gives \textup{(S5)}--\textup{(S10)} and hence the
isomorphism of Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.

The converse is restriction: a completed isomorphism preserving the
chosen representatives, presentation map, Hopf pairing, radical quotient,
and PBW filtration yields the displayed finite representatives, kernels,
pairing matrices, parity dimensions, and PBW maps after projection to
each \(W_\nu\).  If these finite objects are not produced, the claim is
only a determinant or character comparison.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Low-degree bracket information]
\label{prop:low-degree-denominator-brackets}
The denominator algebra gives the following target-side low-degree checks.
With
$$
\alpha(n,l,m)=n\delta_1+m\delta_2+(n+m-l)\delta_3,
$$
the active positive rows through height three are
$$
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c}
\operatorname{ht}\beta & \beta & \gamma(\beta) & (\beta,\beta) &
\smult(\beta)\\ \hline
1&\delta_1&(1,1,0)&2&1\\
1&\delta_2&(0,1,1)&2&1\\
1&\delta_3&(0,-1,0)&2&1\\
2&\delta_1+\delta_2&(1,2,1)&0&10\\
2&\delta_1+\delta_3&(1,0,0)&0&10\\
2&\delta_2+\delta_3&(0,0,1)&0&10\\
3&2\delta_1+\delta_2&(2,3,1)&2&1\\
3&\delta_1+2\delta_2&(1,3,2)&2&1\\
3&2\delta_1+\delta_3&(2,1,0)&2&1\\
3&\delta_1+2\delta_3&(1,-1,0)&2&1\\
3&2\delta_2+\delta_3&(0,1,2)&2&1\\
3&\delta_2+2\delta_3&(0,-1,1)&2&1\\
3&\delta_1+\delta_2+\delta_3&(1,1,1)&-6&-64 .
\end{array}
$$
After choosing even Chevalley generators \(e_i,f_i,h_i\) for the real
simple roots and setting
\[
A_{ij}=(\delta_i,\delta_j),\qquad
E_{ij}:=[e_i,e_j]\quad(i\ne j),
\]
so \(E_{ji}=-E_{ij}\), one has
$$
[h_i,h_j]=0,\qquad
[h_i,e_j]=A_{ij}e_j,\qquad
[h_i,f_j]=-A_{ij}f_j,\qquad
[e_i,f_j]=\delta_{ij}h_i,
$$
and
$$
(\operatorname{ad}e_i)^3e_j=0\quad(i\ne j).
$$
If \(\{i,j,k\}=\{1,2,3\}\), then
$$
[h_i,E_{ij}]=[h_j,E_{ij}]=0,\qquad [h_k,E_{ij}]=-4E_{ij},
$$
$$
[f_i,E_{ij}]=2e_j,\qquad [f_j,E_{ij}]=-2e_i,\qquad
[f_k,E_{ij}]=0.
$$
For ordered \(i\ne j\), put \(E_{iij}:=[e_i,E_{ij}]\).  Then
$$
[e_i,E_{iij}]=0,\qquad
[f_i,E_{iij}]=2E_{ij},\qquad
[f_j,E_{iij}]=0.
$$
For \(i<j\), the isotropic primitive degree
\(a_{ij}:=\delta_i+\delta_j\) has
\[
\smult(a_{ij})=10=1+9:
\]
one even real-real commutator direction \(E_{ij}\) and nine even
Gritsenko--Nikulin isotropic simple directions
\[
u_{ij,1},\ldots,u_{ij,9}\in\mathfrak g_{a_{ij}},
\qquad \tau(ta_{ij})=9\quad(t\ge1).
\]
The orthogonality relations give
\[
[e_i,u_{ij,r}]=[e_j,u_{ij,r}]=0,\qquad
[f_i,u_{ij,r}]=[f_j,u_{ij,r}]=0.
\]
Thus the target splits the signed multiplicity \(10\) at \(a_{ij}\) into
one real-real commutator direction and nine isotropic simple directions.
A compact source must realize this splitting by actual protected Hall
primitives; the equality \(\sdim=10\) alone does not choose the
summands or the orthogonality constants.
In degree \(\delta_{123}:=\delta_1+\delta_2+\delta_3\), the real
bracketings
\[
T_1=[e_1,E_{23}],\qquad
T_2=[e_2,E_{31}],\qquad
T_3=[e_3,E_{12}]
\]
satisfy \(T_1+T_2+T_3=0\).  The brackets
\([e_k,u_{ij,r}]\in\mathfrak g_{\delta_{123}}\) for
\(\{i,j,k\}=\{1,2,3\}\) are not numerical constants until a basis and
parity split of \(\mathfrak g_{\delta_{123}}\) are chosen.  Since
\((\delta_k,a_{ij})=-4\), the same Borcherds--Kac presentation also
imposes the real-string relation
\[
(\operatorname{ad}e_k)^5u_{ij,r}=0
\]
and the analogous relation for the negative generators.  The first
bracket \([e_k,u_{ij,r}]\) is only the first visible map in this string.
The product exponent alone gives only
\[
\smult(\delta_{123})=f(1,1)=-64.
\]
Let
\[
d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{p,123}:=\rootmult_{\overline p}(\delta_{123}),
\qquad p=0,1.
\]
Then
\[
d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{0,123}-d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{1,123}=-64,
\]
but the product exponent alone does not give the two integers
\(d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{0,123}\), \(d^{\mathrm{GN}}_{1,123}\), the bracket
coordinates, or the radical.  Proposition~\ref{prop:delta123-presentation-count}
computes the target presentation values \(29\) and \(93\) from the
Weyl-sum coefficient and the Borcherds--Kac presentation; the compact
source must still reproduce them by protected primitives and the Hopf
pairing.
The first unresolved compact test channel is therefore the following:
produce parity-homogeneous compact primitives
\[
v^{\overline0}_1,\ldots,v^{\overline0}_{29},
\qquad
v^{\overline1}_1,\ldots,v^{\overline1}_{93},
\]
in the descended degree \((1,1,1)\), compute the Hall constants
\[
[e_k^X,u^X_{ij,r}]
=\sum_{a=1}^{29}
C^{\overline0}_{k;ijr,a}v^{\overline0}_a,
\qquad \{i,j,k\}=\{1,2,3\},
\]
the Jacobi relation \(T_1^X+T_2^X+T_3^X=0\), the real-string relations
\((\operatorname{ad}e_k^X)^5u^X_{ij,r}=0\), the completed Hopf-pairing
matrix between degrees \(\delta_{123}\) and \(-\delta_{123}\), with
even block size \(29\) and odd block size \(93\), and the closed radical
quotient of Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.  The
bracket above is even, but the odd basis is still load-bearing: it is
part of the full parity-dimension, PBW, and radical comparison.  This
channel is the first place where the compact Hall source must supply more
than the GN signed multiplicity.
These are denominator-algebra constants.  They are not compact Hall
constants.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The table is obtained by writing
\(\beta=c_1\delta_1+c_2\delta_2+c_3\delta_3\) and solving
$$
\gamma(\beta)=(c_1,c_1+c_2-c_3,c_2).
$$
Then \((\beta,\beta)=-2(4nm-l^2)\), and
\(\smult(\beta)=f(nm,l)\) follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}.  The displayed bracket
constants are the normalized Chevalley, Jacobi and Serre constants for
the symmetric Cartan matrix \(A=((\delta_i,\delta_j))\).  The signs
\(E_{ji}=-E_{ij}\), \([f_i,E_{ij}]=2e_j\), and
\([f_j,E_{ij}]=-2e_i\) follow from the graded Jacobi identity and the
normalization \([e_i,f_i]=h_i\).  The relation
\(T_1+T_2+T_3=0\) is the ordinary Jacobi identity for the even real
generators \(e_1,e_2,e_3\).  For
\(a_{ij}=\delta_i+\delta_j\) and \(\{i,j,k\}=\{1,2,3\}\), one has
\((\delta_k,a_{ij})=-4\), hence the real Borcherds--Kac Serre exponent is
\(1-2(\delta_k,a_{ij})/(\delta_k,\delta_k)=5\).  The equality
\(\tau(ta_{ij})=9\) on primitive isotropic rays is the
Gritsenko--Nikulin isotropic simple-root datum recorded above.  No compact
Hall structure constant is inferred: a compact computation would have to
construct the relevant extension correspondences, protected primitive
bases, orientation signs, the \(\delta_{123}\) channel constants, and the
radical quotient.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The determinant does not determine compact Hall constants]
\label{prop:determinant-does-not-determine-hall-constants}
The scalar OP square, the Borcherds product for \(\Delta_5\), and the
Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator algebra determine the visible signed
exponents
\[
\smult(\alpha)
=\dim\mathfrak g_{\alpha,\overline0}
-\dim\mathfrak g_{\alpha,\overline1}.
\]
They do not determine a compact Hall bracket, compact primitive
representatives, full source parity dimensions, the positive-negative
Hopf pairing, its closed radical quotient, the no-extra-relations theorem,
or completed PBW compatibility.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
A \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded super vector space with the same
signed dimensions gives the same determinant.  Adding a cancelling pair
\(W_\gamma\oplus\Pi W_\gamma\) in any active degree leaves every signed
exponent unchanged, while changing the full parity dimensions.  Equipping
the same graded vector space with the zero bracket also leaves the
determinant unchanged, but it cannot be the denominator algebra because
the target has nonzero real-root brackets, for example
\([e_i,e_j]\neq0\) for \(i\neq j\), and the first timelike channel
requires the \(29|93\) presentation split of
Proposition~\ref{prop:delta123-presentation-count}.  A compact Hall
realization must therefore construct extension correspondences,
orientation signs, protected primitive bases, Hall structure constants,
pairing matrices, radical kernels, and PBW finite-window isomorphisms.
The determinant is a necessary decategorified shadow of these data, not a
source for them.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[First timelike presentation count]
\label{prop:delta123-presentation-count}
Let
\[
\delta_{123}:=\delta_1+\delta_2+\delta_3
=2f_2-f_3+2f_{-2}.
\]
In the Gritsenko--Nikulin additive correction coefficient one has
\[
m(\delta_{123})=-93.
\]
Consequently the target denominator algebra has full parity dimensions
\[
\rootmult_{\overline0}(\delta_{123})=29,\qquad
\rootmult_{\overline1}(\delta_{123})=93.
\]
The \(29\) even directions are the two real-real-real
Borcherds--Kac presentation words
\[
T_1=[e_1,[e_2,e_3]],\qquad
T_2=[e_2,[e_3,e_1]],\qquad
T_3=[e_3,[e_1,e_2]],\qquad T_1+T_2+T_3=0,
\]
together with the \(27\) mixed real-isotropic words
\[
[e_k,u_{ij,r}],\qquad \{i,j,k\}=\{1,2,3\},\quad 1\le r\le9.
\]
The \(93\) odd directions are the negative-norm imaginary simple
generators in degree \(\delta_{123}\).  This is a target-side
presentation count.  It is not a compact Hall computation and is not
deduced from the signed equality \(29-93=-64\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The root \(\delta_{123}\) corresponds in the notation of the Weyl-sum
coefficient formula to
\[
\delta_{123}=(3-1)f_2-\frac{3-1}{2}f_3+(3-1)f_{-2}.
\]
Hence \(m(\delta_{123})=-64^{-1}c_\Delta(3,3,3)\).  After removing the
leading monomial from \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\),
\[
D_5
=q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)},
\]
the finite coefficient calculation in \(q\)- and \(s\)-degree one gives
\[
\left[qrs\right]
\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=93.
\]
Explicitly, only the \(q\)-linear, \(s\)-linear, and \(qs\)-linear
factors enter.  With
\[
A(r)=1-r^{-1},\qquad
B(r)=-(r^{-1}+10+r),
\]
\[
C(r)=-10r^{-2}+64r^{-1}-108+64r-10r^2,
\]
one has
\[
\left[qrs\right]
\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=[r]\ A(r)\bigl(B(r)^2+C(r)\bigr)
\]
and
\[
A(r)\bigl(B(r)^2+C(r)\bigr)
=9r^{-3}-93r^{-2}+90r^{-1}-90+93r-9r^2.
\]
Equivalently \(c_\Delta(3,3,3)=64\cdot93\), so
\(m(\delta_{123})=-93\).  Since this coefficient is negative, the
Gritsenko--Nikulin parity convention makes these \(93\) simple
generators odd.

It remains to count the lower presentation words in the same total
degree.  The multidegree \((1,1,1)\) part of the free Lie algebra on the
three even real generators has dimension \(2\); the three displayed
bracketings satisfy exactly the Jacobi relation
\(T_1+T_2+T_3=0\).  For each primitive isotropic root
\(a_{ij}=\delta_i+\delta_j\), the Gritsenko--Nikulin isotropic
multiplicity is \(\tau(a_{ij})=9\), and the complementary real root
\(\delta_k\) has \((\delta_k,a_{ij})=-4\).  Thus the first mixed
brackets \([e_k,u_{ij,r}]\) are allowed presentation words; the
orthogonality relations kill only the adjacent brackets with
\(\delta_i\) and \(\delta_j\), and the real-string relation occurs first
at \((\operatorname{ad}e_k)^5u_{ij,r}\).  There are
\(3\cdot9=27\) such even words.  No other simple-root decomposition has
total degree \(\delta_{123}\).  The Borcherds--Kac presentation and PBW
therefore give \(2+27=29\) even and \(93\) odd target directions in this
degree.  Their signed difference is
\[
29-93=-64=f(1,1),
\]
which checks the denominator exponent but does not determine the compact
source parity split, bracket constants, pairing matrix, or radical
quotient.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[First saturated primitive-recognition window]
\label{prop:first-saturated-primitive-recognition-window}
Let
\[
W_{\le3}:=
\left\{
\beta=c_1\delta_1+c_2\delta_2+c_3\delta_3\in\mathcal R_+
\;:\;
c_i\ge0,\quad 1\le c_1+c_2+c_3\le3
\right\}.
\]
This is the first downward-saturated finite target window containing the
real simple roots, the primitive isotropic simple-root fibres, and the
first timelike degree.  In \(G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\) the full
parity dimensions in this window are
\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\beta & \rootmult_{\overline0}(\beta) &
\rootmult_{\overline1}(\beta)\\ \hline
\delta_i\ (1\le i\le3) & 1&0\\
\delta_i+\delta_j\ (i<j) & 10&0\\
2\delta_i+\delta_j\ (i\ne j) & 1&0\\
\delta_{123} & 29&93 .
\end{array}
\]
The parity entries use the imported Gritsenko--Nikulin/Kac parity
convention; the target computation checks signed coefficients and
presentation counts, not source parity bases.
Consequently a compact source passes primitive recognition on
\(W_{\le3}\) only after supplying the following finite certificate:
parity-homogeneous representatives with the displayed dimensions; the
Chevalley, real-Serre, orthogonality, and super-sign relations restricted
to \(W_{\le3}\); the Jacobi relation
\[
T_1^X+T_2^X+T_3^X=0;
\]
the \(27\) mixed maps \([e_k^X,u^X_{ij,r}]\) into the even
\(\delta_{123}\)-block; positive-negative Hopf-pairing matrices in every
degree of \(W_{\le3}\) with closed radical kernels stable under the
finite transition maps; the finite kernel equality
\[
\ker\pi_{W_{\le3}}
=
\bigl(\overline{J_{\mathrm{BK}}+\operatorname{Rad}_{\mathrm{GN}}}
\bigr)_{W_{\le3}};
\]
and the associated-graded PBW isomorphism on the truncated enveloping
algebras.  If this finite certificate is supplied, the restricted map
\[
G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})_{W_{\le3}}
\longrightarrow
P^{\Pi,\mathrm{red}}_{X,W_{\le3}}
\]
is an isomorphism of finite Gram-graded Lie superalgebras.  Without the
kernel equality, the Hopf-radical ideal/coideal assertion, and the PBW
associated-graded isomorphism, equality of the displayed dimensions is
not recognition.

The next coefficient checks already lie outside this window.  The exact
finite product computation in \texttt{compute/verify\_square\_root.py}
is target-only: it verifies Borcherds/Gritsenko--Nikulin arithmetic, not
compact Hall representatives, Hopf-pairing matrices, coproduct matrices,
or radical kernels.  It gives
\[
[q^2r^2s]\frac{D_5}{(qrs)^{1/2}}
=[qr^2s^2]\frac{D_5}{(qrs)^{1/2}}
=[qs]\frac{D_5}{(qrs)^{1/2}}
=-90,
\]
and
\[
[q^2r^2s^2]\frac{D_5}{(qrs)^{1/2}}=540.
\]
Thus the Gritsenko--Nikulin additive coefficients are
\[
m(2\delta_1+\delta_2+\delta_3)
=m(\delta_1+2\delta_2+\delta_3)
=m(\delta_1+\delta_2+2\delta_3)=90,
\]
\[
m(2\delta_{123})=-540.
\]
These are target simple-root coefficients.  They do not count the lower
PBW words in those degrees and do not supply compact Hall representatives,
pairing matrices, radicals, or no-extra-relations data.

The first obstruction to extending the displayed finite recognition
statement from \(W_{\le3}\) to height four is already numerical.  The
full signed target root supermultiplicities in the three height-four
timelike degrees are
\[
\smult(2\delta_1+\delta_2+\delta_3)
=\smult(\delta_1+2\delta_2+\delta_3)
=\smult(\delta_1+\delta_2+2\delta_3)=108,
\]
whereas the new negative-norm simple-root coefficients in those same
degrees are \(90\).  Thus each of these degrees carries a signed
height-four residual
\[
108-90=18
\]
coming from lower presentation words after the Borcherds--Kac relations
and radical quotient are imposed.  This number is a signed residual, not
a count of compact PBW basis vectors.  It says precisely that the
height-four window cannot be certified by appending the additive
coefficients alone.

The same phenomenon is visible on the doubled isotropic boundary rays:
for \(i<j\),
\[
\smult(2\delta_i+2\delta_j)=10,\qquad
\tau(2(\delta_i+\delta_j))=9,
\]
so the signed non-simple residual is \(1\) on each doubled isotropic
ray.  These doubled-ray checks test the isotropic multiplicity
convention \(\tau(t(\delta_i+\delta_j))=9\) against the product
exponents; they do not identify compact primitives.

The height-four real-string obstruction is also explicit.  If
\(w_s\), \(1\le s\le93\), denotes an odd negative-norm simple generator
in degree \(\delta_{123}\), then
\[
(\delta_i,\delta_{123})=-2,\qquad
1-2(\delta_i,\delta_{123})/(\delta_i,\delta_i)=3,
\]
and the target presentation contains
\[
(\operatorname{ad}e_i)^3w_s=0,\qquad
(\operatorname{ad}f_i)^3w_s^-=0.
\]
The first brackets \([e_i,w_s]\) land in the three height-four timelike
degrees above and are odd.  A height-four compact recognition certificate
must therefore supply those odd maps, the even simple generators of
multiplicity \(90\), the lower-word relations producing the signed
residual \(18\), the positive-negative pairing matrices, the radical
kernels, and PBW associated-graded compatibility.  Dimension equality
alone still does not prove recognition.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The table is exactly the target data of
Propositions~\ref{prop:low-degree-denominator-brackets} and
\ref{prop:delta123-presentation-count}: the three real simple roots are
even one-dimensional, each primitive isotropic degree has one real-real
commutator and nine even isotropic simple directions, the six height-three
real roots are even one-dimensional, and
\(\delta_{123}\) has presentation dimensions \(29|93\).  The finite
certificate is the restriction of clauses \textup{(S3)}--\textup{(S10)} of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition} to the downward-saturated window
\(W_{\le3}\).  The same proof as the theorem then gives the restricted
isomorphism.  The height-four additive coefficients are computed from the
monic Borcherds product and converted to Gritsenko--Nikulin \(m(a)\) by
the coefficient formula \(m(a)=-64^{-1}c_\Delta(n,l,m)\) of
\cite[Theorem~2.1]{GN}; the script performs this conversion with
\(\alpha(n,l,m)=n\delta_1+m\delta_2+(n+m-l)\delta_3\).  The full signed
height-four target multiplicities are read from the same denominator
theorem:
\[
\smult(\beta)=f(nm,l)
\quad\hbox{for}\quad
\gamma(\beta)=(n,l,m).
\]
For
\(\beta=2\delta_1+\delta_2+\delta_3,\delta_1+2\delta_2+\delta_3,
\delta_1+\delta_2+2\delta_3\) this gives respectively
\((n,l,m)=(2,2,1),(1,2,2),(1,0,1)\), hence the coefficients
\(f(2,2)=108,f(2,2)=108,f(1,0)=108\).  Subtracting the additive
coefficients \(90\) gives the displayed signed residual \(18\).
For the doubled isotropic degrees \(2(\delta_i+\delta_j)\), the
denominator exponent is \(f(4,4)=f(0,0)=10\) in the three symmetric
chambers, while the isotropic simple-root multiplicity is the
Gritsenko--Nikulin constant \(\tau(2(\delta_i+\delta_j))=9\).  Finally,
the real-string exponents follow directly from the Gram matrix:
\((\delta_i,\delta_{123})=-2\), \((\delta_i,\delta_i)=2\), and therefore
the exponent is \(3\).  All displayed numerical checks are asserted in
\texttt{compute/verify\_square\_root.py}.
\end{proof}

\begin{openproblem}[State-side construction of \(D_0\) and the
Dirac--Igusa certificate]
\label{op:compact-igusa-realization}
Construct first the \(D_0\)-certificate of
Definition~\ref{def:first-order-d0-certificate}, and then the full
certificate \(\mathfrak K_X\) of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum}.  The exact open
obligations are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(open \(D_0\)-state)}] construct, for every
\(R\in\mathcal R\), the finite Hall source kernel
\(\mathfrak S_R\) of
Definition~\ref{def:finite-hall-source-kernel}, so that
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-d0-hall-source-construction} produces the
finite state object \(\mathcal H_R^{or}\), pull-push Hall product,
coproduct, primitive bracket, normal-ordered primitive algebra, and
finite CE differential.  Then construct the full finite stage
\(D_{0,R}\) on \(\widehat\Gamma_R\), equivalently the finite
Hall--Dirac atlas \(\mathfrak A_R\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-d0-atlas-parity-obstruction}, including the
Dirac complex, source observable shadow, Pfaffian square, compact parity
lifts, protected integration, and successor transition maps with
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{atlas}}_{R^+R}=
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tr}}_{R^+R}=0\), whose composites give the
non-successor transitions and whose inverse limit is
\(\widehat{\mathcal H}^{or}_{\sigma,S}\);
\item[\textup{(open \(D_0\)-quotient)}] compute and trivialize the reduced
orientation and quotient obstruction tuple
\(\mathfrak o^{or}_{R,\mathcal C}\) for every stable charge stratum and
finite stabilizer appearing at height \(R\), including the zero
\(H^1(BE[N];\mathbb F_2)\)-linearization characters after finite gerbe
null-trivialization, compatibly in \(R\);
\item[\textup{(open \(D_0\)-observable)}] construct the chain-level
\(K3\)-to-\(E\) specialization, the projection-finite chiral shadow, and
the hybrid wrapped sector \(\mathcal F_X^{D_0}\) that recovers positive
elliptic degree before quotienting by translation in \(E\), together with
a source-to-target finite comparison map satisfying
\(\mathfrak o^{obs}_R=0\) on \(\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test}}\);
\item[\textup{(open \(D_0\)-descent)}] construct the finite-topology,
Hochschild, triple-coherence, Jacobi, Frobenius, negative-cyclic, and
Hopf-radical ideal/coideal cochains
\(\Theta_{\Pi,R}\), \(\Theta_{\Pi,R}^{-}\) with
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{top}}_{\Theta,R^+R}=
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Hoch}}_{\Theta,R}=
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{tri}}_{\Theta,R}=
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{Jac}}_{\Theta,R}=
\mathfrak o_{F,R}=
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{cyc}}_{\Theta,R}=
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{rad}}_{\Theta,R}=0,
\]
giving exact compatibility with the normal-ordered homomorphism
\(\overline\Pi_X\) on primitive brackets, equivalently the finite
diagrams \textup{(NO1)--(NO7)} of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-normal-ordering-verification-diagrams}, with
compatibility against the Hopf radical quotients at every transition.
The Picard and finite-fibre subclaims are reduced to
Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-picard-normal-ordering-lift}; the surviving
geometric work is exactly the cyclic/flag/Frobenius/Hopf-adjointness
package of
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-normal-ordering-closure-criterion};
\item[\textup{(open \(D_0\)-Pfaffian)}] construct the Pfaffian line and
finite first-order operator/algebra \(\mathfrak D_{X,R}\) on the reduced
compact quotient
\(\mathfrak Q_R=(\mathfrak M_R/E)^{\mathrm{red}}\), compatible under
\(R^+\to R\), including a trivialization of the Pfaffian square-root
torsor in \(\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak Q_R)[2]\), with compact parity
lifts \(\ell_R(\gamma)\in\mathscr P_R(\gamma)\) on every
\(\gamma\in\Gamma_R^{\mathrm{test},+}\) satisfying
\[
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{supp}}_{R,\gamma}=0,\qquad
\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{par}}_{R,\gamma}=0,
\]
including absence of actual primitive support in target-zero degrees,
coverage of every nonzero Borcherds target degree in the exhausting
windows \(\Gamma_{\Delta,R}\), finite Pfaffian square
\(\mathscr L_{\mathrm{Pf},R}^{\otimes2}\simeq\mathscr L_{\det,R}\),
and normalized leading coefficient \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{lead}}_R=0\).
Negative representatives are supplied only in the primitive-recognition
certificate, through the full positive-negative pairing and Chevalley
data.
The minimal target-window parity model
\(\mathsf P^{\min}_{\Delta,R}\) is already constructed in
Proposition~\ref{prop:cofinal-target-window-parity-model}; the open
compact task is to identify it, or a non-minimal lift in
\(\mathscr P_R(\gamma)\), with actual source primitive spaces and to
prove the no-hidden-cancellation condition if the minimal lift is used;
\item[\textup{(open full certificate)}] construct the strong
orientation monodromy and the chiral Koszul source certificate
\[
\mathfrak K^{\mathrm{Kos}}_{X,R}
=(\mathcal F_{X,\sigma,S,\le R}^{\mathrm{hyb}},C_{X,R},
F^{\mathrm{co}}_{R,\bullet},\Delta_R^{\mathrm{ch}},
b_{X,R},\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R})
\]
of Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-source-certificate}, with
\[
\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{Kos},R}=0
\]
compatibly in \(R\), together with the Koszul
\(R^1\varprojlim=0\) condition for the source coalgebras, completed
bar/cobar systems, target truncations, and cones of \(b_{X,R}\) and
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos},R}\), including
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}=0\) for the hybrid source.  Equivalently,
construct the full finite local/wrapped correspondence atlas, the
properness/admissibility residuals for its pull-push operations, the
quotient-after-correspondence functor, protected integration, the
conilpotent compact source coalgebra, the finite conilpotent filtration,
the source collision coproduct with finite coassociativity, counit, and
transition-continuity diagrams, the bar comparison to
\(\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}})\), and the cobar
quasi-isomorphism to \(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\), rather than using the
target-internal bar--cobar counit.  The cobar residual includes both the
source-internal bar--cobar admissibility
\(\mathfrak o^{\varepsilon,\mathrm{src}}_R\) and the source-to-target
quasi-isomorphism defect \(\mathfrak o^\vartheta_R\).  The residual
components \(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{hyb}}_R\) and
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{sep}}_R\) record, respectively, the finite hybrid
construction and this source/target separation.
Then construct the compact Hall bracket constants, the simple primitive
representatives, the
Borcherds--Kac relation verification, the full compact parity
dimensions, the completed Hopf pairing with its closed radical quotient,
the no-extra-relations theorem, and completed PBW compatibility of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}; equivalently, construct the
cofinal finite-window certificate of
Definition~\ref{def:cofinal-primitive-recognition-certificate}.  The
first finite bracket test is
the \(\delta_1+\delta_2+\delta_3\) channel of
Propositions~\ref{prop:low-degree-denominator-brackets} and
\ref{prop:delta123-presentation-count}: the signed dimension \(-64\)
must be refined to compact \(29|93\) bases, parity split, structure
constants, Jacobi/Serre checks, pairing matrices, and radical quotient.
\end{enumerate}
The proved lattice normal-ordering theorem and the imported denominator
algebra are inputs to this problem.  The scalar square is an
orientation-forgetful check.  None of the three constructs the compact
state-side certificate.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{definition}[Imaginary simple roots]
\label{def:imaginary-simple-roots}
For $a\in \La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}$ set
$$
\mu_{\overline 0}(a)=
\begin{cases}
m(a),& (a,a)<0\ \text{and}\ m(a)>0,\\
\tau(a),& (a,a)=0\ \text{and}\ \tau(a)>0,\\
0,&\text{otherwise},
\end{cases}
$$
and
$$
\mu_{\overline 1}(a)=
\begin{cases}
-m(a),& (a,a)<0\ \text{and}\ m(a)<0,\\
-\tau(a),& (a,a)=0\ \text{and}\ \tau(a)<0,\\
0,&\text{otherwise}.
\end{cases}
$$
This sign split is the Gritsenko--Nikulin BKM parity datum.  The
product statement alone fixes only a Grothendieck representative for the
signed exponent.  Define multisets by
multiplicity:
$$a\in\Delta_{\overline0}^{im}\quad\hbox{with multiplicity }
\mu_{\overline0}(a),$$
$$a\in\Delta_{\overline1}^{im}\quad\hbox{with multiplicity }
\mu_{\overline1}(a).$$
Put
$$\Delta^{im}=\Delta_{\overline0}^{im}\cup\Delta_{\overline1}^{im}.$$
$$\mathcal O_{\mathrm{den}}^{im}
=\bigoplus_{a\in\Delta^{im}}
\left(\mathfrak g_{a,\overline0}\ominus\mathfrak g_{a,\overline1}\right).$$
This is notation inside the denominator algebra; it is not a BPS state
space.
\end{definition}
The real simple roots are
$$\Delta_{\overline0}^{re,\mathrm{simp}}
=\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}=\Poly_{II,prim}
=\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\},\qquad
\Delta_{\overline1}^{re,\mathrm{simp}}=\varnothing.$$
Put
$$\Delta_{\overline p}=\Delta_{\overline p}^{re,\mathrm{simp}}\cup
\Delta_{\overline p}^{im}\qquad(p=0,1),\qquad
\Delta=\Delta_{\overline0}\cup\Delta_{\overline1}.$$
The Cartan data satisfy $(\alpha,\alpha)>0$ for
$\alpha \in \Delta^{re}$, $(\alpha,\alpha)\leq 0$ for
$\alpha \in \Delta^{im}$, and
$(\alpha,\alpha')\leq 0$ for all distinct $\alpha,\alpha'\in\Delta$.
If $(\alpha,\alpha)>0$, then
$$2\frac{(\alpha,\alpha')}{(\alpha,\alpha)} \in \Z,$$
since $(\alpha,\alpha)=2$ and
$\La^{2,1}_{II}=\Z\delta_1+\Z\delta_2+\Z\delta_3$.
\begin{definition}[Generators and relations]
Let $I$ be an index set equipped with a parity map $p:I\to\Z/2\Z$ and a
root map $i\mapsto\alpha_i\in\Delta$, with fibres over an imaginary root
of cardinality $\mu_{\overline p}(a)$ in parity $p$.  If
$i\neq j$ and $\alpha_i=\alpha_j$, the two indices are distinct simple
roots.
$$\operatorname{ch}:I\rightarrow\La^{2,1}_{II},\qquad
i\mapsto\alpha_i.$$
The superalgebra $\autcor$ is generated by
$$h_i,\ e_i,\ f_i,\qquad i\in I.$$
The Cartan subalgebra is identified with $\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C$ by
$h_i\mapsto\alpha_i$.  Relations:

\begin{itemize}
\item $[h_i,e_j]=(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)e_j$ and
$[h_i,f_j]=-(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)f_j$
\item $[e_i,f_j]=\delta_{ij}h_i$
\item if $\alpha_i \in \Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}$ and $i\neq j$, then
$$
(\operatorname{ad} e_i)^{1-2(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)/(\alpha_i,\alpha_i)}
e_j=
(\operatorname{ad} f_i)^{1-2(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)/(\alpha_i,\alpha_i)}
f_j=0
$$
\item if $(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)=0$, then $[e_i,e_j]=[f_i,f_j]=0$
\end{itemize}
\end{definition}

The grading is by $\La^{2,1}_{II}$.  Put
$$Q_+=\sum_{\alpha\in\Delta}\Z_{\geq0}\alpha
\subset\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
The triangular decomposition is
$$\autcor =
\left(\bigoplus_{\alpha \in Q_+\setminus\{0\}}
\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha}\right)
\oplus(\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C)
\oplus
\left(\bigoplus_{\alpha \in Q_+\setminus\{0\}}
\mathfrak{g}_{-\alpha}\right).$$
For $i\in I$,
$$\deg e_i=\alpha_i,\qquad \deg f_i=-\alpha_i,\qquad \deg h_i=0.$$
$$[\mathfrak g_\alpha,\mathfrak g_\beta]\subset
\mathfrak g_{\alpha+\beta}.$$
$$\mathfrak{g}_0=\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C.$$
The positive and negative roots are
$$\mathcal R_+=\{\alpha\in Q_+\setminus\{0\}\mid
\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha}\neq0\},\qquad
\mathcal R_-=-\mathcal R_+.$$
For every root $\alpha$, set
$$\rootmult_{\overline{0}}(\alpha)
=\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha,\overline{0}},\qquad
\rootmult_{\overline{1}}(\alpha)
=\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha,\overline{1}}.$$
The signed root superdimension is
$$\smult(\alpha)=\rootmult_{\overline{0}}(\alpha)
-\rootmult_{\overline{1}}(\alpha).$$
The Weyl--Kac--Borcherds denominator is
$$
\begin{aligned}
\Phi_{\Delta_5}(z)
&=\sum_{w\in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}\det(w)
\left(
e^{-2\pi i(w(\rho),z)}
-\sum_{a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}}
m(a)e^{-2\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)}
\right)\\
&=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\right)^{\smult(\alpha)}.
\end{aligned}
$$
$$\Omega(\La^{2,1}_{II})
=\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\R+i\Cone(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+.$$

\begin{theorem}[Denominator identity]
$$\frac{1}{64}\Delta_5(2Z)=\Phi_{\Delta_5}(z).$$
$$\operatorname{den}(\autcor)=\frac1{64}\Delta_5(2Z).$$
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
$$\frac1{64}\Delta_5(Z)
=\sum_{w\in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}\det(w)
\left(
e^{-\pi i(w(\rho),z)}
-\sum_{a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}}
m(a)e^{-\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)}
\right).$$
$$Z\mapsto2Z:\qquad
e^{-\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)}
\mapsto e^{-2\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)}.$$
Weyl--Kac--Borcherds:
$$e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\right)^{\smult(\alpha)}.$$
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Gram-index cone and denominator cone]
$$\alpha(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}})
=\{\alpha(n,l,m)\mid(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}},\ f(nm,l)\neq0\}
\subset\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
$$
\alpha(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}})
\subset
\mathcal R_+^{\mathrm{vis}}
:=\{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+\mid \smult(\alpha)\neq0\}.
$$
$$\smult(\alpha(n,l,m))
=\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha(n,l,m),\overline0}
-\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha(n,l,m),\overline1}
=f(nm,l)\qquad((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}).$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$$\alpha:\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\to\La^{2,1}_{II},\qquad
(n,l,m)\mapsto2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}.$$
$$q^nr^ls^m=\exp(-\pi i(\alpha(n,l,m),z))$$
$$Z\mapsto2Z.$$
$$\frac1{64}\Delta_5(2Z)
=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\right)^{\smult(\alpha)}.$$
$$\frac1{64}\mathcal D_X(2Z)
=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha(n,l,m),z)}\right)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
The triples in $\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\setminus\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}$
have exponent zero and do not contribute visible product factors.  The
denominator product alone does not prove absence of root spaces with
zero signed superdimension.
$$\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\smult(\alpha(n,l,m))=f(nm,l)
\quad((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}).$$
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[What the denominator determines]
The identity
$$
\frac1{64}\Delta_5(2Z)
=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\right)^{\smult(\alpha)}
$$
determines the signed integers \(\smult(\alpha)\), once the
Gritsenko--Nikulin root set and positive root monoid have been fixed.  It
does not determine invisible zero-superdimension root spaces, the two
parity dimensions
$$
\rootmult_{\overline0}(\alpha),\qquad
\rootmult_{\overline1}(\alpha),
$$
and it does not determine the structure constants
$$
[\mathfrak g_\alpha,\mathfrak g_\beta]\to
\mathfrak g_{\alpha+\beta}.
$$
It also does not determine simple primitive representatives, the
no-extra-relations statement, completed PBW compatibility, or the closed
radical of the positive-negative Hopf pairing.
Thus signed root multiplicity is necessary input for primitive
recognition, but it is not a recognition certificate.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write \(X^\alpha=e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\).  In the completed positive
root monoid algebra,
$$
\log\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}(1-X^\alpha)^{\smult(\alpha)}
=-\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}\sum_{k\ge1}
\frac{\smult(\alpha)}{k}X^{k\alpha}.
$$
Thus a logarithmic coefficient mixes divisor terms \(k\alpha=\lambda\).
The exponents \(\smult(\alpha)\) are recovered recursively by height,
equivalently by Mobius inversion on each primitive ray.  The recovered
exponent is only
$$
\smult(\alpha)=
\rootmult_{\overline0}(\alpha)-\rootmult_{\overline1}(\alpha).
$$
The difference $a-b$ does not determine the pair $(a,b)$, and no
bilinear bracket, PBW filtration, or Hopf-pairing radical appears in the
product.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[What the determinant forgets]
\label{thm:protected-denominator-shadow}
Let
$$
\mathcal B=\bigoplus_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}\mathcal B_\gamma
$$
be any charge-graded super vector space with finite-dimensional
homogeneous pieces and
$$\sdim\mathcal B_{(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l).$$
Then its Gram-graded Euler/Fock determinant is
$$
64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-x^\gamma)^{\sdim\mathcal B_\gamma}
=\Delta_5(Z).
$$
If $\mathcal B$ carries a bracket compatible with charge addition, a
parity split, simple-root representatives, or a Hopf pairing, the
determinant forgets those data and remembers the class of
$\mathcal B$ in
$$K_0(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\hbox{-graded finite super vector spaces}).$$
Thus the determinant of
$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}=\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$ is
the Grothendieck shadow of its denominator bracket.  The Borcherds
denominator bracket exists inside \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\) by the
Gritsenko--Nikulin construction, but the determinant sees only its
charge-graded Grothendieck class.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The Fock determinant lemma gives
$$
\sdet_{\mathcal B}(1-x)
=\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-x^\gamma)^{\sdim\mathcal B_\gamma}.
$$
The hypothesis $\sdim\mathcal B_{(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l)$ identifies this
product with the Borcherds product for $64^{-1}\Delta_5$.  Multiplying
by the vacuum factor gives $\Delta_5$.  A bracket
$$[\mathcal B_\gamma,\mathcal B_{\gamma'}]\to
\mathcal B_{\gamma+\gamma'}$$
does not occur in the determinant formula.  Neither do simple primitive
representatives, parity dimensions, relation constants, completed PBW
data, or a Hopf-pairing radical.  The determinant is therefore invariant
under replacing \(\mathcal B\) by any other graded super vector space with
the same Grothendieck class.  In particular the zero bracket on such a
space gives the same determinant and the wrong Lie algebra, and adjoining
a root-graded cancelling pair \(M\oplus\Pi M\) changes possible brackets
and radicals without changing the signed determinant.
\end{proof}

\section{The scalar square}

Unitarity is used to localize the right-moving K3 supertrace before the
index is taken; the index itself is a charge-graded virtual object that
no longer requires Hilbert positivity, so the OP/DT scalar series below
records charge-graded coefficients of a virtual character, not
dimensions of a positive Hilbert space.

$$Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(q,t,p)=
\sum_{h=0}^{\infty}\sum_{d=0}^{\infty}\sum_{n\in\mathbb{Z}}
\mathbf{DT}^X_{n,(\beta_h,d)}
q^{d-1}t^{\frac{1}{2}\langle\beta_h,\beta_h\rangle}(-p)^n.$$

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{c|c|c|c}
role & OP variable & DT variable & Borcherds variable \\ \hline
\(K3\) norm \(h-1\) & \(q_{\mathrm{OP}}\) & \(t_{\mathrm{DT}}\) & \(q_{\mathrm{Bch}}\) \\
elliptic degree \(d-1\) & \(\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}\) & \(q_{\mathrm{DT}}\) & \(s_{\mathrm{Bch}}\) \\
D0/Fourier index \(n\) & \(p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{iu}\) & \(p_{\mathrm{DT}}\) with \((-p_{\mathrm{DT}})^n\) & \(r_{\mathrm{Bch}}\)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{proposition}[Oberdieck--Pixton normalization]
\label{prop:op-normalization}
Let the Oberdieck--Pixton variables be
$$p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{iu},\qquad q_{\mathrm{OP}},\qquad
\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}.$$
The variable map is
$$q=q_{\mathrm{OP}},\qquad r=p_{\mathrm{OP}},\qquad
s=\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}.$$
The product index set is
\[
h,d\ge0,\qquad h>0\ \hbox{or}\ d>0,
\qquad\hbox{or}\qquad h=d=0,\ k<0.
\]
The Laurent expansion is the Oberdieck--Pixton expansion in its specified
chamber.  The reciprocal \(p_{\mathrm{OP}}\)-direction used to compare it
with a Borcherds cusp expansion is the formal re-expansion convention
\[
0<|\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}|\ll
|q_{\mathrm{OP}}|\ll |p_{\mathrm{OP}}|^{-1}\ll1,
\qquad r=p_{\mathrm{OP}}.
\]
This convention is recorded separately from the imported OP scalar
identity.  The enumerative identity is the Laurent expansion obtained
after \(p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{iu}\) and \(y=-e^{iu}\).
For the displayed DT variables,
$$q_{\mathrm{DT}}=\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}=s,\qquad
t_{\mathrm{DT}}=q_{\mathrm{OP}}=q,\qquad
p_{\mathrm{DT}}=p_{\mathrm{OP}}=r.$$
The product denoted $\chi_{10}$ by Oberdieck--Pixton is
$$\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}
=D_5^2
=\left(64^{-1}\Delta_5\right)^2
=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2.$$
Consequently their primitive reduced partition function is
$$Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-\left(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}\right)^{-1}
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}.$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Oberdieck--Pixton use the primitive expansion \cite[Theorem 1]{OB}
$$
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}
=\sum_{g,h,d}N_{g,h,d}u^{2g-2}
q_{\mathrm{OP}}^{h-1}\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}^{d-1}
$$
and the stable-pairs substitution, in the coordinate convention of
Oberdieck--Pandharipande \cite[Section 2]{OPand},
$$y=-p_{\mathrm{OP}},\qquad p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{iu}.$$
There
$$
\Omega=\begin{pmatrix}\tau&z\\ z&\widetilde\tau\end{pmatrix},\qquad
p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{2\pi iz}=e^{iu},\qquad
q_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{2\pi i\tau},\qquad
\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{2\pi i\widetilde\tau}.
$$
The displayed DT convention uses
$$q_{\mathrm{DT}}^{d-1}t_{\mathrm{DT}}^{h-1}(-p_{\mathrm{DT}})^n,$$
and Bryan records that the DT convention interchanges the $q$ and
$\widetilde q$ variables relative to Oberdieck--Pandharipande
\cite[Definition 2.1 and Conjecture 2.3]{BRYAN}.  This gives the stated
variable map.

Oberdieck--Pixton define the Igusa product by \cite[(3)]{OB}
$$
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}(p,q,\widetilde q)
=pq\widetilde q
\prod(1-p^kq^h\widetilde q^d)^{c(4hd-k^2)}
$$
in the chamber $h>0$ or $d>0$, together with $h=d=0,\ k<0$.  The
exponents are the K3 elliptic-genus coefficients.  Since
$$Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1},\qquad
\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l,$$
those exponents are $2f(nm,l)$.  Therefore the Oberdieck--Pixton monic
product is exactly the square of
$$D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5
=q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
Their Theorem 1, equivalently the Laurent expansion in \cite[(56)]{OB},
gives $Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-1/\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Reduced DT/PT/OP scalar square]
\label{thm:op-square}
Let \(\beta_h\in H_2(S,\Z)\) be primitive and non-zero, with
$$\langle\beta_h,\beta_h\rangle=2h-2.$$
Under the variable map
$$
p=P=e^{iu},\qquad t=Q,\qquad q=T,\qquad
(q_{\mathrm{Bch}},r_{\mathrm{Bch}},s_{\mathrm{Bch}})=(Q,P,T),
$$
one has
$$
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(T,Q,P)
=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T)
=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.
$$
The equality is an equality of Laurent expansions in the OP chamber of
Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}.  It is the theorem-level
OP/DT/PT scalar branch attached to the Behrend-weighted quotient
integration of Proposition~\ref{prop:reduced-scalar-quotient-integration}.
The physical protected-index identification is
Conjecture~\ref{conj:protected-d-brane-index}.
Imprimitive K3 curve classes require the separate imprimitive
multiple-cover certificate; the displayed OP scalar-square theorem is the
primitive-class branch used for the present square-root comparison.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Oberdieck's reduced DT/PT theorem for \(S\times E\),
\cite[Theorem 3(i)]{OberdieckReducedPT}, gives, for every non-zero
\(\beta\in H_2(S,\Z)\) and every \(d\ge0\),
$$
\sum_n\mathbf{DT}^X_{n,(\beta,d)}x^n
=
\sum_n\mathsf P^X_{n,(\beta,d)}x^n.
$$
Set \(x=-P\).  The degree-zero factor is
$$M(-P)^{\chi(S\times E)}=M(-P)^0=1.$$
For primitive \(\beta_h\), the reduced GW/PT comparison of
Oberdieck--Pandharipande \cite[Proposition 5]{OPand} gives
$$
\sum_n\mathsf P^X_{n,(\beta_h,d)}(-P)^n
=
\sum_g\mathsf N^X_{g,h,d}u^{2g-2},\qquad P=e^{iu}.
$$
Multiplying by \(Q^{h-1}T^{d-1}\) and summing over \(h,d\) gives
$$Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(T,Q,P)=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T).$$
Oberdieck--Pixton \cite[Theorem 1]{OB} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization} give
$$Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T)=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.$$
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[OP normalization branch]
\label{def:op-normalization-branch}
The OP/DT normalization branch is the proved enumerative series of
Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square}, displayed as a square in the OP convention:
$$
Z^X_{\square,\mathrm{OP/DT}}
:=Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2},
\qquad
C_{\square,\mathrm{OP/DT}}:=-4096.
$$
The numerical constant \(C_{\square,\mathrm{OP/DT}}=-4096\) is a
\emph{normalization} datum, not an enumerative invariant beyond the
identification of the series itself: it factors as
\(-4096=(-1)\times 64^2\), where the \(64^2\) is the squared theta-leading
coefficient \(([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5)^2\) and the leading
\(-1\) is the OP scalar convention
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}\).  No additional
enumerative content beyond the identification of \(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}\)
with \(D_5^{-2}\) is carried by the constant.
An external scalar-square series, if introduced later, is a Laurent
expansion of the form
$$Z^X_{\square,\mathrm{ext}}(Z)
=\frac{C_{\square,\mathrm{ext}}}{\Delta_5(Z)^2},
\qquad C_{\square,\mathrm{ext}}\in\C^\times,$$
and carries no OP/DT enumerative status unless its source is specified.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Square-root consequence]
For \(\mathfrak s\in\{\mathrm{OP},\mathrm{DT}\}\), with variables
normalised as in Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square},
$$Z^X_{\mathfrak s}(Z)=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.$$
Thus
$$\mathcal{D}_X(Z)^2=\frac{-4096}{Z^X_{\mathfrak s}(Z)},
\qquad \mathcal D_X(Z)=\Delta_5(Z).$$
	The virtual inverse is fixed by the normalized determinant:
$$\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}:=\mathcal D_X^{-1}.$$
A supplied Pfaffian square root may differ from this chosen cusp
trivialization by a sign character; that sign is the orientation datum
sought in Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character} and is
not determined by the OP scalar.  The squared scalar
\(Z^X_{\mathfrak s}=-4096(\mathcal D_X^{-1})^2\) does not fix an
orientation-lifted Pfaffian sign because squaring kills it.  With the
fixed virtual inverse,
$$Z^X_{\mathfrak s}
=-4096\,(\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}})^2,$$
$$|\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}|
=\frac{1}{64}|q|^{-1/2}|r|^{-1/2}|s|^{-1/2}|\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)|.$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square} gives the first display for
\(\mathfrak s=\mathrm{OP}\) and \(\mathfrak s=\mathrm{DT}\).  Hence
$$-4096/Z^X_{\mathfrak s}=\Delta_5^2.$$
The Borcherds determinant \(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\) fixes the
automorphic square-root section in the chosen cusp trivialization.  A
supplied Pfaffian orientation lift may carry an additional sign character,
but that sign is not part of the notation
\(\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}\).  Squaring any supplied
sign choice \(\varepsilon\), with \(\varepsilon^2=1\), gives
$$Z^X_{\mathfrak s}=-4096(\mathcal D_X^{-1})^2
=-4096(\varepsilon\mathcal D_X^{-1})^2,$$
the square-root sign being invisible to the scalar.
Selecting the sign requires an orientation datum, deferred to
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Constants are not orientation data]
The number \(64\) fixes the theta-normalized Igusa section and hence the
Weyl monomial in the determinant:
$$
\Delta_5
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.
$$
The monic denominator section is \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\).  The number
\(4096\) is \(64^2\), appearing because Oberdieck--Pixton use
$$
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2.
$$
Read as a normalization conversion, the OP scalar constant factors as
$$
-4096 \;=\; (-1)_{\mathrm{OP}}\cdot 64^2,
$$
where the leading \(-1\) is the OP scalar convention and \(64^2\) is the
squared theta-leading coefficient
\(([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5)^2\).  It is not the square of an
orientation sign; every square-root sign squares to \(+1\).
The minus sign in
$$
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}
$$
is the OP scalar convention.  None of these constants is the Hall
orientation character.  The automorphic character
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) is fixed by the Maass transformation law, and the
geometric character \(\epsilon_o\), if it exists, must be produced by
orientation-line monodromy as in
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.
\end{remark}

\section{Coefficient dictionary and main synthesis}
\label{sec:coefficient-dictionary-main-synthesis}

The coefficient convention is fixed once and for all by
Eichler--Zagier normalization:
$$
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1},\qquad
\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)=\sum_{n\ge0,\ l\in\Z}f(n,l)q^nr^l.
$$
Equivalently, if \(\phi_{12,1}\) is the first Fourier--Jacobi
coefficient of Igusa's weight-\(12\) form \(F_{12}\)
\cite{Igusa1962,Igusa1964II}, and if
$$
\delta_{12}(\tau)=q\prod_{n\ge1}(1-q^n)^{24},
$$
then
$$
\phi_{0,1}=\frac{\phi_{12,1}}{\delta_{12}}.
$$
The first terms are
$$
\phi_{0,1}
=(r^{-1}+10+r)
+q(10r^{-2}-64r^{-1}+108-64r+10r^2)
$$
$$
\qquad
+q^2(r^{-3}+108r^{-2}-513r^{-1}+808
-513r+108r^2+r^3)+O(q^3).
$$
Thus
$$
f(0,-1)=1,\qquad f(0,0)=10,\qquad
f(1,1)=-64,\qquad f(1,0)=108.
$$
The weak Jacobi support condition is
$$
f(n,l)=0\quad\hbox{unless}\quad n\ge0,\quad 4n-l^2\ge-1,
$$
and \(f(n,l)=f(n,-l)\).  These integers have three distinct readings in
the paper:
$$
\begin{array}{c|c}
\hbox{object} & \hbox{meaning of }f(nm,l) \\ \hline
\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)} & \hbox{virtual \(K_0\)-superdimension} \\
\mathcal D_X & \hbox{Borcherds product exponent} \\
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)} &
\hbox{signed root supermultiplicity on active support}
\end{array}
$$
The first reading is a protected Euler characteristic.  The second and
third readings are automorphic and denominator-algebra incarnations of
the same integer.  This is not an equality of Hilbert spaces, brackets,
or Hall structure constants.

The synthesis is the following spine:
\[
\begin{gathered}
\hbox{virtual determinant}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{formal charge and normal ordering}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{denominator algebra}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{reduced scalar square}
\\
\longrightarrow
\hbox{compact realization problem}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{eight-row certificate extension}.
\end{gathered}
\]
\begin{theorem}[Coefficient dictionary and synthesis theorem]
\label{thm:protected-igusa-determinant}
Let \(X=K3\times E\).  Let
\[
\mathbb U_{n,l}\in K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}}),\qquad
\sdim\mathbb U_{n,l}=f(n,l),
\]
and define the virtual \(K_0\)-determinant object in the cusp chamber by
\[
\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=\mathbb U_{nm,l},\qquad
(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}.
\]

First, the virtual determinant is the theta-normalized Igusa square root:
\[
\mathcal D_X(Z)
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=\Delta_5(Z).
\]
The numerical factor \(64\) is the theta-constant leading coefficient
\([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5\); the monic Borcherds product is
\[
D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5.
\]

Second, the formal dyonic Mukai lattice is additive but its Igusa Gram
shadow is quadratic.  For
\[
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}=\Lambda_S\oplus\Lambda_S,\qquad c=(Q,P),
\]
the map
\[
\Pi_X(c)=\left(\frac{Q^2}{2},Q\cdot P,\frac{P^2}{2}\right)
\]
satisfies
\[
\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c').
\]
The normal-ordered extension
\[
\widehat\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{form}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
\overline\Pi_X(c,T)=\Pi_X(c)-T
\]
is additive, and every formal Gram triple has a primitive saturated
formal lift when \(\Lambda_S\) contains two orthogonal hyperbolic planes.
This does not prove algebraic/effective compact Hall support.  Strict
fixed-lift raw \(\Pi_X\)-descent cannot realize the type-II BKM real-root
strings; Theorem~\ref{thm:raw-gram-descent-no-go} is the obstruction.

Third, under the Lorentzian degree map
\[
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2},
\qquad
q^nr^ls^m=\exp(-\pi i(\alpha(n,l,m),z)),
\]
the same active coefficients are the visible signed root
supermultiplicities of the Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator algebra:
\[
\smult\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)}
=f(nm,l)
\qquad ((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}),
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})
=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z).
\]
This is the Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator theorem.  It determines the
signed root supermultiplicities in the fixed Borcherds datum; it does
not determine compact Hall constants or microscopic brackets.  The
normal-ordered charge extension is the necessary degree-level bridge
from an additive Hall source to these Gram degrees.

Fourth, for the reduced Hilbert-scheme DT/PT/OP scalar branch,
\[
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(T,Q,P)=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T)
=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.
\]
Here
\[
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2=(64^{-1}\Delta_5)^2
=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2,
\qquad
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1};
\]
hence \(-4096=-(64)^2\) is the OP scalar sign together with the
theta-to-monic normalization.  It is not an orientation character.
Thus, with
\[
\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}=\mathcal D_X^{-1},
\]
one has
\[
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}
=-4096\,(\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}})^2.
\]

Fifth, the stronger microscopic comparison
\[
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\overline\Pi_{X,*}^{\Theta}\mathcal F_X)/
\overline{\operatorname{Rad}\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_X}
\cong
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}
\]
is open unless a Dirac--Igusa realization certificate in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum} is supplied.
If such a certificate were supplied, Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}
would identify its primitive denominator with \(64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\); no
such certificate is constructed in this paper.

Sixth, any claimed compact realization must also satisfy three
consequences.
\begin{enumerate}
\item A naive support-local factorization object on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) sees only projection-finite sectors.  If a
one-dimensional subscheme of \(K3\times E\) has positive elliptic
degree, its projection to \(E\) is all of \(E\).  Thus the full
\(s\)-direction of the Igusa product requires finite-stage
local/wrapped data: \(b_R\), rigidified wrapped prequotients, mixed
extension correspondences in both local/wrapped orders,
wrapped/wrapped correspondences, the eight-word two-step binary flag atlas in
\(\mathsf{Corr}^{E,\mathrm{hyb}}_R\), the higher colored residual
\(\mathfrak o^{\mathrm{col}}_R\), properness/admissibility residuals
for the pull-push operations, quotient-after-correspondence
\(Q_{E,R}\)-compatibility, and protected integration with trace degree
\(s^{b_R}\).  Equivalently,
\(\mathfrak O_{\mathrm{hyb},R}=0\) for every finite \(R\).  A separate
global Fock/Hecke mode is only
determinant-level unless it is coupled to the local sector by mixed Hall
actions before the reduced \(E\)-quotient.
\item The automorphic character \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) is theorem-level
data of \(\Delta_5\), and \(\Delta_5^2\) forgets it.  A compact Hall
orientation must construct a strong orientation character
\(\epsilon_o\) and prove
\[
\epsilon_o|_{W^{(2)}(\Lambda^{2,1}_{II})}
=\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\Lambda^{2,1}_{II})}.
\]
The constants \(64\), \(4096\), and the OP minus sign do not solve this
orientation-monodromy problem.  The Hall-side proof must compute the
three simple type-II determinant-line signs and check the reflection
relations.
\item A primitive comparison with \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\) is a
presentation-level recognition certificate, not a consequence of signed
dimensions.  One must supply primitive representatives for the real and
imaginary simple roots, their parities, the Chevalley, real Serre and
orthogonality relations, generation, full root-space parity dimensions,
the completed Hopf pairing and the same closed radical quotient, a
no-extra-relations theorem, and completed PBW compatibility in the
finite-height inverse system, including exact triangular
completion/\(\lim^1\)-vanishing and Koszul Mittag--Leffler exactness for
the chiral cobar comparison.  Under these hypotheses the
Borcherds--Kac universal presentation gives the isomorphism with
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\); without them the determinant fixes only a
Grothendieck class.
\end{enumerate}

Finally, the diagonal-divisor rows extend this same logic.  A row is
promoted beyond its automorphic product only by a row certificate fixing
the modular group or cover, character, divisor, Jacobi seed, product
lattice, Weyl chamber, reflection character, scalar theorem if one is
claimed, orientation data, one-particle index, and primitive algebra
comparison.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Fock trace calculation gives
\[
\mathcal D_X
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x).
\]
The Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin product formula for the input
\(\phi_{0,1}\) identifies this product with \(\Delta_5\), as recorded in
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification}.  The leading coefficient
\(64\) is fixed in the theta-normalized Fourier expansion of
\(\Delta_5\), hence \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\) is the monic product.

The formal charge and normal-ordering statements are
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice},
Lemma~\ref{lem:primitive-lift-every-gram-triple},
Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect},
Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}, and
Definition~\ref{def:gram-corrected-charge-extension}.  They are direct
lattice calculations in the Mukai pairing.  The raw-descent obstruction
is Theorem~\ref{thm:raw-gram-descent-no-go}; it uses the non-zero
second real-root strings recorded in
Proposition~\ref{prop:low-degree-denominator-brackets}.

The Lorentzian monomial identity and pairing computation are in
Section~\ref{sec:duality-principle} and the Weyl-chamber section.  The
root-supermultiplicity and denominator identity are
Theorem~\ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}; the argument \(2Z\)
comes from passing from
\(\exp(-\pi i(\alpha,z))\) to the usual denominator character
\(\exp(-2\pi i(\alpha,z))\).

The reduced scalar identity is Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square}, with the
normalization conversion of Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}.
Since Oberdieck--Pixton use
\(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2\) and prove
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}\), the theta
normalization gives
\[
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}.
\]
Oberdieck's reduced DT/PT comparison and the primitive
Oberdieck--Pandharipande comparison give the same branch for
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}\).

The compact comparison is not used in these proofs.  It is precisely
Open Problem~\ref{op:compact-igusa-realization}.  The
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) obstruction follows because a positive
elliptic-degree curve has one-dimensional image in the irreducible
curve \(E\), hence image \(E\); support separation on disjoint opens of
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) cannot see such a sector.  The automorphic
character computation gives the target values of \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\);
rescaling \(\Delta_5\) by \(64^{-1}\) changes no character.  A compact
orientation statement follows only after (O1) constructs the reduced
quotient orientation, (O1)\(^+\) supplies the honest Weyl transport, and
(O2) supplies the local Pfaffian signs.  The
primitive recognition statement is the universal property of the
Borcherds--Kac presentation recorded in the denominator-algebra section,
together with the closed Hopf-radical and completed PBW hypotheses in
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.  The determinant and scalar
square do not contain the missing presentation, orientation, radical, PBW,
or Hall correspondence data.  The row certificate condition is the same
separation applied to the Clery--Gritsenko catalogue in the next part.
\end{proof}

\part{Diagonal-divisor rows and CHL boundary physics}

\section{Eight diagonal-divisor rows: automorphic and physical status}
\label{sec:eight-dd-rows-status}

The Clery--Gritsenko catalogue gives eight
diagonal-divisor automorphic products.  The Gritsenko--Nikulin and
Govindarajan theorems promote these products to denominator identities
in the rows where the Weyl data are known.  A CHL dyon square, a reduced
CY/DT scalar host, and a compact Hall/chiral host are further structures,
recorded only where their data have been specified.

$$g=2.$$
$$t,N \in \mathbb{Z}_+:\quad \Gamma_t(N) =
\{\begin{pmatrix}*&*t&*&*\\*&*&*&*t^{-1}\\*N&*Nt&*&*\\*Nt&*Nt&*t&*\end{pmatrix}
\in \Sp_4(\mathbb{Q})\mid *\in\mathbb{Z}\}.$$
$$\mathbb H_2/\Gamma_t
\longleftrightarrow\{(1,t)\hbox{-polarized abelian surfaces}\}.$$
$$\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}
=\left\{\begin{pmatrix}a&0\\0&b\end{pmatrix}\mid
a,b\in\mathbb{H}_1\right\}\subset\mathbb{H}_2.$$

\begin{definition}[Physical-host certificate]
\label{def:physical-host-certificate}
For a diagonal-divisor row \(F_j\), a physical-host certificate is a
five-level certificate table
\[
\mathfrak C_j=
\left(
\mathscr A_j,\mathscr D_j,\mathscr S_j,\mathscr Z_j,\mathscr H_j
\right).
\]
The entries have the following meanings.
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathscr A_j\) is the automorphic product certificate: the form
\(F_j\), the group or multiplier cover, the automorphy cocycle, the
character or multiplier with exact order, the diagonal divisor with
multiplicities, the product chamber and branch, the Jacobi input at
every cusp, the product-degree map, the product normalization, and the
source theorem.
\item \(\mathscr D_j\) is the denominator certificate: a
Weyl--Kac--Borcherds denominator algebra with root lattice, Weyl vector,
simple real roots, Weyl chamber, Weyl group, reflection character,
imaginary simple-root coefficients, product side, and Weyl alternating
side.
\item \(\mathscr S_j\) is a CHL/dyon-square certificate: a sourced
dyon-counting scalar form \(\Phi_j\), a row map to the same automorphic
row and cover, and an identity \(F_j^2=\Phi_j\) in the stated chamber.
This is not a denominator theorem and not a CY/DT partition theorem.
\item \(\mathscr Z_j\) is a reduced CY/DT scalar-host certificate: a
compact Calabi--Yau threefold, orbifold Calabi--Yau, or CHL background
with oriented reduced obstruction theory, fixed variables and chamber,
and a proved identity
\[
Z^{X_j}_{\mathrm{red}}(Z)=C_jF_j(Z)^{-2}.
\]
\item \(\mathscr H_j\) is a compact Hall/chiral certificate: an oriented
compact Hall, Drinfeld, or factorization object whose protected
one-particle index gives the product exponents and whose protected
primitive bracket identifies the denominator algebra with the same
orientation/reflection character.
\end{enumerate}
The product row, denominator row, dyon square, reduced scalar host, and
compact Hall/chiral host are separate structures.  None of the five
entries implies another unless a cited theorem constructs the implication.
In particular, matching a weight, a square root, or a comparison symbol
does not fill a certificate.  A row-map theorem must name the host,
charge lattice, effective chamber, modular group or cover, product
lattice, orientation character, one-particle index, scalar identity when
claimed, and primitive Hall/chiral comparison.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Clery--Gritsenko]
In the class of Siegel modular forms with character or multiplier system
for the Hecke-type congruence subgroups $\Gamma_t(N)$ whose divisor is
the union of the $\Gamma_t(N)$-translates of $\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}$
with multiplicity one, there are exactly eight rows
\cite[Theorem 1.4]{GC}.  The nine-candidate list is
\cite[Proposition 1.2]{GC}; the proof of Theorem 1.4 excludes only
the ninth candidate \((t,N;k)=(2,4;\frac12)\).  The congruence
Borcherds product with all
cusp coefficients is \cite[Theorem 3.1]{GC}, with the final Section 3
product displays for $\nabla_3,\nabla_2,\nabla_{3/2}$, and $Q_1$.
\end{theorem}

$$
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c}
j&F_j&\Gamma&\mathrm{wt}(F_j)&\mathrm{character/multiplier}\\ \hline
1&\Delta_5&\Gamma_1&5&v_\eta^{12}\times v_H\\
2&\Delta_2&\Gamma_2&2&v_\eta^{6}\times v_H\\
3&\Delta_1&\Gamma_3&1&v_\eta^{4}\times v_H\\
4&\Delta_{1/2}&\Gamma_4&\frac12&v_\eta^{3}\times v_H\ (\mathrm{degree}\ 8)\\
5&\nabla_3&\Gamma_0^{(2)}(2)&3&\chi_2^{(2)}\times v_H\\
6&\nabla_2&\Gamma_0^{(2)}(3)&2&\chi_2^{(3)}\times v_H\\
7&\nabla_{3/2}&\Gamma_0^{(2)}(4)&\frac32&
\hbox{order-four multiplier } \chi_4^{(4)}\times v_H\\
8&Q_1&\Gamma_2(2)&1&\chi_4^{(2)}\times v_H
\end{array}
$$
$$\operatorname{supp}\operatorname{div}_{\mathbb H_2}(F_j)
=\bigcup_{\gamma\in\Gamma_j}\gamma\langle\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}\rangle,
\qquad
\operatorname{mult}_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}}(F_j)=1.$$

$$F_1=\Delta_5,\qquad
\frac1{64}F_1(2Z)=\operatorname{den}(\autcor).$$

\begin{center}
\begingroup
\setlength{\tabcolsep}{3pt}
\scriptsize
\begin{tabular}{@{}c p{0.14\textwidth} p{0.16\textwidth} p{0.16\textwidth} p{0.17\textwidth} p{0.17\textwidth}@{}}

scalar form, only after fixing the cover and branch &
no reduced CY/DT certificate &
